说起他称为女儿的那些人，沃盖夫人所有的房客都支持她的看法。 As for the creatures whom he called his daughters, all Mme. Vauquer’s boarders were of her opinion.
老女人们总爱在漫漫长夜里嚼舌根，她们最后总能找到一种适用于所有情况的假说。她们就这样孜孜不倦地培养了缜密的逻辑思维能力，于是总是习惯这样思考：“那些来这里的女士看上去很富有。如果高老头自己当真有那么有钱的女儿，就不会住在我旅馆的四楼，每月才支付四十五法郎房费，也不会穿得像穷人一样四处走动了。” With the faculty for severe logic sedulously cultivated by elderly women during long evenings of gossip till they can always find an hypothesis to fit all circumstances, she was wont to reason thus: “If Father Goriot had daughters of his own as rich as those ladies who came here seemed to be, he would not be lodging in my house, on the third floor, at forty-five francs a month; and he would not go about dressed like a poor man.”
没有人能对这些推论提出异议。 No objection could be raised to these inferences.
所以到了一八一九年十一月底，当这幕戏剧将要拉开帷幕的时候，旅馆里的每一个人都对这个可怜的老人有了个极其肯定的看法。 So by the end of the month of November 1819, at the time when the curtain rises on this drama, every one in the house had come to have a very decided opinion as to the poor old man.
他压根就不曾有过妻子或女儿，过度放纵让他沦落到了这种悲惨的境地。一起吃晚餐的客人中有一个是博物馆员工。他有着自己独到的小幽默。他说高老头是一种人形软体动物，应该被列入偏盖螺科。 He had never had either wife or daughter; excesses had reduced him to this sluggish condition; he was a sort of human mollusk who should be classed among the capulidae, so one of the dinner contingent, an @employee@ at the Museum, who had a pretty wit of his own.
跟高里奥比起来，普瓦雷是一只目光锐利的鹰，是一位绅士。 Poiret was an eagle, a gentleman, compared with Goriot.
只要有人和他说话，普瓦雷就会参与进去。但是，他的话语、争论和回答对谈话没有任何实际意义，因为他习惯用不同的字眼来重复其他人所说的话。不过，他的确加入了大家的谈话。他是个活生生的人，看起来懂得感知。而高老头（再次引用博物馆员工的话）在列氏寒暑表上永远都是零度。 Poiret would join the talk, argue, answer when he was spoken to; as a matter of fact, his talk, arguments, and responses contributed nothing to the conversation, for Poiret had a habit of repeating what the others said in different words; still, he did join in the talk; he was alive, and seemed capable of feeling; while Father Goriot (to quote the Museum official again) was invariably at zero degrees—Reaumur.
欧仁·德拉斯蒂涅刚刚回到巴黎。对于那些意识到自身特殊力量，能力被困难处境所激发而暂时超出正常水平的年轻人来说，他的思想状态并不陌生。 Eugene de Rastignac had just returned to Paris in a state of mind not unknown to young men who are conscious of unusual powers, and to those whose faculties are so stimulated by a difficult position, that for the time being they rise above the ordinary level.
拉斯蒂涅第一年的学习是在为法律系的预备考试做准备。这一年让他自由自在地欣赏了巴黎的风景，享受到了一些娱乐活动。 Rastignac’s first year of study for the preliminary examinations in law had left him free to see the sights of Paris and to enjoy some of its amusements.
如果一个学生要着手了解每个剧院的全部剧目并研究巴黎这座大迷宫的里里外外，他的手里就不会有多少时间。 A student has not much time on his hands if he sets himself to learn the repertory of every theatre, and to study the ins and outs of the labyrinth of Paris.
要想知道它的风俗民情，学习语言，并熟悉首都的娱乐活动，他就必须利用自己的假期来探索巴黎的隐秘之处——不论这些地方是好是坏——去学习他最喜欢的东西，并对画廊和博物馆里的珍品形成一些看法。 To know its customs; to learn the language, and become familiar with the amusements of the capital, he must explore its recesses, good and bad, follow the studies that please him best, and form some idea of the treasures contained in galleries and museums.
在人生的这个阶段，一个学生会对各种各样的蠢事感兴趣，并为这些蠢事兴奋不已。在他眼里，这些事情似乎无比重要。 At this stage of his career a student grows eager and excited about all sorts of follies that seem to him to be of immense importance.
他有自己的英雄、自己的伟人——法兰西学院的一名教授。人们花钱请这位教授用听众能够理解的话语来讲授知识。 He has his hero, his great man, a professor at the College de France, paid to talk down to the level of his audience.
他整理了一下自己的领带，对坐在喜剧剧院顶层楼座的女士们搔首弄姿。 He adjusts his cravat, and strikes various attitudes for the benefit of the women in the first galleries at the Opera-Comique.
一样一样入门以后，他脱下了自己的外壳，扩展了自己的生活圈子。最后他领会到社会是由不同的人类阶层组成的。 As he passes through all these successive initiations, and breaks out of his sheath, the horizons of life widen around him, and at length he grasps the plan of society with the different human strata of which it is composed.
如果一开始他只是羡慕阳光明媚的下午在香榭丽舍大街上前行的一队队马车，很快他便会更进一步去妒忌它们的主人。 If he begins by admiring the procession of carriages on sunny afternoons in the Champs-Elysees, he soon reaches the further stage of envying their owners.
在回昂古莱姆过长假之前，他就不知不觉地完成了学业，获得了文学学位和法学学位。 Unconsciously, Eugene had served his apprenticeship before he went back to Angouleme for the long vacation after taking his degrees as bachelor of arts and bachelor of law.
童年的幻想消失了，他从外省带来了的观念也消失了。他带着更健全的智慧、带着更崇高的抱负回到了那里。家乡的一切在他看来就像是古旧庄园里的事物。 The illusions of childhood had vanished, so also had the ideas he brought with him from the provinces; he had returned thither with an intelligence developed, with loftier ambitions, and saw things as they were at home in the old manor house.
他的父亲、母亲、两个兄弟、两个妹妹，还有一个除了养老金外没有其他财产的、年迈的姑妈一起住在拉斯蒂涅家小小的房子里。 His father and mother, his two brothers and two sisters, with an aged aunt, whose whole fortune consisted in annuities, lived on the little estate of Rastignac.
家里所有的财产约有三千法郎，尽管这个数目随着季节会有所变化（葡萄种植区一直都是这样），他们每年都会从收入中为他省出一千二百法郎。 The whole property brought in about three thousand francs; and though the amount varied with the season (as must always be the case in a vine-growing district), they were obliged to spare an unvarying twelve hundred francs out of their income for him.
尽管家人们都好心地瞒着他，他明白家里一直以来的穷困状况。穷困始终压在他们身上。他不由自主地拿自己的两个妹妹——当他还是个小男孩的时候，她们在他眼里看来是如此美丽——和他理想中的美女，巴黎女人比较起来。 He saw how constantly the poverty, which they had generously hidden from him, weighed upon them; he could not help comparing the sisters, who had seemed so beautiful to his boyish eyes, with women in Paris, who had realized the beauty of his dreams.
整个家庭渺茫的未来都靠他了。 The uncertain future of the whole family depended upon him.
家里连面包屑都舍不得浪费，喝的酒是二次压榨的，这些都逃不过他的眼睛。许许多多琐事说也无益，就无需赘述了。它们让他迫切想要出人头地，想要成功的野心也膨胀了十倍。 It did not escape his eyes that not a crumb was wasted in the house, nor that the wine they drank was made from the second pressing; a multitude of small things, which it is useless to speak of in detail here, made him burn to distinguish himself, and his ambition to succeed increased tenfold.
和所有伟大的灵魂一样，他原本打算完全依靠自己的努力来取得成功。但是，他有着典型的南方人性格。这个年轻人仿佛孤零零地漂在宽广的大海中间，不知道怎样利用自己的能力，不知道该驶向哪里，不知道怎么调整风帆，于是他变得晕头转向。这时候，他实施计划的雄心壮志肯定会被削弱。 He meant, like all great souls, that his success should be owing entirely to his merits; but his was pre-eminently a southern temperament, the execution of his plans was sure to be marred by the vertigo that seizes on youth when youth sees itself alone in a wide sea, uncertain how to spend its energies, whither to steer its course, how to adapt its sails to the winds.
一开始，他下定决心要全心全意地投入到学习当中，但是出于社交应酬的需要，他偏离了自己的决定。然后，他了解到女人能给社交生活带来很大的影响，于是突然决定走出房门，进入社会，去那里寻找一个女性保护人。 At first he determined to fling himself heart and soul into his work, but he was diverted from this purpose by the need of society and connections; then he saw how great an influence women exert in social life, and suddenly made up his mind to go out into this world to seek a protectress there.
他是个聪明、热情的年轻人，优雅的外表和阳刚的气质更是彰显出了他的智慧和勇敢。这样的人肯定很容易叫女性着迷，根本不愁找不见女性保护人。 Surely a clever and high-spirited young man, whose wit and courage were set off to advantage by a graceful figure and the vigorous kind of beauty that readily strikes a woman’s imagination, need not despair of finding a protectress.
他在乡间和妹妹们散步的时候突然有了这些念头。从前，他和她们一起就很开心。 These ideas occurred to him in his country walks with his sisters, whom he had once joined so gaily.
女孩们觉得他大大地改变了。 The girls thought him very much changed.
他的姑妈，德马西亚克夫人曾经入过宫廷。在那个位高权重之地，她曾在达官显贵之间游走。 His aunt, Mme. de Marcillac, had been presented at court, and had moved among the brightest heights of that lofty region.
她的那些回忆以前对于自己的侄子侄女来说只是幼稚园的童话故事。现在，这个野心勃勃的年轻人突然在它们中看到了可以在社交上助他取得成功的元素，这一成功至少跟他在法学院取得的成功一样重要。 Suddenly the young man’s ambition discerned in those recollections of hers, which had been like nursery fairy tales to her nephews and nieces, the elements of a social success at least as important as the success which he had achieved at the Ecole de Droit.
他开始向自己的姑妈打听那些亲戚，觉得有些老交情也许还有效。 He began to ask his aunt about those relations; some of the old ties might still hold good.
这位年迈的女士想了想族谱中的各个分支，得出了这样的结论：在所有能够帮助她侄子的那些自私自利的有钱亲戚中，德伯桑子爵夫人是最不可能拒绝他的人。 After much shaking of the branches of the family tree, the old lady came to the conclusion that of all persons who could be useful to her nephew among the selfish genus of rich relations, the Vicomtesse de Beauseant was the least likely to refuse.
因此，她用老式的体裁给这位女士写了一封信，向她推荐了欧仁，并告诉自己的侄子，如果他能取悦德伯桑夫人，德伯桑夫人就会把他介绍给其他亲戚。 To this lady, therefore, she wrote in the old-fashioned style, recommending Eugene to her; pointing out to her nephew that if he succeeded in pleasing Mme. de Beauseant, the Vicomtesse would introduce him to other relations.
所以，回到巴黎几天后，拉斯蒂涅就把他姑妈的信寄给了德伯桑夫人。 A few days after his return to Paris, therefore, Rastignac sent his aunt’s letter to Mme. de Beauseant.
那位子爵夫人给他回复了一张请帖，邀请他参加第二天晚上的舞会。 The Vicomtesse replied by an invitation to a ball for the following evening.
这就是一八一九年十一月末时，“沃盖之家”的大概情况。 This was the position of affairs at the Maison Vauquer at the end of November 1819.
几天后，欧仁参加了德伯桑夫人的舞会，清晨两点才回来。 A few days later, after Mme. de Beauseant’s ball, Eugene came in at two o’clock in the morning.
这个有恒心的学生原本打算开夜车来弥补失去的时间。 The persevering student meant to make up for the lost time by working until daylight.
这是他第一次试图在这个安静的街区以这样的方式度过夜晚。 It was the first time that he had attempted to spend the night in this way in that silent quarter.
虚假的活力让他着了魔。他已经见识到世界壮观、华丽的一面了。 The spell of a factitious energy was upon him; he had beheld the pomp and splendor of the world.
他没有回“沃盖之家”吃晚饭，房客们也许认为他黎明时分会离开舞会，然后走回来。因为过去在参加完普拉多高级住宅区的宴会或者奥德翁剧院的舞会后，他时不时地会这样做，还因此害得自己的丝制长筒袜溅满了泥、轻舞鞋也走了样。 He had not dined at the Maison Vauquer; the boarders probably would think that he would walk home at daybreak from the dance, as he had done sometimes on former occasions, after a fete at the Prado, or a ball at the Odeon, splashing his silk stockings thereby, and ruining his pumps.
事情的经过是这样的。克里斯托夫在插门闩之前，先朝街上看了看，拉斯蒂涅就在这个时候回来了。他原本可以悄悄上楼，不发出一点声响，但跟在后面的克里斯托夫倒是弄出了很大的声响。 It so happened that Christophe took a look into the street before drawing the bolts of the door; and Rastignac, coming in at that moment, could go up to his room without making any noise, followed by Christophe, who made a great deal.
欧仁脱下了礼服，换上了破旧的外套和拖鞋，拿了几块加了粘合剂的煤球点上了火，准备开夜车。他做这一切的时候声音很轻，微弱的声响完全淹没在克里斯托夫上楼时那重重的脚步声中。 Eugene exchanged his dress suit for a shabby overcoat and slippers, kindled a fire with some blocks of patent fuel, and prepared for his night’s work in such a sort that the faint sounds he made were drowned by Christophe’s heavy tramp on the stairs.
欧仁在全身心读法律书之前，先坐在那里出神地想了一会儿。 Eugene sat absorbed in thought for a few moments before plunging into his law books.
他刚刚了解到了一件事，即德伯桑子爵夫人是时尚女王之一，她的府邸被认为是圣日耳曼郊区最舒适的地方。 He had just become aware of the fact that the Vicomtesse de Beauseant was one of the queens of fashion, that her house was thought to be the pleasantest in the Faubourg Saint-Germain.
不仅如此，凭她的财力和家世，她简直就是贵族世界里最引人注目的人物之一。 And not only so, she was, by right of her fortune, and the name she bore, one of the most conspicuous figures in that aristocratic world.
多亏了他的姑妈，多亏了德马西亚克夫人的引荐信，这个穷困的学生在那所府邸里受到了优待，却还不知道他受到的优待是多么高。 Thanks to the aunt, thanks to Mme. de Marcillac’s letter of introduction, the poor student had been kindly received in that house before he knew the extent of the favor thus shown to him.
能在那些奢华的社交沙龙露面几乎就是一张贵族许可证。他进入了巴黎最排外的圈子，现在所有的门都向他敞开了。 It was almost like a patent of nobility to be admitted to those gilded salons; he had appeared in the most exclusive circle in Paris, and now all doors were open for him.
一开始，华丽的宴会让欧仁眼花缭乱，他几乎没能跟子爵夫人说上几句话。后来，他从一群巴黎女神中挑出了一位肯定能叫人一见倾心的女神，对此他很满意。 Eugene had been dazzled at first by the brilliant assembly, and had scarcely exchanged a few words with the Vicomtesse; he had been content to single out a goddess among this throng of Parisian divinities, one of those women who are sure to attract a young man’s fancy.
阿纳斯塔谢·德雷斯多伯爵夫人亭亭玉立、体态优雅。她是巴黎身段最好的女子之一。 The Comtesse Anastasie de Restaud was tall and gracefully made; she had one of the prettiest figures in Paris.
想象一下，一对秀美的黑眸，一只优雅的玉手，还有一只漂亮的秀足。 Imagine a pair of great dark eyes, a magnificently moulded hand, a shapely foot.
她的一举一动都活力四射。德龙侯爵称她为“一个血统纯正的人”，“一个出身名门的人”，这些词代替了“迷人的天使”和莪相(注：莪相是古代爱尔兰说唱诗人)式的夸张称谓。古老的爱情神话彻底消失了，它注定要消亡在时尚的现代生活中。 There was a fiery energy in her movements; the Marquis de Ronquerolles had called her “a thoroughbred,” “a pure pedigree,” these figures of speech have replaced the “heavenly angel” and Ossianic nomenclature; the old mythology of love is extinct, doomed to perish by modern dandyism.
但是对于拉斯蒂涅来说，阿纳斯塔谢·德雷斯多夫人正是他所渴求的女人。 But for Rastignac, Mme. Anastasie de Restaud was the woman for whom he had sighed.
他想方设法在她扇子上的舞伴名单中将自己的名字写了两遍，还在第一次跳方阵舞的时候和她搭了几句话。 He had contrived to write his name twice upon the list of partners upon her fan, and had snatched a few words with her during the first quadrille.
“我怎样才能再看见您，夫人？”他唐突地问道，说话时语调充满了热情，这正是女士们非常喜欢的。 “Where shall I meet you again, Madame?” he asked abruptly, and the tones of his voice were full of the vehement energy that women like so well.
“哦，哪里都可以啊！”她说道，“树林里、谐谑剧场、我家里，都行。” “Oh, everywhere!” said she, “in the Bois, at the Bouffons, in my own house.”
于是，凭着南方人的那股冒险的冲动劲，他充分利用了方阵舞和她邀请他一起跳华尔兹的机会，竭尽全力想和可爱的伯爵夫人熟识起来。 With the impetuosity of his adventurous southern temper, he did all he could to cultivate an acquaintance with this lovely countess, making the best of his opportunities in the quadrille and during a waltz that she gave him.
当他告诉伯爵夫人，自己是德伯桑夫人的堂弟时，他眼中的高贵女士立刻邀请他去她家玩。她笑着和他道别，之后拉斯蒂涅更加觉得自己必须得去拜访她。 When he told her that he was a cousin of Mme. de Beauseant’s, the Countess, whom he took for a great lady, asked him to call at her house, and after her parting smile, Rastignac felt convinced that he must make this visit.
他是多么幸运啊，找到了一个没有嘲笑其无知的人。无知是当时富有、傲慢的年轻人的致命缺点。舞会的宾客有莫林库尔、马克西姆·德拉特尔、德马尔塞、龙格罗、阿尤达-平托和范登埃塞。这些纨绔子弟个个光彩照人、声名显赫，周旋在巴黎打扮得最时尚、最高雅的女士之间——布朗东女士、德朗热公爵夫人、德凯尔加鲁埃伯爵夫人、德塞里夫人、德卡里利安诺公爵夫人、费罗伯爵夫人、德朗蒂夫人、德艾格勒蒙侯爵夫人、菲尔米亚尼夫人、德利斯图梅雷侯爵夫人、德埃斯帕侯爵夫人、德莫弗里涅公爵夫人和格朗利厄等等。 He was so lucky as to light upon some one who did not laugh at his ignorance, a fatal defect among the gilded and insolent youth of that period; the coterie of Maulincourts, Maximes de Trailles, de Marsays, Ronquerolles, Ajuda-Pintos, and Vandenesses who shone there in all the glory of coxcombry among the best-dressed women of fashion in Paris—Lady Brandon, the Duchesse de Langeais, the Comtesse de Kergarouet, Mme. de Serizy, the Duchesse de Carigliano, the Comtesse Ferraud, Mme. de Lanty, the Marquise d’Aiglemont, Mme. Firmiani, the Marquise de Listomere and the Marquise d’Espard, the Duchesse de Maufrigneuse and the Grandlieus.
所以说拉斯蒂涅这个新手碰到了德蒙特里沃侯爵实在很幸运。他是德朗热公爵夫人的情人，是一个和小孩一样单纯的将军。拉斯蒂涅从他口中得知伯爵夫人就住在埃尔德街。 Luckily, therefore, for him, the novice happened upon the Marquis de Montriveau, the lover of the Duchesse de Langeais, a general as simple as a child; from him Rastignac learned that the Comtesse lived in the Rue du Helder.
啊，他是如此年轻，如此渴望见识世界，觊觎着可以拉近自己和梦中情人距离的所有机会。现在，他看到有两家的门已经为他而开了！ Ah, what it is to be young, eager to see the world, greedily on the watch for any chance that brings you nearer the woman of your dreams, and behold two houses open their doors to you!
踏进了德伯桑子爵夫人位于圣日耳曼郊区的府邸；拜倒在居住于德安丁路的德雷斯多伯爵夫人的面前，瞟一眼巴黎的客厅的景色，他明白了只要样貌足够英俊，就有希望在女性的心中找到帮助和庇护！ To set foot in the Vicomtesse de Beauseant’s house in the Faubourg Saint-Germain; to fall on your knees before a Comtesse de Restaud in the Chaussee d’Antin; to look at one glance across a vista of Paris drawing-rooms, conscious that, possessing sufficient good looks, you may hope to find aid and protection there in a feminine heart!
以前，他必须在杂技演员平稳的引领下才敢在绷紧的绳索上走动，因为杂技演员是不可能摔倒的。而今，他感到自己有了足够的雄心壮志，可以丢掉绳索，在一位迷人的女士身上找到最好的平衡杆了。 To feel ambitious enough to spurn the tight-rope on which you must walk with the steady head of an acrobat for whom a fall is impossible, and to find in a charming woman the best of all balancing poles.
他坐在那里这样想了一会儿，一边是法律，另一边是贫穷，他好似看见一位容光焕发的女士出现在奄奄一息的火焰上方。 He sat there with his thoughts for a while, Law on the one hand, and Poverty on the other, beholding a radiant vision of a woman rise above the dull, smouldering fire.
谁不会像欧仁那样，停下来思考一下自己的未来呢？谁不想未来能功成名就呢？ Who would not have paused and questioned the future as Eugene was doing?Who would not have pictured it full of success?
他的思想仿佛插上了翅膀。可正当他觉得自己离开了现实，来到了幸福美满的未来，正坐在德雷斯多夫人旁边的时候，一声叹息打破了夜的宁静。那叹息就好像是负荷过重的圣约瑟发出的嘟囔声。 His wondering thoughts took wings; he was transported out of the present into that blissful future; he was sitting by Mme. de Restaud’s side, when a sort of sigh, like the grunt of an overburdened St. Joseph, broke the silence of the night.
这个学生觉得它就像是死亡的呻吟，不禁全身颤抖起来。 It vibrated through the student, who took the sound for a death groan.
他轻轻地打开房门，走到楼梯平台，瞥见高老头房门底下的那一线微光。 He opened his door noiselessly, went out upon the landing, and saw a thin streak of light under Father Goriot’s door.
欧仁担心他的邻居生病了，就走了过去，透过钥匙孔朝里面看了看。那位老人正忙着在干活。拉斯蒂涅觉得他干的活非常奇怪，非常可疑，因此他觉得自己必须得看清这个自称是面条制造商的人大晚上在干什么勾当才行。他这可是在为大家服务。 Eugene feared that his neighbor had been taken ill; he went over and looked through the keyhole; the old man was busily engaged in an occupation so singular and so suspicious that Rastignac thought he was only doing a piece of necessary service to society to watch the self-styled vermicelli maker’s nocturnal industries.
高老头把桌子翻了过来，很明显，他在用粗绳子把一套银盘子和银杯子绑起来之前，已经大致把它们固定在桌子的横档上了。他拼命地拉紧绳子，那些杯盘都扭曲变形了。看上去他打算把这精致、贵重的金属绞成银条。 The table was upturned, and Goriot had doubtless in some way secured a silver plate and cup to the bar before knotting a thick rope round them; he was pulling at this rope with such enormous force that they were being crushed and twisted out of shape; to all appearance he meant to convert the richly wrought metal into ingots.
“哟，好家伙！”看着高老头健壮的胳膊，拉斯蒂涅想道。老人在绳子的帮助下，像捏面团一样扭着银器，房间里一点声音也没有。 “@Peste!@ what a man!” said Rastignac, as he watched Goriot’s muscular arms; there was not a sound in the room while the old man, with the aid of the rope, was kneading the silver like dough.
“莫非他其实是个贼，或是窝赃的人，在假装愚笨、老迈，故意过着叫花子的生活，那样也许就可以更安全地进行自己的勾当？” “Was he then, indeed, a thief, or a receiver of stolen goods, who affected imbecility and decrepitude, and lived like a beggar that he might carry on his pursuits the more securely?”
欧仁站了一会，反复考虑着这些问题，然后他又从钥匙孔朝里面看去。 Eugene stood for a moment revolving these questions, then he looked again through the keyhole.
高老头解开了他的那卷绳子，又往桌上盖了条毯子，现在正滚动着一堆碾平的银器，非常利落地把它们搓成了长条状。 Father Goriot had unwound his coil of rope; he had covered the table with a blanket, and was now employed in rolling the flattened mass of silver into a bar, an operation which he performed with marvelous dexterity.
“哇，他一定和波兰国王奥古斯特一样强壮！”银条快完成的时候，欧仁自言自语道。 “Why, he must be as strong as Augustus, King of Poland!” said Eugene to himself when the bar was nearly finished.
高老头伤心地看着自己的作品，眼里流下了泪水，然后吹灭了做银条时照明用的蜡烛，躺到了床上。这时，欧仁听见了他的叹气声。 Father Goriot looked sadly at his handiwork, tears fell from his eyes, he blew out the dip which had served him for a light while he manipulated the silver, and Eugene heard him sigh as he lay down again.
“他疯了。”这个学生想。 “He is mad,” thought the student.
“可怜的孩子！”高老头大声地说道。 “@Poor child!@” Father Goriot said aloud.
拉斯蒂涅听见这话，决定保持沉默。他不会草率地指责自己的邻居。 Rastignac, hearing those words, concluded to keep silence; he would not hastily condemn his neighbor.
他正要回房间，突然听见一个奇怪的声音从下面的楼梯传来。这也许是两个穿布底拖鞋的男人上楼梯的声音。 He was just in the doorway of his room when a strange sound from the staircase below reached his ears; it might have been made by two men coming up in list slippers.
欧仁听了听，果然有两个人在那里，他可以听见他们的呼吸声。 Eugene listened; two men there certainly were, he could hear their breathing.
但是，他并没有听见临街的那扇大门打开的声音，过道里也没有脚步声。 Yet there had been no sound of opening the street door, no footsteps in the passage.
突然，他又看见三楼有微弱的光线从沃尔特兰先生的房里传出。 Suddenly, too, he saw a faint gleam of light on the second story; it came from M. Vautrin’s room.
“这个旅馆里一定有一大堆秘密！”他暗自思忖道。 “There are a good many mysteries here for a lodging-house!” he said to himself.
他往楼下走了走，又听了起来。 He went part of the way downstairs and listened again.
金子的撞击声传到了他的耳朵里。 The rattle of gold reached his ears.
转眼蜡烛就被吹灭了，他又清楚地听见了两个人的呼吸声，但是没有开关门的声音。 In another moment the light was put out, and again he distinctly heard the breathing of two men, but no sound of a door being opened or shut.
那两个男人下了楼。他们越走越远，原本就微弱的声音变得更加微弱了。 The two men went downstairs, the faint sounds growing fainter as they went.
“谁在那里？”沃盖夫人在卧室的窗户大喊。 “Who is there?” cried Mme. Vauquer out of her bedroom window.
“是我，沃盖夫人。”沃尔特兰用低沉的声音答道， “I, Mme. Vauquer,” answered Vautrin’s deep bass voice.
“我正要进来了。” “I am coming in.”
“真奇怪！克里斯托夫明明插了门闩。”欧仁一边朝自己房间走，一边说道。 “That is odd! Christophe drew the bolts,” said Eugene, going back to his room.
“看来在巴黎，如果真想弄清楚周围所发生的一切，就得通宵不睡啊。” “You have to sit up at night, it seems, if you really mean to know all that is going on about you in Paris.”
这些小事将他的思绪从野心勃勃的梦想转移开来。他重新开始用功了，但是思想又思绪了正轨，回到了高老头可疑的行为上；德雷斯多夫人的脸在他的眼前飘来飘去，就像一个美好未来的幻影。最后，他握着拳头躺到床上睡下了。 These incidents turned his thought from his ambitious dreams; he betook himself to his work, but his thought wandered back to Father Goriot’s suspicious occupation; Mme. de Restaud’s face swam again and again before his eyes like a vision of a brilliant future; and at last he lay down and slept with clenched fists.
当一个年轻人下定决心要彻夜学习的时候，十次中有七次会一觉睡到天亮的。 When a young man makes up his mind that he will work all night, the chances are that seven times out of ten he will sleep till morning.
二十岁之前没人会熬夜的。 Such vigils do not begin before we are turned twenty.
第二天早上，巴黎浓雾蔽天，让最守时的人都弄错了时间，甚至连最有条不紊的当地人在这样的天气也无法准时应约，一般人在中午起床后还以为才八点。 The next morning Paris was wrapped in one of the dense fogs that throw the most punctual people out in their calculations as to the time; even the most business-like folk fail to keep their appointments in such weather, and ordinary mortals wake up at noon and fancy it is eight o’clock.
这个早上，都九点半了，沃盖夫人还在睡觉。 On this morning it was half-past nine, and Mme. Vauquer still lay abed.
克里斯托夫起晚了，西尔维也起晚了，但是他们和平常一样舒舒服服地坐在那里喝咖啡。 Christophe was late, Sylvie was late, but the two sat comfortably taking their coffee as usual.
西尔维习惯把牛奶上的乳脂撩起来自己吃。这乳脂本来是要给房客们作早餐的。她把剩下来的牛奶煮上一会儿，这样她的女主人就不会发现她不合规矩的行为了。 It was Sylvie’s custom to take the cream off the milk destined for the boarders’ breakfast for her own, and to boil the remainder for some time, so that madame should not discover this illegal exaction.
“西尔维，你知道吗，”克里斯托夫用一片面包蘸了蘸咖啡，说道，“沃尔特兰先生不是个坏人，可昨晚又有两个人来找他了。 “Sylvie,” said Christophe, as he dipped a piece of toast into the coffee, “M. Vautrin, who is not such a bad sort, all the same, had two people come to see him again last night.
如果夫人问起什么，留神别说漏了嘴。” If madame says anything, mind you say nothing about it.”
“他给了你什么好处吗？” “Has he given you something?”
“他这个月给了我五法朗的赏钱，这就像是在说‘不要声张’一样。”“除了他和库蒂尔夫人，哪个不把一便士掰成两瓣花。过年的时候，这旅馆里其余的每一个人用右手打赏完后，都想用左手把所有的赏钱又拿回来。”西尔维说道。 “He gave me a five-franc piece this month, which is as good as saying, ‘Hold your tongue.’”“Except him and Mme. Couture, who doesn’t look twice at every penny, there’s no one in the house that doesn’t try to get back with the left hand all that they give with the right at New Year,” said Sylvie.
“哼！”克里斯托夫说，“他们到底给了你什么？ “And, after all,” said Christophe, “what do they give you?
区区一个五法朗的硬币。 A miserable five-franc piece.
那个高老头过去的两年都是自己擦鞋子的。 There is Father Goriot, who has cleaned his shoes himself these two years past.
那个老乞丐普瓦雷从来都不用鞋油，他宁可喝掉它，也不愿把它涂在靴子上。 There is that old beggar Poiret, who goes without blacking altogether; he would sooner drink it than put it on his boots.
至于那个妄自尊大的学生，他只给了我两法郎。 Then there is that whipper-snapper of a student, who gives me a couple of francs.
两法郎还不够我买刷子。他卖掉了自己的旧衣服，挣了不少钱，那些衣服才值不了那么多钱呢。 Two francs will not pay for my brushes, and he sells his old clothes, and gets more for them than they are worth.
哼！他们真是一群穷光蛋！” Oh! they’re a shabby lot!”
“呸！”西尔维喝了一小口咖啡，说，“我们的公寓是拉丁区最好的，这我是知道的。 “Pooh!” said Sylvie, sipping her coffee, “our places are the best in the Quarter, that I know.
但是，克里斯托夫，关于沃尔特兰那个大家伙，没人跟你说点什么吗？” But about that great big chap Vautrin, Christophe; has any one told you anything about him?”
“有啊。 “Yes.
几天前我在街上碰到了一位先生，他问我：‘你们旅馆是不是住了一位绅士？一个高个子、染了胡子的先生。’ I met a gentleman in the street a few days ago; he said to me, ‘There’s a gentleman in your place, isn’t there? A tall man that dyes his whiskers?'
我告诉他，‘没有，先生，他们都没有染胡子。 I told him, ‘No, sir; they aren’t dyed.
像他一样寻快活的人才没有这个闲工夫呢。’事后，我告诉沃尔特兰先生这件事的时候，他说，‘伙计，做得对。 A gay fellow like him hasn’t the time to do it.’ And when I told M. Vautrin about it afterwards, he said, ‘Quite right, my boy.
以后就这样回答吧。 That is the way to answer them.
没有比让人知道自己的小缺点更烦心的事了。因为这样会满盘皆输。’”“嗯，我也碰到过。”西尔维说，“上次在菜市场，就有个男人骗我，想知道我有没有见过他穿衬衫。 There is nothing more unpleasant than to have your little weaknesses known; it might spoil many a match.’ “Well, and for my part,” said Sylvie, “a man tried to humbug me at the market wanting to know if I had seen him put on his shirt.
简直是胡说八道！ Such bosh!
哟！”她换了个话题，大叫，“那是恩典谷教堂的钟声，都九点四十五了，还没有一个人动弹！” There,” she cried, interrupting herself, “that’s a quarter to ten striking at the Val-de-Grace, and not a soul stirring!”
“呸！他们都出去了。 “Pooh! they are all gone out.
库蒂尔夫人和女孩八点就到圣艾蒂安教堂领圣体去了。 Mme. Couture and the girl went out at eight o’clock to take the wafer at Saint-Etienne.
高老头拿了只包裹不知道去哪里了，那个学生十点下课后才会回来。 Father Goriot started off somewhere with a parcel, and the student won’t be back from his lecture till ten o’clock.
我打扫楼梯时看见他们走的。我还被高老头撞了一下，他的包裹跟铁一样硬。 I saw them go while I was sweeping the stairs; Father Goriot knocked up against me, and his parcel was as hard as iron.
我还想，这老家伙干嘛去呢？ What is the old fellow up to, I wonder?
其余的人把他当玩具一样，他们从来不会让他消停。但他倒是个好人，比他们所有人加起来都要好。 He is as good as a plaything for the rest of them; they can never let him alone; but he is a good man, all the same, and worth more than all of them put together.
他自己给我的赏钱不多，但有时会让我去给夫人们送信，她们穿得光鲜、亮丽，会给我丰厚的小费。” He doesn’t give you much himself, but he sometimes sends you with a message to ladies who fork out famous tips; they are dressed grandly, too.”
“是他说的那些女儿吗，嗯？ “His daughters, as he calls them, eh?
总共有一打吧。” There are a dozen of them.”
“我只给两位夫人送过信——就是来过这里的那两位。”　 “I have never been to more than two—the two who came here.”
“楼上有动静，夫人醒了，我得走了，要不她又要大声嚷嚷了。 “There is madame moving overhead; I shall have to go, or she will raise a fine racket.
看着牛奶，克里斯托夫，别让猫够着它。” Just keep an eye on the milk, Christophe; don’t let the cat get at it.”
西尔维上楼去了女主人的房里。 Sylvie went up to her mistress’ room.
“西尔维！ “Sylvie!
怎么回事？ How is this?
都快十点了，你还让我睡得像个榛睡鼠似的！ It’s nearly ten o’clock, and you let me sleep like a dormouse!
这样的事情从来没有发生过。” Such a thing has never happened before.”
“全怪这大雾，浓得用刀也劈不开。” “It’s the fog; it is that thick, you could cut it with a knife.”
“那早餐准备得怎么样？” “But how about breakfast?”
“哈！我确信，房客们都吃过了。 “Bah! the boarders are possessed, I’m sure.
他们一大早都出去了，那时一条阳光都还没有呢。” They all cleared out before there was a wink of daylight.”
“别说错了，西尔维，”沃盖夫人反驳道，“要说一线太阳光。” “Do speak properly, Sylvie,” Mme. Vauquer retorted; “say a blink of daylight.”
“哦，好，夫人，您说什么就是什么。 “Ah, well, madame, whichever you please.
不管怎样，您十点可以吃早餐。 Anyhow, you can have breakfast at ten o’clock.
那个米绍诺和普瓦雷还没动静。 La Michonnette and Poiret have neither of them stirred.
楼上就只有他们俩，他们睡得像木头似的。” There are only those two upstairs, and they are sleeping like the logs they are.”
“可是，西尔维，你把他们的名字放在一起讲，好像——”“好像什么？”西尔维突然大笑着说道， “But, Sylvie, you put their names together as if—” “As if what?” said Sylvie, bursting into a guffaw.
“好像这两人是一对。” “The two of them make a pair.”
“西尔维，你说奇不奇怪，昨晚克里斯托夫锁门后，沃尔特兰先生是怎么进门的呢？” “It is a strange thing, isn’t it, Sylvie, how M. Vautrin got in last night after Christophe had bolted the door?”
“一点也不奇怪，夫人。 “Not at all, madame.
克里斯托夫听见沃尔特兰先生回来了，就下去给他开门了。 Christophe heard M. Vautrin, and went down and undid the door.
您是在想——？” And here are you imagining that—?”
“把我的紧身胸衣给我，然后快去做好早饭。 “Give me my bodice, and be quick and get breakfast ready.
在剩下的羊肉里加些土豆，饭后甜点可以做水煮梨，选那些一便士五个的梨。” Dish up the rest of the mutton with the potatoes, and you can put the stewed pears on the table, those at five a penny.”
过了一会儿，沃盖夫人下来了，刚好看见猫掀翻了盖着牛奶碗的碟子，开始急匆匆地舔着里面的牛奶。 A few moments later Mme. Vauquer came down, just in time to see the cat knock down a plate that covered a bowl of milk, and begin to lap in all haste.
“你这只小丑！”她大叫起来。 “Mistigris!” she cried.
猫逃走了，但马上又跑回来，在她的脚踝旁蹭来蹭去。 The cat fled, but promptly returned to rub against her ankles.
“好！好，你会拍马屁，你这只老畜生，伪君子！”她说， “Oh! yes, you can wheedle, you old hypocrite!” she said.
“西尔维！西尔维！” “Sylvie!Sylvie!”
“是的，夫人，什么事啊？” “Yes, madame; what is it?”
“看看猫做了什么！” “Just see what the cat has done!”
“这全怪蠢货克里斯托夫。 “It is all that stupid Christophe’s fault.
我早叫他放下手中的活，先把桌子摆好了。 I told him to stop and lay the table.
他到底去干嘛了？” What has become of him?”
“别担心，夫人，这牛奶可以给高老头喝。 “Don’t you worry, madame; Father Goriot shall have it.
我会在里面添点水，他不会觉察到差别的。他从不会注意到任何事情，连他吃的东西也不会注意的。” I will fill it up with water, and he won’t know the difference; he never notices anything, not even what he eats.”
“我在想，这老怪物可以去哪里呢？”沃盖夫人一边把盘子摆到桌子上，一边问道。 “I wonder where the old heathen can have gone?” said Mme. Vauquer, setting the plates round the table.
“谁知道啊？ “Who knows?
他可是擅长各种各样骗人的把戏啊。” He is up to all sorts of tricks.”
“我睡过头了。”沃盖夫人说。 “I have overslept myself,” said Mme. Vauquer.
“但是，夫人，您看起来仍然像玫瑰一样容光焕发啊。” “But madame looks as fresh as a rose, all the same.”
就在这时，门铃响了，沃尔特兰大声地唱着歌，走进了客厅：“世界各地都流传着同一个古老的故事，四处流浪的心灵，飘忽不定的目光。”“哦！沃盖妈妈！早上好啊！”他一看见女房东，立刻大声喊起来，还高兴地用胳膊搂着她的腰。 The door bell rang at that moment, and Vautrin came through the sitting-room, singing loudly: “’Tis the same old story everywhere, a roving heart and a roving glance.“Oh! Mamma Vauquer! good-morning!” he cried at the sight of his hostess, and he put his arm gaily round her waist.
“行了！快放手——”“快喊‘非礼啊！’”他回到道，“快啊，快喊啊！现在，您不就正是那个意思吗？歇一会儿吧，我来帮您摆桌子。啊哈！我是个好人，是吧？”“为了褐发和金发的姑娘啊，一个叹气的爱人啊……”“哦！我刚才看见了一件特别有趣的事——全是偶然看见的。” “There! have done—”“‘Impertinence!’ Say it!” he answered.“Come, say it!Now, isn’t that what you really mean?Stop a bit, I will help you to set the table.Ah! I am a nice man, am I not?”“For the locks of brown and the golden hair a sighing lover...”“Oh! I have just seen something so funny—…Led by chance.”
“什么事？”这位寡妇问道。 “What?” asked the widow.
“今天早上八点半，我看见高老头在多菲内街的那家金铺里。 “Father Goriot in the goldsmith’s shop in the Rue Dauphine at half-past eight this morning.
那里是收旧汤勺、旧叉子和旧金线花边的地方。高老头卖了一块银子，价钱很好。 They buy old spoons and forks and gold lace there, and Goriot sold a piece of silver plate for a good round sum.
对于一个不擅长这门手艺的人来说，他绞出来的银条还真不错呢。” It had been twisted out of shape very neatly for a man that’s not used to the trade.”
“真的吗？ “Really?
你该不会是编的吧？” You don’t say so?”
“是真的。我有一个朋友要移居国外，我去送他上了皇家邮轮后才回来。后来，我看见了高老头，就瞧了瞧他在干什么。这是一桩好笑的事。 “Yes.One of my friends is expatriating himself; I had been to see him off on board the Royal Mail steamer, and was coming back here. I waited after that to see what Father Goriot would do; it is a comical affair.
他回到了拉丁区的格雷斯街上，进了一个放高利贷的人家。人人都知道戈布塞克，他是个自高自大的流氓，愿意用自己父亲的骨头做多米诺骨牌，简直是个土耳其人、异教徒、老犹太人、希腊人。从他手里抢钱是件难事，因为他把自己所有的钱都放进了银行。” He came back to this quarter of the world, to the Rue des Gres, and went into a money-lender’s house; everybody knows him, Gobseck, a stuck-up rascal, that would make dominoes out of his father’s bones, a Turk, a heathen, an old Jew, a Greek; it would be a difficult matter to rob @him@, for he puts all his coin into the Bank.”
“那么，高老头到底在那里干什么？” “Then what was Father Goriot doing there?”
“干什么？”沃尔特兰说， “Doing?” said Vautrin.
“能干什么，不就是吃尽自己的家当嘛！ “Nothing; he was bent on his own undoing.
他就是个傻子，傻到倾家荡产去追——”“他来了！”西尔维叫道。 He is a simpleton, stupid enough to ruin himself by running after—” “There he is!” cried Sylvie.
“克里斯托夫，”高老头喊道，“跟我到楼上来。” “Christophe,” cried Father Goriot’s voice, “come upstairs with me.”
克里斯托夫上了楼，很快就又下来了。 Christophe went up, and shortly afterwards came down again.
“你要去哪里？”沃盖夫人问自己的仆人。 “Where are you going?” Mme. Vauquer asked of her servant.
“出去给高里奥先生送信。” “Out on an errand for M. Goriot.”
“什么信啊？”沃尔特兰说着，一把夺过了克里斯托夫手中的信。 “What may that be?” said Vautrin, pouncing on a letter in Christophe’s hand.
“阿纳斯塔谢·德雷斯多伯爵夫人。”他念道。 “@Mme. la Comtesse Anastasie de Restaud@,” he read.
“你要把信送到哪里？”他把信还给了克里斯托夫，接着问道。 “Where are you going with it?” he added, as he gave the letter back to Christophe.
“送到埃尔德街。 “To the Rue du Helder.
他吩咐我一定要把信亲手交到伯爵夫人的手里。” I have orders to give this into her hands myself.”
“信里面有什么呢？”沃尔特兰把信举到灯下，说道。 “What is there inside it?” said Vautrin, holding the letter up to the light.
“一张钞票？不是的。”他凝视着信封。 “A banknote?No.”He peered into the envelope.
“一张债务清讫的收条！”他大叫， “A receipted account!” he cried.
“不错啊，这老糊涂是真讲义气啊！ “My word! ’tis a gallant old dotard.
老伙计，你去送信吧。”他伸出手放到克里斯托夫的头上，把他的身体像顶针一样转了转说，“你又可以挣好多小费了。” Off with you, old chap,” he said, bringing down a hand on Christophe’s head, and spinning the man round like a thimble; “you will have a famous tip.”
这时，桌子摆好了。 By this time the table was set.
西尔维正在煮牛奶。沃盖夫人在给炉子点火，沃尔特兰在一旁帮忙，还不停地哼着：“世界各地都流传着同一个古老的故事，四处流浪的心灵，飘忽不定的目光。” Sylvie was boiling the milk, Mme. Vauquer was lighting a fire in the stove with some assistance from Vautrin, who kept humming to himself: “The same old story everywhere, a roving heart and a roving glance.”
当一切准备妥当，库蒂尔夫人和塔耶费小姐回来了。 When everything was ready, Mme. Couture and Mlle. Taillefer came in.
“漂亮的女士，您今天早上去哪里了啊？”沃盖夫人转向库蒂尔夫人，问道。 “Where have you been this morning, fair lady?” said Mme. Vauquer, turning to Mme. Couture.
“我们刚刚去山上的圣艾蒂安教堂祷告去了。 “We have just been to say our prayers at Saint-Etienne du Mont.
今天是我们必须去看塔耶费先生的日子。 To-day is the day when we must go to see M. Taillefer.
可怜的小东西！ Poor little thing!
她正像树叶一样颤抖着呢。”库蒂尔夫人坐到火炉的前面，把湿热的靴底拿到火苗前，继续说着。 She is trembling like a leaf,” Mme. Couture went on, as she seated herself before the fire and held the steaming soles of her boots to the blaze.
“维多琳，过来烤火吧。”沃盖夫人说道。 “Warm yourself, Victorine,” said Mme. Vauquer.
“小姐，祈祷上帝让你父亲的心肠变软很正确、很恰当。”沃尔特兰拉了拉椅子，坐得离这个孤儿更近了些，说道，“但是那是不够的。 “It is quite right and proper, mademoiselle, to pray to Heaven to soften your father’s heart,” said Vautrin, as he drew a chair nearer to the orphan girl; “but that is not enough.
你需要的是一个可以让那个怪物清醒清醒的朋友。一个有三百万的野蛮人（他们是这么说的）居然不给你嫁妆。现在的漂亮女孩是需要嫁妆的。” What you want is a friend who will give the monster a piece of his mind; a barbarian that has three millions (so they say), and will not give you a dowry; and a pretty girl needs a dowry nowadays.”
“可怜的孩子！”沃盖夫人说， “Poor child!” said Mme. Vauquer.
“别担心，我的甜心，你那卑鄙可耻的父亲将来一定会自食其果、遭到报应的。” “Never mind, my pet, your wretch of a father is going just the way to bring trouble upon himself.”
听了这一番话，维多琳的眼中含满了泪水。这位寡妇看见库蒂尔夫人对她摆了摆手，就不作声了。 Victorine’s eyes filled with tears at the words, and the widow checked herself at a sign from Mme. Couture.
“只要我们能见到他就行了！”这位总军需官的遗孀说道，“只要我能跟他说上话，能把他妻子的遗书交给他就行了！ “If we could only see him!” said the Commissary-General’s widow; “if I could speak to him myself and give him his wife’s last letter!
我从来不敢冒险把信寄给他，他认得我的字迹——”“‘哦，女人，你们总是备受迫害、委屈而又无辜！’”沃尔特兰打断了她的话，大声嚷起来， I have never dared to run the risk of sending it by post; he knew my handwriting—” “‘Oh woman, persecuted and injured innocent!’” exclaimed Vautrin, breaking in upon her.
“所以，你们现在就落得这般田地，是吗？ “So that is how you are, is it?
过几天我来处理你们的事情，这件事肯定会有一个完满的结局。你们等着瞧吧。” In a few days’ time I will look into your affairs, and it will be all right, you shall see.”
“哦，先生，”维多琳含着泪水，热切地看了一眼沃尔特兰，但是沃尔特兰却没有表现出被她所感动的迹象，“如果您知道任何和我父亲联络的办法，请一定要告诉他，他的爱和我母亲的名誉对我而言比世上所有的财富都要珍贵。 “Oh! sir,” said Victorine, with a tearful but eager glance at Vautrin, who showed no sign of being touched by it, “if you know of any way of communicating with my father, please be sure and tell him that his affection and my mother’s honor are more to me than all the money in the world.
如果您能让他对我稍微好些，我会在上帝面前为您祷告的。 If you can induce him to relent a little towards me, I will pray to God for you.
您可以确信，我会对您感激不尽的——”“世界各地流传着同一个古老的故事。”沃尔特兰用讽刺的声调唱着。 You may be sure of my gratitude—”“@The same old story everywhere@,” sang Vautrin, with a satirical intonation.
就在这个时候，高老头、米绍诺小姐和普瓦雷一起下楼了。西尔维正在做肉汤，准备用它来配羊肉。也许是肉汤的味道宣告了早餐时间的到来。 At this juncture, Goriot, Mlle. Michonneau, and Poiret came downstairs together; possibly the scent of the gravy which Sylvie was making to serve with the mutton had announced breakfast.
七个人就这样聚到了一起，大家互相问早安，然后坐到了桌旁。时针指向了十点，学生的脚步声从外面传来。 The seven people thus assembled bade each other good-morning, and took their places at the table; the clock struck ten, and the student’s footstep was heard outside.
“啊，你回来了，欧仁先生。”西尔维说，“今天每个人都在家吃早饭啊。” “Ah! here you are, M. Eugene,” said Sylvie; “every one is breakfasting at home to-day.”
学生和其他房客互问了早上好，然后坐到了高老头的旁边。 The student exchanged greetings with the lodgers, and sat down beside Goriot.
“我刚刚有了奇遇。”他说着夹了好多羊肉，还切了一片面包。沃盖夫人像往常一样目测着他吃了多少东西。 “I have just met with a queer adventure,” he said, as he helped himself abundantly to the mutton, and cut a slice of bread, which Mme. Vauquer’s eyes gauged as usual.
“奇遇？”普瓦雷质疑道。 “An adventure?” queried Poiret.
“哎！你大惊小怪干嘛，老家伙？” “Well, and what is there to astonish you in that, old boy?”
沃尔特兰对普瓦雷说， Vautrin asked of Poiret.
“欧仁先生总会碰到那种事情。” “M. Eugene is cut out for that kind of thing.”
塔耶费小姐怯生生地偷看了这个年轻学生一眼。 Mlle. Taillefer stole a timid glance at the young student.
“跟我们讲讲你的奇遇！”沃尔特兰先生要求道。 “Tell us about your adventure!” demanded M. Vautrin.
“昨晚，我去参加我表姐德伯桑子爵夫人举办的舞会了。 “Yesterday evening I went to a ball given by a cousin of mine, the Vicomtesse de Beauseant.
她有一所华丽的房子，房间里都挂满了绫罗绸缎——简而言之，昨晚的舞会太棒了，我特别开心，简直像个国王——”“像个翠鸟。”沃尔特兰打断了他。（注：英语中“国王”是king，而“翠鸟”是kingfisher；此处沃尔特兰故意在king之后接上fisher，把“国王”变成了“翠鸟”，是在开玩笑。） She has a magnificent house; the rooms are hung with silk—in short, it was a splendid affair, and I was as happy as a king—” “Fisher,” put in Vautrin, interrupting.
“您这是什么意思，先生？”欧仁气恼地问。 “What do you mean, sir?” said Eugene sharply.
“我说‘翠鸟’是因为翠鸟比国王要快活得多。” “I said ‘fisher,’ because kingfishers see a good deal more fun than kings.”
“很正确，我宁愿当一只无忧无虑的小鸟，也不愿意当国王。”应声虫普瓦雷说，“因为——”“实际上，”这个法律系学生很快打断了他，“我和房里最美的女士跳了舞。她是一位迷人的伯爵夫人，是我见过的最高雅的人。 “Quite true; I would much rather be the little careless bird than a king,” said Poiret the ditto-ist, “because—”“In fact”—the law-student cut him short—“I danced with one of the handsomest women in the room, a charming countess, the most exquisite creature I have ever seen.
她头上戴着桃花编织的花环，那是最漂亮的花束——都是真花，空气中弥漫着花香——行了！无需费力去描述一个翩翩起舞、容光焕发的女士。 There was peach blossom in her hair, and she had the loveliest bouquet of flowers—real flowers, that scented the air—but there! it is no use trying to describe a woman glowing with the dance.
你们得亲眼看她才行！ You ought to have seen her!
嗯，今天早上大约九点钟的时候，我正在格雷斯街上走着，碰到了这位美丽脱俗的伯爵夫人。 Well, and this morning I met this divine countess about nine o’clock, on foot in the Rue de Gres.
哦！我的心跳得好快啊！ Oh! how my heart beat!
我开始以为——”“以为她会来这里。”沃尔特兰热切地注视着这位学生说， I began to think—” “That she was coming here,” said Vautrin, with a keen look at the student.
“我预计她是去拜访放高利贷的戈布塞克。 “I expect that she was going to call on old Gobseck, a money-lender.
如果你曾经研究过巴黎女人的内心，就会发现她们把放高利贷的人放在第一位，其后才是情人。 If ever you explore a Parisian woman’s heart, you will find the money-lender first, and the lover afterwards.
你的伯爵夫人叫做阿纳斯塔谢·德雷斯多，住在埃尔德街。” Your countess is called Anastasie de Restaud, and she lives in the Rue du Helder.”
学生死死地盯着沃尔特兰。 The student stared hard at Vautrin.
听到这些话，高老头抬起了头，瞟了他们俩一眼，眼神中充满了机智与不安，这让房客们都惊讶地看着他。 Father Goriot raised his head at the words, and gave the two speakers a glance so full of intelligence and uneasiness that the lodgers beheld him with astonishment.
“克里斯托夫去得太晚了，她一定是去他那里了！”高老头用痛苦的声音大叫。 “Then Christophe was too late, and she must have gone to him!” cried Goriot, with anguish in his voice.
“果然不出我所料。”沃尔特兰凑到沃盖夫人的耳边小声说道。 “It is just as I guessed,” said Vautrin, leaning over to whisper in Mme. Vauquer’s ear.
高老头继续吃早餐，但是早餐在他看来味如嚼蜡。 Goriot went on with his breakfast, but seemed unconscious of what he was doing.
他从来没有像当时看起来那么傻、那么心不在焉过。 He had never looked more stupid nor more taken up with his own thoughts than he did at that moment.
“沃尔特兰先生，到底是谁告诉你她的名字的？”欧仁问。 “Who the devil could have told you her name, M. Vautrin?” asked Eugene.
“啊哈！你终于问到这个问题了！”沃尔特兰答道， “Aha! there you are!” answered Vautrin.
“坐在那里的高老头知道得非常清楚。 “Old Father Goriot there knew it quite well!
为什么我就不应该知道呢？” And why should I not know it too?”
“高老头？”学生大叫。 “M. Goriot?” the student cried.
“什么？”老人问， “What is it?” asked the old man.
“她昨晚非常漂亮，是吧？” “So she was very beautiful, was she, yesterday night?”
“谁？” “Who?”
“德雷斯多夫人。” “Mme. de Restaud.”
“瞧那老混蛋，”沃盖夫人对沃尔特兰说，“他的眼睛多亮啊！” “Look at the old wretch,” said Mme. Vauquer, speaking to Vautrin; “how his eyes light up!”
“他真的养着那个女人吗？”米绍诺小姐悄声对学生说。 “Then does he really keep her?” said Mlle. Michonneau, in a whisper to the student.
“哦，对，她非常漂亮。”欧仁答道。 “Oh! yes, she was tremendously pretty,” Eugene answered.
高老头用渴望的眼神看着他。 Father Goriot watched him with eager eyes.
“如果德伯桑夫人不在那里，我神圣的伯爵夫人肯定是舞会皇后了。年轻人都只盯着她看。 “If Mme. de Beauseant had not been there, my divine countess would have been the queen of the ball; none of the younger men had eyes for any one else.
我在她的舞伴名单上排第十二位，每次方阵舞她都跳。 I was the twelfth on her list, and she danced every quadrille.
其他的女人都气坏了。 The other women were furious.
如果有女人高兴的话，那她一定是最高兴的！ She must have enjoyed herself, if ever creature did!
常言道：天下之美，莫过于满帆前行的军舰、纵横驰骋的骏马或翩翩起舞的女郎。” It is a true saying that there is no more beautiful sight than a frigate in full sail, a galloping horse, or a woman dancing.”
“事情就是这样发展的。”沃尔特兰说，“昨晚还在公爵夫人的舞会上，今早就在放高利贷的人的办公室里，跑到了社会的最底层——真是个巴黎女人啊！ “So the wheel turns,” said Vautrin; “yesterday night at a duchess’ ball, this morning in a money-lender’s office, on the lowest rung of the ladder—just like a Parisienne!
如果她们的丈夫不能负担她们的挥霍无度，她们就会出卖自己。 If their husbands cannot afford to pay for their frantic extravagance, they will sell themselves.
或者如果不能那样做，她们就会撕开自己母亲的心，去找出点什么来支付自己奢华的生活。 Or if they cannot do that, they will tear out their mothers’ hearts to find something to pay for their splendor.
她们会把世界颠倒过来的。 They will turn the world upside down.
简直是个彻彻底底的巴黎女人！” Just a Parisienne through and through!”
听见学生的话，高老头的脸绽放出了光芒，就像晴天的太阳，但是听到沃尔特兰恶毒的评论，他的脸立刻阴了下来。 Father Goriot’s face, which had shone at the student’s words like the sun on a bright day, clouded over all at once at this cruel speech of Vautrin’s.
“喂，”沃盖夫人说，“你的奇遇是在哪里发生的啊？ “Well,” said Mme. Vauquer, “but where is your adventure?
你有没有跟她讲过话？ Did you speak to her?
你有没有问她要不要学法律？” Did you ask her if she wanted to study law?”
“她没有看见我，”欧仁说， “She did not see me,” said Eugene.
“但是想想看，九点钟在格雷斯街碰到巴黎最美的女人之一！ “But only think of meeting one of the prettiest women in Paris in the Rue des Gres at nine o’clock!
可是她参加完舞会，回到家时最少也是凌晨两点了。 She could not have reached home after the ball till two o’clock this morning.
这不奇怪吗？ Wasn’t it queer?
只有在巴黎才能有这等奇遇啊。” There is no place like Paris for this sort of adventures.”
“哼！这里发生的事比那要有趣的多呢！”沃尔特兰大声嚷嚷道。 “Pshaw! much funnier things than @that@ happen here!” exclaimed Vautrin.
塔耶费小姐几乎没有留意他们的谈话，她全神贯注地想着自己即将进行的新尝试。 Mlle. Taillefer had scarcely heeded the talk, she was so absorbed by the thought of the new attempt that she was about to make.
库蒂尔夫人给她递了个眼神，示意她是时候上楼换衣服了。她俩一出门，高老头也跟着走了。 Mme. Couture made a sign that it was time to go upstairs and dress; the two ladies went out, and Father Goriot followed their example.
“哎，你们瞧见没有？”沃盖夫人对沃尔特兰和桌子周围的其他人说， “Well, did you see?” said Mme. Vauquer, addressing Vautrin and the rest of the circle.
“多明显啊，他正为了那些婆娘要把自己弄得倾家荡产呢。” “He is ruining himself for those women, that is plain.”
“我绝不相信美丽的德雷斯多伯爵夫人是高老头的情妇。”学生大叫道。 “Nothing will ever make me believe that that beautiful Comtesse de Restaud is anything to Father Goriot,” cried the student.
“好吧，如果你不信，就不信吧。”沃尔特兰插话说，“我们也没说一定要你相信。 “Well, and if you don’t,” broke in Vautrin, “we are not set on convincing you.
你太年轻了，还不完全了解巴黎。以后你会发现自己就是我们所说的痴情汉了——”米绍诺小姐听见这些话，飞快地瞟了沃尔特兰一眼。 You are too young to know Paris thoroughly yet; later on you will find out that there are what we call men with a passion—”Mlle. Michonneau gave Vautrin a quick glance at these words.
他们的反应看上去就像是骑兵的马听见了号角声一样。 They seemed to be like the sound of a trumpet to a trooper’s horse.
“啊哈！”沃尔特兰停了下来，仔细地扫了她一眼说，“所以说我们都有些小小的经历，是吧？” “Aha!” said Vautrin, stopping in his speech to give her a searching glance, “so we have had our little experiences, have we?”
这位老处女低下了眼睛，就像看见人体雕像的修女一样。 The old maid lowered her eyes like a nun who sees a statue.
“唔，”他继续说，“一旦那种人的脑袋里有了一种念头，他们就无法摒弃它了。 “Well,” he went on, “when folk of that kind get a notion into their heads, they cannot drop it.
他们一定要从某个特定的泉眼汲水喝——那些泉眼一般都是死水一潭。但是，他们为了得到它，不惜出卖妻子和家人，或者把自己的灵魂出卖给魔鬼。 They must drink the water from some particular spring—it is stagnant as often as not; but they will sell their wives and families, they will sell their own souls to the devil to get it.
对有的人来说，这口泉眼是玩乐，或是证交所，或是音乐，或是画集，或是昆虫标本集。对其他人来说，这口泉眼是某个做得一手令他们称心如意的好菜的女人。 For some this spring is play, or the stock-exchange, or music, or a collection of pictures or insects; for others it is some woman who can give them the dainties they like.
就算你把世上所有的女人都给后一种人，他们也会不屑一顾。他们只会要那个能够满足自己欲望的女人。 You might offer these last all the women on earth—they would turn up their noses; they will have the only one who can gratify their passion.
女人常常会无视他们，残忍地对待他们。他们花大把的钱给自己买来一点点的满足。但是，无论如何，那些傻瓜都不会厌倦，他们会典当自己最后的一张毯子换回五法朗硬币给她。 It often happens that the woman does not care for them at all, and treats them cruelly; they buy their morsels of satisfaction very dear; but no matter, the fools are never tired of it; they will take their last blanket to the pawnbroker’s to give their last five-franc piece to her.
这里的高老头就是那种人。 Father Goriot here is one of that sort.
他生活朴素，因此伯爵夫人能够从他身上榨取钱财——这正是玩乐世界的运转方式。 He is discreet, so the Countess exploits him—just the way of the gay world.
可怜的老家伙只想着她，别的什么都不想。 The poor old fellow thinks of her and of nothing else.
从其他各个方面来看，你会认为他是个愚蠢的畜生。但是，一跟他提到那个话题，他的眼睛就像钻石般闪亮。 In all other respects you see he is a stupid animal; but get him on that subject, and his eyes sparkle like diamonds.
那个秘密不难猜到。 That secret is not difficult to guess.
今天早上，他带了些银器去匠铺熔掉了，然后我看见他去了格雷斯街上的戈布塞克老爹家。 He took some plate himself this morning to the melting-pot, and I saw him at Daddy Gobseck’s in the Rue des Gres.
现在，看看接下来发生了什么——他回到这里，叫克里斯托夫给德雷斯多伯爵夫人送了封信，那个笨蛋克里斯托夫给我们看了地址。信里面还有张债务清讫的收条。 And now, mark what follows—he came back here, and gave a letter for the Comtesse de Restaud to that noodle of a Christophe, who showed us the address; there was a receipted bill inside it.
如果伯爵夫人亲自去放高利贷人的家里，显而易见这是件紧急的事情。 It is clear that it was an urgent matter if the Countess also went herself to the old money lender.
高老头慷慨地资助她。 Father Goriot has financed her handsomely.
没有必要把事情串联起来，事情已经不证自明了。 There is no need to tack a tale together; the thing is self-evident.
所以，学生先生，这一切告诉你，当你的伯爵夫人提着裙角嬉笑、跳舞、卖弄风情、摇晃着她戴着桃花花环的脑袋时，她就像俗语说的那样，是大脚套在小鞋里,难受着呢，她正想着自己或者她的情人的到期偿还不了的借票该怎么办呢。” So that shows you, sir student, that all the time your Countess was smiling, dancing, flirting, swaying her peach-flower crowned head, with her gown gathered into her hand, her slippers were pinching her, as they say; she was thinking of her protested bills, or her lover’s protested bills.”
“你这么一说，我还非得把事实弄清楚不可。”欧仁大声说道，“我明天就去拜访德雷斯多夫人。” “You have made me wild to know the truth,” cried Eugene; “I will go to call on Mme. de Restaud to-morrow.”
“好啊，”普瓦雷应声道，“你是得去拜访德雷斯多夫人啊。” “Yes,” echoed Poiret; “you must go and call on Mme. de Restaud.”
“说不定你还能在那里碰到高老头呢，他客气地为她提供了帮助，肯定会有所回报的。” “And perhaps you will find Father Goriot there, who will take payment for the assistance he politely rendered.”
欧仁不胜厌恶地说： Eugene looked disgusted.
“那么你们的巴黎是个烂泥潭了哦。” “Why, then, this Paris of yours is a slough.”
“而且也是个不同寻常的古怪泥潭。”沃尔特兰答道， “And an uncommonly queer slough, too,” replied Vautrin.
“要是你驾着马车经过时溅上泥——你就是个备受尊敬的人；要是你步行时溅上泥——那么你就是个无赖。 “The mud splashes you as you drive through it in your carriage—you are a respectable person; you go afoot and are splashed—you are a scoundrel.
如果你不幸顺手拿走某件属于别人的东西，他们就会把你拉到法院广场去展览，让大家把你当戏看；如果你偷了一百万，你却会成为各个社交沙龙中谈论的道德楷模。 You are so unlucky as to walk off with something or other belonging to somebody else, and they exhibit you as a curiosity in the Place du Palais-de-Justice; you steal a million, and you are pointed out in every salon as a model of virtue.
而你要付三千万给警察和法院来维持法律和秩序！ And you pay thirty millions for the police and the courts of justice, for the maintenance of law and order!
这是多么妙的事啊！” A pretty slate of things it is!”
“什么，”沃盖夫人大叫，“高老头有没有溶了他的银质牛乳酒盘子？” “What,” cried Mme. Vauquer, “has Father Goriot really melted down his silver posset-dish?”
“盘罩上画着两只斑鸠，是吗？”欧仁问道。 “There were two turtle-doves on the lid, were there not?” asked Eugene.
“是啊，是有。” “Yes, that there were.”
“他很喜欢它吗？”欧仁说， “Then, was he fond of it?” said Eugene.
“他打碎杯碟的时候哭了。 “He cried while he was breaking up the cup and plate.
我碰巧看见了。” I happened to see him by accident.”
“那只盘子对他而言和他自己的生命一样珍贵。”寡妇答道。 “It was dear to him as his own life,” answered the widow.
“现在，你们知道那老家伙有多痴迷了吧！”沃尔特兰大声说， “There! you see how infatuated the old fellow is!” cried Vautrin.
“那个女人能叫人迷失心智，失去自我。”学生上楼去了自己的房间。 “The woman yonder can coax the soul out of him.” The student went up to his room.
沃尔特兰出去了，过了一会儿，库蒂尔夫人和维多琳也乘着西尔维替她们叫的出租马车离开了。 Vautrin went out, and a few moments later Mme. Couture and Victorine drove away in a cab which Sylvie had called for them.
普瓦雷扶着米绍诺小姐，他们一起去植物园度过这一天中阳光最灿烂的两个小时。 Poiret gave his arm to Mlle. Michonneau, and they went together to spend the two sunniest hours of the day in the Jardin des Plantes.
“哎呦，这两人就像结了婚似的。”胖子西尔维评价道， “Well, those two are as good as married,” was the portly Sylvie’s comment.
“他们今天第一次一起出去。 “They are going out together to-day for the first time.
他们是两根干棍子，如果不小心碰到了一起，一定会擦出火花的，就像打火石碰到钢片似的。” They are such a couple of dry sticks that if they happen to strike against each other they will draw sparks like flint and steel.”
“米绍诺小姐得小心自己的披肩了。”沃盖夫人笑着说，“它可是像火绒一样很容易燃烧起来啊。” “Keep clear of Mlle. Michonneau’s shawl, then,” said Mme. Vauquer, laughing; “it would flare up like tinder.”
那天傍晚四点钟的时候，高老头回来了。借着两只冒烟的油灯发出的光，他看到维多琳的眼睛红红的。 At four o’clock that evening, when Goriot came in, he saw, by the light of two smoky lamps, that Victorine’s eyes were red.
沃盖夫人正听她们讲着早上拜访塔耶费先生的情形。她们这次依然无功而返。 Mme. Vauquer was listening to the history of the visit made that morning to M. Taillefer; it had been made in vain.
塔耶费先生厌倦了女儿和他年长的朋友每年的拜访。他终于答应见她们，想要和她们说清楚。 Taillefer was tired of the annual application made by his daughter and her elderly friend; he gave them a personal interview in order to arrive at an understanding with them.
“我亲爱的女士，”库蒂尔夫人对沃盖夫人说，“您想想看，他甚至没有要维多琳坐下，她一直从头站到尾。他非常冷酷、不带一丝感情地叫我们不要去那里自找麻烦。他还说这位年轻的女士（他不会称她为女儿）跑来纠缠他（纠缠！每年就一次，这个卑鄙小人！）只会适得其反，让他越来越讨厌她。因为维多琳的母亲嫁给他时一无所有，所以她也别指望从他这里得到任何东西。实际上，他说了最残酷的话，让这个可怜的孩子嚎啕大哭。 “My dear lady,” said Mme. Couture, addressing Mme. Vauquer, “just imagine it; he did not even ask Victorine to sit down, she was standing the whole time. he said to me quite coolly, without putting himself in a passion, that we might spare ourselves the trouble of going there; that the young lady (he would not call her his daughter) was injuring her cause by importuning him (@importuning!@ once a year, the wretch!); that as Victorine’s mother had nothing when he married her, Victorine ought not to expect anything from him; in fact, he said the most cruel things, that made the poor child burst out crying.
这小东西扑到父亲的脚下，勇敢地大声说道，她坚持拜访他只是为了自己的母亲。她愿意毫无怨言地顺从他，但是她乞求他读一读自己可怜的亡母的遗书。 The little thing threw herself at her father’s feet and spoke up bravely; she said that she only persevered in her visits for her mother’s sake; that she would obey him without a murmur, but that she begged him to read her poor dead mother’s farewell letter.
她拿起信递给了他，用最美的方式说着世上最美的话。我不知道她是在哪里学会这些的，一定是上帝把它们放进她的脑海里的，因为这个可怜的孩子突发灵感，说出了如此优美的话。听了她的话，我像个傻瓜一样大哭起来。 She took it up and gave it to him, saying the most beautiful things in the world, most beautifully expressed; I do not know where she learned them; God must have put them into her head, for the poor child was inspired to speak so nicely that it made me cry like a fool to hear her talk.
可你知道那个怪物那时候在干什么吗？ And what do you think the monster was doing all the time?
他在剪指甲！ Cutting his nails!
他拿起那封浸透塔耶费夫人眼泪的信，扔到了壁炉架上。 He took the letter that poor Mme. Taillefer had soaked with tears, and flung it on to the chimney-piece.
‘好吧。’他说。 ‘That is all right,’ he said.
他伸手想扶起自己的女儿，但是她亲吻起父亲的手来，于是他又把手缩回去了。 He held out his hands to raise his daughter, but she covered them with kisses, and he drew them away again.
真可耻，不是吗？ Scandalous, isn’t it?
他的傻儿子进来后，对他的妹妹理都不理。” And his great booby of a son came in and took no notice of his sister.”
“他们是多么冷酷无情的卑鄙小人啊！”高老头说。 “What inhuman wretches they must be!” said Father Goriot.
库蒂尔夫人没有注意到那位可敬的面条制造商的慨叹，接着说：“父子俩向我鞠躬，说他们有急事得离开，要我谅解他们！然后他们都走出了房间。 “And then they both went out of the room,” Mme. Couture went on, without heeding the worthy vermicelli maker’s exclamation; “father and son bowed to me, and asked me to excuse them on account of urgent business!
这就是我们今天拜访的经过。 That is the history of our call.
嗯，他至少已经见过自己的女儿了。 Well, he has seen his daughter at any rate.
我想不明白他怎么能拒绝承认自己的女儿，他们俩长得一模一样，就像两颗豌豆一样。” How he can refuse to acknowledge her I cannot think, for they are as alike as two peas.”
房客们一个接一个地进来了，他们互相问好，说些无聊的笑话。在巴黎的某些阶层中，这些笑话被认为是幽默、诙谐的。 The boarders dropped in one after another, interchanging greetings and empty jokes that certain classes of Parisians regard as humorous and witty.
他们的笑话大部分内容都很枯燥，笑点就是故意说错一个单词或是打个特定的手势。 Dulness is their prevailing ingredient, and the whole point consists in mispronouncing a word or a gesture.
这种“行话”总是在变化。 This kind of argot is always changing.
笑话的精髓在于某个政治事件引发的流行语、一个发生在治安法庭的小事件、一首街头歌曲或一小段在某个剧院上演的滑稽戏，它们一个月后就会被忘得一干二净。 The essence of the jest consists in some catchword suggested by a political event, an incident in the police courts, a street song, or a bit of burlesque at some theatre, and forgotten in a month.
一切事情的作用都是维持一场语言和思想的羽毛球赛。 Anything and everything serves to keep up a game of battledore and shuttlecock with words and ideas.
透视画是最近的发明，比起全景画来，它可以把视错觉使用得更为到位。透视画让艺术系的学生狂热地将每个词都以拉玛结尾（注：英语中“透视画”的词尾读音为“拉玛”）。 The diorama, a recent invention, which carried an optical illusion a degree further than panoramas, had given rise to a mania among art students for ending every word with RAMA.
“沃盖之家”从房客中的一个年轻艺术家那里感染了这种思想。 The Maison Vauquer had caught the infection from a young artist among the boarders.
“喂，普瓦雷先生儿，”博物馆员工说，“你的健康拉玛怎么样啊？” “Well, Monsieur-r-r Poiret,” said the @employee@ from the Museum, “how is your health-orama?”
接着，没等对方回答，他又转向库蒂尔夫人和维多琳说：“女士们，你们看上去很忧郁啊。” Then, without waiting for an answer, he turned to Mme. Couture and Victorine with a “Ladies, you seem melancholy.”
“晚饭好了没有啊？”奥拉斯·比安卡肖恩大声喊道，他是一位医学院学生，是拉斯蒂涅的朋友，“我的胃都要掉到脚底下去了啊。” “Is dinner ready?” cried Horace Bianchon, a medical student, and a friend of Rastignac’s; “my stomach is sinking @usque ad talones@.”
“外面真是冻拉玛得出奇啊。”沃尔特兰说， “There is an uncommon @frozerama@ outside,” said Vautrin.
“让点地方啊，高老头！ “Make room there, Father Goriot!
真该死，你的脚把火炉的正面全占了。” Confound it, your foot covers the whole front of the stove.”
“大名鼎鼎的沃尔特兰先生，”比安卡肖恩插过话，“你为什么要说冻拉玛呢？ “Illustrious M. Vautrin,” put in Bianchon, “why do you say @frozerama@?
那是不对的，应该说冷拉玛。” It is incorrect; it should be @frozenrama@.”
“不，不应该说冷拉玛，”博物馆员工说，“冻拉玛是对的，和你说‘我的脚冻住了’是一样的道理。”“啊！啊！” “No, it shouldn’t,” said the official from the Museum; “@frozerama@ is right by the same rule that you say ‘My feet are @froze@.’”“Ah! ah!”
“德拉斯蒂涅侯爵殿下，相反定律的博士生来了。”比安卡肖恩说着抓住欧仁的喉咙，几乎让他窒息， “Here is his Excellency the Marquis de Rastignac, Doctor of the Law of Contraries,” cried Bianchon, seizing Eugene by the throat, and almost throttling him.
“嗨，你好啊！你好！”米绍诺小姐轻轻地进来，对大家点点头，坐到了三位女士身边。 “Hallo there! hallo!” Mlle. Michonneau came noiselessly in, bowed to the rest of the party, and took her place beside the three women without saying a word.
“那个老蝙蝠总是让我打寒颤。”比安卡肖恩指着米绍诺小姐低声地对沃尔特兰说， “That old bat always makes me shudder,” said Bianchon in a low voice, indicating Mlle. Michonneau to Vautrin.
“我研究过加尔的骨相学，我确信她长着犹大的反骨。” “I have studied Gall’s system, and I am sure she has the bump of Judas.”
“那么你以前见过这样的案例啦？”沃尔特兰说。 “Then you have seen a case before?” said Vautrin.
“谁没见过？”比安卡肖恩答道。 “Who has not?” answered Bianchon.
“的确，那个苍白的老处女就像那些长长的虫子。只要时间足够长，它们就可以蛀空横梁。” “Upon my word, that ghastly old maid looks just like one of the long worms that will gnaw a beam through, give them time enough.”
“年轻人，就是这样的。”四十岁并且染了胡子的沃尔特兰答道，“那朵玫瑰像所有的玫瑰一样——一生只开了一个早晨。” “That is the way, young man,” returned he of the forty years and the dyed whiskers: “The rose has lived the life of a rose—A morning’s space.”
“啊哈！美味的汤拉玛来了。”当克里斯托夫小心翼翼地端着汤进来时，普瓦雷大叫道。 “Aha! here is a magnificent @soupe-au-rama@,” cried Poiret as Christophe came in bearing the soup with cautious heed.
“不好意思，先生，”沃盖夫人说，“这是汤炖卷心菜。” “I beg your pardon, sir,” said Mme. Vauquer; “it is @soupe aux choux@.”
所有的年轻人都哄堂大笑。 All the young men roared with laughter.
“你说错了，普瓦雷！” “Had you there, Poiret!”
“普—瓦—瓦—雷！你栽在沃盖夫人手里了！” “Poir-r-r-rette! she had you there!”
“沃盖妈妈得两分。”沃尔特兰说。 “Score two points to Mamma Vauquer,” said Vautrin.
“有人注意到了今天早晨的大雾吗？”博物馆员工问。 “Did any of you notice the fog this morning?” asked the official.
“真是场狂雾啊。”比安卡肖恩说，“一场空前的、悲伤的、忧郁的、海绿色的、令人无法呼吸的雾——一场高里奥式的雾！” “It was a frantic fog,” said Bianchon, “a fog unparalleled, doleful, melancholy, sea-green, asthmatical—a Goriot of a fog!”
“一场高里奥拉玛，”艺术系的学生说，“因为你无法在其中看见任何东西。” “A Goriorama,” said the art student, “because you couldn’t see a thing in it.”
“嘿！高里奥大人，他们在谈论你哦！” “Hey! Milord Gaoriotte, they air talking about yoo-o-ou!”
高老头坐在桌子的下首，靠近仆人进出的门。他抬起了头，闻了闻餐巾下面一小块面包的味道——他偶尔会使用做生意时学会的这种老窍门。 Father Goriot, seated at the lower end of the table, close to the door through which the servant entered, raised his face; he had smelt at a scrap of bread that lay under his table napkin, an old trick acquired in his commercial capacity, that still showed itself at times.
“喂，”沃盖女士尖叫道，她的声音盖过了汤勺、盘子的碰撞声和其他人的讲话声，“面包有问题吗？” “Well,” Madame Vauquer cried in sharp tones, that rang above the rattle of spoons and plates and the sound of other voices, “and is there anything the matter with the bread?”
“没有问题，夫人。”他答道，“恰恰相反，它是用最好的谷物做成的，用的是埃唐普镇的面粉。” “Nothing whatever, madame,” he answered; “on the contrary, it is made of the best quality of corn; flour from Etampes.”
“你怎么知道的？”欧仁问。 “How could you tell?” asked Eugene.
“凭它的颜色，凭它的味道。” “By the color, by the flavor.”
“我猜，你闻一闻就知道味道。”沃盖夫人说， “You knew the flavor by the smell, I suppose,” said Mme. Vauquer.
“你变得太抠门了，再这么抠门，以后你不用吃饭，问问味道就能活了。” “You have grown so economical, you will find out how to live on the smell of cooking at last.”
“那不妨为它去领一张专利证书。”博物馆员工大叫，“那样倒也可以发笔横财呢。” “Take out a patent for it, then,” cried the Museum official; “you would make a handsome fortune.”
“别管他，”艺术家说，“他做那种事情是为了迷惑我们，让我们认为他是面条制造商。” “Never mind him,” said the artist; “he does that sort of thing to delude us into thinking that he was a vermicelli maker.”
“看起来你的鼻子是个谷物分类器啊？”博物馆员工询问道。 “Your nose is a corn-sampler, it appears?” inquired the official.
“分什么？”比安卡肖恩问。 “Corn @what@?” asked Bianchon.
“分饼。”“分菜。”“分钱。”“分肉。”“分饭。”“分面包。”“分巧克力。”“分拉玛。”这八个答案像只滚动的火球一般从房间四面八方传来。看到高老头满脸疑惑地盯着别人，就像一个外国人在拼命想听懂他并不懂的外语，大家不禁乐得不可开交了。 “Corn-el.”“Corn-et.”“Corn-elian.”“Corn-ice.”“Corn-ucopia.”“Corn-crake.”“Corn-cockle.”“Corn-orama.” The eight responses came like a rolling fire from every part of the room, and the laughter that followed was the more uproarious because poor Father Goriot stared at the others with a puzzled look, like a foreigner trying to catch the meaning of words in a language which he does not understand.
“分什么？”他转向旁边的沃尔特兰说。 “Corn?...” he said, turning to Vautrin, his next neighbor.
“分你的猪脚，老家伙！”沃尔特兰说着拍了下高老头帽顶，把帽子压下去，蒙住了他的眼睛。 “Corn on your foot, old man!” said Vautrin, and he drove Father Goriot’s cap down over his eyes by a blow on the crown.
可怜的老人就这样被突然袭击了，他不知所措，半晌都没动。 The poor old man thus suddenly attacked was for a moment too bewildered to do anything.
克里斯托夫以为高老头已经喝完了汤，就拿走了他的盘子。等到高老头把帽子从自己的眼睛前掀起来喝汤时，他的汤勺一下碰到了桌子。 Christophe carried off his plate, thinking that he had finished his soup, so that when Goriot had pushed back his cap from his eyes his spoon encountered the table.
大家都笑了起来。 Every one burst out laughing.
“先生，你开的玩笑很讨人厌。”老人说，“如果你再这样惹我——”“哦，老家伙，那又怎样？”沃尔特兰打断了他的话。 “You are a disagreeable joker, sir,” said the old man, “and if you take any further liberties with me—” “Well, what then, old boy?” Vautrin interrupted.
“哼，那么，你总有一天会为此付出昂贵的代价的——”“哦，下地狱吗？”艺术家说，“还是进专门关淘气孩子的小黑房子。” “Well, then, you shall pay dearly for it some day—” “Down below, eh?” said the artist, “in the little dark corner where they put naughty boys.”
“噢，小姐，”沃尔特兰转向维多琳说，“你什么也没吃。 “Well, mademoiselle,” Vautrin said, turning to Victorine, “you are eating nothing.
你爸爸很任性，是吧？” So papa was refractory, was he?”
“简直是个怪物！”库蒂尔夫人说。 “A monster!” said Mme. Couture.
“小姐也许会申请因病暂缓诉讼审理。她现在什么也没吃。 “Mademoiselle might make application for aliment pending her suit; she is not eating anything.
哎！哎！看高老头，看他盯着维多琳小姐的样子。” Eh! eh! just see how Father Goriot is staring at Mlle. Victorine.”
老人忘了吃晚饭，他一心一意地盯着这个可怜的女孩，她脸上的悲伤表情显而易见——父亲不认她，对她的爱也不屑一顾。 The old man had forgotten his dinner, he was so absorbed in gazing at the poor girl; the sorrow in her face was unmistakable,—the slighted love of a child whose father would not recognize her.
“我们都误解高老头了，我亲爱的朋友。”欧仁低声地说， “We are mistaken about Father Goriot, my dear boy,” said Eugene in a low voice.
“他不是个傻瓜，也不是个缺乏活力的人。 “He is not an idiot, nor wanting in energy.
在他身上试一下你的加尔骨相学吧，然后再告诉我你的想法。 Try your Gall system on him, and let me know what you think.
昨晚，我看见他用力扭一个银盘子，就像那盘子是用蜡做成的。从他的脸色判断，他刚刚似乎在想什么特别的事情。 I saw him crush a silver dish last night as if it had been made of wax; there seems to be something extraordinary going on in his mind just now, to judge by his face.
他的生活太神秘了，一定值得研究。 His life is so mysterious that it must be worth studying.
噢！比安卡肖恩你也许会笑我，但我不是开玩笑的。” Oh! you may laugh, Bianchon; I am not joking.”
“这男人是个值得研究的对象，是吗？”比安卡肖恩说，“那好吧！如果他给我机会的话，我会把他解剖。”“不，只要检查一下他的脑袋就行。”“嗯！——就怕他的愚蠢会传染啊。” “The man is a subject, is he?” said Bianchon; “all right!I will dissect him, if he will give me the chance.”“No; feel his bumps.”“Hm!—his stupidity might perhaps be contagious.”
第二章 Chapter 2
第二天，拉斯蒂涅打扮得很雅致。下午三点左右，他出发去拜访德雷斯多夫人。 The next day Rastignac dressed himself very elegantly, and about three o’clock in the afternoon went to call on Mme. de Restaud.
一路上，他都沉浸于狂野而醉人的幻想中。这些幻想填满了年轻人本来就满是激动之情的脑海。 On the way thither he indulged in the wild intoxicating dreams which fill a young head so full of delicious excitement.
他这个岁数的年轻人从不顾及障碍或危险，眼里只有成功。他们肆意挥洒着想象力，让生活变得十分浪漫。可是一旦计划受挫，他们就会变得沮丧而气馁。实际上，所谓的计划都是虚幻的，都只存于他们狂热的幻想中。 Young men at his age take no account of obstacles nor of dangers; they see success in every direction; imagination has free play, and turns their lives into a romance; they are saddened or discouraged by the collapse of one of the visionary schemes that have no existence save in their heated fancy.
倘若没有青年的懵懂无知和畏缩不前，文明社会就永远难以实现。 If youth were not ignorant and timid, civilization would be impossible.
欧仁竭尽全力不让一点泥土沾到身上。可是他还在街道里穿行的时候，他就开始想德雷斯多夫人了，还盘算着该对她说些什么。 Eugene took unheard-of pains to keep himself in a spotless condition, but on his way through the streets he began to think about Mme. de Restaud and what he should say to her.
他用智慧武装自己，在脑海中预想着对话、排练着巧妙的应答，还仿照塔列朗的风格，精心准备了一小段演说，来唤起听者对一系列小事的回忆，这样他就可以为最后的表白铺路搭桥了。表白已经成了他奠定自己未来的基础。就这样想着想着，这个法律系的学生衣服上便溅满了泥污。于是，当他走到卢浮宫区的时候，只得叫人给他的靴子上油、把他的裤子刷干净。 He equipped himself with wit, rehearsed repartees in the course of an imaginary conversation, and prepared certain neat speeches a la Talleyrand, conjuring up a series of small events which should prepare the way for the declaration on which he had based his future; and during these musings the law student was bespattered with mud, and by the time he reached the Palais Royal he was obliged to have his boots blacked and his trousers brushed.
“要是我有钱的话，”他一边将一枚带着以防万一的五法郎硬币破开，一边说道，“我就会坐辆马车，那样我就能自由自在地思考了。” “If I were rich,” he said, as he changed the five-franc piece he had brought with him in case anything might happen, “I would take a cab, then I could think at my ease.”
他总算到了埃尔德街，对门口的仆人说要求见德雷斯多伯爵夫人。 At last he reached the Rue du Helder, and asked for the Comtesse de Restaud.
仆人们轻蔑地瞥着他徒步穿过庭院。他勉强按捺住心中的怒火，相信自己终将有一天会功成名就。 He bore the contemptuous glances of the servants, who had seen him cross the court on foot, with the cold fury of a man who knows that he will succeed some day.
他立刻悟出了仆人眼中的蔑视，因为他一进院子，就看见那里等候着一辆华丽的马车。这让他觉得自己很卑微。 He understood the meaning of their glances at once, for he had felt his inferiority as soon as he entered the court, where a smart cab was waiting.
马车这种夺目的奢华标志似乎暗藏了巴黎生活的所有快乐。 All the delights of life in Paris seemed to be implied by this visible and manifest sign of luxury and extravagance.
那匹戴着精致马具的骏马正在用蹄子刨地。这个法律系学生的心情一下子陷入了低谷。 A fine horse, in magnificent harness, was pawing the ground, and all at once the law student felt out of humor with himself.
他刚才还觉得大脑中处处都是智慧，现在这些智慧却消失殆尽，这让他一下子傻了眼。 Every compartment in his brain which he had thought to find so full of wit was bolted fast; he grew positively stupid.
在等候仆人通报时，他站在前厅的一扇窗下，抬起一只脚，机械地将胳膊肘搭在窗框上，望着窗外的庭院。 He sent up his name to the Countess, and waited in the ante-chamber, standing on one foot before a window that looked out upon the court; mechanically he leaned his elbow against the sash, and stared before him.
时间过得很慢。要不是他有南方人的倔脾气，脑袋一根筋地认为只要心无旁骛就会有奇迹，他早就离开了。 The time seemed long; he would have left the house but for the southern tenacity of purpose which works miracles when it is single-minded.
“先生，夫人在卧室，没法接待任何人。”仆人出来说， “Madame is in her boudoir, and cannot see any one at present, sir,” said the servant.
“她也没给我回复。如果您不介意的话，可以先去餐厅，已经有人在那里了。” “She gave me no answer; but if you will go into the dining-room, there is some one already there.”
拉斯蒂涅对仆人体现的强大力量印象十分深刻，那个仆人一句话就责备、指摘了他的主人。拉斯蒂涅冷静地推开了那个人刚才走进前厅时穿过的那扇门，无非是想让那些傲慢的奴才们看看，他其实很熟悉这个房子。但是，他却不小心进了一间小屋子。屋子里摆满了衣橱，衣橱上放着油灯和烘毛巾的热水管，屋子前面是一条黑暗的走廊和一座暗梯。 Rastignac was impressed with a sense of the formidable power of the lackey who can accuse or condemn his masters by a word; he coolly opened the door by which the man had just entered the ante-chamber, meaning, no doubt, to show these insolent flunkeys that he was familiar with the house; but he found that he had thoughtlessly precipitated himself into a small room full of dressers, where lamps were standing, and hot-water pipes, on which towels were being dried; a dark passage and a back staircase lay beyond it.
前厅传来了偷笑声，这更是让他不知所措。 Stifled laughter from the ante-chamber added to his confusion.
“先生，要去客厅的话，请往这边走。”仆人过度的恭敬好像又是在拿他取乐。 “This way to the drawing-room, sir,” said the servant, with the exaggerated respect which seemed to be one more jest at his expense.
欧仁猛然转过身来，一下子撞到了浴缸上。 Eugene turned so quickly that he stumbled against a bath.
他侥幸地把帽子摁在头上，没让它落入水中。而他刚一转身，黑暗走廊尽头的门打开了。走廊里只有一盏小灯在发出昏暗的光芒。 By good luck, he managed to keep his hat on his head, and saved it from immersion in the water; but just as he turned, a door opened at the further end of the dark passage, dimly lighted by a small lamp.
拉斯蒂涅听到了说话声和亲吻声。他听出来其中一个是德雷斯多夫人，另一个是高老头。 Rastignac heard voices and the sound of a kiss; one of the speakers was Mme. de Restaud, the other was Father Goriot.
欧仁跟着仆人穿过餐厅，来到了客厅。他走近一扇能看得见院子的窗户，在那里站了一会儿。 Eugene followed the servant through the dining-room into the drawing-room; he went to a window that looked out into the courtyard, and stood there for a while.
他想知道，这个高里奥是不是他认识的那个高里奥。 He meant to know whether this Goriot was really the Goriot that he knew.
他的心跳得不同寻常地快。他又想起了沃尔特兰可怕的暗示。 His heart beat unwontedly fast; he remembered Vautrin’s hideous insinuations.
几乎就在欧仁走进房间的时候，一个穿着入时的年轻人突然从房间里走出来，不耐烦地跟站在门边的仆人说：“我走了，莫里斯。 A well-dressed young man suddenly emerged from the room almost as Eugene entered it, saying impatiently to the servant who stood at the door: “I am going, Maurice.
告诉伯爵夫人我都等了半个多小时了。” Tell Madame la Comtesse that I waited more than half an hour for her.”
毋庸置疑，这个傲慢的男人有他傲慢的资本。他说话时带着意大利语的颤音，朝欧仁站着的窗户边走来。他既想看看这个法律系学生的脸，也想看窗外的院子。 Whereupon this insolent being, who, doubtless, had a right to be insolent, sang an Italian trill, and went towards the window where Eugene was standing, moved thereto quite as much by a desire to see the student’s face as by a wish to look out into the courtyard.
“不过还是请伯爵再等一会儿吧，夫人现在有空了。”莫里斯在退回前厅时说。 “But M. le Comte had better wait a moment longer; madame is disengaged,” said Maurice, as he returned to the ante-chamber.
就在这时高老头出现在门边，他从暗梯底部的门出来了。 Just at that moment Father Goriot appeared close to the gate; he had emerged from a door at the foot of the back staircase.
这位可敬的人正准备撑伞离开，却没留意一位纽扣孔上系着缎带、乘着轻便马车的年轻人正要从敞开的大门进来。 The worthy soul was preparing to open his umbrella regardless of the fact that the great gate had opened to admit a tilbury, in which a young man with a ribbon at his button-hole was seated.
高老头根本来不及退后，差点被撞。 Father Goriot had scarcely time to start back and save himself.
马碰到雨伞受了惊，转头就向台阶处撞了过去。 The horse took fright at the umbrella, swerved, and dashed forward towards the flight of steps.
年轻人怒气冲冲地环顾四周，看见了高老头，便强装礼貌，在他出去时点头示意。这就像人们见到放债人一样——只要人们还需要向他借钱，就总会对他点头哈腰——抑或是见到一个名声扫地的人——人们当面会对他毕恭毕敬，一转身就因为认识这样的人而脸红。 The young man looked round in annoyance, saw Father Goriot, and greeted him as he went out with constrained courtesy, such as people usually show to a money-lender so long as they require his services, or the sort of respect they feel it necessary to show for some one whose reputation has been blown upon, so that they blush to acknowledge his acquaintance.
高老头回以友好的点头和亲切的微笑。 Father Goriot gave him a little friendly nod and a good-natured smile.
这一切都发生在电光火石之间。 All this happened with lightning speed.
欧仁被这一幕深深吸引了。直到忽然听到伯爵夫人的声音，他才意识到自己身边还有人。 Eugene was so deeply interested that he forgot that he was not alone till he suddenly heard the Countess’ voice.
“哎！马克西姆，你要走啦？”伯爵夫人娇嗔地说道，话语中带着一丝埋怨。 “Oh! Maxime, were you going away?” she said reproachfully, with a shade of pique in her manner.
伯爵夫人没有留意到门口发生的事情，也没有看到进来了一辆轻便马车。 The Countess had not seen the incident nor the entrance of the tilbury.
拉斯蒂涅一下子转过身来，看到她就站在他面前。她好像在卖弄风情一样，穿着一件宽松的白色山羊绒睡裙，睡裙上缀满了玫瑰色的缎带蝴蝶结，头发随意地盘在头上——正是巴黎妇女早上一惯的装束。她四周散发着一股淡淡的清香——她一定是刚洗过澡——这让她优雅的身姿显得更加柔软，让她的美丽显得更为动人。 Rastignac turned abruptly and saw her standing before him, coquettishly dressed in a loose white cashmere gown with knots of rose-colored ribbon here and there; her hair was carelessly coiled about her head, as is the wont of Parisian women in the morning; there was a soft fragrance about her—doubtless she was fresh from a bath;—her graceful form seemed more flexible, her beauty more luxuriant.
她的眼睛闪闪发光。 Her eyes glistened.
年轻人一眼就能看遍这一切。他感受到这个女人焕发的魅力。就像植物能从空气中找到并汲取养料一样，他不用摸她的手，就能感受到她的冰肌玉肤。 A young man can see everything at a glance; he feels the radiant influence of woman as a plant discerns and absorbs its nutriment from the air; he did not need to touch her hands to feel their cool freshness.
他透过山羊绒睡裙看到了她浅粉色的肌肤。通过微微散开的睡裙，他可以时不时地瞥见她光洁的脖子。这个学生就死死盯在那里。 He saw faint rose tints through the cashmere of the dressing gown; it had fallen slightly open, giving glimpses of a bare throat, on which the student’s eyes rested.
伯爵夫人根本不用穿束身衣，一条腰带就能勾勒出她纤细的腰身曲线。她的脖子惹人怜爱，套在拖鞋里的秀足小巧玲珑。 The Countess had no need of the adventitious aid of corsets; her girdle defined the outlines of her slender waist; her throat was a challenge to love; her feet, thrust into slippers, were daintily small.
当马克西姆捧起她的手亲吻时，欧仁这才注意到了马克西姆的存在，而伯爵夫人这才注意到了欧仁。 As Maxime took her hand and kissed it, Eugene became aware of Maxime’s existence, and the Countess saw Eugene.
“哦！你就是德拉斯蒂涅先生吗？ “Oh! is that you M. de Rastignac?
很高兴见到你。”但是看到她说话时的表情，识相的人都会走开的。 I am very glad to see you,” she said, but there was something in her manner that a shrewd observer would have taken as a hint to depart.
在阿纳斯塔谢伯爵夫人以轻蔑的态度跟这个年轻人打招呼时，马克西姆看了看夫人，又看了看欧仁，他分明是想让后者离开。 Maxime, as the Countess Anastasie had called the young man with the haughty insolence of bearing, looked from Eugene to the lady, and from the lady to Eugene; it was sufficiently evident that he wished to be rid of the latter.
那种眼神明明白白地暗示着这些话：“听我说，亲爱的，快把这个自以为是的小子打发走吧。” An exact and faithful rendering of the glance might be given in the words: “Look here, my dear; I hope you intend to send this little whipper-snapper about his business.”
伯爵夫人看着年轻人的脸色，想要征求他的意见。她这种顺从的神情透露了一个女人的全部心事。就在那一刻，拉斯蒂涅开始极度憎恨这个青年。 The Countess consulted the young man’s face with an intent submissiveness that betrays all the secrets of a woman’s heart, and Rastignac all at once began to hate him violently.
首先，马克西姆面容清秀，满头精心梳理出的漂亮卷发，这让他确信自己的短发丑陋不堪；另外，马克西姆的靴子十分精美、一尘不染，而自己的呢，尽管已经处处小心，还是沾上了一些泥土，这些痕迹会让人看出他是走来的；最后，马克西姆的外套穿在身上服服帖帖、优雅得体——他看上去就像一个俏丽的女人，而欧仁却在下午两点半穿着黑外套。 To begin with, the sight of the fair carefully arranged curls on the other’s comely head had convinced him that his own crop was hideous; Maxime’s boots, moreover, were elegant and spotless, while his own, in spite of all his care, bore some traces of his recent walk; and, finally, Maxime’s overcoat fitted the outline of his figure gracefully, he looked like a pretty woman, while Eugene was wearing a black coat at half-past two.
这位夏朗德省来的聪明孩子觉得自己在这个体格魁梧、身材修长、眼神清澈、面色白皙的花花公子面前处于劣势。他那种人可以肆无忌惮地断送孤儿们的前程。 The quick-witted child of the Charente felt the disadvantage at which he was placed beside this tall, slender dandy, with the clear gaze and the pale face, one of those men who would ruin orphan children without scruple.
没等欧仁说话，德雷斯多夫人就跑进了旁边那个房间。她边跑边用双手提起睡裙的裙摆，活像一只白色的蝴蝶，而马克西姆也跟着冲进房去。 Mme. de Restaud fled into the next room without waiting for Eugene to speak; shaking out the skirts of her dressing-gown in her flight, so that she looked like a white butterfly, and Maxime hurried after her.
愤怒的欧仁跟着马克西姆和伯爵夫人。在大客厅的壁炉前，三个人又一次面面相对。 Eugene, in a fury, followed Maxime and the Countess, and the three stood once more face to face by the hearth in the large drawing-room.
这个法律系学生明知道讨厌的马克西姆觉得他碍手碍脚，但是他就是要让这个花花公子不好受，哪怕这样要冒着触怒德雷斯多夫人的风险，他也在所不惜。 The law student felt quite sure that the odious Maxime found him in the way, and even at the risk of displeasing Mme. de Restaud, he meant to annoy the dandy.
他突然想起自己在德伯桑夫人的舞会上见过这个年轻人。他猜出了马克西姆和德雷斯多夫人的关系。带着年轻人的无畏精神——要么就闯出大祸，要么就事业有成——他自言自语道：“这是我的情敌，我要干掉他。” It had struck him all at once that he had seen the young man before at Mme. de Beauseant’s ball; he guessed the relation between Maxime and Mme. de Restaud; and with the youthful audacity that commits prodigious blunders or achieves signal success, he said to himself, “This is my rival; I mean to cut him out.”
多么鲁莽的决定啊！ Rash resolve!
他不了解这位马克西姆·德特拉尔伯爵先生。这人可是个专门挑拨人家侮辱他，找到理由先开枪把敌人打死的家伙。 He did not know that M. le Comte Maxime de Trailles would wait till he was insulted, so as to fire first and kill his man.
欧仁虽然是一个运动健将和射击好手，但也没达到射二十二次就能击中靶心二十次的程度。 Eugene was a sportsman and a good shot, but he had not yet hit the bulls’ eye twenty times out of twenty-two.
年轻的伯爵坐到壁炉旁的一张矮腿椅子上，拿起火钳在火堆里愤怒地乱搅一通，阿纳斯塔谢精致的脸上立即乌云密布。 The young Count dropped into a low chair by the hearth, took up the tongs, and made up the fire so violently and so sulkily, that Anastasie’s fair face suddenly clouded over.
她转身面对欧仁，困惑地白他一眼。很明显她是在问：“你怎么还不走？” She turned to Eugene, with a cool, questioning glance that asked plainly, “Why do you not go?”
教养好的人会把这样的眼神视为逐客令。 A glance which well-bred people regard as a cue to make their exit.
欧仁强扮欢颜， Eugene assumed an amiable expression.
“夫人，”他说道，“我赶来拜见您——”他突然停了下来。 “Madame,” he began, “I hastened to call upon you—” He stopped short.
客厅门打开了，轻便马车的主人突然出现了。 The door opened, and the owner of the tilbury suddenly appeared.
他把帽子留在门外，也不跟伯爵夫人打招呼，而是若有所思地看了看拉斯蒂涅，然后跟马克西姆握了握手，还热情地说了句“早上好”。这让欧仁大吃一惊。 He had left his hat outside, and did not greet the Countess; he looked meditatively at Rastignac, and held out his hand to Maxime with a cordial “Good morning,” that astonished Eugene not a little.
这个外省来的小伙子根本不明白三角关系带来的快乐。 The young provincial did not understand the amenities of a triple alliance.
“这是德雷斯多先生。”伯爵夫人向这个法律系学生介绍她的丈夫。 “M. de Restaud,” said the Countess, introducing her husband to the law student.
欧仁深深鞠了一躬。 Eugene bowed profoundly.
“这位先生，”她接着将欧仁介绍给她丈夫，“是德拉斯蒂涅先生，因为马西亚克家的关系，和德伯桑子爵夫人是亲戚，我有幸在她家上次的舞会上认识了他。” “This gentleman,” she continued, presenting Eugene to her husband, “is M. de Rastignac; he is related to Mme. la Vicomtesse de Beauseant through the Marcillacs; I had the pleasure of meeting him at her last ball.”
因为马西亚克家的关系，和德伯桑子爵夫人是亲戚！伯爵夫人想显示她的自豪感，表明她家里只接待重要人士，因此才稍微强调了这句话，而这句话却带来了意想不到的效果。 Related to Mme. la Vicomtesse de Beauseant through the Marcillacs!These words, on which the countess threw ever so slight an emphasis, by reason of the pride that the mistress of a house takes in showing that she only receives people of distinction as visitors in her house, produced a magical effect.
伯爵僵硬的表情立即松弛下来，还对这个大学生鞠躬回礼。 The Count’s stiff manner relaxed at once as he returned the student’s bow.
“非常庆幸能有机会认识您。”他说道。 “Delighted to have an opportunity of making your acquaintance,” he said.
马克西姆·德特拉尔不安地看了欧仁一眼，也突然放下了他高傲的身段。 Maxime de Trailles himself gave Eugene an uneasy glance, and suddenly dropped his insolent manner.
一个尊贵的姓氏和仙女的魔棒一样拥有神奇的力量。这个南方年轻人刚才闭塞的脑子终于豁然开朗。拉斯蒂涅精心准备的聪明才智也恢复正常了。 The mighty name had all the power of a fairy’s wand; those closed compartments in the southern brain flew open again; Rastignac’s carefully drilled faculties returned.
就像一束突然出现的亮光射穿了覆盖在巴黎上流社会的阴霾一样，虽然一切还不是很明了，但他开始看清一些东西了。 It was as if a sudden light had pierced the obscurity of this upper world of Paris, and he began to see, though everything was indistinct as yet.
至于沃盖夫人的旅馆和高老头，早就被他抛到脑后了。 Mme. Vauquer’s lodging-house and Father Goriot were very far remote from his thoughts.
“我还以为马西亚克家已经没人了呢。”德雷斯多伯爵对欧仁说。 “I thought that the Marcillacs were extinct,” the Comte de Restaud said, addressing Eugene.
“对啊，没人了。”这个法律系学生回答说， “Yes, they are extinct,” answered the law student.
“我的伯祖父是德拉斯蒂涅骑士，他娶了马西亚克家族的女继承人。 “My great-uncle, the Chevalier de Rastignac, married the heiress of the Marcillac family.
他们只有一个女儿，嫁给了德克拉朗博元帅，就是德伯桑夫人的外祖父。 They had only one daughter, who married the Marechal de Clarimbault, Mme. de Beauseant’s grandfather on the mother’s side.
我们是这个家族的年轻一辈，可是我们年轻一辈都很落魄，因为我那位担任海军中将的伯祖父失去了他效忠国王时所拥有的一切。 We are the younger branch of the family, and the younger branch is all the poorer because my great-uncle, the Vice-Admiral, lost all that he had in the King’s service.
大革命时的政府在清算东印度公司时，拒绝承认我们的索赔。” The Government during the Revolution refused to admit our claims when the Compagnie des Indes was liquidated.”
“您的伯祖父一七八九年以前是不是一直在指挥‘复仇号’？” “Was not your great-uncle in command of the @Vengeur@ before 1789?”
“是的。” “Yes.”
“那么他应该认识我的祖父了，那时他是‘沃里克号’的舰长。” “Then he would be acquainted with my grandfather, who commanded the @Warwick@.”
马克西姆看着德雷斯多夫人，耸了耸肩，好像在说：“要是他再和那小子说海军那点事，咱俩就结束了。” Maxime looked at Mme. de Restaud and shrugged his shoulders, as who should say, “If he is going to discuss nautical matters with that fellow, it is all over with us.”
阿纳斯塔谢立即明白了德特拉尔对她使的眼色。 Anastasie understood the glance that M. de Trailles gave her.
她使出女人绝妙的看家本领，笑着说：“跟我来，马克西姆，我有话跟你说。 With a woman’s admirable tact, she began to smile and said: “Come with me, Maxime; I have something to say to you.
你们两个先生就尽管驾着‘沃里克号’和‘复仇号’一起出海吧。” We will leave you two gentlemen to sail in company on board the @Warwick@ and the @Vengeur@.”
她站起身来，既高兴又俏皮地示意马克西姆跟着她，之后二人就向她卧房的方向走去。 She rose to her feet and signed to Maxime to follow her, mirth and mischief in her whole attitude, and the two went in the direction of the boudoir.
这对身份悬殊（因为在法语中找不到完全对应的词语，这里就从德语中借用了“身份悬殊”这个词）的人走到门边时，伯爵打断了自己与欧仁的谈话。 The @morganatic@ couple (to use a convenient German expression which has no exact equivalent) had reached the door, when the Count interrupted himself in his talk with Eugene.
“阿纳斯塔谢！”他气冲冲地喊着，“就坐一会儿嘛，亲爱的，你明明知道——”“我马上回来。”她打断伯爵的话，“我有事拜托马克西姆去做，现在我要跟他说说这件事。” “Anastasie!” he cried pettishly, “just stay a moment, dear; you know very well that—” “I am coming back in a minute,” she interrupted; “I have a commission for Maxime to execute, and I want to tell him about it.”
她立刻回来了。 She came back almost immediately.
她注意到了丈夫语气上的变化，也知道要是真进了卧房，事情就闹大了。和所有女人一样，她不得不摸清自己丈夫的性格，这样才能按自己的愿望行事。她深知让丈夫理解和信任的底线在哪里，所以她非常注意，在家庭生活中尽量避免小冲突。 She had noticed the inflection in her husband’s voice, and knew that it would not be safe to retire to the boudoir; like all women who are compelled to study their husbands’ characters in order to have their own way, and whose business it is to know exactly how far they can go without endangering a good understanding, she was very careful to avoid petty collisions in domestic life.
麻烦是欧仁惹的，所以伯爵夫人看着马克西姆时眼里带着对这个法律系学生极度的不满。 It was Eugene who had brought about this untoward incident; so the Countess looked at Maxime and indicated the law student with an air of exasperation.
