德特拉尔先生尖刻地对伯爵、伯爵夫人和欧仁说道，“你们都很忙，我不想打扰你们了，再见。”说完就走了出去。 M. de Trailles addressed the Count, the Countess, and Eugene with the pointed remark, “You are busy, I do not want to interrupt you; good-day,” and he went.
“等一下，马克西姆！”伯爵在他背后喊道。 “Just wait a moment, Maxime!” the Count called after him.
“吃个饭再走嘛。”伯爵夫人说着再一次丢下了她的丈夫和欧仁。 “Come and dine with us,” said the Countess, leaving Eugene and her husband together once more.
她跟着马克西姆走进小客厅，他们在那里坐了很长时间，一直等到他们都觉得拉斯蒂涅应该已经走了才起身。 She followed Maxime into the little drawing-room, where they sat together sufficiently long to feel sure that Rastignac had taken his leave.
法律系学生听到他们一会儿笑，一会儿说话，一会儿又没声了，于是心里起了恶意。他在伯爵面前尽展自己的语言才华，又是恭维，又是和他讨论问题，想着最后还能再见到伯爵夫人，好弄明白她和高老头的真正关系。 The law student heard their laughter, and their voices, and the pauses in their talk; he grew malicious, exerted his conversational powers for M. de Restaud, flattered him, and drew him into discussions, to the end that he might see the Countess again and discover the nature of her relations with Father Goriot.
这位伯爵夫人简直是个谜。她有一个丈夫，一个情人——那个马克西姆明显就是她的情人。 This Countess with a husband and a lover, for Maxime clearly was her lover, was a mystery.
维系她和那个老商人的秘密纽带到底是什么呢？ What was the secret tie that bound her to the old tradesman?
他打算参透这个谜，希望借此抓住一个强有力的把柄，好让自己凌驾于这个美丽的典型巴黎女人之上。 This mystery he meant to penetrate, hoping by its means to gain a sovereign ascendency over this fair typical Parisian.
“阿纳斯塔谢！”伯爵又叫起他的夫人。 “Anastasie!” the Count called again to his wife.
“可怜的马克西姆！”她对那年轻人说， “Poor Maxime!” she said, addressing the young man.
“快，我们得乖乖听话了。 “Come, we must resign ourselves.
今晚——”“纳西，我希望，”他在她耳边说，“你下令不招待那个年轻人。他看你时眼睛放光，跟烧红的炭一样。 This evening—” “I hope, Nasie,” he said in her ear, “that you will give orders not to admit that youngster, whose eyes light up like live coals when he looks at you.
他会向你求爱，败坏你的名誉，最后你会让我不得不杀了他。” He will make you a declaration, and compromise you, and then you will compel me to kill him.”
“你疯了吗，马克西姆？”她说， “Are you mad, Maxime?” she said.
“恰恰相反，像他们这样的年轻学生不正是绝妙的避雷针吗？ “A young lad of a student is, on the contrary, a capital lightning-conductor; is not that so?
当然了，我是要让雷斯多疯狂地嫉妒他。” Of course, I mean to make Restaud furiously jealous of him.”
马克西姆哈哈大笑，走出门去。伯爵夫人跟着他，站在窗边看他上车。他扬起鞭子，马便一跃而起。 Maxime burst out laughing, and went out, followed by the Countess, who stood at the window to watch him into his carriage; he shook his whip, and made his horse prance.
一直等到他出门后大门关上，她才回来。 She only returned when the great gate had been closed after him.
“怎么样，亲爱的？”她的伯爵丈夫喊着，“这位先生家的祖产离韦尔特伊不远，就在夏朗德河畔，他的伯祖父跟我的祖父还很熟呢。” “What do you think, dear?” cried the Count, her husband, “this gentleman’s family estate is not far from Verteuil, on the Charente; his great-uncle and my grandfather were acquainted.”
“太好了，我们还有共同认识的人。”伯爵夫人心不在焉地回答。 “Delighted to find that we have acquaintances in common,” said the Countess, with a preoccupied manner.
“还不止呢。”欧仁低声说。 “More than you think,” said Eugene, in a low voice.
“什么意思？”她立即问。 “What do you mean?” she asked quickly.
“因为，就在刚才，”大学生说，“我看见一位先生走出门口。他是高老头，和我住一个旅馆，还是隔壁邻居呢。” “Why, only just now,” said the student, “I saw a gentleman go out at the gate, Father Goriot, my next door neighbor in the house where I am lodging.”
一听到这个名字和用来修饰这个名字的“老头”这个称谓，正在搅着炉火的伯爵仿佛被火钳烫到了手指似的，一把扔了火钳，站起身来。 At the sound of this name, and the prefix that embellished it, the Count, who was stirring the fire, let the tongs fall as though they had burned his fingers, and rose to his feet.
“先生，”他嚷道，“你或许应该称呼他‘高里奥先生’！” “Sir,” he cried, “you might have called him ‘Monsieur Goriot’!”
看到丈夫的恼怒之情，伯爵夫人的脸色起初变得煞白，之后又涨得通红。很明显，她感到很难堪。她强装出自然、随意的语调答道：“他是我们最亲近的人……” The Countess turned pale at first at the sight of her husband’s vexation, then she reddened; clearly she was embarrassed, her answer was made in a tone that she tried to make natural, and with an air of assumed carelessness: “You could not know any one who is dearer to us both...”
她停了下来，看了一眼钢琴，好像想到了什么美好的事物，问道：“您喜欢音乐吗，德拉斯蒂涅先生？” She broke off, glanced at the piano as if some fancy had crossed her mind, and asked, “Are you fond of music, M. de Rastignac?”
“非常喜欢。”欧仁回答时，脸一下子就红了，还有些不安，隐约觉得自己不知怎么竟做了件不妥的蠢事。 “Exceedingly,” answered Eugene, flushing, and disconcerted by a dim suspicion that he had somehow been guilty of a clumsy piece of folly.
“您会唱歌吗？”她大声问道，同时走到钢琴前坐下，手指从琴键的一端滑到另一端。 “Do you sing?” she cried, going to the piano, and, sitting down before it, she swept her fingers over the keyboard from end to end.
啦—啦—啦！ R-r-r-rah!
“不会，夫人。” “No, madame.”
德雷斯多伯爵在屋子里走来走去。 The Comte de Restaud walked to and fro.
“多可惜啊！你失去了一件重要的制胜法宝。‘亲—爱的，亲—爱—的，亲—爱—的，不要—怀—疑’。”伯爵夫人唱了起来。 “That is a pity; you are without one great means of success.—/Ca-ro, ca-a-ro, ca-a-a-ro, non du-bi-ta-re/,” sang the Countess.
欧仁说出高里奥的名字时，好像又挥了一下魔术棒，但是效果却与那句“和德伯桑夫人是亲戚”截然相反。 Eugene had a second time waved a magic wand when he uttered Goriot’s name, but the effect seemed to be entirely opposite to that produced by the formula “related to Mme. de Beauseant.”
他现在的境地就如同某位得到主人恩准的访客，在参观主人私人收集的奇珍异宝时，不小心撞到了摆满了人体雕塑的玻璃橱，里面三四个人头由于没有锁严，在撞击的作用下滚落出来。 His position was not unlike that of some visitor permitted as a favor to inspect a private collection of curiosities, when by inadvertence he comes into collision with a glass case full of sculptured figures, and three or four heads, imperfectly secured, fall at the shock.
他恨不得能找一条地缝钻进去。 He wished the earth would open and swallow him.
德雷斯多夫人的表情拘谨而冷漠，眼神也变得十分冷淡，一直在避免和这个倒霉的法律系学生双目对视。 Mme. de Restaud’s expression was reserved and chilly, her eyes had grown indifferent, and sedulously avoided meeting those of the unlucky student of law.
“夫人，”他说，“如果您和德雷斯多先生还有事要谈，请允许我送上我的祝福——”伯爵夫人摆了摆手，打断了他，急忙说：“我和德雷斯多先生随时欢迎您再来。” “Madame,” he said, “you wish to talk with M. de Restaud; permit me to wish you good-day—” The Countess interrupted him by a gesture, saying hastily, “Whenever you come to see us, both M. de Restaud and I shall be delighted to see you.”
欧仁深深地鞠了一躬后就转身离开。尽管他一再推辞，德雷斯多先生还是坚持要把他送到门厅。 Eugene made a profound bow and took his leave, followed by M. de Restaud, who insisted, in spite of his remonstrances, on accompanying him into the hall.
“以后他来，就说我们不在。”伯爵对莫里斯说。 “Neither your mistress nor I are at home to that gentleman when he calls,” the Count said to Maurice.
欧仁下楼梯时，发现外面正在下雨。 As Eugene set foot on the steps, he saw that it was raining.
“天呀，”他自言自语道，“我刚刚全搞砸了，却还不知道是怎么搞砸的。 “Come,” said he to himself, “somehow I have just made a mess of it, I do not know how.
现在还得赔上我的帽子和大衣。 And now I am going to spoil my hat and coat into the bargain.
我应该躲在角落里啃法律书，以后安安稳稳地做个土里土气的地方法官，再也不期盼其他事了。 I ought to stop in my corner, grind away at law, and never look to be anything but a boorish country magistrate.
要想在这个社会上左右逢源，你得有许多马车、锃亮的靴子和金表链，还有好多其他各种各样的东西；你早上得戴六法郎的白色鹿皮手套，晚上又得戴淡黄色羔皮手套。我怎么有能力进入那样的社会呢？ How can I go into society, when to manage properly you want a lot of cabs, varnished boots, gold watch chains, and all sorts of things; you have to wear white doeskin gloves that cost six francs in the morning, and primrose kid gloves every evening?
高里奥这个老混账，去你的吧！” A fig for that old humbug of a Goriot!”
他走到临街的大门时，一个马车夫正赶着辆出租马车——他也许刚把一对新婚夫妇送到家，就想背着老板赚几个外快——他看到欧仁没带伞，又注意到他的黑外套、白背心、黄手套和上过油的靴子，便停下来用询问的眼神看着他。 When he reached the street door, the driver of a hackney coach, who had probably just deposited a wedding party at their door, and asked nothing better than a chance of making a little money for himself without his employer’s knowledge, saw that Eugene had no umbrella, remarked his black coat, white waistcoat, yellow gloves, and varnished boots, and stopped and looked at him inquiringly.
欧仁感到一种莫名的绝望，这种感觉让他跌入深谷、越跌越深，就像他能在谷底找到一件幸运之事似的。他对马车夫点了点头，然后拾阶上马车。车厢里还散落着白色香橙花花瓣和扎花的铜丝。看来这驾车刚刚拉了一对新婚夫妇。 Eugene, in the blind desperation that drives a young man to plunge deeper and deeper into an abyss, as if he might hope to find a fortunate issue in its lowest depths, nodded in reply to the driver’s signal, and stepped into the cab; a few stray petals of orange blossom and scraps of wire bore witness to its recent occupation by a wedding party.
“您去哪里，先生？”马车夫问道，这时，他已经脱掉了白手套。 “Where am I to drive, sir?” demanded the man, who, by this time, had taken off his white gloves.
“该死的！”欧仁思忖道，“反正都坐上了，总不能花了钱什么都不做吧！—— “Confound it!” Eugene said to himself, “I am in for it now, and at least I will not spend cab-hire for nothing!—
去伯桑府。”他高声说。 Drive to the Hotel Beauseant,” he said aloud.
“哪一个伯桑府？”马车夫问道，这句话出人意料，可把欧仁问倒了。 “Which?” asked the man, a portentous word that reduced Eugene to confusion.
这个打扮入时却涉世未深的年轻人可不知道巴黎有两个伯桑府，他还不知道自己的关系资源有多丰富，只是那些亲戚从不关心他。 This young man of fashion, species incerta, did not know that there were two Hotels Beauseant; he was not aware how rich he was in relations who did not care about him.
“德伯桑子爵，那条街叫——”“格勒内勒，”马车夫猛一扭头接道。 “The Vicomte de Beauseant, Rue—” “De Grenelle,” interrupted the driver, with a jerk of his head.
“您看，还有圣多米尼克街的德伯桑伯爵府和德伯桑侯爵府。”他一边补充，一边收起踏板。 “You see, there are the hotels of the Marquis and Comte de Beauseant in the Rue Saint-Dominique,” he added, drawing up the step.
“我都知道。”欧仁板着脸说。“今天好像每个人都在嘲笑我！”他自言自语着把帽子丢到了对面的座位上。 “I know all about that,” said Eugene, severely.—“Everybody is laughing at me to-day, it seems!” he said to himself, as he deposited his hat on the opposite seat.
“今天的冒失行为会花我一大笔钱，但不管怎样，我能以全副贵族行头去拜访我那个所谓的表姐了。 “This escapade will cost me a king’s ransom, but, at any rate, I shall call on my so-called cousin in a thoroughly aristocratic fashion.
高里奥已经花了我十法郎了，这个老不死的。 Goriot has cost me ten francs already, the old scoundrel.
哎呀！我要把今天的遭遇告诉德伯桑夫人，说不定还能取悦她呢。 My word! I will tell Mme. de Beauseant about my adventure; perhaps it may amuse her.
她肯定知道那个标致的女人和那个没尾巴的老硕鼠之间有什么见不得光的关系。 Doubtless she will know the secret of the criminal relation between that handsome woman and the old rat without a tail.
与其去取悦那个无耻女人，还不如来讨好我的表姐。依我看，那个无耻的女人奢侈得很呢。 It would be better to find favor in my cousin’s eyes than to come in contact with that shameless woman, who seems to me to have very expensive tastes.
光是提到子爵夫人的名字就能有如此影响力，要是美丽的子爵夫人自己对我产生了兴趣，就一定可以帮我扭转乾坤。 Surely the beautiful Vicomtesse’s personal interest would turn the scale for me, when the mere mention of her name produces such an effect.
我们得把眼光放高点。 Let us look higher.
你若想达到天堂的高度，就必须直面上帝。” If you set yourself to carry the heights of heaven, you must face God.”
他脑子里涌出的无数想法可以归结为以上几句话。 The innumerable thoughts that surged through his brain might be summed up in these phrases.
他平静了一些。看着外面的雨，他坚定的信念也开始恢复。 He grew calmer, and recovered something of his assurance as he watched the falling rain.
他告诉自己，虽然自己仅剩的两个宝贵的五法郎硬币就要被挥霍掉了，但是这些钱花得还挺值，因为这样保住了自己的衣帽和靴子。听到马车夫喊着：“麻烦您，开开门！”这使他兴奋不已。 He told himself that though he was about to squander two of the precious five-franc pieces that remained to him, the money was well laid out in preserving his coat, boots, and hat; and his cabman’s cry of “Gate, if you please,” almost put him in spirits.
一个穿着鲜红色和金色衣服的瑞士人过来应门。大门拉动时，铰链发出闷响。拉斯蒂涅心满意足，看着他的马车穿过门洞，停在雨篷下的台阶前。 A Swiss, in scarlet and gold, appeared, the great door groaned on its hinges, and Rastignac, with sweet satisfaction, beheld his equipage pass under the archway and stop before the flight of steps beneath the awning.
穿着蓝红大衣的马车夫跳下马车，放下踏板。 The driver, in a blue-and-red greatcoat, dismounted and let down the step.
欧仁迈出马车时，听到柱子后面有人笑得喘不上气了。 As Eugene stepped out of the cab, he heard smothered laughter from the peristyle.
三四个仆人在拿这辆粉墨登场的马车找乐子。 Three or four lackeys were making merry over the festal appearance of the vehicle.
这个法律系的学生立即明白他们笑的原因了。他感觉出自己的马车和巴黎最精美的有蓬马车之间存在着巨大反差。一个头上抹了粉的马车夫似乎费了好大劲才拉住两匹神采奕奕、烦躁不安的马。 In another moment the law student was enlightened as to the cause of their hilarity; he felt the full force of the contrast between his equipage and one of the smartest broughams in Paris; a coachman, with powdered hair, seemed to find it difficult to hold a pair of spirited horses, who stood chafing the bit.
在德安丁路上德雷斯多夫人的院子里，他看到过一个衣着整齐的二十六岁年轻人，而在圣日耳曼郊区他又看到一辆属于身居高位者的奢华的马车，那辆马车用三万法郎也买不下来。 In Mme. de Restaud’s courtyard, in the Chaussee d’Antin, he had seen the neat turnout of a young man of six-and-twenty; in the Faubourg Saint-Germain he found the luxurious equipage of a man of rank; thirty thousand francs would not have purchased it.
“有谁在这里呢？”欧仁想。 “Who can be here?” said Eugene to himself.
虽然反应慢了点，他也开始意识到，在巴黎很难找到一个没有伴侣的女人，而要征服一个王后般的女人，只是为她流血出力可不够。 He began to understand, though somewhat tardily, that he must not expect to find many women in Paris who were not already appropriated, and that the capture of one of these queens would be likely to cost something more than bloodshed.
“真该死！ “Confound it all!
我想我表姐也应该有自己的马克西姆了。” I expect my cousin also has her Maxime.”
他走上楼梯，感到万念俱灰。 He went up the steps, feeling that he was a blighted being.
面前的玻璃门打开了，仆人们都严肃得像正在被马梳梳过的驴子似的。 The glass door was opened for him; the servants were as solemn as jackasses under the curry comb.
欧仁目前只到过伯桑府一楼的舞厅。从接到邀请到出席舞会之间的时间太短，以至于他没来得及拜访表姐。所以他也从未见过德伯桑夫人的房间。今天他将第一次在这高贵、典雅的房间里观察这位伟大的女性，而这些绝佳的布置也展现了这位优雅贵妇的性格和生活方式。 So far, Eugene had only been in the ballroom on the ground floor of the Hotel Beauseant; the fete had followed so closely on the invitation, that he had not had time to call on his cousin, and had therefore never seen Mme. de Beauseant’s apartments; he was about to behold for the first time a great lady among the wonderful and elegant surroundings that reveal her character and reflect her daily life.
因为他有德雷斯多夫人的客厅作为参照，所以好奇心愈发强烈起来。 He was the more curious, because Mme. de Restaud’s drawing-room had provided him with a standard of comparison.
四点半时，德伯桑子爵夫人露面了。 At half-past four the Vicomtesse de Beauseant was visible.
要是早五分钟，她就不会接待这个表弟了，但是欧仁对巴黎各府邸公认的规矩一窍不通。 Five minutes earlier she would not have received her cousin, but Eugene knew nothing of the recognized routine of various houses in Paris.
他跟着仆人，走上了一座刷着白漆、铺着红地毯的宽敞楼梯。楼梯镀金的栏杆之间摆满了鲜花。他就这样被带进了德伯桑夫人的房间。 He was conducted up the wide, white-painted, crimson-carpeted staircase, between the gilded balusters and masses of flowering plants, to Mme. de Beauseant’s apartments.
他并不知道近来关于德伯桑夫人的流言蜚语。这些谣言版本不一，成为夜晚巴黎各个沙龙里人们交头接耳议论的话题之一。 He did not know the rumor current about Mme. de Beauseant, one of the biographies told, with variations, in whispers, every evening in the salons of Paris.
三年以来，她的名字总是会和一个才大气粗、声名显赫的葡萄牙贵族——德阿尤达·平托侯爵联系在一起。 For three years past her name had been spoken of in connection with that of one of the most wealthy and distinguished Portuguese nobles, the Marquis d’Ajuda-Pinto.
这种纯洁的联系对这两个相互吸引的人而言，有着相当大的魔力，以至于他们容不得第三人的打扰。 It was one of those innocent liaisons which possess so much charm for the two thus attached to each other that they find the presence of a third person intolerable.
因此，德伯桑子爵也向世人树立了良好的榜样，尽量显得优雅得体，尊重这种地位悬殊的关系。 The Vicomte de Beauseant, therefore, had himself set an example to the rest of the world by respecting, with as good a grace as might be, this morganatic union.
这段友谊刚刚开始的时候，无论谁去拜访子爵夫人，总能在那里见到德阿尤达·平托侯爵。 Any one who came to call on the Vicomtesse in the early days of this friendship was sure to find the Marquis d’Ajuda-Pinto there.
因为在这种情形下，德伯桑夫人不可能闭门谢客。她只得冷淡地接待客人，总是看着天花板，好像对房顶更感兴趣似的。于是所有人都识趣地意识到自己严重地打扰到了她。到最后巴黎人人都知道，两点到四点去拜访德伯桑夫人都会打扰她，她也总算在这个时间段得享安宁。 As, under the circumstances, Mme. de Beauseant could not very well shut her door against these visitors, she gave them such a cold reception, and showed so much interest in the study of the ceiling, that no one could fail to understand how much he bored her; and when it became known in Paris that Mme. de Beauseant was bored by callers between two and four o’clock, she was left in perfect solitude during that interval.
她跟着德伯桑先生和德阿尤达·平托先生一起去看谐谑剧或歌剧。而德伯桑先生，像这世上修养极好的人一样，总是在安顿好妻子和这位葡萄牙人后就离开了。 She went to the Bouffons or to the Opera with M. de Beauseant and M. d’Ajuda-Pinto; and M. de Beauseant, like a well-bred man of the world, always left his wife and the Portuguese as soon as he had installed them.
但是德阿尤达·平托先生总要结婚的，而德洛希斐特小姐正是合适人选。 But M. d’Ajuda-Pinto must marry, and a Mlle.de Rochefide was the young lady.
至今整个上流社会只有一个人对这场联姻一无所知，那个人就是德伯桑夫人。 In the whole fashionable world there was but one person who as yet knew nothing of the arrangement, and that was Mme. de Beauseant.
她的一些朋友曾向她暗示过这种可能性，但她却置之一笑，认为朋友妒忌她，想从中作梗。 Some of her friends had hinted at the possibility, and she had laughed at them, believing that envy had prompted those ladies to try to make mischief.
如今，结婚告示马上就要张贴出来了。虽然那天这位葡萄牙美男子也来了，想把这件事婉转地告知子爵夫人，但是他至今也没勇气说他自己背叛了她。 And now, though the bans were about to be published, and although the handsome Portuguese had come that day to break the news to the Vicomtesse, he had not found courage as yet to say one word about his treachery.
这是怎么一回事呢？ How was it?
毫无疑问，没什么事比下这样一个最后通牒更难了。 Nothing is doubtless more difficult than the notification of an ultimatum of this kind.
有的男人宁愿冒着生命危险，站在敌人面前被人用剑或手枪指着，也不愿对着一个女人又哭又骂两个小时，最后晕死过去，不得不对她施救。因为他们认为前一种情况让自己觉得更自在。 There are men who feel more at their ease when they stand up before another man who threatens their lives with sword or pistol than in the presence of a woman who, after two hours of lamentations and reproaches, falls into a dead swoon and requires salts.
于是，这时的德阿尤达·平托先生如坐针毡、焦虑不安、急于开溜。 At this moment, therefore, M. d’Ajuda-Pinto was on thorns, and anxious to take his leave.
他告诉自己，消息总会通过其他什么渠道传到德伯桑夫人那里的。他准备写信给她，觉得写信比当面说出那些句句钻心的话要好。 He told himself that in some way or other the news would reach Mme. de Beauseant; he would write, it would be much better to do it by letter, and not to utter the words that should stab her to the heart.
于是当仆人通报欧仁·德拉斯蒂涅先生求见时，德阿尤达·平托侯爵开心得浑身一震。 So when the servant announced M. Eugene de Rastignac, the Marquis d’Ajuda-Pinto trembled with joy.
毋庸置疑，恋爱中的女人更擅长对情人百般猜忌，而不是用各种变化给对方的幸福带来新意。一旦要被抛弃时，她就会本能地诠释对方每一个姿势的含义。诠释的过程快得就像维吉尔（注：古罗马诗人）的马能透过微风嗅到主人的气息一样。 To be sure, a loving woman shows even more ingenuity in inventing doubts of her lover than in varying the monotony of his happiness; and when she is about to be forsaken, she instinctively interprets every gesture as rapidly as Virgil’s courser detected the presence of his companion by snuffing the breeze.
因此，德伯桑夫人一眼就看穿了他不由自主地流露出的满足、兴奋之意。虽然变化细微，但是流露出的感情却真实得可怕。 It was impossible, therefore, that Mme. de Beauseant should not detect that involuntary thrill of satisfaction; slight though it was, it was appalling in its artlessness.
欧仁还没搞明白一件事情，在巴黎，无论要拜访谁，首先都要把主人、女主人和他们的整个家族史都打听清楚，以避免弄出什么糟糕的差错。波兰人将这种差错说得惟妙惟肖：“在你的车上套五头牛！” Eugene had yet to learn that no one in Paris should present himself in any house without first making himself acquainted with the whole history of its owner, and of its owner’s wife and family, so that he may avoid making any of the terrible blunders which in Poland draw forth the picturesque exclamation, “Harness five bullocks to your cart!”
这样说可能是因为一旦你一步踏空就会陷入泥沼，这样就需要五头牛一齐用力才能将你拉出来。 Probably because you will need them all to pull you out of the quagmire into which a false step has plunged you.
要是到今天我们法语中还没有相应的说法来描绘对话中出现的这般灾难，大概是因为人们相信这样的事情决计不可能发生。在巴黎，每一件丑闻都会被宣传得尽人皆知。 If, down to the present day, our language has no name for these conversational disasters, it is probably because they are believed to be impossible, the publicity given in Paris to every scandal is so prodigious.
在经历了德雷斯多夫人家里的尴尬后又出现在德伯桑夫人的客厅里，这也只有欧仁能做得出来，他的性格简直和赶牛车的车夫一样。 After the awkward incident at Mme. de Restaud’s, no one but Eugene could have reappeared in his character of bullock-driver in Mme. de Beauseant’s drawing-room.
换成是德雷斯多夫人和德特拉尔先生，他们就会觉得他非常碍事，但对于德阿尤达先生来说，他的到来却是在帮他解围。 But if Mme. de Restaud and M. de Trailles had found him horribly in the way, M. d’Ajuda hailed his coming with relief.
“再见。”这位葡萄牙人说着急忙走向门口，此时欧仁进入了这间小巧别致、粉色与灰色交融的客厅，虽然奢华但独具品味。 “Good-bye,” said the Portuguese, hurrying to the door, as Eugene made his entrance into a dainty little pink-and-gray drawing-room, where luxury seemed nothing more than good taste.
“晚上见，”德伯桑夫人说着回头望了侯爵一眼， “Until this evening,” said Mme. de Beauseant, turning her head to give the Marquis a glance.
“我们晚上不是要去看戏吗？” “We are going to the Bouffons, are we not?”
“我去不了了。”他回答的时候手已经在门把手上了。 “I cannot go,” he said, with his fingers on the door handle.
德伯桑夫人站了起来，向他招手，让他回来。 Mme. de Beauseant rose and beckoned to him to return.
她根本就没有注意到欧仁。欧仁正站在那里，被身边这些耀眼的奇景弄得眼花缭乱。他在想着《一千零一夜》里面的故事成了现实，而他面前的女人却像根本没有意识到他的存在一样。 She did not pay the slightest attention to Eugene, who stood there dazzled by the sparkling marvels around him; he began to think that this was some story out of the Arabian Nights made real, and did not know where to hide himself, when the woman before him seemed to be unconscious of his existence.
子爵夫人举起了右手的食指，优雅地示意侯爵坐到她身旁。 The Vicomtesse had raised the forefinger of her right hand, and gracefully signed to the Marquis to seat himself beside her.
侯爵感觉到了这手势中傲慢、忿怒之气，便转身走向她。 The Marquis felt the imperious sway of passion in her gesture; he came back towards her.
欧仁看着他，不无妒忌之心。 Eugene watched him, not without a feeling of envy.
“他便是那辆马车的主人！”他暗自说， “That is the owner of the brougham!” he said to himself.
“但是必须要有一对神采奕奕的骏马、身穿制服的仆人和滚滚金流才能吸引巴黎女子的目光吗？” “But is it necessary to have a pair of spirited horses, servants in livery, and torrents of gold to draw a glance from a woman here in Paris?”
奢靡这个恶魔撕咬着他的心脏，贪婪灼烧着他的血管，连喉咙都因为对金子的渴望而燥热难忍。 The demon of luxury gnawed at his heart, greed burned in his veins, his throat was parched with the thirst of gold.
他一个季度能拿一百三十法郎。 He had a hundred and thirty francs every quarter.
而他的父母、兄弟姐妹和姑妈一个月才花不到两百法郎。 His father, mother, brothers, sisters, and aunt did not spend two hundred francs a month among them.
他将自己的实际境况和理想状况在心里快速比较了一下，得出的结果让他变得迟钝起来。 This swift comparison between his present condition and the aims he had in view helped to benumb his faculties.
“为什么去不了？”子爵夫人笑着问葡萄牙人， “Why not?” the Vicomtesse was saying, as she smiled at the Portuguese.
“你为什么去不了意大利大街？” “Why cannot you come to the Italiens?”
“有正经事做！我要和英国大使共进晚餐。” “Affairs! I am to dine with the English Ambassador.”
“别理他啊。” “Throw him over.”
男人一旦编出一句谎话，就不得不谎上加谎。 When a man once enters on a course of deception, he is compelled to add lie to lie.
德阿尤达先生于是笑着说：“你这是在对我下命令吗？” M. d’Ajuda therefore said, smiling, “Do you lay your commands on me?”
“当然是。” “Yes, certainly.”
“我就是要你这句话。”他回答说。他带着能够让任何一个女人打消疑虑的眼神看了她一眼，好掩饰心中的真实想法。 “That was what I wanted to have you say to me,” he answered, dissembling his feelings in a glance which would have reassured any other woman.
他捧起子爵夫人的手，吻了一下，然后离开了。 He took the Vicomtesse’s hand, kissed it, and went.
欧仁用手拨了拨头发，很不自在地鞠了一躬。 Eugene ran his fingers through his hair, and constrained himself to bow.
他想现在德伯桑夫人总该注意到他了。但是她突然猛冲出去，冲到了走廊的窗边，看着德阿尤达先生上了马车。她听着他下指令，然后听到瑞士仆人传令给马车夫说：“去德洛希斐特先生家。” He thought that now Mme. de Beauseant would give him her attention; but suddenly she sprang forward, rushed to a window in the gallery, and watched M. d’Ajuda step into his carriage; she listened to the order that he gave, and heard the Swiss repeat it to the coachman: “To M. de Rochefide’s house.”
听到那些话，看到德阿尤达先生急忙冲上马车的动作，她简直就像被电闪雷击了一般。她走回客厅，极度的恐惧吞噬着她的心。 Those words, and the way in which M. d’Ajuda flung himself back in the carriage, were like a lightning flash and a thunderbolt for her; she walked back again with a deadly fear gnawing at her heart.
这种最可怕的灾难只会发生在上流社会中。 The most terrible catastrophes only happen among the heights.
子爵夫人回到自己的房间，坐在桌边，拿起一张精美的信纸。 The Vicomtesse went to her own room, sat down at a table, and took up a sheet of dainty notepaper.
“如果你没有和英国大使共进晚餐，”她写道，“而是去了洛希斐特家，那么你欠我个说法，我等着听你解释。” “When, instead of dining with the English Ambassador,” she wrote, “you go to the Rochefides, you owe me an explanation, which I am waiting to hear.”
由于手不停发抖，字迹不是很清晰，于是她重新描了几个字母。接着她签上“克莱尔·德布戈涅”的首字母C，然后便按铃叫人。 She retraced several of the letters, for her hand was trembling so that they were indistinct; then she signed the note with an initial C for “Claire de Bourgogne,” and rang the bell.
“雅克，”她对一位立即出现的仆人说，“拿上纸条，七点半去德洛希斐特府上，请德阿尤达侯爵收启。 “Jacques,” she said to the servant, who appeared immediately, “take this note to M. de Rochefide’s house at half-past seven and ask for the Marquis d’Ajuda.
要是德阿尤达先生在那里，留下条子就走，不用等回信；要是他不在，就把纸条带回来给我。” If M. d’Ajuda is there, leave the note without waiting for an answer; if he is not there, bring the note back to me.”
“子爵夫人，客厅里还有客人呢。” “Madame la Vicomtess, there is a visitor in the drawing-room.”
“噢！对了，当然。”她说着便打开门。 “Ah! yes, of course,” she said, opening the door.
欧仁开始觉得非常不安，但是最终子爵夫人还是出来了。在他们交谈之时，子爵夫人战栗的声音又让他的心起了波澜。 Eugene was beginning to feel very uncomfortable, but at last the Vicomtesse appeared; she spoke to him, and the tremulous tones of her voice vibrated through his heart.
“请原谅，先生，”她说，“我刚才要写封信。 “Pardon me, monsieur,” she said; “I had a letter to write.
现在没事了。” Now I am quite at liberty.”
她几乎不知道自己说了些什么，因为她说话时还在想着：“噢！莫非他想娶德洛希斐特小姐？ She scarcely knew what she was saying, for even as she spoke she thought, “Ah! he means to marry Mlle.de Rochefide?
但是他还是单身吗？ But is he still free?
今晚就得把这桩婚事搞砸，否则……但是明天之前我也应该知道结局了。” This evening the marriage shall be broken off, or else…But before to-morrow I shall know.”
“表姐……”那个学生说道。 “Cousin...” the student replied.
“嗯？”子爵夫人傲慢的眼神让欧仁打了个冷颤。他知道这一句“嗯？”代表什么。他在这三个小时里学到了很多，开始变得警觉起来。 “Eh?” said the Vicomtesse, with an insolent glance that sent a cold shudder through Eugene; he understood what that “Eh?” meant; he had learned a great deal in three hours, and his wits were on the alert.
他脸红了，改口叫道：“夫人……”。之后犹豫了片刻，他继续说道， He reddened: “Madame...” he began; he hesitated a moment, and then went on.
“请原谅我，我急需的庇护，能扯上一丁点亲戚关系对我也没坏处。” “Pardon me; I am in such need of protection that the nearest scrap of relationship could do me no harm.”
德伯桑夫人莞尔一笑，但笑得很苦涩。即使是现在她也感觉得到即将来临的痛苦，空气中弥漫着暴风雨爆发前的压抑气息。 Mme. de Beauseant smiled but there was sadness in her smile; even now she felt forebodings of the coming pain, the air she breathed was heavy with the storm that was about to burst.
“要是您知道我家的处境，”他继续说，“您一定愿意做个乐善好施的美丽教母，慈祥地为您保护的人扫除障碍。” “If you knew how my family are situated,” he went on, “you would love to play the part of a beneficent fairy godmother who graciously clears the obstacles from the path of her protege.”
“哦，表弟，”她笑着说，“那我能帮上什么忙呢？” “Well, cousin,” she said, laughing, “and how can I be of service to you?”
“这我也说不好。 “But do I know even that?
我跟您是远房亲戚，即使是远亲，关系也不甚明显，但对我来说这已经是完美的天赐之物了。 I am distantly related to you, and this obscure and remote relationship is even now a perfect godsend to me.
您让我感到困惑，我都不记得要跟您说些什么了。 You have confused my ideas; I cannot remember the things that I meant to say to you.
在巴黎我谁也不认识……哦，对了！只要您能给我点忠告，能把我看成一个乐意拜倒在您裙下、愿为您舍命的可怜孩子就行了。” I know no one else here in Paris...Ah! if I could only ask you to counsel me, ask you to look upon me as a poor child who would fain cling to the hem of your dress, who would lay down his life for you.”
“你会为我杀人吗？” “Would you kill a man for me?”
“杀一双都成。”欧仁说。 “Two，” said Eugene.
“你是个孩子。 “You, child.
是的，你还是个孩子。”她强忍着泪水说，“你会爱得很真诚的。” Yes, you are a child,” she said, keeping back the tears that came to her eyes; “you would love sincerely.”
“噢！”他抬头喊道。 “Oh!” he cried, flinging up his head.
这个学生大胆的回答勾起了子爵夫人对他的兴趣。 The audacity of the student’s answer interested the Vicomtesse in him.
这个南方傻小子第一次耍起了心眼。 The southern brain was beginning to scheme for the first time.
在德雷斯多夫人的蓝色卧房和德伯桑夫人的玫瑰色客厅之间，他提前三年读完了一套在巴黎潜在的规则。那是一种高等法律，而且研习者要是对其融会贯通的话，就等于驶上了一条通向成功的康庄大道。 Between Mme. de Restaud’s blue boudoir and Mme. de Beauseant’s rose-colored drawing-room he had made a three years’ advance in a kind of law which is not a recognized study in Paris, although it is a sort of higher jurisprudence, and, when well understood, is a highroad to success of every kind.
“对了！这就是我要说的！”欧仁说， “Ah! that is what I meant to say!” said Eugene.
“我在您的舞会上见到过德雷斯多夫人，今天早上我去拜访了她。” “I met Mme. de Restaud at your ball, and this morning I went to see her.”
“你一定妨碍到德雷斯多夫人了。”德伯桑夫人笑着说。 “You must have been very much in the way,” said Mme. de Beauseant, smiling as she spoke.
“确实是。 “Yes, indeed.
我初来乍到，要是没有您的忠告，我肯定会到处犯错，到处招人嫌。 I am a novice, and my blunders will set every one against me, if you do not give me your counsel.
我觉得，在巴黎很难碰到一位年轻、貌美、富有、时尚的女性愿意教我为人处世的方法，而你们女性能将其诠释得非常好。 I believe that in Paris it is very difficult to meet with a young, beautiful, and wealthy woman of fashion who would be willing to teach me, what you women can explain so well—life.
到处都是德特拉尔先生那样的人。 I shall find a M. de Trailles everywhere.
所以我就来请教您，希望您帮我揭开谜底，求求您告诉我，早上我究竟错在哪里了。 So I have come to you to ask you to give me a key to a puzzle, to entreat you to tell me what sort of blunder I made this morning.
我提到了一个老头——”“德朗热公爵夫人来了。”雅克打断了法律系学生的话。欧仁做出一个手势，说明他非常恼火。 I mentioned an old man—” “Madame la Duchess de Langeais,” Jacques cut the student short; Eugene gave expression to his intense annoyance by a gesture.
“如果你想要成功，”子爵夫人低声说，“首先不能喜怒形于色。” “If you mean to succeed,” said the Vicomtesse in a low voice, “in the first place you must not be so demonstrative.”
“噢！早上好，亲爱的。”她继续说道，同时站起身来，穿过屋子拉起了公爵夫人的手。她们似乎亲如姐妹。公爵夫人则以最美丽、最优雅的方式给予回应。 “Ah! good morning, dear,” she continued, and rising and crossing the room, she grasped the Duchess’ hands as affectionately as if they had been sisters; the Duchess responded in the prettiest and most gracious way.
“一对密友！”拉斯蒂涅自言自语道， “Two intimate friends!” said Rastignac to himself.
“自此我就有两个庇护人啦。这两个女人是好朋友，不用说，那位新来的公爵夫人肯定会对她朋友的表弟感兴趣的。” “Henceforward I shall have two protectresses; those two women are great friends, no doubt, and this newcomer will doubtless interest herself in her friend’s cousin.”
“我真是有幸能接待您这样的贵客，亲爱的安托瓦妮特！”德伯桑夫人招呼道。 “To what happy inspiration do I owe this piece of good fortune, dear Antoinette?” asked Mme. de Beauseant.
“是这样的，我在德洛希斐特先生家门前看到了德阿尤达·平托先生，所以我想你应该是独自在家了。” “Well, I saw M. d’Ajuda-Pinto at M. de Rochefide’s door, so I thought that if I came I should find you alone.”
公爵夫人说出这些要人命的话时，德伯桑夫人没有闭紧双唇，脸色没有涨红，她的表情也没有变化。更准确地说，她紧锁的眉头都骤然松开了。 Mme. de Beauseant’s mouth did not tighten, her color did not rise, her expression did not alter, or rather, her brow seemed to clear as the Duchess uttered those deadly words.
“要是我知道有客人在——”公爵夫人看了一眼欧仁，补充道。 “If I had known that you were engaged—” the speaker added, glancing at Eugene.
“这位是欧仁·德拉斯蒂涅先生，我的一个表弟。”子爵夫人介绍说。 “This gentleman is M. Eugene de Rastignac, one of my cousins,” said the Vicomtesse.
“你有德蒙特里沃将军的消息吗？”她继续问道， “Have you any news of General de Montriveau?” she continued.
“塞里奇昨天跟我说他现在哪里都不去，您今天见过他没？” “Serizy told me yesterday that he never goes anywhere now; has he been to see you to-day?”
据说公爵夫人疯狂地爱着这位德蒙特里沃先生，但他却背信弃义。她的心被这句话狠狠地揪了一下，红着脸回答说：“他昨天在爱丽舍宫呢。” It was believed that the Duchess was desperately in love with M. de Montriveau, and that he was a faithless lover; she felt the question in her very heart, and her face flushed as she answered: “He was at the Elysee yesterday.”
“去办公吗？” “In attendance?”
“克莱尔，”公爵夫人再看德伯桑夫人时，眼神里饱含着怨恨之情，“你一定知道德阿尤达·平托先生要娶德洛希斐特小姐了，这桩婚事明天就要公布于众了。” “Claire,” returned the Duchess, and hatred overflowed in the glances she threw at Mme. de Beauseant; “of course you know that M. d’Ajuda-Pinto is going to marry Mlle.de Rochefide; the bans will be published to-morrow.”
这句话深深地伤害了子爵夫人，她脸色煞白，不过还是笑着说：“这只不过是傻瓜们用来自娱自乐的一个谣言。 This thrust was too cruel; the Vicomtesse’s face grew white, but she answered, laughing, “One of those rumors that fools amuse themselves with.
洛希斐特家配得起德阿尤达这个葡萄牙最高贵的姓氏吗？ What should induce M. d’Ajuda to take one of the noblest names in Portugal to the Rochefides?
洛希斐特家被封为贵族好像还是昨天的事。” The Rochefides were only ennobled yesterday.”
“但是据说伯莎每年能拿到二十万里弗赫呢。” “But Bertha will have two hundred thousand livres a year, they say.”
“德阿尤达先生那么有钱，不会为了钱而结婚的。” “M. d’Ajuda is too wealthy to marry for money.”
“但是，亲爱的，德洛希斐特小姐可是个可人儿啊。” “But, my dear, Mlle.de Rochefide is a charming girl.”
“是吗？” “Indeed?”
“实际上，他们今天还会共进晚餐，这事算是板上钉钉了。 “And, as a matter of fact, he is dining with them to-day; the thing is settled.
我就纳闷你怎么了解得那么少。” It is very surprising to me that you should know so little about it.”
德伯桑夫人回过头来面对拉斯蒂涅。 Mme. de Beauseant turned to Rastignac.
“先生，你究竟做了什么错事？”她问， “What was the blunder that you made, monsieur?” she asked.
“这可怜的孩子涉世未深，安托瓦妮特，我们说的话他一点也不明白。 “The poor boy is only just launched into the world, Antoinette, so that he understands nothing of all this that we are speaking of.
就算可怜可怜这孩子吧，我们的话明天再说。 Be merciful to him, and let us finish our talk to-morrow.
你知道，到了明天一切将会公布于众，到时候就知道你出于好心告诉我的小道消息准确与否了。” Everything will be announced to-morrow, you know, and your kind informal communication can be accompanied by official confirmation.”
公爵夫人从头到脚地打量着欧仁，那种傲慢的眼神简直要把他压碎，并将他彻底毁灭。 The Duchess gave Eugene one of those insolent glances that measure a man from head to foot, and leave him crushed and annihilated.
“夫人，我不小心冒犯了德雷斯多夫人，我完全错在不小心上。”这位法律系学生说。他脑袋转得飞快，早就看穿了她们友好的谈话中暗藏着辛辣的讥讽。 “Madame, I have unwittingly plunged a dagger into Mme. de Restaud’s heart; unwittingly—therein lies my offence,” said the student of law, whose keen brain had served him sufficiently well, for he had detected the biting epigrams that lurked beneath this friendly talk.
“如果一个人故意伤害你，却知道他让你有多痛苦，你可能会继续接受他，也可能会惧怕他们。但是如果一个人伤害了你，却笨得不知道他伤人有多深的话，他就会被看成不会把握机会的傻瓜，会遭到大家的鄙视。” “You continue to receive, possibly you fear, those who know the amount of pain that they deliberately inflict; but a clumsy blunderer who has no idea how deeply he wounds is looked upon as a fool who does not know how to make use of his opportunities, and every one despises him.”
德伯桑夫人看了这个学生一眼，从她的眼神中可以看到她的心中交织着崇高与感恩。 Mme. de Beauseant gave the student a glance, one of those glances in which a great soul can mingle dignity and gratitude.
德伯桑夫人的目光给了他极大的安慰。在公爵夫人傲慢地审视下，这位法律系学生的思维越来越敏捷。公爵夫人看他的样子，就像拍卖员为了给拍卖品估价而在仔细查看一般。 It was like balm to the law student, who was still smarting under the Duchess’ insolent scrutiny; she had looked at him as an auctioneer might look at some article to appraise its value.
“再想想我刚才还和德雷斯多伯爵谈笑风生，夫人，我跟您说这些，是因为，”他谦恭而略带一丝狡黠地转向公爵夫人，继续说，“我只是一个可怜的大学生，在这世上又孤独又穷困——”“您别这样说，德拉斯蒂涅先生。 “Imagine, too, that I had just made some progress with the Comte de Restaud; for I should tell you, madame,” he went on, turning to the Duchess with a mixture of humility and malice in his manner, “that as yet I am only a poor devil of a student, very much alone in the world, and very poor—”“You should not tell us that, M. de Rastignac.
我们女人从不在意这些没人爱听的话。” We women never care about anything that no one else will take.”
“噢！”欧仁说， “Bah!” said Eugene.
“我只有二十二岁，我必须下决心弥补我这个年龄的劣势。 “I am only two-and-twenty, and I must make up my mind to the drawbacks of my time of life.
而且，我正在为我的过错忏悔，还有哪里能比这间迷人的忏悔室更好呢。您在这间客厅犯下罪孽，可以在别的客厅得到宽恕。” Besides, I am confessing my sins, and it would be impossible to kneel in a more charming confessional; you commit your sins in one drawing-room, and receive absolution for them in another.”
公爵夫人的脸色变得越来越冷漠，她不喜欢学生说这些话时的无礼口吻。为了显出自己认为这些话品位低俗，她转向子爵夫人，说：“这位先生才来——”德伯桑夫人立即开始嘲笑她表弟和公爵夫人。 The Duchess’ expression grew colder, she did not like the flippant tone of these remarks, and showed that she considered them to be in bad taste by turning to the Vicomtesse with—“This gentleman has only just come—” Mme. de Beauseant began to laugh outright at her cousin and at the Duchess both.
“他才来到巴黎，亲爱的，正在找老师帮他提高品位呢。” “He has only just come to Paris, dear, and is in search of some one who will give him lessons in good taste.”
“公爵夫人，”欧仁说，“我们想了解我们所爱慕的人，知道他们的秘密，这不是很平常吗？” “Mme. la Duchesse,” said Eugene, “is it not natural to wish to be initiated into the mysteries which charm us?”
（“算了吧，”他暗自想，“我敢肯定我说的话已经很优雅了。”）“不过我相信德雷斯多夫人自己也是德特拉尔先生的‘学生’吧。”公爵夫人说。 (“Come, now,” he said to himself, “my language is superfinely elegant, I’m sure.”) “But Mme. de Restaud is herself, I believe, M. de Trailles’ pupil,” said the Duchess.
“这我就不清楚了，夫人。”这个法律系学生回答，“我还莽撞地冲到他们中间了。 “Of that I had no idea, madame,” answered the law student, “so I rashly came between them.
其实我同这位女士的丈夫相处得很好，夫人一度对我也还算客气，直到我突然想到要和他们说，我认识一个人，之前我刚好瞧见他从后楼梯上下来，还在走廊尽头和伯爵夫人亲吻。” In fact, I got on very well with the lady’s husband, and his wife tolerated me for a time until I took it into my head to tell them that I knew some one of whom I had just caught a glimpse as he went out by a back staircase, a man who had given the Countess a kiss at the end of a passage.”
“他是谁？”两位女士异口同声地问。 “Who was it?” both women asked together.
“一个住在圣马尔索郊区（注：圣马塞尔郊区的别名），每月靠两个路易过活的老头，我这个穷学生也住在那里。 “An old man who lives at the rate of two louis a month in the Faubourg Saint-Marceau, where I, a poor student, lodge likewise.
他真是个不幸的人，每个人都笑话他——我们都叫他‘高老头’。”“天啊，你真是个小孩。”子爵夫人叫道，“德雷斯多夫人过去就是高里奥小姐啊！” He is a truly unfortunate creature, everybody laughs at him—we all call him ‘Father Goriot.’”“Why, child that you are,” cried the Vicomtesse, “Mme. de Restaud was a Mlle. Goriot!”
“面条制造商的女儿。”公爵夫人补充道，“那个小姑娘进宫时，一个糕点师傅的女儿正好也在场。 “The daughter of a vermicelli manufacturer,” the Duchess added; “and when the little creature went to Court, the daughter of a pastry-cook was presented on the same day.
你还记得吗，克莱尔？ Do you remember, Claire?
国王发笑了，还用拉丁文说了几个关于面粉的笑话。 The King began to laugh, and made some joke in Latin about flour.
人——怎么说来着？人——”“都是一样的面粉。”欧仁说。 People—what was it?—People—” “@Ejusdem farinae@,” said Eugene.
“对了，就是这句。”公爵夫人说。 “Yes, that was it,” said the Duchess.
“哦！那是她父亲？”这个法律系学生大为吃惊，继续问道。 “Oh! is that her father?” the law student continued, aghast.
“当然了。这老头有两个女儿。可以这么说，他很宠爱两个女儿，但她们几乎都不认他了。” “Yes, certainly; the old man had two daughters; he dotes on them, so to speak, though they will scarcely acknowledge him.”
“那小女儿不是嫁给了一个有德国姓氏的银行家了吗？”子爵夫人转向德朗热夫人闻道，“是不是叫德纽沁根男爵？ “Didn’t the second daughter marry a banker with a German name?” the Vicomtesse asked, turning to Mme. de Langeais, “a Baron de Nucingen?
她不是叫德尔菲娜吗？ And her name is Delphine, is it not?
是那个在歌剧院有个侧面包厢的金发女人吧？ Isn’t she a fair-haired woman who has a side-box at the Opera?
她有时会去看谐谑剧，大声笑着来吸引别人的注意。” She comes sometimes to the Bouffons, and laughs loudly to attract attention.”
公爵夫人笑着说：“我真佩服你，亲爱的。 The Duchess smiled and said: “I wonder at you, dear.
你怎么会对那种人如此感兴趣呢？ Why do you take so much interest in people of that kind?
肯定有人像德雷斯多以前那样，疯狂地爱上这位阿纳斯塔谢小姐和她的面粉袋。 One must have been as madly in love as Restaud was, to be infatuated with Mlle. Anastasie and her flour sacks.
哦！他以后会发现她不是一个好对象。 Oh! he will not find her a good bargain!
她现在落在德特拉尔先生手上了，他会毁掉她的。” She is in M. de Trailles’ hands, and he will ruin her.”
“她们还不理睬她们的父亲！”欧仁重复道。 “And they do not acknowledge their father!” Eugene repeated.
“对啊！她们的父亲，这个父亲真是个父亲。”子爵夫人回答说，“据说他是个慈祥的父亲，给了每个女儿五六十万法郎，帮她们嫁个好郎君，保证以后她们能过好日子。然而，他每年却只给自己留八千或一万里弗赫。他想着女儿终究是女儿，她们两个活好了，他等于活了两遍，她们两个成家了，他等于有了两个家，而且家里的人会爱戴他、尊敬他、重视他。 “Oh! well, yes, their father, the father, a father,” replied the Vicomtesse, “a kind father who gave them each five or six hundred thousand francs, it is said, to secure their happiness by marrying them well; while he only kept eight or ten thousand livres a year for himself, thinking that his daughters would always be his daughters, thinking that in them he would live his life twice over again, that in their houses he should find two homes, where he would be loved and looked up to, and made much of.
但两年时间里，两个女婿都把他赶出家门，就像他是社会最底层的流浪汉一样。” And in two years’ time both his sons-in-law had turned him out of their houses as if he were one of the lowest outcasts.”
欧仁的眼里泛着泪光。 Tears came into Eugene’s eyes.
他的心里仍保存着年轻人的信仰。他刚离家不久，心里还装着纯洁、高尚的亲情，这还是他在巴黎初次体验文明的战场。 He was still under the spell of youthful beliefs, he had just left home, pure and sacred feelings had been stirred within him, and this was his first day on the battlefield of civilization in Paris.
真挚的情感有多么强的感染力啊，有好一阵子三人都相顾无言。 Genuine feeling is so infectious that for a moment the three looked at each other in silence.
“啊，我的上帝！”德朗热夫人说，“这件事情看起来的确很可怕，但我们天天见到这样的事情。 “@Eh, mon Dieu!@” said Mme. de Langeais; “yes, it seems very horrible, and yet we see such things every day.
难道就没有个原因吗？ Is there not a reason for it?
告诉我，亲爱的，你有没有真正想过什么才是女婿？ Tell me, dear, have you ever really thought what a son-in-law is?
女婿就是这样一类人，我们为他养大与我们有着千丝万缕联系的小宝贝——十七岁前，她是家里快乐的源泉，正如拉马丁（注：拉马丁是法国十八世末到十九世纪中期著名的作家、诗人和政治家）所说的那样，她有“洁白的灵魂”，但十七岁之后，她就会突然变成家里痛苦的源泉。女婿过来把她从我们的手中夺走，他的爱从一开始就像一把斧子，从根上斩断了我们女儿过去所有的情谊，砍断了她和家里的所有联系。 A son-in-law is the man for whom we bring up, you and I, a dear little one, bound to us very closely in innumerable ways; for seventeen years she will be the joy of her family, its ‘white soul,’ as Lamartine says, and suddenly she will become its scourge.When HE comes and takes her from us, his love from the very beginning is like an axe laid to the root of all the old affection in our darling’s heart, and all the ties that bound her to her family are severed.
昨天，我们的女儿还只想着她的父母，就像我们只想着她一样；但是明天，她就会变成一个带着敌意的陌生人。 But yesterday our little daughter thought of no one but her mother and father, as we had no thought that was not for her; by to-morrow she will have become a hostile stranger.
这样的悲剧总在我们眼皮底下上演。 The tragedy is always going on under our eyes.
这边你看见一位父亲为儿子牺牲自己，儿媳却对他蛮横无理到了极点。 On the one hand you see a father who has sacrificed himself to his son, and his daughter-in-law shows him the last degree of insolence.
那边一个女婿又把他岳母赶出家门了。 On the other hand, it is the son-in-law who turns his wife’s mother out of the house.
我有时听人说，近来，世上已经没有什么令人吃惊的事了，但是女婿这台戏格外令人吃惊。且不说我们的婚姻，这台戏都变成一出拙劣的闹剧了。 I sometimes hear it said that there is nothing dramatic about society in these days; but the Drama of the Son-in-law is appalling, to say nothing of our marriages, which have come to be very poor farces.
我可以把那个老面条商的遭遇解释得一清二楚。 I can explain how it all came about in the old vermicelli maker’s case.
我想我记得那个弗里奥——”“高里奥，夫人。” I think I recollect that Foriot—” “Goriot, madame.”
“是的，大革命时期，那个莫里奥曾是他们区的区长。 “Yes, that Moriot was once President of his Section during the Revolution.
他知道那次有名的粮食短缺的内幕。那时，他以成本价十倍的价钱出售面粉，靠着倒卖面粉积累了第一笔财富。 He was in the secret of the famous scarcity of grain, and laid the foundation of his fortune in those days by selling flour for ten times its cost.
他屯足了面粉。 He had as much flour as he wanted.
我祖母的管家就卖给他很多。 My grandmother’s steward sold him immense quantities.
毫无疑问，诺里奥和救国委员会瓜分了那笔暴利，那些人过去一直都这样干。 No doubt Noriot shared the plunder with the Committee of Public Salvation, as that sort of person always did.
我记起来那个管家还告诉我祖母，说她也许可以安安全全地住在格朗维莱尔，因为她的麦子就是一张很好的公民证。 I recollect the steward telling my grandmother that she might live at Grandvilliers in complete security, because her corn was as good as a certificate of civism.
后来他们说，那个把麦子卖给那些侩子手的洛里奥只钟情于一件事——溺爱女儿。 Well, then, this Loriot, who sold corn to those butchers, has never had but one passion, they say—he idolizes his daughters.
他把一个女儿安顿在雷斯多家，把另一个嫁到纽沁根家族。德纽沁根男爵是一个富有的银行家，他后来变成保皇党的人了。 He settled one of them under Restaud’s roof, and grafted the other into the Nucingen family tree, the Baron de Nucingen being a rich banker who had turned Royalist.
你明白当初波拿巴是皇帝，两个女婿还尽量忍受这个支持大革命的老家伙。但波旁王朝复辟之后，德雷斯多先生对老头的生活圈子感到厌烦了，那银行家就更厌恶他了。 You can quite understand that so long as Bonaparte was Emperor, the two sons-in-law could manage to put up with the old Ninety-three; but after the restoration of the Bourbons, M. de Restaud felt bored by the old man’s society, and the banker was still more tired of it.
他的女儿们依旧爱戴他，她们想‘羊与洋白菜兼得’。所以在没有访客的时候，她们会探望待乔里奥，假装非常爱慕父亲。 His daughters were still fond of him; they wanted ‘to keep the goat and the cabbage,’ so they used to see Joriot whenever there was no one there, under pretence of affection.
‘今天来吧，爸爸，我们会全心全意服侍您，这样就更好了！’等等诸如此类的话。 ‘Come to-day, papa, we shall have you all to ourselves, and that will be much nicer!’ and all that sort of thing.
至于我，亲爱的，我相信爱是有洞察力的，这个大革命时期的可怜老头的心肯定在滴血。 As for me, dear, I believe that love has second-sight: poor Ninety-three; his heart must have bled.
他看出女儿们因为他而觉得羞愧，还看出如果她们真爱自己的丈夫，那么他的拜访就会离间他们的感情。 He saw that his daughters were ashamed of him, that if they loved their husbands his visits must make mischief.
所以他牺牲了自己。 So he immolated himself.
他做出牺牲是因为他是父亲，于是他自愿退出了。 He made the sacrifice because he was a father; he went into voluntary exile.
他的女儿们心满意足了，所以他觉得这是他能做的最好事情了。但这却是一宗父亲和女儿合谋的家庭犯罪。 His daughters were satisfied, so he thought that he had done the best thing he could; but it was a family crime, and father and daughters were accomplices.
这样的情形随处可见。 You see this sort of thing everywhere.
这多里奥老头不过是女儿客厅里溅的一点泥，不然还能是什么呢？ What could this old Doriot have been but a splash of mud in his daughters’ drawing-rooms?
他只是碍手碍脚、惹人厌烦的那个人，而且连他自己也讨厌自己。 He would only have been in the way, and bored other people, besides being bored himself.
父女三人之间发生的事也可能会发生在巴黎最漂亮的女人和她最爱的男人之间。如果她的爱使人厌倦，他会走开。他不惜使出最卑微的把戏来躲开她。 And this that happened between father and daughters may happen to the prettiest woman in Paris and the man she loves the best; if her love grows tiresome, he will go; he will descend to the basest trickery to leave her.
爱和友谊，都是如此。 It is the same with all love and friendship.
我们的心如同一座宝库，假使你一次倾尽所有财富，你就会破产。 Our heart is a treasury; if you pour out all its wealth at once, you are bankrupt.
这些将情感挥霍一空的人和那一类挥霍到身无分文的人一样，得不到人们的同情。 We show no more mercy to the affection that reveals its utmost extent than we do to another kind of prodigal who has not a penny left.
她们父亲已经把他的全部给了女儿。 Their father had given them all he had.
二十年来，他对她们倾注了所有心血。之后的一天，他又把自己所有的家产都给了她们。 For twenty years he had given his whole heart to them; then, one day, he gave them all his fortune too.
女孩们榨干柠檬后，就把残余物扔进了排水沟。” The lemon was squeezed; the girls left the rest in the gutter.”
“这个社会真卑鄙。”子爵夫人边说边拔着披肩上的细线。 “The world is very base,” said the Vicomtesse, plucking at the threads of her shawl.
说话时，她没有抬头。德朗热夫人说这故事时，有些话是冲着她说的，这些话正中要害。 She did not raise her head as she spoke; the words that Mme. de Langeais had meant for her in the course of her story had cut her to the quick.
“卑鄙？ “Base?
哦，不是的。”公爵夫人回答说，“世界就是这样运转的，没别的。 Oh, no,” answered the Duchess; “the world goes its own way, that is all.
如果我这样说，只是证明我没有被这个世道愚弄。 If I speak in this way, it is only to show that I am not duped by it.
我想的跟你一样。”她说着握紧了子爵夫人的手。 I think as you do,” she said, pressing the Vicomtesse’s hand.
“这个世界就是一个大泥潭，我们要努力站在高处。” “The world is a slough; let us try to live on the heights above it.”
她站起来亲吻了德伯桑夫人的额头，然后说：“你今天看起来非常迷人，亲爱的。我之前从来没见到你的脸色这么好过。” She rose to her feet and kissed Mme. de Beauseant on the forehead as she said: “You look very charming to-day, dear.I have never seen such a lovely color in your cheeks before.”
接着她向这位表弟微微点头后便走出去了。 Then she went out with a slight inclination of the head to the cousin.
“高老头真令人尊敬啊！”欧仁自言自语道，同时想起自己那晚看到他的邻居将一个银盘扭成奇形怪状的一团。 “Father Goriot is sublime!” said Eugene to himself, as he remembered how he had watched his neighbor work the silver vessel into a shapeless mass that night.
德伯桑夫人没有听见他的话，她想得入神了。 Mme. de Beauseant did not hear him; she was absorbed in her own thoughts.
这样的沉默维持了好几分钟都没有被打破。这位法律系学生几乎因为这种尴尬的气氛而手脚麻痹了，他既不敢离开，也不敢逗留，又不敢开口说话。 For several minutes the silence remained unbroken till the law student became almost paralyzed with embarrassment, and was equally afraid to go or stay or speak a word.
“这个世界真是卑贱、粗暴而且恶毒。”子爵夫人终于说道， “The world is basely ungrateful and ill-natured,” said the Vicomtesse at last.
“只要你一碰上麻烦，就会有朋友来告诉你这个消息，用刀尖刺你的心脏，还让你欣赏刀柄。 “No sooner does a trouble befall you than a friend is ready to bring the tidings and to probe your heart with the point of a dagger while calling on you to admire the handle.
讽刺、挖苦接踵而至！ Epigrams and sarcasms already!
啊！我要保护自己！” Ah! I will defend myself!”
她仰起头，那个姿势正好显出她贵妇人的气质，那种骄傲的眼神散发出闪电般的光芒。 She raised her head like the great lady that she was, and lightnings flashed from her proud eyes.
“啊！”她一边转向欧仁一边问，“你还在吗？” “Ah!” she said, as she saw Eugene, “are you there?”
“是的，还在。”他可怜兮兮地回答。 “Still,” he said piteously.
“那么，德拉斯蒂涅先生，你该给这个社会它应得的惩罚。 “Well, then, M. de Rastignac, deal with the world as it deserves.
你想要成功吗？ You are determined to succeed?
我会帮助你。 I will help you.
你会测出女人堕落得有多深，你也会衡量出男人虚荣得有多可悲。 You shall sound the depths of corruption in woman; you shall measure the extent of man’s pitiful vanity.
虽然人生这部书我已经读得非常透彻了，但以前始终有几页没有读到。 Deeply as I am versed in such learning, there were pages in the book of life that I had not read.
现在我都明白了。 Now I know all.
你越是冷血、越会算计，就走得越远。 The more cold-blooded your calculations, the further you will go.
如果你冷酷无情地打击了别人，别人就会怕了你。 Strike ruthlessly; you will be feared.
对你来说，世间男女只能是驿马，轮班上路，在用尽他们最后一丝力气后，就把他们丢在路边，这样你才能抵达自己远大抱负的目的地。 Men and women for you must be nothing more than post-horses; take a fresh relay, and leave the last to drop by the roadside; in this way you will reach the goal of your ambition.
你看，除非有女人对你感兴趣，你在这里什么都不是，而且她必须年轻、富有，经常出入交际场所。 You will be nothing here, you see, unless a woman interests herself in you; and she must be young and wealthy, and a woman of the world.
然而，如果你还有真情，就把它当成宝贝一样好好锁起来，别让任何人起疑心，否则你会迷失自我，你将不再是行刑官，而会变成受害者。 Yet, if you have a heart, lock it carefully away like a treasure; do not let any one suspect it, or you will be lost; you would cease to be the executioner, you would take the victim’s place.
如果你真的遇到你的真爱，要坚决保守秘密！ And if ever you should love, never let your secret escape you!
在你确定敞开心扉之前，不要相信任何人。 Trust no one until you are very sure of the heart to which you open your heart.
要学会怀疑每一个人，为了你还未到来的真爱，要对每件事怀有戒心。 Learn to mistrust every one; take every precaution for the sake of the love which does not exist as yet.
听着，米格尔，”——这个名字自然而然地从她口中说出来，她都没注意到自己叫错了——“还有比忘恩负义的女儿遗弃父亲、希望父亲早死这种丑闻更可怕的事情呢，这就是两姐妹之间的敌意。 Listen, Miguel”—the name slipped from her so naturally that she did not notice her mistake—“there is something still more appalling than the ingratitude of daughters who have cast off their old father and wish that he were dead, and that is a rivalry between two sisters.
雷斯多出身良好，他的夫人也被这个圈子接受了，而且她还进过宫；而她的妹妹呢，她有钱的妹妹德尔菲娜·德纽沁根——大资本家的老婆——被妒忌心折磨得快要忿怒而死了。 Restaud comes of a good family, his wife has been received into their circle; she has been presented at court; and her sister, her wealthy sister, Mme. Delphine de Nucingen, the wife of a great capitalist, is consumed with envy, and ready to die of spleen.
这就是两姐妹之间的鸿沟——其实，她们再也不是姐妹了——这两个女人拒绝承认她们的父亲，也不承认彼此。 There is gulf set between the sisters—indeed, they are sisters no longer—the two women who refuse to acknowledge their father do not acknowledge each other.
所以德纽沁根夫人为了能进我的沙龙，就算让她把从圣拉扎尔街到格勒内勒街的土舔干净，她都愿意。 So Mme. de Nucingen would lap up all the mud that lies between the Rue Saint-Lazare and the Rue de Grenelle to gain admittance to my salon.
她幻想着能通过德马尔塞来达到自己的目的，她已经把自己变成德马尔塞的奴隶了，她却让他感到厌恶了。 She fancied that she should gain her end through de Marsay; she has made herself de Marsay’s slave, and she bores him.
德马尔赛一点都不关心她。 De Marsay cares very little about her.
如果你能把她引见给我，那么你会成为她的甜心，她的便雅悯（注：“便雅悯”为《圣经》人物，指受宠爱的幼子），她会崇拜你的。 If you will introduce her to me, you will be her darling, her Benjamin; she will idolize you.
如果在那之后，你能爱上她，就尽情地爱吧；要是没有爱上她，就好好利用她。 If, after that, you can love her, do so; if not, make her useful.
我会在人多的社交聚会中邀请她一两次，但是在早上这里绝不接待她。 I will ask her to come once or twice to one of my great crushes, but I will never receive her here in the morning.
我看见她时，会点头打招呼，那也就足够了。 I will bow to her when I see her, and that will be quite sufficient.
你说出高老头的名字时，德雷斯多伯爵夫人家的大门就对你关上了。 You have shut the Comtesse de Restaud’s door against you by mentioning Father Goriot’s name.
是的，我的好朋友，你可以去她家二十次，但你会发现二十次她都不在家。 Yes, my good friend, you may call at her house twenty times, and every time out of the twenty you will find that she is not at home.
他们的仆人都得到了命令，不会接待你了。 The servants have their orders, and will not admit you.
很好，那么，就让高老头为你进入她姐姐的家门争取权利吧。 Very well, then, now let Father Goriot gain the right of entry into her sister’s house for you.
这位美丽的德纽沁根夫人会为你发出战争的信号。 The beautiful Mme. de Nucingen will give the signal for a battle.
一旦她将你挑中，其他的女人都会为你疯狂，她的敌人、对手和密友都会想从她那里把你抢到手。 As soon as she singles you out, other women will begin to lose their heads about you, and her enemies and rivals and intimate friends will all try to take you from her.
有一些女人，她们爱上一个男人，仅仅因为其他女人看中了他。就像一些市井妇人一样，真是一群可怜虫。我们戴什么帽子，她们也跟着戴，希望由此学到我们的风度。 There are women who will fall in love with a man because another woman has chosen him; like the city madams, poor things, who copy our millinery, and hope thereby to acquire our manners.
你会成功的，在巴黎拥有成功就是拥有一切，成功是开启权力之门的钥匙。 You will have a success, and in Paris success is everything; it is the key of power.
如果女人觉得你有智慧、有天赋，只要你自己不戳穿自己，男人也会跟着相信你的。 If the women credit you with wit and talent, the men will follow suit so long as you do not undeceive them yourself.
那时，你什么都想做，你会去很多地方，会看清这个世界的本质——这个世界只不过是笨蛋和无赖的聚居之地。 There will be nothing you may not aspire to; you will go everywhere, and you will find out what the world is—an assemblage of fools and knaves.
但是你既不要当笨蛋也不要当无赖。 But you must be neither the one nor the other.
我会把我的姓氏给你，它就像阿里阿德涅的线索一样。你带着它进迷宫吧，别把它浪费了。”她说着看了拉斯蒂涅一眼。她的眼神和颈部曲线如王后般高雅，“将来干干净净地把它还给我。 I am giving you my name like Ariadne’s clue of thread to take with you into the labyrinth; make no unworthy use of it,” she said, with a queenly glance and curve of her throat; “give it back to me unsullied.
好了，现在你走吧，让我清静一会儿。 And now, go; leave me.
我们女人也有自己的仗要打。” We women also have our battles to fight.”
“不管什么时候，如果你需要一个忠心的人为你点燃导火线——”“怎么样？”她问。 “And if you should ever need some one who would gladly set a match to a train for you—” “Well?” she asked.
他拍拍胸口，与表姐相视一笑当作回答，然后就走了。 He tapped his heart, smiled in answer to his cousin’s smile, and went.
已经五点了，欧仁觉得饿了，他害怕自己赶不上晚饭，这一忧虑使他感到了能在巴黎扶摇直上的快乐。 It was five o’clock, and Eugene was hungry; he was afraid lest he should not be in time for dinner, a misgiving which made him feel that it was pleasant to be borne so quickly across Paris.
有了身体上的舒适，那么思想上就可以自由地与困扰他的想法作斗争了。 This sensation of physical comfort left his mind free to grapple with the thoughts that assailed him.
耻辱感通常会使他这年纪的人狂怒不已。当这些人的信仰被动摇了，他们就会对社会挥舞起拳头，发誓要报仇。 A mortification usually sends a young man of his age into a furious rage; he shakes his fist at society, and vows vengeance when his belief in himself is shaken.
刚才，拉斯蒂涅因为那句“德雷斯多伯爵夫人家的大门就对你关上了”而倍受打击。 Just then Rastignac was overwhelmed by the words, “You have shut the Countess’ door against you.”
“我要去她家！”他对自己说，“如果德伯桑夫人是对的，如果她永远不接待我——我……那么，德雷斯多夫人将会在巴黎的每一间沙龙里都碰到我。 “I shall call!” he said to himself, “and if Mme. de Beauseant is right, if I never find her at home—I...well, Mme. de Restaud shall meet me in every salon in Paris.
我要学习剑术，再练习一下射击，然后杀了她的马克西姆！” I will learn to fence and have some pistol practice, and kill that Maxime of hers!”
“但我有钱吗？”内心的一个声音喊道， “And money?” cried an inward monitor.
“钱的问题怎么解决，我从哪里弄钱呢？” “How about money, where is that to come from?”
突然，他眼前浮现出了德雷斯多伯爵夫人家的客厅和客厅里的奢华气派。 And all at once the wealth displayed in the Countess de Restaud’s drawing-room rose before his eyes.
那是高老头之女曾梦寐以求的奢华：满屋金碧辉煌、外表光彩照人，像暴发户一样讲求庸俗的排场，像情妇一样放荡、铺张。 That was the luxury which Goriot’s daughter had loved too well, the gilding, the ostentatious splendor, the unintelligent luxury of the parvenu, the riotous extravagance of a courtesan.
但当他想起德伯桑公馆的庄严、高贵时，这一迷人的景象顿时黯然失色了。 Then the attractive vision suddenly went under an eclipse as he remembered the stately grandeur of the Hotel de Beauseant.
他的幻想游走在巴黎这个宏大世界的上流社会，脑子里聚集了无数坏念头，他的眼界更宽了，良知也变得更加能屈能伸了。 As his fancy wandered among these lofty regions in the great world of Paris, innumerable dark thoughts gathered in his heart; his ideas widened, and his conscience grew more elastic.
他看清了世界的本来面目，看到富人是怎样凌驾于法律体系和公众舆论之上，发现成功才是最终的决定因素。 He saw the world as it is; saw how the rich lived beyond the jurisdiction of law and public opinion, and found in success the ultima ratio mundi.
“沃尔特兰说得没错，成功才是美德！”他对自己说。 “Vautrin is right, success is virtue!” he said to himself.
到了新圣热讷维耶沃街，他冲进房间拿出十法郎付给车夫，然后就去吃饭了。 Arrived in the Rue Neuve-Sainte-Genevieve, he rushed up to his room for ten francs wherewith to satisfy the demands of the cabman, and went in to dinner.
他环顾了一下肮脏的屋子，看到十八个穷困潦倒的家伙像马厩里的牲畜一样准备吃东西，这个场面让他非常厌恶。 He glanced round the squalid room, saw the eighteen poverty-stricken creatures about to feed like cattle in their stalls, and the sight filled him with loathing.
突如其来的转变和巨大的反差变成了一剂强有力的兴奋剂。他的野心不断膨胀，最后超出了所有的阶级限制。 The transition was too sudden, and the contrast was so violent that it could not but act as a powerful stimulant; his ambition developed and grew beyond all social bounds.
一方面，他看到了社会最迷人、最精致的一面，看到了激情澎湃的年轻人，看到了他们容貌姣好、热情洋溢的脸庞。他们被包围在奢侈品和艺术品装饰的美妙场景中；另一方面，他又看到了社会的昏暗面，看到每张脸上都沾着泥污，没有任何激情，用来装饰场景的只有绳索、滑车和没有遮盖的机械。 On the one hand, he beheld a vision of social life in its most charming and refined forms, of quick-pulsed youth, of fair, impassioned faces invested with all the charm of poetry, framed in a marvelous setting of luxury or art; and, on the other hand, he saw a sombre picture, the miry verge beyond these faces, in which passion was extinct and nothing was left of the drama but the cords and pulleys and bare mechanism.
德伯桑夫人的忠告、那个弃妇愤怒时说的话、她盛怒之下的建议涌上欧仁的心头，贫穷是现成的解说者。 Mme. de Beauseant’s counsels, the words uttered in anger by the forsaken lady, her petulant offer, came to his mind, and poverty was a ready expositor.
拉斯蒂涅决定双管齐下，以保证成功，他会成为一个学识渊博的法律博士和一个时尚男性的。 Rastignac determined to open two parallel trenches so as to insure success; he would be a learned doctor of law and a man of fashion.
他显然还是个孩子！ Clearly he was still a child!
这两条路是渐近线，永远不可能有交点。 Those two lines are asymptotes, and will never meet.
“你太无精打采了，侯爵大人。”沃尔特兰说。他敏锐的目光似乎能看穿别人藏在内心最深处的秘密。 “You are very dull, my lord Marquis,” said Vautrin, with one of the shrewd glances that seem to read the innermost secrets of another mind.
“别叫我‘侯爵大人’，我现在没心情听别人开这个玩笑。”欧仁回答说， “I am not in the humor to stand jokes from people who call me ‘my lord Marquis,” answered Eugene.
“如果他不是十足的骗子，在巴黎，一位侯爵一年至少能拿到十万里弗赫，而一个在‘沃盖之家’的房客绝不会是命运的宠儿。” “A marquis here in Paris, if he is not the veriest sham, ought to have a hundred thousand livres a year at least; and a lodger in the Maison Vauquer is not exactly Fortune’s favorite.”
沃尔特兰看拉斯蒂涅的眼神中一半是父亲般的温暖，一半是轻蔑。 Vautrin’s glance at Rastignac was half-paternal, half-contemptuous.
“傲慢的小子！”他似乎在说，“我一口就可以吞掉他！” “Puppy!” it seemed to say; “I should make one mouthful of him!”
之后他回答说：“你心情不好，或许是因为你刚才去拜访美丽的德雷斯多伯爵夫人时没有成功吧。” Then he answered: “You are in a bad humor; perhaps your visit to the beautiful Comtesse de Restaud was not a success.”
“她以后不会再接待我了，因为我告诉她，她的父亲跟我们坐在一张桌子上吃饭。”拉斯蒂涅叫道。 “She has shut her door against me because I told her that her father dined at our table,” cried Rastignac.
房里的人都交换了一下眼色，高老头垂下了头。 Glances were exchanged all round the room; Father Goriot looked down.
“你把鼻烟吹进我眼睛啦。”他一边对旁边的人说，一边稍稍转过去，用手擦着脸。 “You have sent some snuff into my eye,” he said to his neighbor, turning a little aside to rub his hand over his face.
“从今往后，谁再欺负高老头，就是跟我过不去，”欧仁说着看了一眼老头旁边的人，“我们加起来都没他重要。——女士除外。”他冲着塔耶费小姐补充了一句。 “Any one who molests Father Goriot will have henceforward to reckon with me,” said Eugene, looking at the old man’s neighbor; “he is worth all the rest of us put together.—I am not speaking of the ladies,” he added, turning in the direction of Mlle. Taillefer.
欧仁的话引起了轰动，他的语气使整个饭桌上的人都安静了下来。 Eugene’s remarks produced a sensation, and his tone silenced the dinner-table.
只有沃尔特兰一个人说话了， Vautrin alone spoke.
“要是你想保护高老头，并且自认为是他的责任编辑，那么你得做个百发百中的狙击手，还要学会击剑。”他半开玩笑地说。 “If you are going to champion Father Goriot, and set up for his responsible editor into the bargain, you had need be a crack shot and know how to handle the foils,” he said, banteringly.
“我就打算这么做。”欧仁说。 “So I intend,” said Eugene.
“那么，你今天就正式披挂上阵了？” “Then you are taking the field today?”
“也许吧。”拉斯蒂涅回答说， “Perhaps,” Rastignac answered.
“但是，我不需要向任何人解释，尤其是在我不想知道别人夜里都在做什么的时候。” “But I owe no account of myself to any one, especially as I do not try to find out what other people do of a night.”
沃尔特兰斜着眼看着拉斯蒂涅， Vautrin looked askance at Rastignac.
“我的孩子，要是你不想被木偶欺骗，你必须走到后台去看这场演出。不要从幕布的缝隙里看。 “If you do not mean to be deceived by the puppets, my boy, you must go behind and see the whole show, and not peep through holes in the curtain.
这就够了。”他看到欧仁快要发火了，就加了一句， That is enough,” he added, seeing that Eugene was about to fly into a passion.
“只要你愿意，我们随时可以闲聊几句。” “We can have a little talk whenever you like.”
大家都感到了郁闷和压抑。 There was a general feeling of gloom and constraint.
高老头听了大学生这番话，深感沮丧，而没有注意到其他房客的内心起了变化，也没有意识到他遇见了一位保护人，能帮他从此免受迫害。 Father Goriot was so deeply dejected by the student’s remark that he did not notice the change in the disposition of his fellow-lodgers, nor know that he had met with a champion capable of putting an end to the persecution.
“那就是说，坐在这里的高里奥先生是一位伯爵夫人的父亲。”沃盖夫人小声说。 “Then, M. Goriot sitting there is the father of a countess,” said Mme. Vauquer in a low voice.
“还是一位男爵夫人的父亲。”拉斯蒂涅回答道。 “And of a baroness,” answered Rastignac.
“这就是他的全部能力了。”比安卡肖恩对拉斯蒂涅说，“我看过他的脑袋，上面只有一处隆起的地方——装的全是父爱，他一定是位永远都会疼爱女儿的父亲。” “That is about all he is capable of,” said Bianchon to Rastignac; “I have taken a look at his head; there is only one bump—the bump of Paternity; he must be an ETERNAL FATHER.”
欧仁太专注于想自己的事，听了比安卡肖恩的笑话后并没有发笑。 Eugene was too intent on his thoughts to laugh at Bianchon’s joke.
他决定采纳德伯桑夫人的提议来获得利益，并想着怎样才能获取必要的资金。 He determined to profit by Mme. de Beauseant’s counsels, and was asking himself how he could obtain the necessary money.
他变得非常严肃。 He grew grave.
社会这一辽阔的热带稀树草原尽现于他眼前，一切都呈现在他面前，可是没有一件是他的。 The wide savannas of the world stretched before his eyes; all things lay before him, nothing was his.
吃完晚饭，其他房客都走了，只有他独自留在餐厅。 Dinner came to an end, the others went, and he was left in the dining-room.
“这样看来，你见到我女儿了？”高老头颤颤巍巍地问道。他的声音打断了欧仁的沉思。 “So you have seen my daughter?” Goriot spoke tremulously, and the sound of his voice broke in upon Eugene’s dreams.
年轻人抓起老人的手，看着他，眼神中带着几分善意。 The young man took the elder’s hand, and looked at him with something like kindness in his eyes.
“您是一位善良而高贵的人。”他说， “You are a good and noble man,” he said.
“我们以后再谈您的女儿。” “We will have some talk about your daughters by and by.”
不等高老头回答，他就站起身来，径自回房去了。 He rose without waiting for Goriot’s answer, and went to his room.
在房间里，他给母亲写了下面这封信：“我亲爱的母亲——您还能再哺育一次您的孩子吗？我马上就能飞黄腾达了，但是我需要一千两百法郎——无论如何，我都需要这笔钱。 There he wrote the following letter to his mother:—“My Dear Mother,—Can you nourish your child from your breast again?I am in a position to make a rapid fortune, but I want twelve hundred francs—I must have them at all costs.
不要把这件事告诉我父亲，他也许会反对。要是我得不到这笔钱，我也许会被带上一条不归路，以摆脱纠缠我的绝望。 Say nothing about this to my father; perhaps he might make objections, and unless I have the money, I may be led to put an end to myself, and so escape the clutches of despair.
我见到你时，会告诉您事情的全部。 I will tell you everything when I see you.
关于我的近况，我就不多说了，要想把事情说得完整、清楚，得说好几十页呢。 I will not begin to try to describe my present situation; it would take volumes to put the whole story clearly and fully.
我善良的母亲，我没有赌博，也不欠别人一分一毫，但是如果您想保住您给我的这条命，就一定要寄给我这笔钱。 I have not been gambling, my kind mother, I owe no one a penny; but if you would preserve the life that you gave me, you must send me the sum I mention.
事实上，我去见了德伯桑子爵夫人，她答应以她的影响力来帮助我。我必须进入社交圈，却没钱买一双好看的手套。 As a matter of fact, I go to see the Vicomtesse de Beauseant; she is using her influence for me; I am obliged to go into society, and I have not a penny to lay out on clean gloves.
我可以只吃粗茶淡饭过活，必要时也可以什么都不吃，但是我不能不买他们在这块地方种植葡萄的工具。 I can manage to exist on bread and water, or go without food, if need be, but I cannot do without the tools with which they cultivate the vineyards in this country.
我必须立刻下定决心，向目标进发，不然我的后半生就要陷入泥沼、不得翻身了。 I must resolutely make up my mind at once to make my way, or stick in the mire for the rest of my days.
我知道您将所有希望都寄托在我的身上，我也想快点实现这些愿望。 I know that all your hopes are set on me, and I want to realize them quickly.
我善良的母亲，卖一点您的旧首饰吧，很快我就能送给您其他首饰了。 Sell some of your old jewelry, my kind mother; I will give you other jewels very soon.
我很清楚家里的状况，也知道这样的牺牲意味着什么，您别认为我轻易就说出了这些话。要是可以，我就成魔鬼了。 I know enough of our affairs at home to know all that such a sacrifice means, and you must not think that I would lightly ask you to make it; I should be a monster if I could.
您一定得明白，我是急需这笔钱，迫不得已才哀求您的。 You must think of my entreaty as a cry forced from me by imperative necessity.
我们的未来就全靠这些钱了，我要用这笔钱打响我的第一炮，因为巴黎的生活就是一场永无止息的战争。 Our whole future lies in the subsidy with which I must begin my first campaign, for life in Paris is one continual battle.
如果您还是筹不齐这笔钱，因此不得不卖掉姑妈的项链，告诉她，我会寄给她更漂亮的项链。”信里还有其他类似的话。 If you cannot otherwise procure the whole of the money, and are forced to sell our aunt’s lace, tell her that I will send her some still handsomer,” and so forth.
他写信问妹妹们要她们的储蓄——她们会做出牺牲把钱给他，并向家人保守这个秘密吗？ He wrote to ask each of his sisters for their savings—would they despoil themselves for him, and keep the sacrifice a secret from the family?
为了增加胜算，他又触碰了她们争强好胜的心弦——年轻、兴奋的心中总是猛烈跃动着争强好胜之情——让她们柔软的心产生同情。 To his request he knew that they would not fail to respond gladly, and he added to it an appeal to their delicacy by touching the chord of honor that vibrates so loudly in young and high-strung natures.
尽管他心怀大志，但他写完信后，不禁担心起来。他的心跳得很快，身体也在发抖。 Yet when he had written the letters, he could not help feeling misgivings in spite of his youthful ambition; his heart beat fast, and he trembled.
他知道妹妹们住在人迹罕至的庄园里，有着一尘不染的高贵心灵；他知道他的要求会带给妹妹怎样的烦恼和乐趣；他知道她们坐在果树下谈论自己正在巴黎的亲爱哥哥时，会是多么开心。 He knew the spotless nobleness of the lives buried away in the lonely manor house; he knew what trouble and what joy his request would cause his sisters, and how happy they would be as they talked at the bottom of the orchard of that dear brother of theirs in Paris.
他的眼前浮现出一幅幅画面。借着一束强烈的光芒，他仿佛看到他的妹妹们正偷偷数着自己小金库里的存款，使出一些小女生的伎俩，让钱以“匿名人”的名义寄到他手里。这是她们人生中第一次试图以一个谎言来表现她们慷慨、无私的高贵品格。 Visions rose before his eyes; a sudden strong light revealed his sisters secretly counting over their little store, devising some girlish stratagem by which the money could be sent to him @incognito@, essaying, for the first time in their lives, a piece of deceit that reached the sublime in its unselfishness.
“妹妹的心如钻石般纯洁，它的温柔有如深海！”他自言自语道。 “A sister’s heart is a diamond for purity, a deep sea of tenderness!” he said to himself.
他因为那些信而感到羞耻。 He felt ashamed of those letters.
有这样的心灵，她们的许愿会是多么有力啊！她们诚心向上天祈祷，这股热情是多么纯洁啊！ What power there must be in the petitions put up by such hearts; how pure the fervor that bears their souls to Heaven in prayer!
她们从自我牺牲中得到的快乐是多么地强烈啊！ What exquisite joy they would find in self-sacrifice!
要是母亲无法筹齐他所要的钱，她的内心会多么悲痛啊！ What a pang for his mother’s heart if she could not send him all that he asked for!
而这些高贵的情感，这些巨大的牺牲，会成为他用来接近德尔菲娜·德纽沁根的阶梯。 And this noble affection, these sacrifices made at such terrible cost, were to serve as the ladder by which he meant to climb to Delphine de Nucingen.
几滴眼泪从他眼里掉了下来，如同扔进壁炉里、投进神圣爱火中的几颗乳香。 A few tears, like the last grains of incense flung upon the sacred altar fire of the hearth, fell from his eyes.
他来来回回地走着，感动中夹杂着绝望。 He walked up and down, and despair mingled with his emotion.
高老头透过半敞的门看着他。 Father Goriot saw him through the half-open door.
“怎么了，先生？”他站在门边问。 “What is the matter, sir?” he asked from the threshold.
“啊！我的邻居，我是一个儿子和哥哥，就像您是一位父亲一样。 “Ah! my good neighbor, I am as much a son and brother as you are a father.
您对阿纳斯塔谢伯爵夫人的担心是对的，有一位马克西姆·德特拉尔先生，他会把她毁掉的。” You do well to fear for the Comtesse Anastasie; there is one M. Maxime de Trailles, who will be her ruin.”
高老头退了出去，同时嘴里还嘟囔了几句，但是欧仁没听清楚他在说什么。 Father Goriot withdrew, stammering some words, but Eugene failed to catch their meaning.
第二天早上，拉斯蒂涅出去寄信了。 The next morning Rastignac went out to post his letters.
直到最后一刻他还是犹豫不决，但最后还是把信扔进了信箱。 Up to the last moment he wavered and doubted, but he ended by flinging them into the box.
“我会成功的！”他对自己说。 “I shall succeed!” he said to himself.
赌徒也这样说，伟大的船长也这样说。这句话虽说拯救了一些人，但被它毁掉的人更多。 So says the gambler; so says the great captain; but the three words that have been the salvation of some few, have been the ruin of many more.
过了几天，欧仁去拜访德雷斯多夫人，她不在家。 A few days after this Eugene called at Mme. de Restaud’s house; she was not at home.
他尝试过三次，三次都发现大门紧锁，即便他都是仔细挑选德特拉尔先生不在的时间去的。 Three times he tried the experiment, and three times he found her doors closed against him, though he was careful to choose an hour when M. de Trailles was not there.
子爵夫人没错。 The Vicomtesse was right.
这个学生的学业已经荒废许久了。 The student studied no longer.
他在课堂上露面，只是为了应付点名，在答了到，证明自己出席之后，就立即离开。 He put in an appearance at lectures simply to answer to his name, and after thus attesting his presence, departed forthwith.
他正经历一个论证推理的过程，而这一过程对大部分学生都不陌生。 He had been through a reasoning process familiar to most students.
他意识到将学习推迟到考试之前的最后一刻是明智的选择。他打定主意将第二年和第三年的课程全部挤在第三年完成，想着那时他会认真读书，尽全力完成自己法律专业的课程。 He had seen the advisability of deferring his studies to the last moment before going up for his examinations; he made up his mind to cram his second and third years’ work into the third year, when he meant to begin to work in earnest, and to complete his studies in law with one great effort.
与此同时，他已经在巴黎这个海洋中航行十五个月了，期间他撒下渔网、设好鱼线，以此网罗一个女保护人和一笔财富。 In the meantime he had fifteen months in which to navigate the ocean of Paris, to spread the nets and set the lines that would bring him a protectress and a fortune.
那个星期，他见过德伯桑夫人两次。他会看着德阿尤达侯爵驾车离开后再进屋。 Twice during that week he saw Mme. de Beauseant; he did not go to her house until he had seen the Marquis d’Ajuda drive away.
这位伟大的女性在之后的一些日子里依旧以胜利者的姿态出现，她是圣日耳曼郊区最有诗意的人。德阿尤达·平托侯爵和德洛希斐特小姐的婚事也延期了。 Victory for yet a few more days was with the great lady, the most poetic figure in the Faubourg Saint-Germain; and the marriage of the Marquis d’Ajuda-Pinto with Mlle.de Rochefide was postponed.
因为害怕即将失去幸福，这些日子里她沉溺在从未体验过的狂喜之中。但是不管怎样，结局都是差不多的。 The dread of losing her happiness filled those days with a fever of joy unknown before, but the end was only so much the nearer.
德阿尤达侯爵和洛希斐特家都认为这次争吵与和解是一件很幸运的事。德伯桑夫人（他们是这样希望的）会渐渐接受这桩婚事，最终会牺牲每天早上与德阿尤达的会面，以成全这位男士的事业，成全这件她应该早就料到却又迫在眉睫的事。 The Marquis d’Ajuda and the Rochefides agreed that this quarrel and reconciliation was a very fortunate thing; Mme. de Beauseant (so they hoped) would gradually become reconciled to the idea of the marriage, and in the end would be brought to sacrifice d’Ajuda’s morning visits to the exigencies of a man’s career, exigencies which she must have foreseen.
尽管他们每天都会郑重其事地说新的誓言，德阿尤达先生只是在逢场作戏，而子爵夫人却渴望受到欺骗。 In spite of the most solemn promises, daily renewed, M. d’Ajuda was playing a part, and the Vicomtesse was eager to be deceived.
“她没有像英雄一般从窗户跳下，而是头朝地从楼梯上摔下来。”她最亲密的朋友德朗热公爵夫人说。 “Instead of taking a leap heroically from the window, she is falling headlong down the staircase,” said her most intimate friend, the Duchesse de Langeais.
不过这段幸福的回光返照持续了许久，让子爵夫人能为年轻的表弟服务。 Yet this after-glow of happiness lasted long enough for the Vicomtesse to be of service to her young cousin.
她对他有了几分迷信般的依恋之情。 She had a half-superstitious affection for him.
在一个女人处于危机，看不到任何怜悯的目光或任何充满真诚安慰的眼神时，欧仁对她表现出了同情和爱慕之情。要是一个男人时刻都准备着能够抚慰人心的谄言媚语，那么这一定是因为他怀有私利动机。 Eugene had shown her sympathy and devotion at a crisis when a woman sees no pity, no real comfort in any eyes; when if a man is ready with soothing flatteries, it is because he has an interested motive.
拉斯蒂涅下定决心要了解高老头的全部过往经历，他要在试图入住德纽沁根公馆之前弄清处境。 Rastignac made up his mind that he must learn the whole of Goriot’s previous history; he would come to his bearings before attempting to board the Maison de Nucingen.
他的调查结果可以概括如下：大革命之前的那些年月，让-若阿基姆·高里奥只不过是一个面条商雇佣的工人。 The results of his inquiries may be given briefly as follows:—In the days before the Revolution, Jean-Joachim Goriot was simply a workman in the employ of a vermicelli maker.
他是一个技术娴熟而又节俭的工人，也十分有进取心。他的老板在一七八九年的动荡中意外被害，他便买下了老板的铺子。 He was a skilful, thrifty workman, sufficiently enterprising to buy his master’s business when the latter fell a chance victim to the disturbances of 1789.
高里奥把店铺开在裘森尼街上，离谷物交易市场很近。 Goriot established himself in the Rue de la Jussienne, close to the Corn Exchange.
出于清晰、准确的判断力，他接受了该区区长的职位，以确保他的生意在危险时期受到那些当权者的保护。 His plain good sense led him to accept the position of President of the Section, so as to secure for his business the protection of those in power at that dangerous epoch.
这一谨慎的举措为他带来成功。他的财富积累始于大饥荒时期（不管是真的还是假的），那时巴黎各种谷物的价格都大幅上涨。 This prudent step had led to success; the foundations of his fortune were laid in the time of the Scarcity (real or artificial), when the price of grain of all kinds rose enormously in Paris.
那时人们经常在面包房门口为了一块面包大打出手，而另一些人则去杂货店买意大利面，从不为此争吵。 People used to fight for bread at the bakers’ doors; while other persons went to the grocers’ shops and bought Italian paste foods without brawling over it.
那一年，高里奥赚到了钱。之后，那笔钱使他成为了大资本家，使他面对小买主占据了全面的优势。此外，他只是有着平庸之人的好运气罢了。他的平庸拯救了他。 It was during this year that Goriot made the money, which, at a later time, was to give him all the advantage of the great capitalist over the small buyer; he had, moreover, the usual luck of average ability; his mediocrity was the salvation of him.
他没有引起任何人的嫉妒。直到有钱不再是危险的事之后，人们才察觉到他的富有。他的聪明才智全部都放在商业投机上，而非政治上。 He excited no one’s envy, it was not even suspected that he was rich till the peril of being rich was over, and all his intelligence was concentrated, not on political, but on commercial speculations.
对于涉及到谷物、面粉和“粗面粉”，还有谷物生产、储藏和质量的问题，高里奥是绝对的权威。 Goriot was an authority second to none on all questions relating to corn, flour, and “middlings”; and the production, storage, and quality of grain.
他能估计收成，预计市场价格。他从西西里岛买谷物，从俄罗斯进口小麦。 He could estimate the yield of the harvest, and foresee market prices; he bought his cereals in Sicily, and imported Russian wheat.
任何人，只要听过他滔滔不绝地谈论控制粮食进出口规章的人，只要见识过他对这门学问的理解程度，以及他对相关法则的敏锐洞察力、对粮食系统运转的缺陷的看法，都会认为他是当部长的材料。 Any one who had heard him hold forth on the regulations that control the importation and exportation of grain, who had seen his grasp of the subject, his clear insight into the principles involved, his appreciation of weak points in the way that the system worked, would have thought that here was the stuff of which a minister is made.
他耐心、积极、坚毅、精力充沛、行动敏捷，以鹰眼般敏锐的目光俯瞰着自己的全盘生意。 Patient, active, and persevering, energetic and prompt in action, he surveyed his business horizon with an eagle eye.
在粮食领域，没有事能让他大吃一惊。他能预见所有事情，知道所有正在发生的事情，也总能对自己的计划保密。他是能快速了解形势的外交家，是在日常事务中耐心而奋力前行的士兵。 Nothing there took him by surprise; he foresaw all things, knew all that was happening, and kept his own counsel; he was a diplomatist in his quick comprehension of a situation; and in the routine of business he was as patient and plodding as a soldier on the march.
但是在他生意范围之外，他什么都不懂。 But beyond this business horizon he could not see.
过去，他经常在闲暇时间站在店铺的门槛边，靠着门框。 He used to spend his hours of leisure on the threshold of his shop, leaning against the framework of the door.
他一从自己那间又小又黑的账房出来，就又变成那个粗枝大叶、反应迟钝的工人了:对论证推理一窍不通，对精神愉悦毫无感觉，在剧院里昏昏欲睡。简而言之就是巴黎的多利本人，别人对于他的愚蠢也无能无力。 Take him from his dark little counting-house, and he became once more the rough, slow-witted workman, a man who cannot understand a piece of reasoning, who is indifferent to all intellectual pleasures, and falls asleep at the play, a Parisian Dolibom in short, against whose stupidity other minds are powerless.
这种人在本质上相差无几，几乎在所有这些人的内心深处，你都可以发现一份值得尊敬的情感。 Natures of this kind are nearly all alike; in almost all of them you will find some hidden depth of sublime affection.
两种真挚的情感占据着面条商的内心，以至于他将其他任何感情都排除在外了。他似乎将他的全部精力都倾注于这两种情感之中，如同他将所有智慧都用于粮食生意上一样。 Two all-absorbing affections filled the vermicelli maker’s heart to the exclusion of every other feeling; into them he seemed to put all the forces of his nature, as he put the whole power of his brain into the corn trade.
他虔诚地爱慕着他的妻子——一个拉布里富农的独女——他对她的爱没有边际。 He had regarded his wife, the only daughter of a rich farmer of La Brie, with a devout admiration; his love for her had been boundless.
高里奥觉得他妻子可爱、多情的性情散发着温柔的力量，这与他自己截然不同。 Goriot had felt the charm of a lovely and sensitive nature, which, in its delicate strength, was the very opposite of his own.
男人因为保护别人而感到骄傲。面对柔弱、无法自保的女人，男人的保护欲就会激发。还有什么本能比保护欲更深地植根于男人内心呢？ Is there any instinct more deeply implanted in the heart of man than the pride of protection, a protection which is constantly exerted for a fragile and defenceless creature?
爱情是慷慨之人的快乐之源，让他们心怀感激，无比温暖。将保护欲和爱情放在一起，你就能解释人性中很多奇特的不协调现象。 Join love thereto, the warmth of gratitude that all generous souls feel for the source of their pleasures, and you have the explanation of many strange incongruities in human nature.
在过了七年没有眼光灿烂的幸福时光后，高里奥失去了妻子。 After seven years of unclouded happiness, Goriot lost his wife.
他是多么不幸啊。 It was very unfortunate for him.
她正开始在其他方面显示自己的优势，也许她会给予他空洞的灵魂一些滋养，她也许能拓宽他的视野，为他的思想指明其他的方向。 She was beginning to gain an ascendency over him in other ways; possibly she might have brought that barren soil under cultivation, she might have widened his ideas and given other directions to his thoughts.
但她死了，父爱的本能在他身上发展到了几近癫狂的状态。 But when she was dead, the instinct of fatherhood developed in him till it almost became a mania.
由于妻子的死亡，他被阻滞的情感便全部转嫁到女儿身上，他在溺爱女儿的过程中感到十分满足。 All the affection balked by death seemed to turn to his daughters, and he found full satisfaction for his heart in loving them.
不时会有条件不错的人来向他求婚。有钱商人或农场主都希望把自己的女儿嫁给他。他们还为了这件事相互较劲，给他好处来诱惑他再婚，但他决定继续做鳏夫。 More or less brilliant proposals were made to him from time to time; wealthy merchants or farmers with daughters vied with each other in offering inducements to him to marry again; but he determined to remain a widower.
他的岳父，那个他认为唯一一个与他有着坚定友谊的人，说高里奥发誓会忠诚于自己死去的妻子。 His father-in-law, the only man for whom he felt a decided friendship, gave out that Goriot had made a vow to be faithful to his wife’s memory.
那些谷物交易市场上的常客们认为这种行为很愚蠢，无法理解它的可敬之处。他们互相拿这件事来说笑，还给高里奥起了一个可笑的绰号。 The frequenters of the Corn Exchange, who could not comprehend this sublime piece of folly, joked about it among themselves, and found a ridiculous nickname for him.
他们中有一个斗胆（讨价还价时喝了点酒后）叫了他的绰号，结果这位面条商一拳打得他一头栽进了奥卜林街的排水沟里。 One of them ventured (after a glass over a bargain) to call him by it, and a blow from the vermicelli maker’s fist sent him headlong into a gutter in the Rue Oblin.
他一想起自己的孩子，就把其他所有事都抛到脑后了。大家都知道他对她们的爱让他焦虑不安。有一天，一位希望除掉他而保住自己生意的竞争对手告诉他，德尔菲娜刚才被一辆出租马车撞倒了。 He could think of nothing else when his children were concerned; his love for them made him fidgety and anxious; and this was so well known, that one day a competitor, who wished to get rid of him to secure the field to himself, told Goriot that Delphine had just been knocked down by a cab.
这位面条商的脸色马上变得惨白，立即离开交易市场，之后几天都没回去。开始他很震惊，后来才发现这是虚惊一场。这一惊一乍让他病倒了。 The vermicelli maker turned ghastly pale, left the Exchange at once, and did not return for several days afterwards; he was ill in consequence of the shock and the subsequent relief on discovering that it was a false alarm.
然而，这一次，这个冒犯者虽然肩膀已经被打得淤青，却仍未逃过一劫。在这个人生意的关键时刻，高里奥让他破了产，迫使他从谷物交易市场消失。 This time, however, the offender did not escape with a bruised shoulder; at a critical moment in the man’s affairs, Goriot drove him into bankruptcy, and forced him to disappear from the Corn Exchange.
不难料到，两个女儿都被宠坏了。 As might have been expected, the two girls were spoiled.
尽管有六万法郎的收入，高里奥自己却花不了一千二百法郎，他的全部乐趣只在于满足两个女儿心血来潮的想法。 With an income of sixty thousand francs, Goriot scarcely spent twelve hundred on himself, and found all his happiness in satisfying the whims of the two girls.
他请了最好的老师，让阿纳斯塔谢和德尔菲娜得到良好的教育，取得应有的成就。 The best masters were engaged, that Anastasie and Delphine might be endowed with all the accomplishments which distinguish a good education.
她们有一个女伴——她们真是幸运，她是一个判断力强、品味好的女性。她们学骑马；她们还有一架马车供自己使用；她们过得跟有钱老爵爷养的情妇一样；她们只要说出自己的愿望，她们的父亲就会赶紧实现她们无比奢侈的愿望，要的回报也只不过是一个吻而已。 They had a chaperon—luckily for them, she was a woman who had good sense and good taste;—they learned to ride; they had a carriage for their use; they lived as the mistress of a rich old lord might live; they had only to express a wish, their father would hasten to give them their most extravagant desires, and asked nothing of them in return but a kiss.
高里奥将两个女儿奉为天使，自己就自然沦落到她们之下了。 Goriot had raised the two girls to the level of the angels; and, quite naturally, he himself was left beneath them.
可怜的人啊！他爱她们，甚至爱她们给他的痛苦。 Poor man! he loved them even for the pain that they gave him.
女孩们到了出嫁年龄时，父亲就让她们自己挑选新郎。 When the girls were old enough to be married, they were left free to choose for themselves.
她们每人都得到父亲的一半财产作为嫁妆。当德雷斯多伯爵因为仰慕阿纳斯塔谢的美貌而前去求婚时，她对社交圈的渴望使她离开了父亲的房子，进入了一个更尊贵的社会圈子。 Each had half her father’s fortune as her dowry; and when the Comte de Restaud came to woo Anastasie for her beauty, her social aspirations led her to leave her father’s house for a more exalted sphere.
德尔菲娜喜欢钱，她嫁给了纽沁根这位有德国血统的银行家，他的祖上在神圣罗马帝国时期就被封为了男爵。 Delphine wished for money; she married Nucingen, a banker of German extraction, who became a Baron of the Holy Roman Empire.
高里奥还是以前那个面条商。 Goriot remained a vermicelli maker as before.
他的女儿和女婿们开始提出异议。虽然他的整个生命都与他的生意紧密联系在一起，他们却不想看到他再做生意了。 His daughters and his sons-in-law began to demur; they did not like to see him still engaged in trade, though his whole life was bound up with his business.
之后五年，他都不肯同意他们的乞求，但最后他让步了，同意带着卖店铺的钱，和自己最后几年存下的钱退休。 For five years he stood out against their entreaties, then he yielded, and consented to retire on the amount realized by the sale of his business and the savings of the last few years.
