你看，我还是很自私，我在帮你换房子这件事上怀有私利动机。 You see, there was plenty of selfishness on my part; I have an interested motive in helping you to change lodgings.
要是我提点要求，你不会拒绝我，是不是，嗯？” You will not refuse me if I ask you something; will you, eh?”
“什么要求？” “What is it?”
“在你房间上面的五楼有一个房间和其他房间连在一起，我会住在那里，那样可以吗？ “There is a room on the fifth floor, up above your rooms, that is to let along with them; that is where I am going to live, isn’t that so?
我越来越老了，我离我的女儿们太远了。 I am getting old; I am too far from my girls.
我不会妨碍你们，但是我会在那里，就这些。 I shall not be in the way, but I shall be there, that is all.
每天晚上你会过来告诉我她的事情。 You will come and talk to me about her every evening.
这不会打扰到你，不是吗？ It will not put you about, will it?
我会在你进门之前就上床，但是我会听到你上来，我就会对自己说,‘他刚才见过我的小德尔菲娜。 I shall have gone to bed before you come in, but I shall hear you come up, and I shall say to myself, ‘He has just seen my little Delphine.
他和她跳过舞了，她很开心，多亏了他。’要是我病了，听到你在楼下走动，知道你什么时候离开，什么时候回来会使我很高兴。那里离香榭丽舍大街也只有一步之遥，她们天天去那里，所以我就肯定能看到她们了，而现在有时候我会去的太晚。 He has been to a dance with her, and she is happy, thanks to him.’ If I were ill, it would do my heart good to hear you moving about below, to know when you leave the house and when you come in.It is only a step to the Champs-Elysees, where they go every day, so I shall be sure of seeing them, whereas now I am sometimes too late.
还有——也许她会来看你！ And then—perhaps she may come to see you!
我就能听到她的声音，看到她穿着她带夹层的柔软皮上衣，优雅地走着猫步。 I shall hear her, I shall see her in her soft quilted pelisse tripping about as daintily as a kitten.
在这一个月里，她又变成了我的小女儿了，那么无忧无虑、那么快乐。 In this one month she has become my little girl again, so light-hearted and gay.
她的灵魂在复苏，她的幸福则归功于你！ Her soul is recovering, and her happiness is owing to you!
哦！我会为你做你办不到的事。 Oh! I would do impossibilities for you.
就在刚才她对我说,‘我很开心，爸爸！’当她们生硬地说着‘父亲’时，我会浑身打颤，但是当她们叫我‘爸爸’时，我就想起了所有旧的回忆。 Only just now she said to me, ‘I am very happy, papa!’ When they say ‘father’ stiffly, it sends a chill through me; but when they call me ‘papa,’ it brings all the old memories back.
我感到那时最像她们的父亲，我甚至觉得她们只属于我，不属于其他任何人。” I feel most their father then; I even believe that they belong to me, and to no one else.”
这个善良的人揉了揉眼睛，哭了。 The good man wiped his eyes, he was crying.
“我已经很久没有听到她们那样说话，她们已经很久没有像今天这样挽着我的胳膊了。 “It is a long while since I have heard them talk like that, a long, long time since she took my arm as she did to-day.
没错，事实上，上次我和我的一个女儿并肩走在一起，绝对是十年前的事了。 Yes, indeed, it must be quite ten years since I walked side by side with one of my girls.
和她并肩同步，感受到她裙子的触碰，感受她胳膊的温暖，这是多么让人愉快啊！ How pleasant it was to keep step with her, to feel the touch of her gown, the warmth of her arm!
还有，今天早上我去哪里都带着德尔菲娜，我和她一起购物，又把她送回了家。 Well, I took Delphine everywhere this morning; I went shopping with her, and I brought her home again.
哦！你必须让我住在你附近。 Oh! you must let me live near you.
某一天你也许会需要人帮你的忙，我就会立刻帮你处理那些事情了。 You may want some one to do you a service some of these days, and I shall be on the spot to do it.
哦！要是那个阿尔萨斯人死了，要是他的痛风病能侵袭他的胃，那么我可怜的孩子会多么幸福啊！ Oh! if only that great dolt of an Alsatian would die, if his gout would have the sense to attack his stomach, how happy my poor child would be!
你会成为我的女婿，你会在世人的注视下成为她的丈夫。 You would be my son-in-law; you would be her husband in the eyes of the world.
呸！她对幸福一无所知，我原谅了她所有的过失。 Bah! she has known no happiness, that excuses everything.
我们在天上的父一定支持世上爱着他们儿女的父亲。 Our Father in heaven is surely on the side of fathers on earth who love their children.
她多么爱你啊！”他说着停了一下，之后抬起了头， How fond of you she is!” he said, raising his head after a pause.
“我们一起四处闲逛的时候，她始终都在说你。 “All the time we were going about together she chatted away about you.
‘他长得太漂亮了，爸爸，是不是？ ‘He is so nice-looking, papa; isn’t he?
他心地很善良！他有没有跟你说起过我？’哼！她说了许多关于你的事，多得足以编一本书了，从阿图瓦街到帕诺拉马巷，她都把心里话全部倾诉给我听了。 He is kind-hearted!Does he talk to you about me?’Pshaw! she said enough about you to fill whole volumes; between the Rue d’Artois and the Passage des Panoramas she poured her heart out into mine.
就在这个愉快的早上，我一点都不觉得自己老了，我觉得自己像羽毛那么轻。 I did not feel old once during that delightful morning; I felt as light as a feather.
我告诉她你怎样把那张钞票给我，这把我的心肝宝贝感动得哭了。 I told her how you had given the banknote to me; it moved my darling to tears.
但是，你壁炉架上的这个东西是什么呢？”高老头最后说。 But what can this be on your chimney-piece?” said Father Goriot at last.
拉斯蒂涅没做出任何反应，他正在丧失耐性。 Rastignac had showed no sign, and he was dying of impatience.
欧仁神色迷惘，默默地盯着他的邻居。 Eugene stared at his neighbor in dumb and dazed bewilderment.
他想起了沃尔特兰，想起了明天早上的那场决斗，还有他即将实现的宝贵愿望。这两种思想的强烈反差让他觉得自己在经历一场噩梦。 He thought of Vautrin, of that duel to be fought to-morrow morning, and of this realization of his dearest hopes, and the violent contrast between the two sets of ideas gave him all the sensations of nightmare.
他走向壁炉架，看见了一个小方盒子，将其打开后，看到了一只用纸包着的百里鸽牌手表，纸上则写着：“我想让你每时每刻都想着我，因为……“德尔菲娜。” He went to the chimney-piece, saw the little square case, opened it, and found a watch of Breguet’s make wrapped in paper, on which these words were written: “I want you to think of me every hour, @because@…“DELPHINE.”
最后一个词无疑暗含着曾经发生在两人之间的某个场景。 That last word doubtless contained an allusion to some scene that had taken place between them.
欧仁被感动了。 Eugene felt touched.
这个金表壳里有他的印章，印章表面覆盖了一层瓷釉。 Inside the gold watch-case his arms had been wrought in enamel.
这个小东西的链子、钥匙、做工和设计正如他所想象的那样，他早就渴望得到这样一只表了。 The chain, the key, the workmanship and design of the trinket were all such as he had imagined, for he had long coveted such a possession.
高老头容光焕发。 Father Goriot was radiant.
当然，他已经答应告诉他女儿这一幕的每一个小细节和欧仁对这份礼物所作出的反应。他分享着年轻人的愉悦和兴奋，而且似乎是三个人中最开心的那个。 Of course he had promised to tell his daughter every little detail of the scene and of the effect produced upon Eugene by her present; he shared in the pleasure and excitement of the young people, and seemed to be not the least happy of the three.
由于自己和女儿的缘故，他已经爱上拉斯蒂涅了。 He loved Rastignac already for his own as well as for his daughter’s sake.
“你得去见见她，她今晚会等你的。 “You must go and see her; she is expecting you this evening.
阿尔萨斯那个大笨蛋要去和他的歌剧院舞女吃晚饭。 That great lout of an Alsatian is going to have supper with his opera-dancer.
啊哈！当我的律师向他说明他的境地时，他看起来非常愚蠢。 Aha! he looked very foolish when my attorney let him know where he was.
他说他崇拜我的女儿，是吗？ He says he idolizes my daughter, does he?
他最好不要招惹她，要不然我会杀了他。 He had better let her alone, or I will kill him.
想到我的德尔菲娜是他的妻子，就已经足够让我杀了他了。”他长叹一声，“但是就算杀了那畜生也不算犯了杀人罪，他就是个长着牛脑袋的猪——你愿意让我和你住在一起，不是吗？” To think that my Delphine is his”—He heaved a sigh—“it is enough to make me murder him, but it would not be manslaughter to kill that animal; he is a pig with a calf’s brains.—You will take me with you, will you not?”
“没错，亲爱的高老头，您很清楚我多么爱慕您——”“是的，我的确非常清楚。 “Yes, dear Father Goriot; you know very well how fond I am of you—” “Yes, I do know very well.
你不会因为我而感到羞愧，是吗？ You are not ashamed of me, are you?
你不会！ Not you!
让我们拥抱一下吧。”他挥出双臂抱着这个学生的脖子， Let me embrace you,” and he flung his arms around the student’s neck.
“你会让她非常开心的，答应我你会！ “You will make her very happy; promise me that you will!
你今晚会去见她，不是吗？” You will go to her this evening, will you not?”
“哦！是的。 “Oh! yes.
我必须出去了，我手头有点要紧事要办。” I must go out; I have some urgent business on hand.”
“我能帮上什么忙吗？” “Can I be of any use?”
“要我说，是的！ “My word, yes!
在我去见德纽沁根夫人的时候，你能不能去一下老塔耶费那里？ Will you go to old Taillefer’s while I go to Mme. de Nucingen?
叫他今晚和我约个时间，这可是人命关天的事。” Ask him to make an appointment with me some time this evening; it is a matter of life and death.”
“真的吗，年轻人！”高老头脸色大变，喊道，“你真向他女儿求爱了吗，就像楼下那些笨蛋说的那样？…… “Really, young man!” cried Father Goriot, with a change of countenance; “are you really paying court to his daughter, as those simpletons were saying down below?...
我的老天啊！你还不知道我高里奥打你一拳是什么滋味呢。你要是一脚踏两船，我一拳就能把你打得不能玩……哦！这不可能！” Tonnerre de dieu! you have no notion what a tap la is like, and if you are playing a double game, I shall put a stop to it by one blow of the fist…Oh! the thing is impossible!”
“我向你发誓我在这世上只爱一个女人。”这个学生说， “I swear to you that I love but one woman in the world,” said the student.
“我刚刚才弄清楚这个。” “I only knew it a moment ago.”
“哦！多么开心啊！”高老头喊道。 “Oh! what happiness!” cried Goriot.
“但是小塔耶费已经被叫出去了，明天早上会有一场决斗，我听说他可能会赔上性命。” “But young Taillefer has been called out; the duel comes off to-morrow morning, and I have heard it said that he may lose his life in it.”
“但是这关你什么事？”高老头说。 “But what business is it of yours?” said Goriot.
“哦，我必须要告诉他，他也许可以阻止他的儿子去决斗——”就在那时，沃尔特兰的声音打断了他们。他站在门槛旁，唱着：“哦！里夏尔，哦，我的王！ “Why, I ought to tell him so, that he may prevent his son from putting in an appearance—” Just at that moment Vautrin’s voice broke in upon them; he was standing at the threshold of his door and singing: “Oh! Richard, oh my king!
全世界都放弃了你！ All the world abandons thee!
布劳！布劳！布劳！布劳！布劳！ Broum! broum! broum! broum! broum!
世界各地都流传着同一个古老的故事，四处流浪的心灵和……的啦，啦，啦。” The same old story everywhere, a roving heart and a...tra la la.”
“先生们！”克里斯托夫喊道，“汤已经好了，所有人都在等你们呢。” “Gentlemen!” shouted Christophe, “the soup is ready, and every one is waiting for you.”
“在这里，”沃尔特兰冲着楼下对他说，“给我拿一瓶我的波多尔葡萄酒。” “Here,” Vautrin called down to him, “come and take a bottle of my Bordeaux.”
“你觉得这只表漂亮吗？”高老头问。 “Do you think your watch is pretty?” asked Goriot.
“她的品味很好，不是吗？ “She has good taste, hasn’t she?
嗯？”沃尔特兰、高老头和拉斯蒂涅一起下楼，因为他们三个迟到了，所以只能坐在一起了。 Eh?”Vautrin, Father Goriot, and Rastignac came downstairs in company, and, all three of them being late, were obliged to sit together.
欧仁吃饭时尽量和沃尔特兰保持疏远，但是后者呢，在沃盖夫人看来那么迷人、再机智不过了。 Eugene was as distant as possible in his manner to Vautrin during dinner; but the other, so charming in Mme. Vauquer’s opinion, had never been so witty.
他生动的俏皮话和机智的谈吐让一桌人都心情舒畅。 His lively sallies and sparkling talk put the whole table in good humor.
他的信心和镇定让欧仁觉得恐怖。 His assurance and coolness filled Eugene with consternation.
“哦，你今天碰上什么事了？”沃盖夫人问， “Why, what has come to you to-day?” inquired Mme. Vauquer.
“你开心得像只云雀。” “You are as merry as a skylark.”
“我做成一笔好买卖之后总是很开心。” “I am always in spirits after I have made a good bargain.”
“买卖？”欧仁说。 “Bargain?” said Eugene.
“嗯，没错，买卖。 “Well, yes, bargain.
我刚才交了很多货，我会拿到一笔可观的佣金——米绍诺小姐，”他注意到那个老处女正在仔细地观察着他，便继续说道，“是不是我脸上有什么不对，你才用如此锐利的目光盯着我？ I have just delivered a lot of goods, and I shall be paid a handsome commission on them—Mlle. Michonneau,” he went on, seeing that the elderly spinster was scrutinizing him intently, “have you any objection to some feature in my face, that you are making those lynx eyes at me?
跟我说说，我会为你做出改变的…… Just let me know, and I will have it changed to oblige you…
我敢肯定，我们不会为此吵架，普瓦雷？”他向这个退休的公务员使了使眼色，补充道。 We shall not fall out about it, Poiret, I dare say?” he added, winking at the superannuated clerk.
“我的天哪，你应该像模特一样站在那里，滑稽地模仿赫拉克勒斯。”年轻画家说。 “Bless my soul, you ought to stand as model for a burlesque Hercules,” said the young painter.
“我会的，的确！要是米绍诺小姐答应像拉雪兹神父公墓的维纳斯一样坐着就行了。”沃尔特兰回答道。 “I will, upon my word!If Mlle. Michonneau will consent to sit as the Venus of Pere-Lachaise,” replied Vautrin.
“普瓦雷还在这里了。”比安卡肖恩暗示说。 “There’s Poiret,” suggested Bianchon.
“哦！普瓦雷就做普瓦雷。 “Oh! Poiret shall pose as Poiret.
他可以是花园之神！”沃尔特兰喊道，“他的名字就是梨的意思——”“一个熟过之后开始腐烂的梨！”比安卡肖恩插话说。 He can be a garden god!” cried Vautrin; “his name means a pear—” “A sleepy pear!” Bianchon put in.
“那你就是插在梨和奶酪之间了。” “You will come in between the pear and the cheese.”
“你们都在说些什么！”沃盖夫人说，“你最好请我们大家喝点你的波尔多葡萄酒，我看见那里放着一瓶了。 “What stuff are you all talking!” said Mme. Vauquer; “you would do better to treat us to your Bordeaux; I see a glimpse of a bottle there.
那东西会让我们大家保持心情愉悦，而且对胃也好。” It would keep us all in a good humor, and it is good for the stomach besides.”
“先生们，”沃尔特兰说道，“总管夫人让我们遵守纪律。 “Gentlemen,” said Vautrin, “the Lady President calls us to order.
库蒂尔夫人和维多琳小姐不会因你们的笑话而心存恶意，但是也要尊重无辜、上了年纪的高老头。 Mme. Couture and Mlle. Victorine will take your jokes in good part, but respect the innocence of the aged Goriot.
我提议喝一两杯波尔多葡萄酒拉玛。这酒因为拉菲特(注：“拉菲特”是十七世纪末到十八世纪初的法国海盗，在一把一二年战争中帮助了美国，之后其罪行得到赦免。)这个名字而有了双重含义，我可没有任何政治暗示——过来，你这个淘气鬼！”他边说着，边看了一眼克里斯托夫，他站在那里没有动弹。 I propose a glass or two of Bordeauxrama, rendered twice illustrious by the name of Laffite, no political allusions intended.—Come, you Turk!” he added, looking at Christophe, who did not offer to stir.
“克里斯托夫！ “Christophe!
这里！ Here!
怎么，叫你呢，你怎么不答应？ What, you don’t answer to your own name?
给我们倒酒，小淘气！” Bring us some liquor, Turk!”
“好的，先生。”克里斯托夫拿出酒瓶说道。 “Here it is, sir,” said Christophe, holding out the bottle.
沃尔特兰给欧仁和高老头的杯子里斟满了酒，之后又故意在自己的杯子里倒了几滴，并在旁边两个人喝酒的时候抿了一点。 Vautrin filled Eugene’s glass and Goriot’s likewise, then he deliberately poured out a few drops into his own glass, and sipped it while his two neighbors drank their wine.
他突然做出一副痛苦状。 All at once he made a grimace.
“有木塞味！”他喊道， “Corked!” he cried.
“真见鬼！ “The devil!
你把剩下的酒喝了吧，克里斯托夫，去找另外一瓶，从右手边拿，这个你知道。 You can drink the rest of this, Christophe, and go and find another bottle; take from the right-hand side, you know.
我们有十六个人，拿八瓶出来。” There are sixteen of us; take down eight bottles.”
“要是你准备请客的话，”画家说，“我会付给你一百个栗子。” “If you are going to stand treat,” said the painter, “I will pay for a hundred chestnuts.”
“哦！哦！” “Oh! oh!”
“嘣！” “Booououh!”
“噗！” “Prrr!”
桌上的每一个人都大呼小叫，好像放烟火时的爆竹声。 These exclamations came from all parts of the table like squibs from a set firework.
“来吧，沃盖妈妈，来两瓶香槟。”沃尔特兰叫道。 “Come, now, Mama Vauquer, a couple of bottles of champagne,” called Vautrin.
“啊！亏你想得出！ “@Quien!@ just like you!
你为什么不立即把整个房子都要去。 Why not ask for the whole house at once.
两瓶香槟，那就是十二法郎！ A couple of bottles of champagne; that means twelve francs!
我知道，花出去的钱永远都挣不回来了！ I shall never see the money back again, I know!
但要是欧仁先生愿意付账的话，我还有一些醋栗酒。” But if M. Eugene has a mind to pay for it, I have some currant cordial.”
“她的醋栗酒就像黑色顿服药一样难喝。”这个医科学生嘀咕道。 “That currant cordial of hers is as bad as a black draught,” muttered the medical student.
“闭嘴，比安卡肖恩。”拉斯蒂涅叫道，“提到黑色顿服药，我就觉得—— “Shut up, Bianchon,” exclaimed Rastignac; “the very mention of black draught makes me feel—.
是的，无论如何都得要香槟，我会出钱的。”他补充道。 Yes, champagne, by all means; I will pay for it,” he added.
“西尔维，”沃盖夫人叫着，“拿点小饼干来，还有小蛋糕。” “Sylvie,” called Mme. Vauquer, “bring in some biscuits, and the little cakes.”
“那些蛋糕都发霉、长毛了。”沃尔特兰说, “Those little cakes are moldy graybeards,” said Vautrin.
“就拿点饼干来吧。” “But trot out the biscuits.”
倒上了波尔多酒，饭桌上显出从未有过的生气，大家也越来越开心。 The Bordeaux wine circulated; the dinner table became a livelier scene than ever, and the fun grew fast and furious.
模仿各种动物的叫声和大笑声混在一起。博物馆员工模仿猫叫的声音就像某种不明的动物叫春一样，八种声音同时喊出下面这些变奏曲：“磨剪刀喽！” Imitations of the cries of various animals mingled with the loud laughter; the Museum official having taken it into his head to mimic a cat-call rather like the caterwauling of the animal in question, eight voices simultaneously struck up with the following variations:“Scissors to grind!”
“卖鸟食繁缕喽！” “Chick-weeds for singing bir-ds!”
“白兰地酒味饼干喽，女士们！” “Brandy-snaps, ladies!”
“修瓷器喽！” “China to mend!”
“船来喽！” “Boat ahoy!”
“卖打老婆、拍衣服的棒子喽！” “Sticks to beat your wives or your clothes!”
“卖旧衣服喽！” “Old clo’!”
“熟透的樱桃喽！” “Cherries all ripe!”
但是胜利的棕榈叶授予了用鼻音叫着“修——雨伞喽！”的比安卡肖恩。 But the palm was awarded to Bianchon for the nasal accent with which he rendered the cry of “Umbrellas to me-end!”
片刻之后，房间里就充满了让人头痛欲裂的喧闹声，充满了一阵无聊的举动和猫儿音乐会，沃尔特兰则是这支乐队的指挥，他此时还留意下欧仁和高老头。 A few seconds later, and there was a head-splitting racket in the room, a storm of tomfoolery, a sort of cats’ concert, with Vautrin as conductor of the orchestra, the latter keeping an eye the while on Eugene and Father Goriot.
喝下的酒似乎已经冲上他们两个的脑袋了。 The wine seemed to have gone to their heads already.
他们靠着椅背，以一种严肃的态度看着这场混乱。他们只喝了一点酒，都专心地想着他们这晚即将做的事情，但是却都觉得无法站起来行走。 They leaned back in their chairs, looking at the general confusion with an air of gravity, and drank but little; both of them were absorbed in the thought of what lay before them to do that evening, and yet neither of them felt able to rise and go.
沃尔特兰不时地瞟他们俩一眼，关注着他们脸上表情的变化，他就在他们俩眼皮低垂就快要闭上的时候，俯身在拉斯蒂涅耳边说：“我的小伙子，你还不至于精明到能骗得了沃尔特兰老爹，他太爱你了，他不会让你搞砸你的事情的。 Vautrin gave a side glance at them from time to time, and watched the change that came over their faces, choosing the moment when their eyes drooped and seemed about to close, to bend over Rastignac and to say in his ear:—“My little lad, you are not quite shrewd enough to outwit Papa Vautrin yet, and he is too fond of you to let you make a mess of your affairs.
我一旦下决心要做一件事，除了上帝就没人能阻止得了我。 When I have made up my mind to do a thing, no one short of Providence can put me off.
啊哈！我们要去老塔耶费那里警告他，把秘密公布于众！ Aha! we were for going round to warn old Taillefer, telling tales out of school!
烤炉热了，面揉好了，准备好做面包了；明天我们就要把它吃掉，把面包渣扫掉；我们不会搞砸这次烤面包行动？……不，不，一切都就绪了！ The oven is hot, the dough is kneaded, the bread is ready for the oven; to-morrow we will eat it up and whisk away the crumbs; and we are not going to spoil the baking?...No, no, it is all as good as done!
我们可能要忍受一点良心的审视，但是这些也会随着面包一起被消化的。 We may suffer from a few conscientious scruples, but they will be digested along with the bread.
就在我们打盹的时候，陆军上校弗朗谢森尼伯爵就会用他的剑尖为米歇尔·塔耶费的财产继承扫清障碍了。 While we are having our forty winks, Colonel Count Franchessini will clear the way to Michel Taillefer’s inheritance with the point of his sword.
维多琳则会接管她哥哥的钱，每年舒舒服服地就会有一万五千法郎了。 Victorine will come in for her brother’s money, a snug fifteen thousand francs a year.
我已经查过了，知道她已故母亲的财产超过三十万——”这些话欧仁都听见了，但是却不能说出一个字。他的舌头好像和上腭粘在了一起了，无法抗拒的睡意正在他身上蔓延。 I have made inquiries already, and I know that her late mother’s property amounts to more than three hundred thousand—” Eugene heard all this, and could not answer a word; his tongue seemed to be glued to the roof of his mouth, an irresistible drowsiness was creeping over him.
他还是能看到这张饭桌和周围人的面孔，但是这一切都好像被蒙上了一层明亮的薄雾一样。 He still saw the table and the faces round it, but it was through a bright mist.
很快喧闹声开始平息下来，房客们一个接一个地走了。 Soon the noise began to subside, one by one the boarders went.
最后，参加这个晚宴的人只剩下沃盖夫人、库蒂尔夫人、维多琳小姐、沃尔特兰和高老头。拉斯蒂涅仿佛是在梦境中一样，他看着沃盖夫人忙着收拾酒瓶，将每个酒瓶里剩余的酒倒进另外的瓶子里。 At last, when their numbers had so dwindled that the party consisted of Mme. Vauquer, Mme. Couture, Mlle. Victorine, Vautrin, and Father Goriot, Rastignac watched as though in a dream how Mme. Vauquer busied herself by collecting the bottles, and drained the remainder of the wine out of each to fill others.
“哦！他们好闹腾啊！ “Oh! how uproarious they are!
年轻多好啊！”这个寡妇说。 What a thing it is to be young!” said the widow.
这些就是欧仁听懂的最后几句话了。 These were the last words that Eugene heard and understood.
“没人能像沃尔特兰先生这么风趣。”西尔维说。 “There is no one like M. Vautrin for a bit of fun like this,” said Sylvie.
“嘿，听听克里斯托夫的鼾声，他的鼾声就像转动的陀螺一样。” “There, just hark at Christophe, he is snoring like a top.”
“再见，妈妈，”沃尔特兰说，“我要去街上的剧院看马蒂先生的《荒山》，那是从《孤独者》中截取的一出好戏……要是您喜欢的话，我会带上您和这两位小姐——”“谢谢你，我不去了。”库蒂尔夫人说。 “Good-bye, mamma,” said Vautrin; “I am going to a theatre on the boulevard to see M. Marty in @Le Mont Sauvage@, a fine play taken from @Le Solitaire@…If you like, I will take you and these two ladies—”“Thank you; I must decline,” said Mme. Couture.
“什么！我亲爱的女士！”沃尔特兰叫道，“不去看根据《孤独者》写的戏剧，阿塔拉·德夏多布里昂的作品？ “What! my good lady!” cried Mme. Vauquer, “decline to see a play founded on the @Le Solitaire@, a work by Atala de Chateaubriand?
我们那么欣赏那本书，去年夏天在树下看时，哭得就像马格达伦（注：“马格达伦”指悔改的妓女）一样。这是一部改进后的作品，可能会对你们年轻女士有启发。” We were so fond of that book that we cried over it like Magdalens under the line-trees last summer, and then it is an improving work that might edify your young lady.”
“我们不准去看戏剧。”维多琳回答道。 “We are forbidden to go to the play,” answered Victorine.
“看看，那边两个都在他们的椅子上睡着了。”沃尔特兰说着滑稽地摇了摇两个熟睡之人的头。 “Just look, those two yonder have dropped off where they sit,” said Vautrin, shaking the heads of the two sleepers in a comical way.
他改变了学生的睡姿，把他的头靠在椅背上，这样能让他舒服一点，然后又热情地亲吻了他的额头，唱道：“睡吧，小宝贝们，我看着你们睡觉。” He altered the sleeping student’s position, settled his head more comfortably on the back of his chair, kissed him warmly on the forehead, and began to sing:“Sleep, little darlings; I watch while you slumber.”
“我担心他会生病。”维多琳说。 “I am afraid he may be ill,” said Victorine.
“那留在这里照顾他吧。”沃尔特兰回答说。 “Then stop and take care of him,” returned Vautrin.
“作为一个温顺而贤良的妻子，这是你的责任。”他在她耳边低声说道， “’Tis your duty as a meek and obedient wife,” he whispered in her ear.
“这个年轻人崇拜你，你会成为他的小媳妇——这是你的福气。 “The young fellow worships you, and you will be his little wife—there’s your fortune for you.
总之，”他又大声说，“他们从此会过上幸福的生活，所有乡下人都会非常尊敬他们，他们会子孙满堂的。 In short,” he added aloud, “they lived happily ever afterwards, were much looked up to in all the countryside, and had a numerous family.
这就是所有浪漫故事的结尾——现在，妈妈，”他转向沃盖夫人，搂着她的腰，继续说道，“我独自出去叫马车的时候，你要戴上你的系带帽，穿上你最好的绣花丝绸，围上伯爵夫人的围巾。” That is how all the romances end.—Now, mamma,” he went on, as he turned to Madame Vauquer and put his arm round her waist, “put on your bonnet, your best flowered silk, and the countess’ scarf, while I go out and call a cab—all my own self.”
之后他就出门了，边走边唱着：“哦！太阳！神圣的太阳！ And he started out, singing as he went:“Oh! sun! divine sun!
你让每一个南瓜成熟。” Ripening the pumpkins every one.”
“我的天啊！ “My goodness!
哦，我肯定！ Well, I’m sure!
库蒂尔夫人，和这样的男人在一起，就算住顶楼我也会很幸福——看那里！”她环顾四周找寻那个老面条商，“高老头在那里喝得半醉。 Mme. Couture, I could live happily in a garret with a man like that.—There, now!” she added, looking round for the old vermicelli maker, “there is that Father Goriot half seas over.
他从没想过带我去任何地方，这个老吝啬鬼。 A1354 never thought of taking me anywhere,the old skinflint.
但是他整个人快要倒下去了。 But he will measure his length somewhere.
哎呀！他这么大年纪的人这样失去理性，真丢脸！ My word! it is disgraceful to lose his senses like that, at his age!
你会告诉我说，他不会失去他本来就没有的理性——西尔维，把他送回房间吧！” You will be telling me that he couldn’t lose what he hadn’t got—Sylvie, just take him up to his room!”
西尔维扶着他的胳膊，支撑着他上楼，像扔包裹一样把他原模原样地扔在了床上。 Sylvie took him by the arm, supported him upstairs, and flung him just as he was, like a package, across the bed.
“可怜的小伙子！”库蒂尔夫人说着拨开盖住欧仁眼睛的头发，“他就像个年轻姑娘，不知道什么是恣意放纵呢。” “Poor young fellow!” said Mme. Couture, putting back Eugene’s hair that had fallen over his eyes; “he is like a young girl, he does not know what dissipation is.”
“哦，我能告诉你这个，我知道。”沃盖夫人说，“我开这个旅馆有三十年了，就像俗话所说的那样，我阅人无数，但是从未见到一个像欧仁先生这样漂亮并且长着一副贵族相的年轻人。 “Well, I can tell you this, I know,” said Mme. Vauquer, “I have taken lodgers these thirty years, and a good many have passed through my hands, as the saying is, but I have never seen a nicer nor a more aristocratic looking young man than M. Eugene.
他睡觉的样子看起来多英俊啊！ How handsome he looks sleeping!
就让他的头靠着你的肩膀吧，库蒂尔夫人。 Just let his head rest on your shoulder, Mme. Couture.
哼！他向维多琳小姐那里倒过去了。 Pshaw! he falls over towards Mlle. Victorine.
年轻的事物总能得到特别的眷佑。 There’s a special providence for young things.
再过去一点点，他的头就要撞到椅子的把手上，就要撞破头了。 A little more, and he would have broken his head against the knob of the chair.
他们俩会凑成相配的一对，这两人一定会的！” They’d make a pretty pair those two would!”
“嘘，我的好邻居，”库蒂尔夫人叫道，“你说的这件事——”“咳！”沃盖夫人插嘴说，“他听不见——这里，西尔维！过来帮我穿衣服。 “Hush, my good neighbor,” cried Mme. Couture, “you are saying such things—” “Pooh!” put in Mme. Vauquer, “he does not hear.—Here, Sylvie! come and help me to dress.
我要穿上我最好的胸衣。” I shall put on my best stays.”
“什么！刚吃完饭就穿最好的胸衣，夫人？”西尔维说， “What! your best stays just after dinner, madame?” said Sylvie.
“不，您可以让其他人帮您系带子。 “No, you can get some one else to lace you.
我是不会做谋杀您的凶手的。 I am not going to be your murderer.
这样做太轻率了，可能会搭上您的性命。” It’s a rash thing to do, and might cost you your life.”
“我不在乎，我必须为沃尔特兰先生争点光。” “I don’t care, I must do honor to M. Vautrin.”
“您真的喜欢您的继承人到了如此地步了？” “Are you so fond of your heirs as all that?”
“来吧，西尔维，别顶嘴了。”这个寡妇说着离开了这个房间。 “Come, Sylvie, don’t argue,” said the widow, as she left the room.
“她这个年纪，也这样！”这个厨娘指着她的女主人对维多琳说道。 “At her age, too!” said the cook to Victorine, pointing to her mistress as she spoke.
只剩下库蒂尔夫人和她监护的小姐在餐厅了，欧仁则靠着维多琳的肩膀睡着了。 Mme. Couture and her ward were left in the dining-room, and Eugene slept on Victorine’s shoulder.
克里斯托夫的鼾声在这寂静的房间里回响；欧仁安静的呼吸在这强烈的对比下显得更安静了，他睡觉的样子像小孩子一样安详。 The sound of Christophe’s snoring echoed through the silent house; Eugene’s quiet breathing seemed all the quieter by force of contrast, he was sleeping as peacefully as a child.
维多琳很开心，她可以自由地表现出那些慈爱的举动，这些举动真诚地释放了充斥于女人天性中的所有情感。他和她如此靠近,以至于她能够感觉到他心脏的跳动。维多琳的脸上露出一种近乎母性的保护和下意识的骄傲神情。 Victorine was very happy; she was free to perform one of those acts of charity which form an innocent outlet for all the overflowing sentiments of a woman’s nature; he was so close to her that she could feel the throbbing of his heart; there was a look of almost maternal protection and conscious pride in Victorine’s face.
她年轻无邪的心中充满了无数的想法，其中有一种是因为近距离接触而产生的狂喜和悸动。 Among the countless thoughts that crowded up in her young innocent heart, there was a wild flutter of joy at this close contact.
“可怜的好孩子！”库蒂尔夫人紧握着她的手说。 “Poor, dear child!” said Mme. Couture, squeezing her hand.
这位老妇人看着这个女孩。 The old lady looked at the girl.
维多琳天真无邪而楚楚可怜的脸由于新幸福的降临而容光焕发，她的脸使人回想到几幅纯真的中世纪艺术品，当时的画家省略了装饰品，而将画笔所有的神奇力量集中在从容、一丝不苟的轮廓和象牙色的面庞，似乎抓住了天堂里几分金碧辉煌的气势。 Victorine’s innocent, pathetic face, so radiant with the new happiness that had befallen her, called to mind some naive work of mediaeval art, when the painter neglected the accessories, reserving all the magic of his brush for the quiet, austere outlines and ivory tints of the face, which seems to have caught something of the golden glory of heaven.
“毕竟，他不过喝了两杯酒，妈妈。”维多琳的手指划过欧仁的头发，说道。 “After all, he only took two glasses, mamma,” said Victorine, passing her fingers through Eugene’s hair.
“其实，他要是一个放荡的青年，孩子，他就会像其他人那样喝酒的。 “Indeed, if he had been a dissipated young man, child, he would have carried his wine like the rest of them.
他的睡意为他赢得了信誉。” His drowsiness does him credit.”
街上传来一阵车轮声。 There was a sound of wheels outside in the street.
“沃尔特兰先生来了，妈妈。”这个女孩说道， “There is M. Vautrin, mamma,” said the girl.
“把欧仁先生扶开。 “Just take M. Eugene.
我不愿让那个人这样看到我这样，他看人的眼神有一些好像是在玷污你的灵魂，让你觉得你好像一丝不挂一样。” I would rather not have that man see me like this; there are some ways of looking at you that seem to sully your soul and make you feel as though you had nothing on.”
“哦，不，你说错了！”库蒂尔夫人说， “Oh, no, you are wrong!” said Mme. Couture.
“沃尔特兰先生是一位杰出人物，他让我有一点想起我已故的丈夫，可怜的库蒂尔先生，虽然粗野但是心地善良、嘴坏心不坏。” “M. Vautrin is a worthy man; he reminds me a little of my late husband, poor dear M. Couture, rough but kind-hearted; his bark is worse than his bite.”
正当她说话的时候，沃尔特兰走了进来。他没出声，但是看了一会儿这两张年轻的脸形成的画面——洒下的灯光像是在轻抚他们。 Vautrin came in while she was speaking; he did not make a sound, but looked for a while at the picture of the two young faces—the lamplight falling full upon them seemed to caress them.
“好了，”他交叉双臂，说道，“多美的画面啊！ “Well,” he remarked, folding his arms, “here is a picture!
这会让贝尔纳丹·德圣皮埃尔（他有着美好的灵魂）写出一些令人愉快的作品的，《保罗和维尔贞妮》就是他写的。 It would have suggested some pleasing pages to Bernardin de Saint-Pierre (good soul), who wrote @Paul et Virginie@.
年轻就是迷人，库蒂尔夫人！——继续睡吧，可怜的孩子。”他边补充着，边看着欧仁，“幸运有时会在你睡着的时候降临——这个年轻人身上有种东西感动着我、吸引着我，夫人。”他继续说道，“我知道他的心地就像他的脸那样美好。 Youth is very charming, Mme. Couture!—Sleep on, poor boy,” he added, looking at Eugene, “luck sometimes comes while you are sleeping.—There is something touching and attractive to me about this young man, madame,” he continued; “I know that his nature is in harmony with his face.
看看吧，一个天真的人，头靠在一个天使的肩膀上！ Just look, the head of a cherub on an angel’s shoulder!
他应当有人来爱。 He deserves to be loved.
要是我是一个女人，我会为他而死（不——没那么傻），我会为他而活的。” If I were a woman, I would die (no—not such a fool), I would live for him.”
他弯下腰去，在这个寡妇的耳边说道: He bent lower and spoke in the widow’s ear.
“当我看见他们俩在一起的时候，夫人，我不禁想到上帝为他们创造了彼此。他悄无声息地做着这件事，考验着他们的感情和心灵。”他低声说着, “When I see those two together, madame, I cannot help thinking that Providence meant them for each other; He works by secret ways, and tries the reins and the heart,” he said in a loud voice.
“当我看见你们，我的孩子们，被类似纯洁和人类所有的情感联系起来时，我对自己说，未来已经不可能将你们分开了。 “And when I see you, my children, thus united by a like purity and by all human affections, I say to myself that it is quite impossible that the future should separate you.
上帝是公正的。”——他转向维多琳。 God is just.”—He turned to Victorine.

的的确确，你很快就会是巴黎最富有的女继承人之一了。 Upon my word, you will be one of the richest heiresses in Paris before very long.
你会为爱你的男人堆起金山。 You will heap riches on the man who loves you.
你的父亲会需要你，让你和他住在一起。 Your father will want you to go and live with him.
你会和一个又年轻、英俊、有头衔的男人结婚，他会非常爱你。” You will marry a young and handsome man with a title, and he will idolize you.”
那卖弄风情的寡妇下楼了，她沉重的脚步声打断了沃尔特兰的算命。 The heavy footsteps of the coquettish widow, who was coming down the stairs, interrupted Vautrin’s fortune-telling.
“沃盖妈妈来了，您像明星一样美丽，穿衣服穿得差一点丢了性命。是不是有点憋得慌？”他搂着这位夫人，问道，“胸部绷得太紧了，妈妈！ “Here is Mamma Vauquerre, fair as a starr-r-r, dressed within an inch of her life.Aren’t we a trifle pinched for room?” he inquired, with his arm round the lady; “we are screwed up very tightly about the bust, mamma!

“这个人说着法国式的殷勤话！”这个寡妇侧身在库蒂尔夫人的耳边说道。 “There is a man who can talk the language of French gallantry!” said the widow, bending to speak in Mme. Couture’s ear.

他把双手放在两人的头上。 And he laid a hand on either head.

“你觉得沃尔特兰先生会和我私奔吗？”她放低声音，又说道。 “Do you think that M. Vautrin means to run away with me?” she added, lowering her voice.
“悲哉!”这个寡妇说。 “Lack-a-day!” said the widow.
“哦！亲爱的妈妈，但愿事情真会像善人沃尔特兰先生说的那样发生！”维多琳看着自己的手，叹了一口气说道。 “Oh! mamma dear, suppose it should really happen as that kind M. Vautrin said!” said Victorine with a sigh as she looked at her hands.
只剩下这两位女士了。 The two women were alone together.
“哎呀，要让这预言实现也不是很难，”年长一些的夫人说，“只要你的魔鬼哥哥一掉下马，他——”“哦！妈妈。” “Why, it wouldn’t take much to bring it to pass,” said the elderly lady; “just a fall from his horse, and your monster of a brother—” “Oh! mamma.”
“上帝啊！ “Good Lord!
嗯，也许诅咒一个敌人是罪过。”寡妇说道， Well, perhaps it is a sin to wish bad luck to an enemy,” the widow remarked.
“我会为此忏悔的。 “I will do penance for it.
但是，我还是会带着极大的喜悦在他的坟上撒满鲜花的，这是事实。 Still, I would strew flowers on his grave with the greatest pleasure, and that is the truth.
他就是那么黑心肠！ Black-hearted, that he is!
那个懦弱的家伙不为自己的母亲辩护，还连哄带骗不让你分遗产。 The coward couldn’t speak up for his own mother, and cheats you out of your share by deceit and trickery.
我的表姐有一大笔她自己的财产，但是你很不幸，婚前协定中没有说她带来了多少财产。” My cousin had a pretty fortune of her own, but unluckily for you, nothing was said in the marriage-contract about anything that she might come in for.”
“要是我的财富要建立在牺牲其他人的性命之上，那么我会很不好受。”维多琳说， “It would be very hard if my fortune is to cost some one else his life,” said Victorine.
“要是只有我哥哥死了，我才能得到快乐的话，我宁愿一辈子住在这里。” “If I cannot be happy unless my brother is to be taken out of the world, I would rather stay here all my life.”
“我的天啊！这就像善人沃尔特兰先生说得那样，而且你看，他还满怀虔诚之心呢。”库蒂尔夫人说， “@Mon Dieu!@ it is just as that good M. Vautrin says, and he is full of piety, you see,” Mme. Couture remarked.
“让我很欣慰的是，他不像其他人那样不信奉上帝。那些人说起万能的主，说话的语气比说起魔鬼还要不敬。 “I am very glad to find that he is not an unbeliever like the rest of them that talk of the Almighty with less respect than they do of the Devil.
嗯，就像他说的那样，谁知道上帝乐意带我们走哪一条路呢？” Well, as he was saying, who can know the ways by which it may please Providence to lead us?”
在西尔维的帮助下，两位女士终于将欧仁扶回了他的房间。她们将他平放在床上，厨娘则解开了他的衣服让他睡得更舒服些。 With Sylvie’s help the two women at last succeeded in getting Eugene up to his room; they laid him on the bed, and the cook unfastened his clothes to make him more comfortable.
在她们离开房间之前，维多琳趁着她的监护人转身的时候，在欧仁的额头上吻了一下，感受这偷来的愉悦带给她的所有乐趣。 Before they left the room, Victorine snatched an opportunity when her guardian’s back was turned, and pressed a kiss on Eugene’s forehead, feeling all the joy that this stolen pleasure could give her.
之后，她环顾屋内，好像在将那天所有不可言说的幸福感觉聚集成一个念头。她的记忆汇成了一幅画面。她就这样想着入睡 ，她是巴黎最快乐的人。 Then she looked round the room, and gathering up, as it were, into one single thought all the untold bliss of that day, she made a picture of her memories, and dwelt upon it until she slept, the happiest creature in Paris.
沃尔特兰在狂欢期间趁机往欧仁和高老头的酒里下了药，那晚的狂欢毁了他自己。 That evening’s merry-making, in the course of which Vautrin had given the drugged wine to Eugene and Father Goriot, was his own ruin.
给人灌醉了的比安卡肖恩，忘了跟米绍诺小姐提“鬼上当”的事。 Bianchon, flustered with wine, forgot to open the subject of Trompe-la-Mort with Mlle. Michonneau.
只要提起这个名字就会让沃尔特兰提高警惕。而沃尔特兰，或者不妨说出他的真名，雅克·科兰，实际上就是那个臭名昭著的逃犯。 The mere mention of the name would have set Vautrin on his guard; for Vautrin, or, to give him his real name, Jacques Collin, was in fact the notorious escaped convict.
但是就是那个笑话，那个拉雪兹神父公墓的维纳斯，最终决定了他的命运。 But it was the joke about the Venus of Pere-Lachaise that finally decided his fate.
米绍诺小姐想着这个人慷慨大方，想到自己帮助他在夜里逃跑能拿到更多好处，几乎下定决心要警告这个犯人了。然而事实上，她却陪着普瓦雷出去，去圣安妮小街找那位著名的探长了，她仍然想着那人是一个叫龚杜罗的地方主管，她必须和他合作。 Mlle. Michonneau had very nearly made up her mind to warn the convict and to throw herself on his generosity, with the idea of making a better bargain for herself by helping him to escape that night; but as it was, she went out escorted by Poiret in search of the famous chief of detectives in the Petite Rue Saint-Anne, still thinking that it was the district superintendent—one Gondureau—with whom she had to do.
这位部长客气地接待了两个来访者。 The head of the department received his visitors courteously.
他们谈了一小会儿，明确安排了一些细节问题。 There was a little talk, and the details were definitely arranged.
米绍诺小姐问他要了执行调查所需要的药。 Mlle. Michonneau asked for the draught that she was to administer in order to set about her investigation.
但是这位重要人物明显的满意之情让米绍诺小姐陷入了思考，她开始意识到这桩生意牵扯的不单是抓一个在逃犯的问题。 But the great man’s evident satisfaction set Mlle. Michonneau thinking; and she began to see that this business involved something more than the mere capture of a runaway convict.
在他打开桌子的抽屉翻找那个小药瓶的时候，她绞尽脑汁思索着这个问题。于是她得出结论，由于囚犯向警察告密，因此警察期望得到一大笔钱。 She racked her brains while he looked in a drawer in his desk for the little phial, and it dawned upon her that in consequence of treacherous revelations made by the prisoners the police were hoping to lay their hands on a considerable sum of money.
但是在她向这个圣安妮小街的老狐狸暗示了她的怀疑之后，这位官员露出了微笑，试图打消她的疑虑。 But on hinting her suspicions to the old fox of the Petite Rue Saint-Anne, that officer began to smile, and tried to put her off the scent.
“这是个错觉。”他说， “A delusion,” he said.
“科兰的机构是现在所发现的危险机构之中最危险的一个。 “Collin’s @sorbonne@ is the most dangerous that has yet been found among the dangerous classes.
就这些，而且那些流氓也清楚地意识到那一点了。 That is all, and the rascals are quite aware of it.
他们团结在他周围，总而言之，他是其联盟中的主心骨，是他们的波拿巴，在他们中间非常受欢迎。 They rally round him; he is the backbone of the federation, its Bonaparte, in short; he is very popular with them all.
这流氓绝不会在格雷夫广场被砍下木块的。 The rogue will never leave his @chump@ in the Place de Greve.”
米绍诺小姐似乎感到很迷惑，所以龚杜罗就为她解释那两个暗语。 As Mlle. Michonneau seemed mystified, Gondureau explained the two slang words for her benefit.
“机构”和“木块”是两个很有说服力的表达方式，是从盗贼的黑话中借用来的词语，所有人类中的小偷都被迫从两个方面看待人类的头颅。 Sorbonne and @chump@ are two forcible expressions borrowed from thieves’ Latin, thieves, of all people, being compelled to consider the human head in its two aspects.
“机构”就是一个活人的头颅，是用来思考的工具——是他的顾问；“木块”则是一个轻蔑的称呼，暗示了当斧子砍下一颗人头之后，那颗脑袋就变得多么没有价值。 A sorbonne is the head of a living man, his faculty of thinking—his council; a chump is a contemptuous epithet that implies how little a human head is worth after the axe has done its work.
“科兰让我们出尽洋相，”他继续说， “Collin is playing us off,” he continued.
“当我们碰上像英国锻造的钢条一样的家伙时，我们总是只有一条路可走——他一想到要稍微反抗一下，我们就可以杀了他。 “When we come across a man like a bar of steel tempered in the English fashion, there is always one resource left—we can kill him if he takes it into his head to make the least resistance.
我们正在考虑明天早上杀掉科兰的几种方法。 We are reckoning on several methods of killing Collin to-morrow morning.
这就省了审判过程，这个社会也可以省下他的看守费用，还有饭钱。 It saves a trial, and society is rid of him without all the expense of guarding and feeding him.
考虑到安排这个案子上庭、召集证人、支付证人的花费、执行判决，在你可以消灭这些毫无用处的人之前，所有正式手续就要花费三千法郎，这远比给你们的钱要多。 What with getting up the case, summoning witnesses, paying their expenses, and carrying out the sentence, it costs a lot to go through all the proper formalities before you can get quit of one of these good-for-nothings, over and above the three thousand francs that you are going to have.
而且这种方法也节省时间。 There is a saving in time as well.
只要在‘鬼上当’的肚子上插一刀，就能阻止许多罪案的发生，挽救五十个小混混，防止他们步他的后尘。他们就会非常小心，避免自己被送上法庭。 One good thrust of the bayonet into Trompe-la-Mort’s paunch will prevent scores of crimes, and save fifty scoundrels from following his example; they will be very careful to keep themselves out of the police courts.
这就是彻底地完成了警察的工作，真正的慈善家会告诉你阻止罪行比惩罚罪行要好得多。” That is doing the work of the police thoroughly, and true philanthropists will tell you that it is better to prevent crime than to punish it.”
“而且你们这是在为我们的国家效力。”普瓦雷说。 “And you do a service to our country,” said Poiret.
“确实是的，你今晚说的话非常有道理，这才是真正的你。”这位部长说， “Really, you are talking in a very sensible manner tonight, that you are,” said the head of the department.
“是的，当然，我们在为国效力，而且我们也付出了很多。 “Yes, of course, we are serving our country, and we are very hardly used too.
我们为这个社会做了很大的贡献，却没有得到认可。 We do society very great services that are not recognized.
实际上，一个上等人必须跳出世俗的偏见，一个基督徒必须甘心接受带来正确结果的灾祸，就算获得正确的方式很不同寻常也要接受。 In fact, a superior man must rise above vulgar prejudices, and a Christian must resign himself to the mishaps that doing right entails, when right is done in an out-of-the-way style.
巴黎还是巴黎，您看！ Paris is Paris, you see!
这恰好诠释了我的生活——我很荣幸，祝您晚安，小姐。 That is the explanation of my life.—I have the honor to wish you a good-evening, mademoiselle.
我早上会带上我的人去国王花园。 I shall bring my men to the Jardin du Roi in the morning.
叫克里斯托夫去一趟布丰街，告诉他在您之前见我的地方找龚杜罗先生就行了——您的仆人，先生。 Send Christophe to the Rue du Buffon, tell him to ask for M. Gondureau in the house where you saw me before.—Your servant, sir.
要是您有什么东西被偷了，就来找我，我会尽力将您丢的东西物归原主。” If you should ever have anything stolen from you, come to me, and I will do my best to get it back for you.”
“那么，现在，”普瓦雷对米绍诺小姐说，“还有一些笨蛋一听到警察二字就吓得魂飞魄散呢。 “Well, now,” Poiret remarked to Mlle. Michonneau, “there are idiots who are scared out of their wits by the word police.
和那位先生谈话真是感到愉快，而且他想叫你做的事就像打招呼那么简单。第二天注定会成为“沃盖之家”史上最非同寻常的一天。 That was a very pleasant-spoken gentleman, and what he wants you to do is as easy as saying ‘Good-day.’”The next day was destined to be one of the most extraordinary in the annals of the Maison Vauquer.
迄今为止，在平静的公寓生活中，最让人吃惊的事情莫过于离奇的假德朗贝梅尼尔公爵夫人事件，不过这件事已经像流星一般一闪而过了。 Hitherto the most startling occurrence in its tranquil existence had been the portentous, meteor-like apparition of the sham Comtesse de l’Ambermesnil.
但是这个伟大日子带来的灾难将会使之前所有的事件都显得暗淡无光，将为沃盖夫人的余生和她的房客门提供无穷无尽的话题。 But the catastrophes of this great day were to cast all previous events into the shade, and supply an inexhaustible topic of conversation for Mme. Vauquer and her boarders so long as she lived.
首先，高老头和欧仁·德拉斯蒂涅两人一直睡到快十一点。 In the first place, Goriot and Eugene de Rastignac both slept till close upon eleven o’clock.
午夜才从盖特剧院回来的沃盖夫人，也会一直睡到十点半。 Mme. Vauquer, who came home about midnight from the Gaite, lay a-bed till half-past ten.
睡过头的克里斯托夫（他喝完了沃尔特兰的第一瓶酒）耽误了他的工作。尽管早餐时间延误了，但是普瓦雷和米绍诺小姐没有一句怨言。 Christophe, after a prolonged slumber (he had finished Vautrin’s first bottle of wine), was behindhand with his work, but Poiret and Mlle. Michonneau uttered no complaint, though breakfast was delayed.
对于维多琳和库蒂尔夫人来说，她们也会睡到很晚。 As for Victorine and Mme. Couture, they also lay late.
沃尔特兰八点之前就出去了，不过刚好在早餐准备好的时候回来了。 Vautrin went out before eight o’clock, and only came back just as breakfast was ready.
所以当西尔维和克里斯托夫十一点一刻上楼去挨个敲门，告知早餐好了的时候，也没有人提出抗议。 Nobody protested, therefore, when Sylvie and Christophe went up at a quarter past eleven, knocked at all the doors, and announced that breakfast was waiting.
就在西尔维和男仆在楼上的时候，第一个下来的米绍诺小姐将药瓶里的东西倒进属于沃尔特兰的银质杯子里——那只杯子和其他杯子一起放在双重蒸锅里，锅里热着早间冲咖啡用的奶油。 While Sylvie and the man were upstairs, Mlle. Michonneau, who came down first, poured the contents of the phial into the silver cup belonging to Vautrin—it was standing with the others in the bain-marie that kept the cream hot for the morning coffee.
老处女利用旅馆的这个习惯来执行她的任务。 The spinster had reckoned on this custom of the house to do her stroke of business.
最终七个房客都坐在了一起，都费了一阵力气。 The seven lodgers were at last collected together, not without some difficulty.
就在欧仁伸着懒腰、打着哈欠下楼的时候，守门人递给他一封德纽沁根夫人的来信。 Just as Eugene came downstairs, stretching himself and yawning, a commissionaire handed him a letter from Mme. de Nucingen.
信里这样写着：“一想到你，我既没有感到虚伪的自负，也没有感到怒气，我的朋友。 It ran thus:—“I feel neither false vanity nor anger where you are concerned, my friend.
我一直等你等到凌晨两点。 Till two o’clock this morning I waited for you.
哦，等一个你爱的人！ Oh, that waiting for one whom you love!
经过这种折磨的人不会让其他人承受这种痛苦了。 No one that had passed through that torture could inflict it on another.
现在，我知道你之前从没爱过别人。 I know now that you have never loved before.
到底发生什么事了呢？ What can have happened?
我的心里充满了焦虑。 Anxiety has taken hold of me.
要不是我怕泄露心中的秘密，我就会亲自过去弄清楚到底发生了什么事。 I would have come myself to find out what had happened, if I had not feared to betray the secrets of my heart.
在这个时候，我怎么能走出门或坐车出门呢？ How can I walk out or drive out at this time of day?
这不会毁了我吗？ Would it not be ruin?
我充分感受到，做女人是多么悲惨的一件事啊。 I have felt to the full how wretched it is to be a woman.
给我写点什么，打消我的疑虑吧，告诉我为什么父亲跟你说了之后，你却还是不来找我。 Send a word to reassure me, and explain how it is that you have not come after what my father told you.
我会生气的，但是我会原谅你。 I shall be angry, but I will forgive you.
说一句话吧，看在我可怜的份上。 One word, for pity’s sake.
你很快就会来找我，是不是？ You will come to me soon, will you not?
要是你很忙，给我写几个字就够了。 If you are busy, a line will be enough.
说‘我会赶去你那里，’或者说，‘我病了’。但是要是你病了，我父亲会来告诉我。 Say, ‘I will hasten to you,’ or else, ‘I am ill.’ But if you were ill my father would have come to tell me so.
到底发生什么事了呢？……” What can have happened?...”
“是的，到底发生什么事了呢？”欧仁大声叫道，之后就匆忙下楼去餐厅，他将那封信揉成一团，不再看一眼。 “Yes, indeed, what has happened?” exclaimed Eugene, and, hurrying down to the dining-room, he crumpled up the letter without reading any more.
“几点了？” “What time is it?”
“十一点半。”沃尔特兰说着往自己的咖啡里放了一块糖。 “Half-past eleven,” said Vautrin, dropping a lump of sugar into his coffee.
这个在逃犯以冷峻而迷人的目光瞥了一眼欧仁。据说拥有这种魔力的男人凭借这一瞥能镇住精神病院里发狂的疯子。 The escaped convict cast a glance at Eugene, a cold and fascinating glance; men gifted with this magnetic power can quell furious lunatics in a madhouse by such a glance, it is said.
欧仁的四肢都在发抖。 Eugene shook in every limb.
街上传来了车轮的声音，下一秒钟，一个脸上有疤的男人就冲进了房间。 There was the sound of wheels in the street, and in another moment a man with a scared face rushed into the room.
那是塔耶费先生的一个仆人，库蒂尔夫人立刻认出了那套制服。 It was one of M. Taillefer’s servants; Mme. Couture recognized the livery at once.
“小姐，”他叫道，“您的父亲要见您——出了一件可怕的事！ “Mademoiselle,” he cried, “your father is asking for you—something terrible has happened!
弗雷德里克先生在一场决斗中被刺中前额，医生已经说没救了。 M. Frederic has had a sword thrust in the forehead in a duel, and the doctors have given him up.
您已经赶不及去跟他道别了！他已经昏迷了。” You will scarcely be in time to say good-bye to him! he is unconscious.”
“可怜的年轻人！”沃尔特兰叫道， “Poor young fellow!” exclaimed Vautrin.
“为什么人们在有了三万里弗赫的稳定收入时，还要去打架呢？ “How can people brawl when they have a certain income of thirty thousand livres?
年轻人总是不太规矩，这是事实。” Young people have bad manners, and that is a fact.”
“先生！”欧仁喊道。 “Sir!” cried Eugene.
“哦，你想说什么，你这个大男孩！”沃尔特兰边说边平静地喝下他的咖啡。他这个动作米绍诺小姐都细细地看在眼里。她看得过于专心，以至于没工夫理会那个别人都吃惊得说不出话的消息。 “Well, what then, you big baby!” said Vautrin, swallowing down his coffee imperturbably, an operation which Mlle. Michonneau watched with such close attention that she had no emotion to spare for the amazing news that had struck the others dumb with amazement.
“在巴黎不是每天早上都有决斗吗？”沃尔特兰又说道。 “Are there not duels every morning in Paris?” added Vautrin.
“我跟你一起去，维多琳。”库蒂尔夫人说完，两位女士就匆忙离开了，帽子也没戴，围巾也没围。 “I will go with you, Victorine,” said Mme. Couture, and the two women hurried away at once without either hats or shawls.
在维多琳离开之前，她用那包含泪水的眼睛看了欧仁一眼，好像在说——“我没有想到我们的幸福会让我掉眼泪！” But before she went, Victorine, with her eyes full of tears, gave Eugene a glance that said—“How little I thought that our happiness should cost me tears!”
“我的天啊，您是先知，沃尔特兰先生。”沃盖夫人说。 “Dear me, you are a prophet, M. Vautrin,” said Mme. Vauquer.
“我精通一切。”沃尔特兰说。 “I am all sorts of things,” said Vautrin.
“很奇怪，不是吗？”沃盖夫人说。她又将一系列应景而平常的话串在了一起。 “Queer, isn’t it?” said Mme. Vauquer, stringing together a succession of commonplaces suited to the occasion.
“死神不事先和我们商量就将我们带走。 “Death takes us off without asking us about it.
真是白发人送黑发人。 The young often go before the old.
我们女人真是幸运，不用去决斗，但是我们也有一些男人不用承受的委屈。 It is a lucky thing for us women that we are not liable to fight duels, but we have other complaints that men don’t suffer from.
我们要生孩子，而且需要很长时间才能从其中恢复过来。 We bear children, and it takes a long time to get over it.
维多琳真是发了横财啦！ What a windfall for Victorine!
她父亲现在要承认她了！” Her father will have to acknowledge her now!”
“嘿！”沃尔特兰看着欧仁说，“昨天她还一文不名，今天早上她就成了百万富婆了。” “There!” said Vautrin, looking at Eugene, “yesterday she had not a penny; this morning she has several millions to her fortune.”
“我说，欧仁先生！”沃盖夫人大声叫道，“你已经脱离困境啦！” “I say, M. Eugene!” cried Mme. Vauquer, “you have landed on your feet!”
就在这感叹发出之时，高老头看着这个法律系学生，看到那封揉成一团的信还在他的手里。 At this exclamation, Father Goriot looked at the student, and saw the crumpled letter still in his hand.
“你还没有看完呢！ “You have not read it through!
这是什么意思？ What does this mean?
你要像其他人那样吗?”他问。 Are you going to be like the rest of them?” he asked.
“夫人，我决不会娶维多琳小姐。”欧仁以恐怖而厌恶的表情转向沃盖夫人说道，这让在场的旁观者都吃了一惊。 “Madame, I shall never marry Mlle. Victorine,” said Eugene, turning to Mme. Vauquer with an expression of terror and loathing that surprised the onlookers at this scene.
高老头抓住了这个学生的手，热情地一把握住。 Father Goriot caught the student’s hand and grasped it warmly.
他都快要亲这只手了。 He could have kissed it.
“哦，吼！”沃尔特兰说，“意大利人有一句很好的谚语——让时间去验证。” “Oh, ho!” said Vautrin, “the Italians have a good proverb—@Col tempo@.”
“有回复了吗？”德纽沁根夫人的信使对欧仁说。 “Is there any answer?” said Mme. de Nucingen’s messenger, addressing Eugene.
“就说我会立即过去的。” “Say that I will come directly.”
那个人走了。 The man went.
欧仁正处于如此强烈的刺激之中，以至于他不能保持谨慎了。 Eugene was in a state of such violent excitement that he could not be prudent.
“接下来要做什么？”他大声叫道， “What is to be done?” he exclaimed aloud.
“没有证据！” “There are no proofs!”
沃尔特兰开始笑了起来。 Vautrin began to smile.
尽管他吃下的药已经有了作用，但是这个罪犯如此健壮，他站了起来，看了拉斯蒂涅一眼，以空洞的声音说道：“运气是在我们睡觉的时候到来的，年轻人。”之后就僵硬地倒了下去，就好像被打死了一样。 Though the drug he had taken was doing its work, the convict was so vigorous that he rose to his feet, gave Rastignac a look, and said in hollow tones, “Luck comes to us while we sleep, young man,” and fell stiff and stark, as if he were struck dead.
“这就是神圣的正义！”欧仁说， “So there is a Divine Justice!” said Eugene.
“恩，如果有的话，这就是！ “Well, if ever!
可怜又可爱的沃尔特兰先生怎么了？” What has come to that poor dear M. Vautrin?”
“中风了！”米绍诺小姐喊道。 “A stroke!” cried Mlle. Michonneau.
喂，西尔维！姑娘，快去叫医生。”那位寡妇叫道。 “Here, Sylvie! girl, run for the doctor,” called the widow.
“哦，拉斯蒂涅先生，去找一下比安卡肖恩先生吧，尽快；西尔维可能赶不及见到我们的医生，格兰普雷尔先生。” “Oh, M. Rastignac, just go for M. Bianchon, and be as quick as you can; Sylvie might not be in time to catch our doctor, M. Grimprel.”
拉斯蒂涅很高兴能有个借口逃离这个恐怖的地方，他急忙去找医生只不过是逃避罢了。 Rastignac was glad of an excuse to leave that den of horrors, his hurry for the doctor was nothing but a flight.
“嘿，克里斯托夫，去药剂师那里要一点治中风的药。” “Here, Christophe, go round to the chemist’s and ask for something that’s good for the apoplexy.”
克里斯托夫也走了。 Christophe likewise went.
“高老头，帮我们把他抬上楼去吧。” “Father Goriot, just help us to get him upstairs.”
大家拥着沃尔特兰，小心翼翼地将他从狭窄的楼梯抬上去，平放在他的床上。 Vautrin was taken up among them, carried carefully up the narrow staircase, and laid upon his bed.
“我留在这里也没有用，所以我要去见我的女儿。”高里奥先生说。 “I can do no good here, so I shall go to see my daughter,” said M. Goriot.
“自私的老家伙！”沃盖夫人喊着说, “Selfish old thing!” cried Mme. Vauquer.
“好，滚吧，我希望你像狗一样死去。” “Yes, go; I wish you may die like a dog.”
“你去看看能不能找出点乙醚。”米绍诺小姐对沃盖夫人说。在普瓦雷的帮助下，米绍诺小姐已经解开了病人的衣服。 “Just go and see if you can find some ether,” said Mlle. Michonneau to Mme. Vauquer; the former, with some help from Poiret, had unfastened the sick man’s clothes.
沃盖夫人下楼进了自己的房间，留下米绍诺小姐，她就能任意操控这个局面了。 Mme. Vauquer went down to her room, and left Mlle. Michonneau mistress of the situation.
“现在！拉下他的衬衣，把他翻过身来，快！ “Now! just pull down his shirt and turn him over, quick!
你也许有点用，能让我的端庄不受玷污，”她对普瓦雷说，“不至于像个树桩一样站在那里没用。” You might be of some use in sparing my modesty,” she said to Poiret, “instead of standing there like a stock.”
沃尔特兰被翻了过来，米绍诺小姐在他的肩膀上用力拍了一下，两个白底红字的不祥字母便显现出来。 Vautrin was turned over; Mlle. Michonneau gave his shoulder a sharp slap, and the two portentous letters appeared, white against the red.
“嘿，你轻轻松松就挣到了三千法郎了。”普瓦雷说。他支撑着沃尔特兰，而米绍诺小姐则为他重新穿上衬衣。“喔！ “There, you have earned your three thousand francs very easily,” exclaimed Poiret, supporting Vautrin while Mlle. Michonneau slipped on the shirt again.—“Ouf!
他多沉啊。”他将这个罪犯放平的时候补充道。 How heavy he is,” he added, as he laid the convict down.
“嘘！ “Hush!
或许这里有个保险箱！”这个老处女兴致勃勃地说道。她的目光似乎能穿透墙壁，她那双贪婪的眼睛仔细检查着家具上的每一个物件， Suppose there is a strong-box here!” said the old maid briskly; her glances seemed to pierce the walls, she scrutinized every article of the furniture with greedy eyes.
“我们能找出什么借口来打开那个桌子吗？” “Could we find some excuse for opening that desk?”
“那可能不太合适。”普瓦雷回答说。 “It mightn’t be quite right,” responded Poiret to this.
“又有什么坏处呢？ “Where is the harm?
这是从各种人那里偷来的钱，所以那钱现在不属于任何人。 It is money stolen from all sorts of people, so it doesn’t belong to any one now.
但是我们没时间了，沃盖来了。” But we haven’t time, there is the Vauquer.”
“乙醚在这里。”那位女士说， “Here is the ether,” said that lady.
“我不得不说今天可是多事之日啊。 “I must say that this is an eventful day.
天啊！那个人不可能是中风，他像凝乳一样白。” Lord! that man can’t have had a stroke; he is as white as curds.”
“像凝乳一样白？”普瓦雷跟着说道。 “White as curds?” echoed Poiret.
“而且他的脉搏也稳定了。”这个寡妇把手放在他的胸脯上说。 “And his pulse is steady,” said the widow, laying her hand on his breast.
“稳定了？”普瓦雷惊讶地说。 “Steady?” said the astonished Poiret.
“他没事了。” “He is all right.”
“你这样认为吗？”普瓦雷问。 “Do you think so?” asked Poiret.
“主啊！ “Lord!
是的，他看起来就像在睡觉一样。 Yes, he looks as if he were sleeping.
西尔维已经去叫医生了。 Sylvie has gone for a doctor.
我说，米绍诺小姐，他正吸着乙醚呢。 I say, Mlle. Michonneau, he is sniffing the ether.
唉！只是一阵痉挛。 Pooh! it is only a spasm.
他的脉搏很平稳。 His pulse is good.
他就像土耳其人一样强壮。 He is as strong as a Turk.
您看看，小姐，他胸口的毛发多浓密，这种人能活到一百岁。 Just look, mademoiselle, what a fur tippet he has on his chest; that is the sort of man to live till he is a hundred.
不过他假发戴得很牢靠。 His wig holds on tightly, however.
我的天啊！那是粘上去的，他的头发是红色的，这就是他戴假发的原因了。 Dear me! it is glued on, and his own hair is red; that is why he wears a wig.
他们说红头发的人不是最好的人就是最坏的人。 They say that red-haired people are either the worst or the best.
我想他是不是一个好人呢？” Is he one of the good ones, I wonder?”
“好到可以吊死了。”普瓦雷说。 “Good to hang,” said Poiret.
“你是说吊在美女的脖子上吧。”米绍诺小姐赶忙说道。 “Round a pretty woman’s neck, you mean,” said Mlle Michonneau, hastily.
“赶快走开吧，普瓦雷先生。 “Just go away, M. Poiret.
在你们男人生病的时候，照顾你们是女人的职责。 It is a woman’s duty to nurse you men when you are ill.
而且，为了你正在做的事情好，你也可以走了。”她又说， Besides, for all the good you are doing, you may as well take yourself off,” she added.
“沃盖夫人和我会好好照顾亲爱的沃尔特兰先生的。” “Mme. Vauquer and I will take great care of dear M. Vautrin.
普瓦雷踮着脚尖一声不吭地出去了，就像一只被主人踢出家门的狗。 Poiret went out on tiptoe without a murmur, like a dog kicked out of the room by his master.
拉斯蒂涅出来想透一下气，活动活动。他想呼吸新鲜空气，他觉得自己快要窒息了。 Rastignac had gone out for the sake of physical exertion; he wanted to breathe the air, he felt stifled.
昨晚他还打算阻止这场安排在今天早上八点半的谋杀。 Yesterday evening he had meant to prevent the murder arranged for half-past eight that morning.
到底发生了什么？ What had happened?
他现在应该做什么呢？ What ought he to do now?
他想着自己可能被牵连在内了，不禁浑身发抖。 He trembled to think that he himself might be implicated.
沃尔特兰的冷酷更加让他惊慌不已。 Vautrin’s coolness still further dismayed him.
“但是，沃尔特兰怎么能没留一句遗言就死了呢？”拉斯蒂涅问自己。 “Yet, how if Vautrin should die without saying a word?” Rastignac asked himself.
他在卢森堡花园的小径中匆忙地走着，好像正义的猎犬正在后面追赶他，而他已经听到了一群狗的叫声一样。 He hurried along the alleys of the Luxembourg Gardens as if the hounds of justice were after him, and he already heard the baying of the pack.
“嘿？”比安卡肖恩大声喊，“你看《飞行员报》了吗？” “Well?” shouted Bianchon, “you have seen the @Pilote@?”
《飞行员报》是一份激进的报纸，是由蒂索先生主编的。 The @Pilote@ was a Radical sheet, edited by M. Tissot.
它比早报晚发行几个小时，主要代表农村订阅者的利益；因为它比一般的地区报纸早二十四小时将早间新闻传送到各个省市地区。 It came out several hours later than the morning papers, and was meant for the benefit of country subscribers; for it brought the morning news into provincial districts twenty-four hours sooner than the ordinary local journals.
“这里面记载了一件绝妙的事。”这位科钦医院的住院医生说道， “There is a wonderful history in it,” said the house student of the Hopital Cochin.
“年轻的塔耶费激怒了保守派弗朗谢森尼伯爵，伯爵就将几寸剑尖刺进了他的前额。 “Young Taillefer called out Count Franchessini, of the Old Guard, and the Count put a couple of inches of steel into his forehead.
小维多琳就成为巴黎最富有的女继承人之一了！ And here is little Victorine one of the richest heiresses in Paris!
要是我们早知道是这样，嗯？ If we had known that, eh?
死亡真是个靠运气的游戏！ What a game of chance death is!
他们说维多琳和你很亲密，这是真的吗？” They say Victorine was sweet on you; was there any truth in it?”
“闭嘴，比安卡肖恩，我决不会娶她。 “Shut up, Bianchon; I shall never marry her.
我爱上了一位迷人的女士，她也爱我，所以——”“你说这话，就好像你要毁了自己来忠诚于她似的。 I am in love with a charming woman, and she is in love with me, so—” “You said that as if you were screwing yourself up to be faithful to her.
我应该看看这个值得你牺牲塔耶费大人钱财的女人！” I should like to see the woman worth the sacrifice of Master Taillefer’s money!”
“地狱所有的恶魔都跟上我了吗？”拉斯蒂涅喊道。 “Are all the devils of hell at my heels?” cried Rastignac.
“你怎么了？ “What is the matter with you?
你疯了吗？ Are you mad?
把你的手给我。”比安卡肖恩说，“让我给你把把脉。 Give us your hand,” said Bianchon, “and let me feel your pulse.
你发烧了。” You are feverish.”
“去沃盖妈妈那里吧。”拉斯蒂涅说，“那个卑鄙的沃尔特兰已经倒了下去，就像死了一样。” “Just go to Mother Vauquer’s,” said Rastignac; “that scoundrel Vautrin has dropped down like one dead.”
“啊哈！”比安卡肖恩说着留下拉斯蒂涅一个人在那里反省，“你证实了我的怀疑，现在我要证实我自己的了。” “Aha!” said Bianchon, leaving Rastignac to his reflections, “you confirm my suspicions, and now I mean to make sure for myself.”
这个法律系学生散步了很长时间，这对他来说是一次难忘的经历。 The law student’s long walk was a memorable one for him.
他稍微审视了自己的良知。 He made in some sort a survey of his conscience.
在一番仔细审视、犹豫和自我反省之后，他的荣誉最终平安通过了这次尖锐而可怕的考验，就像铁棒经受住了英式的锤炼一样。 After a close scrutiny, after hesitation and self-examination, his honor at any rate came out scatheless from this sharp and terrible ordeal, like a bar of iron tested in the English fashion.
他想起高老头前晚信心满怀的样子；他回忆起在阿图瓦街为他布置的房间，他也由此能离德尔菲娜更近；随后他又想起了那封信，他又读了一遍，亲吻了信纸。 He remembered Father Goriot’s confidences of the evening before; he recollected the rooms taken for him in the Rue d’Artois, so that he might be near Delphine; and then he thought of his letter, and read it again and kissed it.
“这样的爱是我安全的支柱。”他对自己说， “Such a love is my anchor of safety,” he said to himself.
“老人家必定心如刀绞！ “How the old man’s heart must have been wrung!
他没有说任何他所承受的事，但是谁不会猜测呢？ He says nothing about all that he has been through; but who could not guess?
那么，我要像对待父亲一样对待他，他的生活应该就会很幸福的。 Well, then, I will be like a son to him; his life shall be made happy.
要是她在乎我，她会常常过来陪他度过一天的。 If she cares for me, she will often come to spend the day with him.
伟大的德雷斯多伯爵夫人是个没心肝的家伙，她会让她的父亲去当她的大厅守门人。 That grand Comtesse de Restaud is a heartless thing; she would make her father into her hall porter.
亲爱的德尔菲娜！她对老人更好一点，她值得我去爱。 Dear Delphine! she is kinder to the old man; she is worthy to be loved.
啊！今晚我应该会非常快乐！” Ah! this evening I shall be very happy!”
他摘下他的手表，欣赏了一番。 He took out his watch and admired it.
“我除了成功，一无所有！ “I have had nothing but success!
要是两个人打算永远相爱，他们就会相互扶持，所以我能接受这个。 If two people mean to love each other for ever, they may help each other, and I can take this.
而且，我也会成功的，我会百倍地偿还她。 Besides, I shall succeed, and I will pay her a hundredfold.
在这种联络关系中，没有任何违法之处，也没什么能让最严格的道德家皱眉头的地方。 There is nothing criminal in this liaison; nothing that could cause the most austere moralist to frown.
有多少备受尊敬的人都牵涉进类似的关系中啊！ How many respectable people contract similar unions!
我们没有欺骗任何人，而欺骗让我们的人格蒙羞。 We deceive nobody; it is deception that makes a position humiliating.
要是你说了谎话，你马上就贬低了自己。 If you lie, you lower yourself at once.
她和她的丈夫已经分居很久了。 She and her husband have lived apart for a long while.
而且，要是我去见那个阿尔萨斯人，让他休了他不能给予其幸福的妻子，会怎么样呢？” Besides, how if I called upon that Alsatian to resign a wife whom he cannot make happy?”
拉斯蒂涅的自我斗争持续了很久。尽管年轻人的审慎不可避免地占了上风，但是大约四点半的时候，难以抗拒的好奇心驱使他在暮色降临之时回到了“沃盖之家”。 Rastignac’s battle with himself went on for a long while; and though the scruples of youth inevitably gained the day, an irresistible curiosity led him, about half-past four, to return to the Maison Vauquer through the gathering dusk.
比安卡肖恩已近给沃尔特兰服用了催吐剂，并将他的胃里的呕吐物收集起来，用于在医院做化学分析。 Bianchon had given Vautrin an emetic, reserving the contents of the stomach for chemical analysis at the hospital.
米绍诺小姐的殷勤和爽快进一步增强了他对她的猜疑。 Mlle. Michonneau’s officious alacrity had still further strengthened his suspicions of her.
此外，沃尔特兰恢复得如此之快，以至于让人们不由得怀疑这旅馆里有人密谋算计了这个所有欢乐的领导者。 Vautrin, moreover, had recovered so quickly that it was impossible not to suspect some plot against the leader of all frolics at the lodging-house.
拉斯蒂涅进来的时候，沃尔特兰正站在餐厅的壁炉前面。 Vautrin was standing in front of the stove in the dining-room when Rastignac came in.
听到小塔耶费决斗的消息，所有房客都比平时更快地聚集起来。 All the lodgers were assembled sooner than usual by the news of young Taillefer’s duel.
他们急切地想知道关于这件事的任何细节，讨论着维多琳前途可能会发生的变化。 They were anxious to hear any detail about the affair, and to talk over the probable change in Victorine’s prospects.
只有高老头缺席，但其他人都在议论纷纷。 Father Goriot alone was absent, but the rest were chatting.
欧仁一进房间，就遇上了沃尔特兰难以捉摸的眼神。 No sooner did Eugene come into the room, than his eyes met the inscrutable gaze of Vautrin.
这和之前解读他思想的目光一模一样——那目光有着能唤醒他心中邪恶念头的力量。 It was the same look that had read his thoughts before—the look that had such power to waken evil thoughts in his heart.
他打了一个寒战。 He shuddered.
“哦，亲爱的孩子。”这个在逃犯说道，“我一时半会儿可能还死不了呢。 “Well, dear boy,” said the escaped convict, “I am likely to cheat death for a good while yet.
据这些女士们说，我刚才中风了，那一下连头牛都吃不消，但是我神奇地恢复了。” According to these ladies, I have had a stroke that would have felled an ox, and come off with flying colors.”
“你是说公牛吧。”那寡妇大声说。 “A bull you might say,” cried the widow.
“看见我还活着，你可能真的会觉得遗憾。”沃尔特兰在拉斯蒂涅的耳边说，他觉得自己已经猜到这个学生的想法了， “You really might be sorry to see me still alive,” said Vautrin in Rastignac’s ear, thinking that he guessed the student’s thoughts.
“你对自己一定很有信心了。” “You must be mighty sure of yourself.”
“米绍诺小姐前天说到一位叫‘鬼上当’的先生，”比安卡肖恩说，“的确，这个名字对你来说非常恰当。” “Mlle. Michonneau was talking the day before yesterday about a gentleman named @Trompe-la-Mort@,” said Bianchon; “and, upon my word, that name would do very well for you.”
沃尔特兰好像被雷击了一下似的。 Vautrin seemed thunderstruck.
他脸色发白，踉踉跄跄地向后退去。 He turned pale, and staggered back.
他那有吸引力的目光，像一道明亮的光线一样投到了米绍诺小姐身上。在这种强烈意志的影响之下，这个老处女向后退着，浑身发抖，最后瘫在椅子里。 He turned his magnetic glance, like a ray of vivid light, on Mlle. Michonneau; the old maid shrank and trembled under the influence of that strong will, and collapsed into a chair.
温厚的面具从这个罪犯的脸上卸了下来。从他那明摆着的凶恶表情中，普瓦雷感到这个老处女有危险，于是急忙走到他们中间。 The mask of good-nature had dropped from the convict’s face; from the unmistakable ferocity of that sinister look, Poiret felt that the old maid was in danger, and hastily stepped between them.
房客一点也看不懂这一幕。他们哑口无言，呆呆地旁观着。 None of the lodgers understood this scene in the least, they looked on in mute amazement.
所有人都停了下来。 There was a pause.
就在那时，外面传来了踏步声。似乎有士兵在外面，因为街边的人行道上有几把来复枪叩击的声音。 Just then there was a sound of tramping feet outside; there were soldiers there, it seemed, for there was a ring of several rifles on the pavement of the street.
当四个人从客厅进来的时候，科兰正机械地环顾四周墙壁，想找一条路逃走。 Collin was mechanically looking round the walls for a way of escape, when four men entered by way of the sitting-room.
“以国王和法律的名义！”一位官员说道，但是这句话淹没在了一片震惊的咕哝声中。 “In the name of the King and the Law!” said an officer, but the words were almost lost in a murmur of astonishment.
房间陷入了静默。 Silence fell on the room.
房客们为其中的三位先生让了路，那三个人每人手上都有一支上了膛的手枪，放在口袋里。 The lodgers made way for three of the men, who had each a hand on a cocked pistol in a side pocket.
跟着侦探的两名警察守住了客厅的门口，又有两个人出现在通往楼梯的门口。 Two policemen, who followed the detectives, kept the entrance to the sitting-room, and two more men appeared in the doorway that gave access to the staircase.
从花园传来脚步声，又传来几个士兵叩击来复枪，击中窗下鹅卵石的声音。 A sound of footsteps came from the garden, and again the rifles of several soldiers rang on the cobblestones under the window.
“鬼上当”所有能逃出生天的机会都被阻断了，所有人都本能地将目光转向他。 All chance of salvation by flight was cut off for Trompe-la-Mort, to whom all eyes instinctively turned.
探长径直向他走去，开始时用力在他脑袋上打一巴掌。于是假发脱落，露出了科兰丑陋无比的整张脸。 The chief walked straight up to him, and commenced operations by giving him a sharp blow on the head, so that the wig fell off, and Collin’s face was revealed in all its ugliness.
这一头砖红色的短寸头暗含着狡猾和可怕的力量，整个头和他强健有力的身躯相协调。在那一刻地狱之火似乎在他的眼中闪烁。 There was a terrible suggestion of strength mingled with cunning in the short, brick-red crop of hair, the whole head was in harmony with his powerful frame, and at that moment the fires of hell seemed to gleam from his eyes.
就在那一刹那，真正的沃尔特兰闪现，全然呈现在众人面前。他们了解他的过去、他的现在、他的将来、他无情的教条、他的行为、他对自己快乐的信仰、他的玩世不恭和对人性的蔑视所授予他的王权，还有他抵抗所有审判的躯体中所蕴含的力量。 In that flash the real Vautrin shone forth, revealed at once before them all; they understood his past, his present, and future, his pitiless doctrines, his actions, the religion of his own good pleasure, the majesty with which his cynicism and contempt for mankind invested him, the physical strength of an organization proof against all trials.
热血涌上他的脸，他如野猫般怒目圆睁。 The blood flew to his face, and his eyes glared like the eyes of a wild cat.
他突然后退；他发出的野蛮的力量和凶猛的咆哮让房客们都惊叫不已。 He started back with savage energy and a fierce growl that drew exclamations of alarm from the lodgers.
看着这个狮子般的动作，警察们在一片喧嚷声的掩护下拿起了手枪。 At that leonine start the police caught at their pistols under cover of the general clamor.
科兰看到隐隐放光的枪口，知道自己处境危险，便立即显示出最高层次的精神力量。 Collin saw the gleaming muzzles of the weapons, saw his danger, and instantly gave proof of a power of the highest order.
他脸色突变的那一幕可怕而庄严。他只能被比喻成充满蒸汽的大锅炉，那种蒸汽能炸飞山脉，可是这股可怕的力量却只要滴一滴冷水就能立刻驱散。 There was something horrible and majestic in the spectacle of the sudden transformation in his face; he could only be compared to a cauldron full of the steam that can send mountains flying, a terrific force dispelled in a moment by a drop of cold water.
冷却他狂怒的那滴水就是像闪电一样在他脑中一闪而过的念头。 The drop of water that cooled his wrathful fury was a reflection that flashed across his brain like lightning.
他开始微笑，低下头看着自己的假发。 He began to smile, and looked down at his wig.
“您今天并不是特别有礼貌。”他对探长说着，向警察点了点头，伸出了双手。 “You are not in the politest of humors to-day,” he remarked to the chief, and he held out his hands to the policemen with a jerk of his head.
“先生，”他说，“戴上链锁或者手铐吧。 “Gentlemen,” he said, “put on the bracelets or the handcuffs.
我请在场的各位作证，我没有反抗。” I call on those present to witness that I make no resistance.”
一阵钦佩的嘟囔声像火焰和岩浆一样从这个人类火山中突然喷出，跑遍整个屋子，又同样突然停息了。 A murmur of admiration ran through the room at the sudden outpouring like fire and lava flood from this human volcano, and its equally sudden cessation.
“还有笔买卖等着你呢，破坏大王。”这个罪犯看着这位著名的警署指挥官，说道。 “There’s a sell for you, master crusher,” the convict added, looking at the famous director of police.
“快，脱衣服！”圣安妮小街的人轻蔑地说。 “Come, strip!” said he of the Petite Rue Saint-Anne, contemptuously.
“为什么？”科兰问， “Why?” asked Collin.
“还有女士在场呢，我什么事都没有否认，而且我投降了。” “There are ladies present; I deny nothing, and surrender.”
他停顿了一下，环顾整间屋子，好像一个即将征服观众的演说者。 He paused, and looked round the room like an orator who is about to overwhelm his audience.
“记下这个，拉沙佩勒老爹。”他对着那个身材矮小、头发花白的老人说。那个人独自坐在桌子的另一头。他从公文包里取出一份打印好的表格，开始填写文件。 “Take this down, Daddy Lachapelle,” he went on, addressing a little, white-haired old man who had seated himself at the end of the table; and after drawing a printed form from the portfolio, was proceeding to draw up a document.
“我承认自己是雅克·科兰，又名‘鬼上当’，被判二十年劳役拘禁，而且我刚才证明了我并非浪得虚名——要是我稍微抬一下手，”他对着其他房客继续说，“站在远处的那三个卑鄙混蛋就会让沃盖妈妈家里的壁炉沾上鲜血。 “I acknowledge myself to be Jacques Collin, otherwise known as Trompe-la-Mort, condemned to twenty years’ penal servitude, and I have just proved that I have come fairly by my nickname.—If I had as much as raised my hand,” he went on, addressing the other lodgers, “those three sneaking wretches yonder would have drawn claret on Mamma Vauquer’s domestic hearth.
那三个混账合谋陷害我。” The rogues have laid their heads together to set a trap for me.”
沃盖妈妈听了这些话后，头晕目眩，都快昏过去了。 Mme. Vauquer felt sick and faint at these words.
“天啊！”她哭喊着，“这简直让人不敢相信，就在昨晚我还和他在盖特剧院呢！”她对西尔维说。 “Good Lord!” she cried, “this does give one a turn; and me at the Gaite with him only last night!” she said to Sylvie.
“冷静一些，妈妈。”科兰继续说， “Summon your philosophy, mamma,” Collin resumed.
“昨晚坐在我在盖特剧院的包厢里很不幸吗？ “Is it a misfortune to have sat in my box at the Gaite yesterday evening?
那么，你们就比我们要好吗？ After all, are you better than we are?
你们烙在心里的标记比我们肩膀上的这个标记更可耻。这是个烂到骨子里的社会，你们都是这社会里的软弱无力的人。 The brand upon our shoulders is less shameful than the brand set on your hearts, you flabby members of a society rotten to the core.
你们之中最优秀的人也不配和我相提并论。” Not the best man among you could stand up to me.”
他的目光落在了拉斯蒂涅身上，他对学生说话时的愉快笑容似乎和他眼中的野蛮表情很不相称，“我们的小协议仍然有效，亲爱的孩子，你可以在任何你喜欢的时候接受！ His eyes rested upon Rastignac, to whom he spoke with a pleasant smile that seemed strangely at variance with the savage expression in his eyes.—“Our little bargain still holds good, dear boy; you can accept any time you like!
你明白吗？” Do you understand?”
之后他唱了起来：“一个迷人而质朴的女孩，我的方谢特。” And he sang:“A charming girl is my Fanchette In her simplicity.”
“别自寻烦恼。”他继续说，“我能拿到钱。 “Don’t you trouble yourself,” he went on; “I can get in my money.
他们太害怕我了，不敢跟我使花招。” They are too much afraid of me to swindle me.”
这个罪犯的牢狱经历，包括语言和习惯、从幽默到恐怖的强烈转变、骇人听闻的气概、轻浮和神秘的深度，逐一从这个讲话者的口中显现出来了。他好像再也不是一个人了，而是一种堕落种族的典范和喉舌，那是一个残忍、逢迎、头脑清醒却野蛮的种族。 The convicts’ prison, its language and customs, its sudden sharp transitions from the humorous to the horrible, its appalling grandeur, its triviality and its dark depths, were all revealed in turn by the speaker’s discourse; he seemed to be no longer a man, but the type and mouthpiece of a degenerate race, a brutal, supple, clear-headed race of savages.
在某一刻科兰成为了地狱诗人，在那里能找到所有能打动人性的思想和激情（除了悔改之外）。 In one moment Collin became the poet of an inferno, wherein all thoughts and passions that move human nature (save repentance) find a place.
他看着拉斯蒂涅，好像堕落的大天使一样，准备抗争到底。 He looked about him like a fallen archangel who is for war to the end.
拉斯蒂涅垂下了眼睛，承认了这种罪恶的关系，以补偿自己邪恶的想法。 Rastignac lowered his eyes, and acknowledged this kinship claimed by crime as an expiation of his own evil thoughts.
“是谁背叛了我呢？”科兰边说边用可怕的眼神扫视着整个屋子。 “Who betrayed me?” said Collin, and his terrible eyes traveled round the room.
突然他的目光落在了米绍诺小姐身上。 Suddenly they rested on Mlle. Michonneau.
“是你，老太婆！”他说， “It was you, old cat!” he said.
“那次假中风就是你搞的鬼，锐利的目光！……只要我说两句话，不到一个星期你的喉咙就会被割断，但是我原谅你，我是个基督徒。 “That sham stroke of apoplexy was your doing, lynx eyes!...Two words from me, and your throat would be cut in less than a week, but I forgive you, I am a Christian.
你也没有出卖我。 You did not sell me either.
但是是谁呢？——啊哈！你可以上楼搜查。”他听到警官打开他的衣橱，拿走他的财物，大声喊道， But who did?—Aha! you may rummage upstairs,” he shouted, hearing the police officers opening his cupboards and taking possession of his effects.
“巢穴是空的，昨天鸟都飞走了，你们依然一无所知。 “The nest is empty, the birds flew away yesterday, and you will be none the wiser.
我的账本在这里呢。”他敲着自己的额头说， My ledgers are here,” he said tapping his forehead.
“现在我知道是谁出卖我了！ “Now I know who sold me!
只能是外号叫‘丝线’的那个混蛋。 It could only be that blackguard Fil-de-Soie.
就是他，老警官，嗯？”他转向那位探长说道， That is who it was, old catchpoll, eh?” he said, turning to the chief.
“把钞票放在那上面时，时间把握得刚刚好。 “It was timed so neatly to get the banknotes up above there.
没给你剩下一分钱——间谍！ There is nothing left for you—spies!
对于‘丝线’来说，他不到两个星期就会丧命，即便你们派出所有警力保护他也没用。 As for Fil-de-Soie, he will be under the daisies in less than a fortnight, even if you were to tell off the whole force to protect him.
你们给米绍诺多少钱？”他问那些警官， How much did you give the Michonnette?” he asked of the police officers.
“一千克朗？ “A thousand crowns?
哦，你这个腐朽的尼龙、包头的碎布、墓地上的维纳斯，我比那些值钱多了。 Oh you Ninon in decay, Pompadour in tatters, Venus of the graveyard, I was worth more than that!
要是你事先警告过我，你能拿到六千法郎。 If you had given me warning, you should have had six thousand francs.
啊！你没想到吧，你这个卖人血肉的老奸商，要不我就会有优待了。 Ah! you had no suspicion of that, old trafficker in flesh and blood, or I should have had the preference.
是的，我宁愿花六千法郎，省去一场不方便的旅途和钱财的损失。”当他们把手铐套在他手腕上时，他说， Yes, I would have given six thousand francs to save myself an inconvenient journey and some loss of money,” he said, as they fastened the handcuffs on his wrists.
“这些家伙以拖延事务为乐，他们把这件事一直拖到最后，让我闲着。 “These folks will amuse themselves by dragging out this business till the end of time to keep me idle.
要是他们直接把我送进监狱，我可以很快用我的老把戏出来，才用不着理会巴黎警察局调查部门的那些笨蛋呢。 If they were to send me straight to jail, I should soon be back at my old tricks in spite of the duffers at the Quai des Orfevres.
那里的人都会掏心掏肺地帮他们的将军——他们的好‘鬼上当’——扫除障碍。 Down yonder they will all turn themselves inside out to help their general—their good Trompe-la-Mort—to get clear away.
你们中有一个能像我这样说，他有上万兄弟时刻准备为他赴汤蹈火吗？”他骄傲地问。 Is there a single one among you that can say, as I can, that he has ten thousand brothers ready to do anything for him?” he asked proudly.
“这里还是有些好东西的。”他拍拍自己的心口说，“我从不背叛任何人！——看看你，你这个荡妇，”他对那老处女说，“他们都害怕我，你看见了吗？ “There is some good there,” he said tapping his heart; “I have never betrayed any one!—Look you here, you slut,” he said to the old maid, “they are all afraid of me, do you see?
但是他们看见你就恶心。 But the sight of you turns them sick.
拿你的不义之财吧。” Rake in your gains.”
他沉默了一会儿，看着四周房客们的表情。 He was silent for a moment, and looked round at the lodgers’ faces.
“你们这些笨蛋，全都是！ “What dolts you are, all of you!
你们之前从没有见过罪犯吗？ Have you never seen a convict before?
站在你们面前的科兰，他这种罪犯，不会比其他人懦弱。他抬高嗓门抵抗社会契约的巨大骗局，就像让-雅克那样，他的弟子会骄傲地表明自己的立场。 A convict of Collin’s stamp, whom you see before you, is a man less weak-kneed than others; he lifts up his voice against the colossal fraud of the Social Contract, as Jean-Jacques did, whose pupil he is proud to declare himself.
总而言之，我只身一人在这里抵抗政府，还有其全额资助的审判庭和警察机关，我是他们所有人的对手。” In short, I stand here single-handed against a Government and a whole subsidized machinery of tribunals and police, and I am a match for them all.”
“天啊！”画家喊道，“要是把他画下来，该是多壮观的一幅素描啊！” “Ye gods!” cried the painter, “what a magnificent sketch one might make of him!”
“看看这里，你们这些等着他上叫绞刑架的先生们，绞刑架下可见证了不少妇女变成寡妇（这个绰号饱含阴暗的诗意，是罪犯们为绞刑架起的）。发发善心，告诉我，是不是‘丝线’出卖了我。 “Look here, you gentlemen-in-waiting to his highness the gibbet, master of ceremonies to the widow” (a nickname full of sombre poetry, given by prisoners to the guillotine), “be a good fellow, and tell me if it really was Fil-de-Soie who sold me.
我不想让他为其他人受苦，这不公平。” I don’t want him to suffer for some one else, that would not be fair.”
但是探长还没来得及回答，随行的其他人已经搜完楼上下来了。 But before the chief had time to answer, the rest of the party returned from making their investigations upstairs.
所有东西都被打开，同时被记录在册。 Everything had been opened and inventoried.
他们和探长说了几句话，正式的备案已经完成了。 A few words passed between them and the chief, and the official preliminaries were complete.
“先生们，”科兰对房客们说，“他们马上会带我走。 “Gentlemen,” said Collin, addressing the lodgers, “they will take me away directly.
你们让我在这里住得非常愉快，我会以感激之心会回忆这段时光的。 You have all made my stay among you very agreeable, and I shall look back upon it with gratitude.
请接受我的告别，允许我从普罗旺斯给你们寄些无花果。” Receive my adieux, and permit me to send you figs from Provence.”
他向前走了一两步，然后转向欧仁，又看了他一眼。 He advanced a step or two, and then turned to look once more at Rastignac.
“再见了，欧仁，”之前，他的说话方式粗暴无情，现在却奇特地过渡到了悲伤而温和的口吻，他说道， “Good-bye, Eugene,” he said, in a sad and gentle tone, a strange transition from his previous rough and stern manner.
“要是你缺钱的话，我已经给你介绍一个忠心的朋友了。”尽管他戴着手铐，他还是做出了一个抵御的动作，像剑师一样喊道，“一，二！”，接着刺了出去。 “If you should be hard up, I have left you a devoted friend,” and, in spite of his shackles, he managed to assume a posture of defense, called, “One, two!” like a fencing-master, and lunged.
“要是出问题了，尽管利用这个资源， “If anything goes wrong, apply in that quarter.
人力、物力都任凭你使唤。” Man and money, all at your service.”
这个陌生讲话者的动作十分滑稽，所以只有拉斯蒂涅知道这个手势之下的严肃意义。 The strange speaker’s manner was sufficiently burlesque, so that no one but Rastignac knew that there was a serious meaning underlying the pantomime.
警察、士兵和侦探一离开屋子，正在给主人太阳穴擦醋的西尔维看了看四周不知所措的房客们。 As soon as the police, soldiers, and detectives had left the house, Sylvie, who was rubbing her mistress’ temples with vinegar, looked round at the bewildered lodgers.
“嗳，”她说，“尽管如此，他还是个真男人，他是的。” “Well,” said she, “he was a man, he was, for all that.”
她的话打破了魔障。 Her words broke the spell.
所有人都太激动了，他们被各种情绪感动着，都说不出话来。 Every one had been too much excited, too much moved by very various feelings to speak.
但是现在，房客们开始面面相觑，然后所有的目光都立刻落在了米绍诺小姐身上，那个瘦弱、干枯、没精打采、木乃伊般干瘪的身躯正蜷缩在炉子旁边。她的眼睛低垂着，仿佛害怕自己绿色的眼罩不能遮住那些人的面部表情。 But now the lodgers began to look at each other, and then all eyes were turned at once on Mlle. Michonneau, a thin, shriveled, dead-alive, mummy-like figure, crouching by the stove; her eyes were downcast, as if she feared that the green eye-shade could not shut out the expression of those faces from her.
这个身躯和她长久以来激起的厌恶感，顿时找到了解释。 This figure and the feeling of repulsion she had so long excited were explained all at once.
窒息的嘀咕声充满了整个屋子，大家的意见如此一致，似乎同一种厌恶情绪将所有的声音定格在了一个调子上。 A smothered murmur filled the room; it was so unanimous, that it seemed as if the same feeling of loathing had pitched all the voices in one key.
米绍诺小姐听到了这些，也没有起身。 Mlle. Michonneau heard it, and did not stir.
第一个动的是比安卡肖恩，他向旁边的人侧过身去，低声说：“要是那个人还留在这里和我们一起吃饭，我就要搬家了。” It was Bianchon who was the first to move; he bent over his neighbor, and said in a low voice, “If that creature is going to stop here, and have dinner with us, I shall clear out.”
眨眼间，屋子里除了普瓦雷以外的所有人都和这个医科学生有着相同的看法，于是医科学生在大多数人的支持下，走到长者普瓦雷跟前。 In the twinkling of an eye it was clear that every one in the room, save Poiret, was of the medical student’s opinion, so that the latter, strong in the support of the majority, went up to that elderly person.
“比起我们其他人，你和米绍诺小姐更亲密一些。”他说，“跟她说说，让她明白她必须走人，立刻走。” “You are more intimate with Mlle. Michonneau than the rest of us,” he said; “speak to her, make her understand that she must go, and go at once.”
“立刻！”普瓦雷惊诧地应声说道。 “At once!” echoed Poiret in amazement.
之后他走向那个蜷缩着的躯体，在她耳边说了几句话。 Then he went across to the crouching figure, and spoke a few words in her ear.
“这一季度我已经提前付清了帐，我和其他人一样都有权利留在这里。”她用毒蛇般的眼神看着那些房客说。 “I have paid beforehand for the quarter; I have as much right to be here as any one else,” she said, with a viperous look at the boarders.
“完全不用担心！我们会共同努力，把钱退给你的。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “Never mind that!We will club together and pay you the money back,” said Rastignac.
“先生站在科兰那边，”她以质问、邪恶的目光瞥了这个法律系学生一眼，说道，“这不难猜出原因。” “Monsieur is taking Collin’s part,” she said, with a questioning, malignant glance at the law student; “it is not difficult to guess why.”
欧仁听了这些话，便冲上前去，仿佛要跳到她身上掐她的脖子。 Eugene started forward at the words, as if he meant to spring upon her and wring her neck.
那一瞥揭露了他深藏心底的背叛，也照亮了他丑陋的内心。 That glance, and the depths of treachery that it revealed, had been a hideous enlightenment.
“别理她！”其他房客大声说。 “Let her alone!” cried the boarders.
拉斯蒂涅交叉双臂，没有说话。 Rastignac folded his arms and was silent.
“别再把这个犹大小姐留下了。”画家转向沃盖夫人说, “Let us have no more of Mlle. Judas,” said the painter, turning to Mme. Vauquer.
“要是你不赶米绍诺小姐走的话，夫人，我们都会离开你的旅馆，而且不管我们走到哪里，我们都会说，这里只有罪犯和间谍。 “If you don’t show the Michonneau the door, madame, we shall all leave your shop, and wherever we go we shall say that there are only convicts and spies left there.
要是你赶她走了，我们就会对这件事守口如瓶。说到底，这种事就是在最好的社会里也许都会发生，除非他们在将那些人送上囚船的时候，在他们额头上留下印记。 If you do the other thing, we will hold our tongues about the business; for when all is said and done, it might happen in the best society until they brand them on the forehead, when they send them to the hulks.
他们不应该让这些罪犯伪装成体面的市民在巴黎四周走动，继续做着他们原本那一套招摇撞骗的滑稽行为。” They ought not to let convicts go about Paris disguised like decent citizens, so as to carry on their antics like a set of rascally humbugs, which they are.”
听到这些，沃盖夫人神奇地恢复过来了。 At this Mme. Vauquer recovered miraculously.
她坐了起来，抱起双臂；她的眼睛现在睁得很圆，而且看不出一点流泪的迹象。 She sat up and folded her arms; her eyes were wide open now, and there was no sign of tears in them.
“什么，你真的打算毁了我这盘生意吗，我亲爱的先生？ “Why, do you really mean to be the ruin of my establishment, my dear sir?
那边是善良的沃尔特兰先生——天呐。”她哭喊道，又插了一句，“我不禁叫起了他的这个名字，他用这个名字将自己伪装成了一个诚实的人！ There is M. Vautrin—Goodness,” she cried, interrupting herself, “I can’t help calling him by the name he passed himself off by for an honest man!
已经有一间房子空出来了，你还想让我在季度中途赶走两个房客，这时候没人会搬进来——”“先生们，我们戴上帽子，去索邦广场的弗利科托餐厅吃饭吧。”比安卡肖恩喊道。 There is one room to let already, and you want me to turn out two more lodgers in the middle of the season, when no one is moving—”“Gentlemen, let us take our hats and go and dine at Flicoteaux’s in the Place Sorbonne,” cried Bianchon.
沃盖夫人扫视四周，马上有了新主意。 Mme. Vauquer glanced round, and saw in a moment on which side her interest lay.
她向米绍诺小姐蹒跚走去。 She waddled across to Mlle. Michonneau.
“过来，现在，”她说，“您不会毁了我的生意，是吗，嗯？ “Come, now,” she said; “you would not be the ruin of my establishment, would you, eh?
您有着珍贵而善良的灵魂。 There’s a dear, kind soul.
您看看这些先生们都把我逼到什么地步了，今晚就先上楼回房吧。” You see what a pass these gentlemen have brought me to; just go up to your room for this evening.”
“不可能！”房客们喊道， “Never a bit of it!” cried the boarders.
“她必须走，现在就走！” “She must go, and go this minute!”
“但是这位可怜的女士还没有吃晚餐呢。”普瓦雷哀怨地乞求道。 “But the poor lady has had no dinner,” said Poiret, with piteous entreaty.
“她爱去哪里吃就去哪里吃。”几个声音喊道， “She can go and dine where she likes,” shouted several voices.
“把她赶出去，这个间谍！” “Turn her out, the spy!”
“把他们俩都赶出去！ “Turn them both out!
一对间谍！” Spies!”
“先生们，”普瓦雷哭诉着，他心中溢满了勇气——爱将勇气给予这个绵羊般的男人，“请尊重女性。” “Gentlemen,” cried Poiret, his heart swelling with the courage that love gives to the ovine male, “respect the weaker sex.”
“间谍不分性别！”画家说。 “Spies are of no sex!” said the painter.
“一个珍贵的性别拉玛！” “A precious sexorama!”
“把她扔到大街拉玛上！” “Turn her into the streetorama!”
“先生们，这样做不礼貌！ “Gentlemen, this is not manners!
要是你们要赶人出门，也不能随随便便、不事先告知吧。 If you turn people out of the house, it ought not to be done so unceremoniously and with no notice at all.
我们付了钱，我们不会走。”普瓦雷说道。他戴上帽子，坐在了米绍诺小姐身边，而沃盖夫人正在劝这位小姐。 We have paid our money, and we are not going,” said Poiret, putting on his cap, and taking a chair beside Mlle. Michonneau, with whom Mme. Vauquer was remonstrating.
“淘气的孩子！”画家一脸滑稽地说，“快走开，淘气的小家伙！” “Naughty boy!” said the painter, with a comical look; “run away, naughty little boy!”
“你看，”比安卡肖恩说，“要是你们不走，我们其他人就会走。”于是房客们纷纷向客厅门口走去。 “Look here,” said Bianchon; “if you do not go, all the rest of us will,” and the boarders, to a man, made for the sitting-room-door.
“哦！小姐，该怎么办？”沃盖夫人叫了起来， “Oh! mademoiselle, what is to be done?” cried Mme. Vauquer.
“我是个没用的女人。 “I am a ruined woman.
您不能留在这里了，他们会越走越远，还会动起手来呢。” You can’t stay here; they will go further, do something violent.”
米绍诺小姐站了起来。 Mlle. Michonneau rose to her feet.
“她要走了！——她不会走！——她要走了！——不，她不会走。” “She is going!—She is not going!—She is going!—No, she isn’t.”
反抗者们的举动表明了他们的敌意，加上此起彼伏的惊叹，这一切迫使米绍诺小姐离开了。 These alternate exclamations, and a suggestion of hostile intentions, borne out by the behavior of the insurgents, compelled Mlle. Michonneau to take her departure.
她低声在自己女房东的耳边做了一些约定，然后说道：“我会去比诺夫人那里。”她面带威胁地说道。 She made some stipulations, speaking in a low voice in her hostess’ ear, and then—“I shall go to Mme. Buneaud’s,” she said, with a threatening look.
“您想去哪里就去哪里，小姐。”沃盖夫人说，她将选择自己生意上的对手看成是粗暴的侮辱。 “Go where you please, mademoiselle,” said Mme. Vauquer, who regarded this choice of an opposition establishment as an atrocious insult.
“去和比诺住去吧，那里的酒会让猫腹绞痛，食物劣质又不干净。” “Go and lodge with the Buneaud; the wine would give a cat the colic, and the food is cheap and nasty.”
房客们站在两边，让她走出去，没有说一句话。 The boarders stood aside in two rows to let her pass; not a word was spoken.
普瓦雷留恋地在后面看着米绍诺小姐，这无疑反映了他对去留问题还在犹豫。那些因为米绍诺小姐的离开而满心欢喜的房客们看着他大笑起来。 Poiret looked so wistfully after Mlle. Michonneau, and so artlessly revealed that he was in two minds whether to go or stay, that the boarders, in their joy at being quit of Mlle. Michonneau, burst out laughing at the sight of him.
“嘘！——嘘！——嘘！ “Hist!—st!—st!
普瓦雷。”画家喊道， Poiret,” shouted the painter.
“你好！ “Hallo!
我说，普瓦雷，你好！” I say, Poiret, hallo!”
博物馆员工则开始唱道：“动身去叙利亚，年轻美丽的迪努瓦……”“你走吧，你肯定十分渴望离开，‘嗜好所在，锲而不舍’！”比安卡肖恩说。 The @employee@ from the Museum began to sing:“Partant pour la Syrie, Le jeune et beau Dunois...”“Get along with you; you must be dying to go, @trahit sua quemque voluptas!@” said Bianchon.
“维吉尔的名句，意译下就是，每个人都朝着他自己的品味靠近。”助教说道。 “Every one to his taste—free rendering from Virgil,” said the tutor.
米绍诺小姐动了一下，好像是要抓普瓦雷的手臂，那种恳求的目光让他无法抗拒。 Mlle. Michonneau made a movement as if to take Poiret’s arm, with an appealing glance that he could not resist.
