老处女靠着他，他们俩一起走了出去，之后传出了一阵鼓掌声和隆隆的笑声。 The two went out together, the old maid leaning upon him, and there was a burst of applause, followed by peals of laughter.
“好样的，普瓦雷！” “Bravo, Poiret!”
“谁能想到老普瓦雷会这样做呢！” “Who would have thought it of old Poiret!”
“太阳神普瓦雷！” “Apollo Poiret!”
“战神普瓦雷！” “Mars Poiret!”
“无畏的普瓦雷！” “Intrepid Poiret!”
就在那时，一个信使给沃盖夫人带来一封信，她读完之后，瘫倒在椅子里。 A messenger came in at that moment with a letter for Mme. Vauquer, who read it through, and collapsed in her chair.
“要是还有这样的晴天霹雳，”她哭着说，“这房子最好立马烧为平地算了！”！ “The house might as well be burned down at once,” cried she, “if there are to be any more of these thunderbolts!
今天下午三点，小塔耶费去世了。 Young Taillefer died at three o’clock this afternoon.
上天对我很公正，因为我只想这些女士们好，却牺牲了那个可怜的人。 It serves me right for wishing well to those ladies at that poor man’s expense.
库蒂尔夫人和维多琳小姐希望我把她们的东西送过去，因为她们会和维多琳的父亲一起住。 Mme. Couture and Victorine want me to send their things, because they are going to live with her father.
塔耶费先生允许他的女儿把库蒂尔夫人留在那里，当女伴陪着她。 M. Taillefer allows his daughter to keep old Mme. Couture as her lady companion.
空出来四个房间了！五个房客都走了！……她坐了起来，好像要嚎啕大哭起来。 Four rooms to let! and five lodgers gone!...She sat up, and seemed about to burst into tears.
“我想霉运降临在这个旅馆了。”她哭着说。 “Bad luck has come to lodge here, I think,” she cried.
从街上又一次传来车轮声。 Once more there came a sound of wheels from the street outside.
“什么！又有人发横财了！”西尔维评论道。 “What! another windfall for somebody!” was Sylvie’s comment.
但是进来的是高老头，他看起来容光焕发、兴高采烈，仿佛又回到了年轻时代。 But it was Goriot who came in, looking so radiant, so flushed with happiness, that he seemed to have grown young again.
“高老头坐马车了！”房客们喊道，“世界末日要到了。” “Goriot in a cab!” cried the boarders; “the world is coming to an end.”
这个有着高尚灵魂的人径直走向欧仁。欧仁则站在角落，沉浸于思考之中。他将一只手放在这个年轻人的手臂上。 The good soul made straight for Eugene, who was standing wrapped in thought in a corner, and laid a hand on the young man’s arm.
“过来。”他说道，眼睛里充满了快乐。 “Come,” he said, with gladness in his eyes.
“那么你还没听说这个消息吧？”欧仁说， “Then you haven’t heard the news?” said Eugene.
“沃尔特兰是个在逃犯，他们刚才将他逮捕了，还有小塔耶费去世了。” “Vautrin was an escaped convict; they have just arrested him; and young Taillefer is dead.”
“很好，但是这和我们有什么关系呢？”高老头回答说， “Very well, but what business is it of ours?” replied Father Goriot.
“我将在你的房间里和我的女儿共进晚餐，你明白吗？ “I am going to dine with my daughter in @your house@, do you understand?
她在等着你呢。 She is expecting you.
快来！” Come!”
他使劲拉着拉斯蒂涅，他们就像私奔的情人那样匆匆忙忙地走了。 He carried off Rastignac with him by main force, and they departed in as great a hurry as a pair of eloping lovers.
“现在，我们吃晚饭吧。”画家叫道，然后所有人都拉过椅子坐到桌前。 “Now, let us have dinner,” cried the painter, and every one drew his chair to the table.
“啊，我从不，”魁梧的西尔维说， “Well, I never,” said the portly Sylvie.
“今天什么事都不对劲！ “Nothing goes right to-day!
我的扁豆炖羊肉烧焦了！ The haricot mutton has caught!
呸！你们必须得把它吃了，虽然烧焦了，不吃的话，就更可惜了！” Bah! you will have to eat it, burned as it is, more’s the pity!”
沃盖夫人完全泄了气，她说不出一句话来。她环顾着桌子周围，看着原本应该有十八个人的桌子上只坐了十个人，但是每个人都想方设法安慰她、鼓励她。 Mme. Vauquer was so dispirited that she could not say a word as she looked round the table and saw only ten people where eighteen should be; but every one tried to comfort and cheer her.
起先，在这随租附带的晚餐上，大家像往常一样谈论着沃尔特兰和当天发生的事；但是谈话总会落在有趣的话题上，如决斗、监牢、司法、监狱生活和法律应当做出的变动。 At first the dinner contingent, as was natural, talked about Vautrin and the day’s events; but the conversation wound round to such topics of interest as duels, jails, justice, prison life, and alterations that ought to be made in the laws.
他们很快就把话题从雅克·科兰、维多琳和她哥哥扯到了很远。 They soon wandered miles away from Jacques Collin and Victorine and her brother.
那里可能只坐了十个人，但是他们的声音却有二十个人那么响。的确，人似乎比平常多，这就是昨天和今天的唯一差别。 There might be only ten of them, but they made noise enough for twenty; indeed, there seemed to be more of them than usual; that was the only difference between yesterday and to-day.
对他人的命运漠不关心，在这个自私的世界是一件理所应当的事。他们在悲剧发生的第二日，就在巴黎发生的各个事件中找寻新的新闻，以满足他们每日更新的欲望，这种漠不关心的态度很快就占了上风。 Indifference to the fate of others is a matter of course in this selfish world, which, on the morrow of tragedy, seeks among the events of Paris for a fresh sensation for its daily renewed appetite, and this indifference soon gained the upper hand.
沃盖夫人自己在希望的抚慰之下平静下来，而传达希望的人正是壮实的西尔维。 Mme. Vauquer herself grew calmer under the soothing influence of hope, and the mouthpiece of hope was the portly Sylvie.
那一日对于欧仁来说就像做梦一般，这种不真实的感觉一直延续到了晚上。即便他有着充沛的精力和清醒的头脑，但挨着高老头坐在马车里，他的脑子还是一片混乱。 That day had gone by like a dream for Eugene, and the sense of unreality lasted into the evening; so that, in spite of his energetic character and clear-headedness, his ideas were a chaos as he sat beside Goriot in the cab.
这个老人的声音中满含非同寻常的欢愉，但是欧仁在被诸多情感震撼之后，他耳朵里听到的声音就好像梦中的声音一样。 The old man’s voice was full of unwonted happiness, but Eugene had been shaken by so many emotions that the words sounded in his ears like words spoken in a dream.
“今天早上那幢房子大功告成啦！ “It was finished this morning!
我们三个会一起在那里吃晚餐，一起！ All three of us are going to dine there together, together!
你明白吗？ Do you understand?
这四年来，我还没有和德尔菲娜一起吃过饭呢，我的小德尔菲娜，我会和她呆一整个晚上！ I have not dined with my Delphine, my little Delphine, these four years, and I shall have her for a whole evening!
从早上开始，我们就一直在你的房子里。 We have been at your lodging the whole time since morning.
我穿着衬衫，挽着袖子，像个搬运工一样，一直在帮忙搬家具。 I have been working like a porter in my shirt sleeves, helping to carry in the furniture.
啊哈！你不知道她有多美，她会坐在桌边看着我，‘这里，爸爸，试一下这个，很好吃。’但是我不能吃。 Aha! you don’t know what pretty ways she has; at table she will look after me, ‘Here, papa, just try this, it is nice.’And I shall not be able to eat.
哦，我已经很久没有和她一起像我们这样安安静静地过日子了。” Oh, it is a long while since I have been with her in quiet every-day life as we shall have her.”
“这个世界真的好像翻转过来了一样。” “It really seems as if the world has been turned upside down.”
“翻转过来？”高老头重复道， “Upside down?” repeated Father Goriot.
“哎呀，这个世界从来就没有这样正确过。 “Why, the world has never been so right-side up.
在街上，我只看见微笑的脸庞，人们真诚的握手，彼此地拥抱。人们看上去都很高兴，似乎他们要去和女儿吃饭呢。他们吃下的精美晚餐，还是她和我去英国咖啡馆叫主厨做的呢。 I see none but smiling faces in the streets, people who shake hands cordially and embrace each other, people who all look as happy as if they were going to dine with their daughter, and gobble down a nice little dinner that she went with me to order of the chef at the Cafe des Anglais.
但是，哼！有她在你身边，胆汁和苦艾都会变得跟蜂蜜一样甜。” But, pshaw! with her beside you gall and wormwood would be as sweet as honey.”
“我感觉我好像又活过来了。”欧仁说。 “I feel as if I were coming back to life again,” said Eugene.
“什么，快一点！”高老头推下前面的玻璃窗喊道。 “Why, hurry up there!” cried Father Goriot, letting down the window in front.
“走快一点，要是你十分钟之内到达我指定的地方，我给你五法郎。” “Get on faster; I will give you five francs if you get to the place I told you of in ten minutes time.”
听到这样的诱惑，马车夫便以不可思议的速度穿过巴黎街头。 With this prospect before him the cabman crossed Paris with miraculous celerity.
“这家伙跟爬似的！”高老头说。 “How that fellow crawls!” said Father Goriot.
“可是你要带我去哪里呢？” “But where are you taking me?”
欧仁问他。 Eugene asked him.
“去你的房子啊。”高老头说。 “To your own house,” said Goriot.
马车在阿图瓦街停了下来。 The cab stopped in the Rue d’Artois.
高老头先下了马车，带着鳏夫回归单身汉生活的鲁莽劲，给那人扔下十法郎。 Father Goriot stepped out first and flung ten francs to the man with the recklessness of a widower returning to bachelor ways.
“上楼去。”他对拉斯蒂涅说。 “Come along upstairs,” he said to Rastignac.
他们穿过庭院，爬上四楼一间崭新、漂亮的房子。 They crossed a courtyard, and climbed up to the third floor of a new and handsome house.
他们在一扇门前停下，但是在高老头按下门铃之前，德纽沁根夫人的女仆泰蕾兹开了门。 There they stopped before a door; but before Goriot could ring, it was opened by Therese, Mme. de Nucingen’s maid.
欧仁发现自己身处一间迷人的套房之中。套房包括一个前厅，一个小客厅，一间卧室，一间书房，从窗外望去是个花园。 Eugene found himself in a charming set of chambers; an ante-room, a little drawing-room, a bedroom, and a study, looking out upon a garden.
小客厅里的家具和装饰都十分雅致、迷人，柔和的光线洒满房间。德尔菲娜则从壁炉旁的一张矮椅上站起身来，走到欧仁面前。 The furniture and the decorations of the little drawing-room were of the most daintily charming description, the room was full of soft light, and Delphine rose up from a low chair by the fire and stood before him.
她将壁炉架的火炉栏放下来，然后便说起话来，她的每一个音节都亲切、柔和。 She set her fire-screen down on the chimney-piece, and spoke with tenderness in every tone of her voice.
“我们必须去找您，先生，您反应太迟钝了！” “So we had to go in search of you, sir, you who are so slow to understand!”
泰蕾兹离开了房间。 Therese left the room.
这个学生将德尔菲娜揽入怀中，紧紧地抱住了她，他的眼里充满了喜悦的泪水。 The student took Delphine in his arms and held her in a tight clasp, his eyes filled with tears of joy.
他现在所处的环境和他之前所目睹的一幕幕场景形成了强烈的对比。对于神经一直紧绷的拉斯蒂涅来说，他实在是承受不住了。在一整天的紧张和刺激过后，他已经身心俱疲，快要被这一切击垮了。 This last contrast between his present surroundings and the scenes he had just witnessed was too much for Rastignac’s over-wrought nerves, after the day’s strain and excitement that had wearied heart and brain; he was almost overcome by it.
“我敢肯定他喜欢你。”高老头低声说。这时欧仁迷惑地倒在沙发上，完全说不出话来，也不知道魔术棒是如何或为何一挥，就完成了这个最终的场景转变。 “I felt sure myself that he loved you,” murmured Father Goriot, while Eugene lay back bewildered on the sofa, utterly unable to speak a word or to reason out how and why the magic wand had been waved to bring about this final transformation scene.
“但是你必须来看看你的房子。”德纽沁根夫人说。 “But you must see your rooms,” said Mme. de Nucingen.
她抓起他的手，把她带进一间屋子，屋里的摆设和地毯都和她自己房子里的一样。事实上，精细到最微小的细节都一模一样，这就是德尔菲娜的房间，只不过小了一些。 She took his hand and led him into a room carpeted and furnished like her own; indeed, down to the smallest details, it was a reproduction in miniature of Delphine’s apartment.
“这里没有床。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “There is no bed,” said Rastignac.
“是的，先生。”她红着脸，捏紧他的手，回答说。 “No, monsieur,” she answered, reddening, and pressing his hand.
欧仁看着她，尽管他还年轻，也明白了恋爱中的女人如何将羞怯之心深藏于自己的心中。 Eugene, looking at her, understood, young though he yet was, how deeply modesty is implanted in the heart of a woman who loves.
“你是我们只能永远爱慕的那一种人。”他在她耳边说， “You are one of those beings whom we cannot choose but to adore for ever,” he said in her ear.
“是的，爱情越深刻、越真切，就应该越神秘、隐藏越深。我敢这样说，是因为我们太了解彼此了。 “Yes, the deeper and truer love is, the more mysterious and closely veiled it should be; I can dare to say so, since we understand each other so well.
没人会知道我们的秘密。” No one shall learn our secret.”
“哦！我想我是个外人了。”父亲抱怨说。 “Oh! so I am nobody, I suppose,” growled the father.
“你非常了解‘我们’就意味着你。” “You know quite well that ‘we’ means you.”
“啊！这正是我想要的。 “Ah! that is what I wanted.
你不介意我，是不是？ You will not mind me, will you?
我会像一个善良的精灵一样走来走去，即使不被看见，也会让他人在任何地方都能能感受到我的存在，不是吗？ I shall go and come like a good fairy who makes himself felt everywhere without being seen, shall I not?
嗯，德尔菲内特、尼内特、德德尔——这不是我的好主意吗，是我跟你说‘阿图瓦街上有几间漂亮的房子出租，我们来为他布置这些屋子？’她还不愿意听呢！ Eh, Delphinette, Ninette, Dedel—was it not a good idea of mine to say to you, ‘There are some nice rooms to let in the Rue d’Artois; let us furnish them for him?’And she would not hear of it!
啊！你们的幸福全都是我的功劳。 Ah! your happiness has been all my doing.
我是你们幸福与存在的作者。 I am the author of your happiness and of your existence.
要是他们能幸福，父亲定然总是在付出，总是在付出——要不然他们就不是父亲了。” Fathers must always be giving if they would be happy themselves; always giving—they would not be fathers else.”
“这就是事情的始末吗？”欧仁问道。 “Was that how it happened?” asked Eugene.
“是的。她还不愿意听我的呢。她害怕人们说闲话，就好像他们要说你的那些废话能跟幸福相比较似的！ “Yes.She would not listen to me.She was afraid that people would talk, as if the rubbish that they say about you were to be compared with happiness!
唉，所有的女人都梦想做自己已经做过的事情——”高老头发现没人在听他说话，因为德纽沁根夫人已经带着拉斯蒂涅进了书房。他听到了亲吻的声音，即便那声音很小。 Why, all women dream of doing what she has done—” Father Goriot found himself without an audience, for Mme. de Nucingen had led Rastignac into the study; he heard a kiss given and taken, low though the sound was.
书房和其他房子一样，布置得很优雅，什么都不缺。 The study was furnished as elegantly as the other rooms, and nothing was wanting there.
“我们有没有猜中你的心意？”当他们回到客厅吃饭的时候，她问道。 “Have we guessed your wishes rightly?” she asked, as they returned to the drawing-room for dinner.
“是的，”他说，“有过之而无不及，啊！ “Yes,” he said, “only too well, alas!
这幢房子充分展示了奢华，让我的美梦成真。这里的高贵满足了一个年轻人所有浪漫的憧憬，深深地吸引着我，我只感觉到这是我应得的东西，但是我不能从你那里接受这些，我还太穷，不能——”“啊！啊！你这就对我说不了。”她的语气中带着调皮的蛮横，还迷人地微微撅起了嘴，这是女人说说笑笑、消除疑虑的方法。 For all this luxury so well carried out, this realization of pleasant dreams, the elegance that satisfies all the romantic fancies of youth, appeals to me so strongly that I cannot but feel that it is my rightful possession, but I cannot accept it from you, and I am too poor as yet to—”“Ah! ah! you say me nay already,” she said with arch imperiousness, and a charming little pout of the lips, a woman’s way of laughing away scruples.
但是欧仁在不久之前就曾严肃地自我反省过，沃尔特兰的被捕直白地向他展示了他脚前的这个陷阱有多深。慷慨和自尊的本能在他心中加固，他不允许自己因诱惑而放弃自己高尚的决定。 But Eugene had submitted so lately to that solemn self-questioning, and Vautrin’s arrest had so plainly shown him the depths of the pit that lay ready to his feet, that the instincts of generosity and honor had been strengthened in him, and he could not allow himself to be coaxed into abandoning his high-minded determinations.
他的心里充满了深深的忧郁。 Profound melancholy filled his mind.
“你真的要拒绝吗？”德纽沁根夫人说， “Do you really mean to refuse?” said Mme. de Nucingen.
“你知道这样的拒绝意味着什么吗？ “And do you know what such a refusal means?
意味着你不相信你自己，你不敢和我有联系。 That you are not sure of yourself, that you do not dare to bind yourself to me.
你真的害怕背叛我的感情吗？ Are you really afraid of betraying my affection?
要是你爱我，要是我——爱你，为什么你要在这么微不足道的责任面前退缩呢？ If you love me, if I—love you, why should you shrink back from such a slight obligation?
你只要了解我布置这间单身套房时的喜悦心情，就再也不会犹豫了，那时你就会请求我原谅你的犹豫不决了。 If you but knew what a pleasure it has been to see after all the arrangements of this bachelor establishment, you would not hesitate any longer, you would ask me to forgive you for your hesitation.
我拿着一些属于你的钱，我好好利用了这些钱，就是这么回事。 I had some money that belonged to you, and I have made good use of it, that is all.
你以为做这些是因为你胸襟宽阔，那你就大错特错了。 You mean this for magnanimity, but it is very little of you.
你所要求的远不止这些……啊！”当欧仁饱含激情的目光落在她身上时，她大声说道，“而且你把一点小事弄得非常复杂。 You are asking me for far more than this…Ah!” she cried, as Eugene’s passionate glance was turned on her, “and you are making difficulties about the merest trifles.
哦，要是你无论怎样都对我没有一点爱意的话，就拒绝吧，一定要拒绝。 Oh, if you feel no love whatever for me, refuse, by all means.
我的命运就拴在你的一句话上。 My fate hangs on a word from you.
说呀！——父亲，”她停了一下，说道，“跟他讲讲道理。 Speak!—Father,” she said after a pause, “make him listen to reason.
我和他一样重视名誉，他难道想象不到吗？” Can he imagine that I am less nice than he is on the point of honor?”
高老头脸上带着平静的笑容，他看着、听着这有意思的争吵，好像他已经为生命中所有的悲伤找到了慰藉一样。 Father Goriot was looking on and listening to this pretty quarrel with a placid smile, as if he had found some balm for all the sorrows of life.
“你多孩子气啊！”她抓住了欧仁的手，又哭了起来， “Child that you are!” she cried again, catching Eugene’s hand.
“你的生命才刚刚开始。一开始，你会遇到很多人认为难以克服的障碍。一个女人用手开启了这条道路，但你却退缩了！ “You are just beginning life; you find barriers at the outset that many a man finds insurmountable; a woman’s hand opens the way and you shrink back!
啊，你必定会成功的！ Why, you are sure to succeed!
你的前途会一片光明。 You will have a brilliant future.
成功就写在你宽阔的额头上，你还怕还不起我今天借给你的债吗？ Success is written on that broad forehead of yours, and will you not be able to repay me my loan of today?
旧时候的妇女不是都会为她的骑士戴好佩剑和头盔，穿好甲胄，找一匹战马，让他骑马比武，为她而战吗？ Did not a lady in olden times arm her knight with sword and helmet and coat of mail, and find him a charger, so that he might fight for her in the tournament?
嗯，欧仁，我提供给你的这些东西就是现代的武器。无论谁想干出点成绩，他都需要这样的工具。 Well, then, Eugene, these things that I offer you are the weapons of this age; every one who means to be something must have such tools as these.
要是你住的顶楼与爸爸的房间差不多的话，那么也一定是间漂亮的房子了。 A pretty place your garret must be if it is like papa’s room!
看，晚饭早就好了。 See, dinner is waiting all this time.
你想让我不高兴吗？——你为什么不回答？”她摇着他的脑袋说。 Do you want to make me unhappy?—Why don’t you answer?” she said, shaking his hand.
“天哪！爸爸，快让他下决心，否则我就走人，再也不会见他了。” “@Mon Dieu!@ papa, make up his mind for him, or I will go away and never see him any more.”
“我要帮你下定决心。”高老头缓过神来，说道， “I will make up your mind,” said Goriot, coming down from the clouds.
“现在，我亲爱的欧仁先生，下一步就是从犹太人那里借钱了，是不是？” “Now, my dear M. Eugene, the next thing is to borrow money of the Jews, isn’t it?”
“这肯定于事无补。”欧仁说。 “There is positively no help for it,” said Eugene.
“那好，我来借钱给你。”另一个说道，他拿出一个便宜的皮夹，比他穿得还要破烂。 “All right, I will give you credit,” said the other, drawing out a cheap leather pocket-book, much the worse for wear.
“我自己已经变成犹太人了，我付了所有的帐单，这是发票。 “I have turned Jew myself; I paid for everything; here are the invoices.
你一分钱也不欠了，这里所有东西的账单都付清了。 You do not owe a penny for anything here.
这笔钱的数目也不算大——最多五千法郎，我会借给你这笔钱。 It did not come to very much—five thousand francs at most, and I am going to lend you the money myself.
我不是女人——你可以拒绝我。 I am not a woman—you can refuse me.
你应该在一张小纸上写个收据，随时都可以还给我。” You shall give me a receipt on a scrap of paper, and you can return it some time or other.”
德尔菲娜和欧仁惊讶地看着对方，眼里涌出了泪水。 Delphine and Eugene looked at each other in amazement, tears sprang to their eyes.
拉斯蒂涅伸出了他的手，激动地抓住了高老头的手。 Rastignac held out his hand and grasped Goriot’s warmly.
“哎呀，这是干什么？ “Well, what is all this about?
你们不是我的孩子吗？” Are you not my children?”
“哦！我可怜的父亲，”德纽沁根夫人说，“你是怎么做到的呢？” “Oh! my poor father,” said Mme. de Nucingen, “how did you do it?”
“啊！现在是你问我了。 “Ah! now you ask me.
当我决定要把他安排得离你近一点时，当我看到你买东西的样子就好像在选结婚礼物时，我对自己说，‘她绝对付不起这些钱。’律师说，在你丈夫被迫吐出你的财产之前，法律程序会持续六个月之久。 When I made up my mind to move him nearer to you, and saw you buying things as if they were wedding presents, I said to myself, ‘She will never be able to pay for them.’The attorney says that those law proceedings will last quite six months before your husband can be made to disgorge your fortune.
好倒是好。 Well and good.
我卖掉了每年支付我一千三百五十里弗赫的基金财产，然后花一万五千法郎买了一个稳定性好的年金，那样我每年有一千二百法郎。 I sold out my property in the funds that brought in thirteen hundred and fifty livres a year, and bought a safe annuity of twelve hundred francs a year for fifteen thousand francs.
之后用余下的钱付了你们的账。 Then I paid your tradesmen out of the rest of the capital.
至于我呢，孩子们，我在楼上有一间屋子，每年五十克朗。我每天用两个法郎就可以过上王公般的生活，我还能剩下一些钱呢。 As for me, children, I have a room upstairs for which I pay fifty crowns a year; I can live like a prince on two francs a day, and still have something left over.
我用不着在衣服上花什么钱，因为我的衣服从没穿坏过。 I shall not have to spend anything much on clothes, for I never wear anything out.
过去的半个月里，我一直都在偷笑，并暗自想着，‘他们会多么快乐啊！’而且——那么，现在，你们不快乐吗？” This fortnight past I have been laughing in my sleeve, thinking to myself, ‘How happy they are going to be!’ and—well, now, are you not happy?”
“哦！爸爸！爸爸！”德纽沁根夫人哭着冲向她的父亲，之后他父亲将她抱在膝上。 “Oh papa! papa!” cried Mme. de Nucingen, springing to her father, who took her on his knee.
她在他的脸上亲吻着，她金色的头发扫过他的脸颊，她的眼泪滴在他满是皱纹的脸上，那张皱巴巴的脸变得如此容光焕发。 She covered him with kisses, her fair hair brushed his cheek, her tears fell on the withered face that had grown so bright and radiant.
“亲爱的父亲，您是多好的一位父亲啊！ “Dear father, what a father you are!
不，普天之下没有一个父亲能像您这样。 No, there is not another father like you under the sun.
要是欧仁之前就爱您，他现在对您会是什么感觉啊？” If Eugene loved you before, what must he feel for you now?”
“哦，孩子们，哦，德尔菲内特！”高老头叫道，他已经十年没有感受过女儿的心贴着他的胸膛跳动了，“你想让我快乐而死吗？ “Why, children, why Delphinette!” cried Goriot, who had not felt his daughter’s heart beat against his breast for ten years, “do you want me to die of joy?
我脆弱的心脏要破碎了！ My poor heart will break!
过来，欧仁先生，我们两清了。” Come, Monsieur Eugene, we are quits already.”
老人紧紧将她抱在胸口，他的拥抱如此炽热而充满激情，她不禁叫了出来。 And the old man strained her to his breast with such fierce and passionate force that she cried out.
“哦！您把我弄疼了！”她说。 “Oh! you are hurting me!” she said.
“我把你弄疼了！” “I am hurting you!”
听到这些话，他脸色变得苍白。 He grew pale at the words.
他脸上的痛苦表情，似乎已经超过了人类认知的范围。 The pain expressed in his face seemed greater than it is given to humanity to know.
这位父权基督的痛苦只可与那些大画家的杰作相比，他们留给我们的那些作品，记录了他们眼中人类救世主为整个世界所承受的巨大苦痛。 The agony of this Christ of paternity can only be compared with the masterpieces of those princes of the palette who have left for us the record of their visions of an agony suffered for a whole world by the Savior of men.
高老头轻轻地亲吻了她的腰部——他的手指刚才曾过于粗暴地抓住了她的腰部。 Father Goriot pressed his lips very gently against the waist that his fingers had grasped too roughly.
“哦，不，不。”他大声说道， “Oh! no, no,” he cried.
“我没有弄疼你，不是吗？” “I have not hurt you, have I?”
他的笑容似乎在重复这个问题。 And his smile seemed to repeat the question.
“你刚才的大喊声伤害到我了——这些东西花的可不止那些钱呢。”他在她的耳边说着，又温柔地亲了她一下，“但是这件事我得瞒着他，否则他会生气。” “YOU have hurt me with that cry just now.—The things cost rather more than that,” he said in her ear, with another gentle kiss, “but I had to deceive him about it, or he would have been angry.”
欧仁在无穷无尽的爱意面前，坐在那里惊讶得说不出话来。他盯着高老头，脸上露出了纯朴的羡慕之情，而这种羡慕造就了一个年轻人的信仰。 Eugene sat dumb with amazement in the presence of this inexhaustible love; he gazed at Goriot, and his face betrayed the artless admiration which shapes the beliefs of youth.
“我会配得上这所有的一切。”他喊道。 “I will be worthy of all this,” he cried.
“哦！我的欧仁，这是多么高贵啊。”德纽沁根夫人亲吻了这个法律系学生的额头。 “Oh! my Eugene, that is nobly said,” and Mme. de Nucingen kissed the law student on the forehead.
“他为你放弃了塔耶费小姐和她的百万财产。”高老头说， “He gave up Mlle. Taillefer and her millions for you,” said Father Goriot.
“是的，那个小家伙爱上你了，现如今她哥哥死了，她就是个大财主了。” “Yes, the little thing was in love with you, and now that her brother is dead she is as rich as Croesus.”
“哦！你干嘛告诉她？”拉斯蒂涅叫道。 “Oh! why did you tell her?” cried Rastignac.
“欧仁，”德尔菲娜在他耳边说，“今晚我只有一件憾事。 “Eugene,” Delphine said in his ear, “I have one regret now this evening.
啊！我会多么爱你！直到永远！” Ah! how I will love you! and for ever!”
“这是自你们姐妹俩结婚以来我最快乐的一天了！”高老头哭着说， “This is the happiest day I have had since you two were married!” cried Goriot.
“上帝能够让我承受任何痛苦，只要这些痛苦不是你给我的。我还可以说，‘在二月这短短的一个月里，我得到了其他人一辈子也无法得到的这么多幸福。’看着我，菲芬！”他对他的女儿说， “God may send me any suffering, so long as I do not suffer through you, and I can still say, ‘In this short month of February I had more happiness than other men have in their whole lives.’—Look at me, Fifine!” he said to his daughter.
“她非常美丽，不是吗？ “She is very beautiful, is she not?
现在，告诉我，你见过很多女人肤色如此美丽、柔和吗——还有她小小的酒窝？ Tell me, now, have you seen many women with that pretty soft color—that little dimple of hers?
不，我想没有。 No, I thought not.
嗯，但是对于我来说，我从来没有见过这么美丽的女人。 Ah, well, and but for me this lovely woman would never have been.
而且很快，幸福——你给的幸福——将使她美丽一千倍。 And very soon happiness will make her a thousand times lovelier, happiness through you.
邻居，要是需要的话，我可以为你放弃我在天堂的位置，去下地狱。 I could give up my place in heaven to you, neighbor, if needs be, and go down to hell instead.
来吧，我们一起吃饭吧。”他几乎没意识到自己在说什么，又补充道，“这一切都是我们的。” Come, let us have dinner,” he added, scarcely knowing what he said, “everything is ours.”
“可怜又可爱的父亲！” “Poor dear father!”
他站起来走向她，用手捧起她的脸，在她的辫子上亲了一下。 He rose and went over to her, and took her face in his hands, and set a kiss on the plaits of hair.
“你知道吗，小家伙，你能让我多么高兴啊——你付出一点点我就能很高兴了！ “If you only knew, little one, how happy you can make me—how little it takes to make me happy!
你会时不时来看我一下吗？ Will you come and see me sometimes?
我会住在上面，就一步路的事。 I shall be just above, so it is only a step.
答应我，说你会来！” Promise me, say that you will!”
“是的，亲爱的父亲。” “Yes, dear father.”
“再说一次。” “Say it again.”
“说的，我会来，我善良的父亲。” “Yes, I will, my kind father.”
“嘘！嘘！如果由着我的性子，我就会让你说上一百遍。 “Hush! hush! I should make you say it a hundred times over if I followed my own wishes.
我们吃饭吧。” Let us have dinner.”
那晚，三个人都表现得像孩子一样。高老头的狂热情绪和那两个人相比绝对是有过之而无不及。 The three behaved like children that evening, and Father Goriot’s spirits were certainly not the least wild.
他躺在他女儿的脚边，亲吻她的双脚，盯着她的双眼，用头蹭着她的裙子。总而言之，没有一个年轻的情人能比他更放纵、更温柔了。 He lay at his daughter’s feet, kissed them, gazed into her eyes, rubbed his head against her dress; in short, no young lover could have been more extravagant or more tender.
“你看！”德尔菲娜看了一眼欧仁说，“要是我的父亲和我们在一起，他就独占了我。 “You see!” Delphine said with a look at Eugene, “so long as my father is with us, he monopolizes me.
他早晚会变得碍手碍脚。” He will be rather in the way sometimes.”
欧仁自己也已经感觉到某些由嫉妒引起的绞痛，顾不上责备这番言论带有一丝忘恩负义了。 Eugene had himself already felt certain twinges of jealousy, and could not blame this speech that contained the germ of all ingratitude.
“那么这个房子什么时候能住呢？”欧仁看看四周，问道， “And when will the rooms be ready?” asked Eugene, looking round.
“我想我们今晚得离开这里。” “We must all leave them this evening, I suppose.”
“是的，但是明天你必须过来和我吃饭。”她向他投去意味深长的眼神，回答道， “Yes, but to-morrow you must come and dine with me,” she answered, with an eloquent glance.
“我们会在意大利剧院度过一晚。” “It is our night at the Italiens.”
“我会去楼下的后座。”她的父亲说。 “I shall go to the pit,” said her father.
这时已经是午夜了。 It was midnight.
德纽沁根夫人的马车正等着她，高老头和这个学生则走回“沃盖之家”。他们谈论着德尔菲娜，谈话渐渐升温，直到两种强烈的激情引起了两人之间奇特的敌对情绪。 Mme. de Nucingen’s carriage was waiting for her, and Father Goriot and the student walked back to the Maison Vauquer, talking of Delphine, and warming over their talk till there grew up a curious rivalry between the two violent passions.
欧仁不禁感觉到这位父亲无私的爱比他自己的爱更深刻、更坚定。 Eugene could not help seeing that the father’s self-less love was deeper and more steadfast than his own.
对于这位仰慕者来说，德尔菲娜总是那么纯洁、美丽，她父亲的喜爱则从洋溢着爱的整个过去和未来中汲取热情。 For this worshiper Delphine was always pure and fair, and her father’s adoration drew its fervor from a whole past as well as a future of love.
他们发现沃盖夫人坐在火炉边，西尔维和克里斯托夫正陪着她。这位年老的女房东坐在那里，就像马略坐在迦太基的废墟中一样。女房东正等着还留在这里的两个房客，和富有同情心的西尔维哀叹自己的命运。 They found Mme. Vauquer by the stove, with Sylvie and Christophe to keep her company; the old landlady, sitting like Marius among the ruins of Carthage, was waiting for the two lodgers that yet remained to her, and bemoaning her lot with the sympathetic Sylvie.
拜伦的诗歌中记录了塔索的哀歌。这曲哀歌无疑非常动人，但是就单纯的现实影响力而言，则远不及这个寡妇心灵深处的哭泣那么深远。 Tasso’s lamentations as recorded in Byron’s poem are undoubtedly eloquent, but for sheer force of truth they fall far short of the widow’s cry from the depths.
“早上就只煮三杯咖啡吧，西尔维！ “Only three cups of coffee in the morning, Sylvie!
哦，天啊！这样清空你的房子已经足够伤你的心了。 Oh dear! to have your house emptied in this way is enough to break your heart.
什么是生活，如今我的房客们都走了？ What is life, now my lodgers are gone?
什么都不是。 Nothing at all.
就想想看！ Just think of it!
就好像家具全部都搬出了房子，可是你的家具就是你的命啊。 It is just as if all the furniture had been taken out of the house, and your furniture is your life.
我是怎么触怒了上天，惹来这一切的麻烦？ How have I offended heaven to draw down all this trouble upon me?
所有的扁豆和土豆都是按二十个人的分量准备的。 And haricot beans and potatoes laid in for twenty people!
警察还来我们家了！ The police in my house too!
我们现在要靠着土豆过活了，克里斯托夫不得不走了！” We shall have to live on potatoes now, and Christophe will have to go!”
熟睡着的萨瓦人听了这句突然醒过来，不解地说：“夫人。” The Savoyard, who was fast asleep, suddenly woke up at this, and said, “Madame,” questioningly.
“可怜的小伙子！”西尔维说，“他就像条狗。” “Poor fellow!” said Sylvie, “he is like a dog.”
“还是在淡季！ “In the dead season, too!
没人现在搬家。 Nobody is moving now.
我想知道还有人会从什么地方搬来。 I would like to know where the lodgers are to drop down from.
这让我心烦意乱。 It drives me distracted.
而且那个老巫婆米绍诺还把普瓦雷带走了！ And that old witch of a Michonneau goes and takes Poiret with her!
她做了什么，让他如此倾心于她？ What can she have done to make him so fond of her?
他就像一只小狗一样跟着她乱跑。” He runs about after her like a little dog.”
“天啊！”西尔维摇着头说，“那帮老处女什么伎俩都使得出来。” “Lord!” said Sylvie, flinging up her head, “those old maids are up to all sorts of tricks.”
“他们说那个可怜的沃尔特兰先生是个罪犯。”这个寡妇继续说， “There’s that poor M. Vautrin that they made out to be a convict,” the widow went on.
“哎，你知道我接受不了这个，西尔维，我无法让自己相信这一切。 “Well, you know that is too much for me, Sylvie; I can’t bring myself to believe it.
他是那么活泼的一个人，为他每晚的咖啡每月支付十五法郎，也从不赊账。” Such a lively man as he was, and paid fifteen francs a month for his coffee of an evening, paid you very penny on the nail too.”
“他是个出手阔绰的人！”克里斯托夫说。 “And open-handed he was!” said Christophe.
“肯定是搞错了。”西尔维说。 “There is some mistake,” said Sylvie.
“啊，没有搞错！他自己都承认了！”沃盖夫人说， “Why, no there isn’t! he said so himself!” said Mme. Vauquer.
“想想所有这些事情都发生在我的房子里，在这个你从不会看到猫走过的地方。 “And to think that all these things have happened in my house, and in a quarter where you never see a cat go by.
让我这个老实的女人说，这就像一场梦。 On my word as an honest woman, it’s like a dream.
因为，看看这里，我们看着路易十六的灾难降临；我们见证皇帝的没落；我们看他卷土重来而又被打倒。所有这些事情都不奇怪，但是旅馆轻易不会受到革命的影响。 For, look here, we saw Louis XVI meet with his mishap; we saw the fall of the Emperor; and we saw him come back and fall again; there was nothing out of the way in all that, but lodging-houses are not liable to revolutions.
你可以没有国王，但是你还是要吃饭；只要是一个体面的女人，有着德孔夫兰的出身和教养，她就会在晚饭时给你准备各种好吃的东西，除了世界末日——但是这里，现在就是世界末日，现在就是！” You can do without a king, but you must eat all the same; and so long as a decent woman, a de Conflans born and bred, will give you all sorts of good things for dinner, nothing short of the end of the world ought to—but there, it is the end of the world, that is just what it is!”
“我听说米绍诺小姐为了每年一千克朗的回报就做出了这些伤天害理的事。”西尔维大声说。 “And to think that Mlle. Michonneau who made all this mischief is to have a thousand crowns a year for it, so I hear,” cried Sylvie.
“不要说她，她是个邪恶的女人！”沃盖夫人说， “Don’t speak of her, she is a wicked woman!” said Mme. Vauquer.
“她还要去比诺那里，她的要价比成本还低。 “She is going to the Buneaud, who charges less than cost.
但是比诺什么都做得出来，在她的一生之中，她肯定做过可怕的事——抢劫和谋杀。 But the Buneaud is capable of anything; she must have done frightful things, robbed and murdered people in her time.
她应该被判终生监禁而不是那个可怜的人——”这时欧仁和高老头按了门铃。 SHE ought to be put in jail for life instead of that poor dear—”Eugene and Goriot rang the door-bell at that moment.
“啊！我的两位忠诚的房客回来了。”寡妇叹了一口气，说。 “Ah! here are my two faithful lodgers,” said the widow, sighing.
但是这两位忠诚房客脑子里都只有阴暗的回忆，记录着旅馆里发生的不幸。他们不慌不忙地对女房东说他们将要搬到安丁路上。 But the two faithful lodgers, who retained but shadowy recollections of the misfortunes of their lodging-house, announced to their hostess without more ado that they were about to remove to the Chaussee d’Antin.
“西尔维！”寡妇哭喊道，“这是压在骆驼上的最后一根稻草——先生们，你们这是要置我于死地啊！ “Sylvie!” cried the widow, “this is the last straw.—Gentlemen, this will be the death of me!
这太让我心烦了！ It has quite upset me!
我胸口有千斤重！ There’s a weight on my chest!
我今天老了十岁！ I am ten years older for this day!
真的，我快要发疯了！ Upon my word, I shall go out of my senses!
那些扁豆怎么办！——哦，那么，要是这里只剩下我一个人，你明天可以走了，克里斯托夫——晚安，先生们。”说完她就走了。 And what is to be done with the haricots!—Oh, well, if I am to be left here all by myself, you shall go to-morrow, Christophe.—Good-night, gentlemen,” and she went.
“现在是怎么一回事？”欧仁问西尔维。 “What is the matter now?” Eugene inquired of Sylvie.
“天啊！每一个人都忙着自己的事，这让她惊慌失措了。 “Lord! everybody is going about his business, and that has addled her wits.
看！她在楼上哭呢。 There! she is crying upstairs.
哭出来对她有好处。 It will do her good to snivel a bit.
自从我跟着她以来，这还是她第一次流眼泪呢。” It’s the first time she has cried since I’ve been with her.”
到了早晨，沃盖夫人，用她自己的话说，已经“接受这件事了”。 By the morning, Mme. Vauquer, to use her own expression, had “made up her mind to it.”
的确，她的神色依旧哀伤。那正是一个女人失去她所有房客时的神情。她的生活方式突然被彻底改变了，但她还是十分理智。 True, she still wore a doleful countenance, as might be expected of a woman who had lost all her lodgers, and whose manner of life had been suddenly revolutionized, but she had all her wits about her.
她的忧伤真挚而深刻，这是情绪上的真正苦痛，因为她在经济上受挫，而她的生活规律也被打破了。 Her grief was genuine and profound; it was real pain of mind, for her purse had suffered, the routine of her existence had been broken.
一个情人和他情妇永别时向闺房窗子的回眸一望也不及沃盖夫人看着饭桌前空下的座位时那么悲伤。 A lover’s farewell glance at his lady-love’s window is not more mournful than Mme. Vauquer’s survey of the empty places round her table.
欧仁安慰她，告诉寡妇比安卡肖恩在医院的住处就要到期了，他肯定会搬来他的（拉斯蒂涅的）房间；而且博物馆员工也时常表示，他愿意住在库蒂尔夫人的房间里；不久之后，她的家就会恢复老样子了。 Eugene administered comfort, telling the widow that Bianchon, whose term of residence at the hospital was about to expire, would doubtless take his (Rastignac’s) place; that the official from the Museum had often expressed a desire to have Mme. Couture’s rooms; and that in a very few days her household would be on the old footing.
“但愿上帝如此安排，我亲爱的先生！ “God send it may, my dear sir!
但是霉运已经来这里安家了。 But bad luck has come to lodge here.
十天之内这座房子里必定有人会死，你等着瞧。”然后她悲惨地环顾餐厅。 There’ll be a death in the house before ten days are out, you’ll see,” and she gave a lugubrious look round the dining-room.
“我想会轮到谁呢？” “Whose turn will it be, I wonder?”
“幸好我们就要搬走了。”欧仁低声对高老头说。 “It is just as well that we are moving out,” said Eugene to Father Goriot in a low voice.
“夫人。”西尔维满脸恐惧地跑过来说，“我已经三天没见米斯蒂格里斯了。” “Madame,” said Sylvie, running in with a scared face, “I have not seen Mistigris these three days.”
“啊！要是我的猫死了，要是它离开我们走了，我——”这个可怜的妇人说不下去了。她紧握双手，把脸埋在扶手椅椅背里，着实被这个可怕的征兆吓坏了。 “Ah! well, if my cat is dead, if HE has gone and left us, I—” The poor woman could not finish her sentence; she clasped her hands and hid her face on the back of her armchair, quite overcome by this dreadful portent.
第五章 Chapter 5
晌午时分，邮差来到了那一区，欧仁收到了一封信。 By twelve o’clock, when the postman reaches that quarter, Eugene received a letter.
信封很漂亮，封缄上盖有伯桑家的印章。信里有一张请帖，邀请他参加子爵夫人举办的盛大舞会。这场舞会已经在巴黎被谈论了一个月了。 The dainty envelope bore the Beauseant arms on the seal, and contained an invitation to the Vicomtesse’s great ball, which had been talked of in Paris for a month.
除了请帖，里面还有一张给欧仁的小字条。 A little note for Eugene was slipped in with the card.
“先生，我想您会很乐意代我向德纽沁根夫人致意。因此，我按照您的要求给您寄来了请帖。 “I think, monsieur, that you will undertake with pleasure to interpret my sentiments to Mme. de Nucingen, so I am sending the card for which you asked me to you.
我很高兴能认识德雷斯多夫人的妹妹。 I shall be delighted to make the acquaintance of Mme. de Restaud’s sister.
请您一定要把那位迷人的女士介绍给我认识，不要让她独占了您的爱，因为您欠我的爱还不少呢。 Pray introduce that charming lady to me, and do not let her monopolize all your affection, for you owe me not a little in return for mine.
德伯桑子爵夫人” VICOMTESSE DE BEAUSEANT.”
“嗯，”欧仁第二遍读字条的时候，自言自语道，“德伯桑夫人写得很明白，她不欢迎德纽沁根男爵。” “Well,” said Eugene to himself, as he read the note a second time, “Mme. de Beauseant says pretty plainly that she does not want the Baron de Nucingen.”
他立刻高兴地去了德尔菲娜家。 He went to Delphine at once in his joy.
他给她带来了这个喜讯，无疑会因此而得到奖赏。 He had procured this pleasure for her, and doubtless he would receive the price of it.
德纽沁根夫人正在梳妆打扮。 Mme. de Nucingen was dressing.
拉斯蒂涅急切地想得到自己盼望了一年还没有得到的奖赏，自然极不耐烦。他极力克制自己的急不可耐，在她的卧室里等着。 Rastignac waited in her boudoir, enduring as best he might the natural impatience of an eager temperament for the reward desired and withheld for a year.
这样的感觉一生中只能体会到一次。 Such sensations are only known once in a life.
男人爱上的第一个女人，如果她确实是个女人——也就是说，如果她能从构成巴黎生活必不可少的美妙事物中脱颖而出，吸引到他——她就永远是天下无双的。 The first woman to whom a man is drawn, if she is really a woman—that is to say, if she appears to him amid the splendid accessories that form a necessary background to life in the world of Paris—will never have a rival.
在巴黎，爱情是一件与众不同又遥不可及的事情。因为在那里，虽然人们想利用普通的事件掩盖自己的动机或者炫耀自己伪装得天衣无缝的无私精神，但是不管男人还是女人都不会轻易上当。 Love in Paris is a thing distinct and apart; for in Paris neither men nor women are the dupes of the commonplaces by which people seek to throw a veil over their motives, or to parade a fine affectation of disinterestedness in their sentiments.
在这个国中国，女人不只需要满足感官和精神的需求，她们也十分清楚地意识到自己还要履行更重要的义务，即她们必须满足无穷无尽的虚荣心。这种虚荣心渗透到了这个叫做社会的生命有机体的每根纤维。 In this country within a country, it is not merely required of a woman that she should satisfy the senses and the soul; she knows perfectly well that she has still greater obligations to discharge, that she must fulfil the countless demands of a vanity that enters into every fibre of that living organism called society.
爱情对于她来说是最重要的，但本质上是虚荣、厚颜无耻、招摇过市、挥金如土的骗子。 Love, for her, is above all things, and by its very nature, a vainglorious, brazen-fronted, ostentatious, thriftless charlatan.
如果说在路易十四的宫廷，每个女人都羡慕德拉瓦利埃小姐，因为她不计后果地奉献热情，使得伟大的君主不惜撕烂自己无价的褶皱袖边来帮助他们的私生子德韦尔芒杜瓦公爵降生，那么我们对其他的社会上层人士还有什么指望呢？ If at the Court of Louis XIV there was not a woman but envied Mlle.de la Valliere the reckless devotion of passion that led the grand monarch to tear the priceless ruffles at his wrists in order to assist the entry of a Duc de Vermandois into the world—what can you expect of the rest of society?
你必须得年轻、富有、有头衔。如果可能的话，还得拥有更多，因为你带到神殿的香越多，上帝就会越喜欢你这个崇拜者。 You must have youth and wealth and rank; nay, you must, if possible, have more than these, for the more incense you bring with you to burn at the shrine of the god, the more favorably will he regard the worshiper.
爱情是一种宗教，信仰它所要付出的代价理所当然要比信仰其他各种神都要昂贵。爱情这个破坏者停留片刻后就会消失。他宛如街上的顽童，其踪迹需通过他造成的破坏才能追踪得到。 Love is a religion, and his cult must in the nature of things be more costly than those of all other deities; Love the Spoiler stays for a moment, and then passes on; like the urchin of the streets, his course may be traced by the ravages that he has made.
丰富的感情和想象力是住在阁楼里的穷小子的诗意情趣，没有那种财富，爱情还怎么存在呢？ The wealth of feeling and imagination is the poetry of the garret; how should love exist there without that wealth?
如果有些人不信邪，不遵守巴黎信条的严格约束，那么他们只能生活在孤独之中。 If there are exceptions who do not subscribe to these Draconian laws of the Parisian code, they are solitary examples.
这样的人远离主流生活，因此不会受社会教条影响而偏离自己的意愿。他们居住在某个源源不断的清泉旁边，守着绿阴而不愿离开，乐于倾听自己周围和内心世界的一切回音，耐心地等待着自己飞升到天堂的日子，同时以怜悯的眼光看着俗世中的人们。 Such souls live so far out of the main current that they are not borne away by the doctrines of society; they dwell beside some clear spring of ever-flowing water, without seeking to leave the green shade; happy to listen to the echoes of the infinite in everything around them and in their own souls, waiting in patience to take their flight for heaven, while they look with pity upon those of earth.
拉斯蒂涅和大多数预先体会到权势和伟大氛围的年轻人一样,打算全副武装地进入上层社会。熊熊燃烧的征服欲已经支配了他。也许意识到了自己的力量，但是至今他仍然既不知道自己的终极目标是什么，也不知道如何才能达到这一目标。 Rastignac, like most young men who have been early impressed by the circumstances of power and grandeur, meant to enter the lists fully armed; the burning ambition of conquest possessed him already; perhaps he was conscious of his powers, but as yet he knew neither the end to which his ambition was to be directed, nor the means of attaining it.
没有纯洁、神圣的爱情来充实人的生命时，野心也许就会变得非常高尚，可以打败所有的个人兴趣，并且会把整个国家而非个人作为其崇高的目标。 In default of the pure and sacred love that fills a life, ambition may become something very noble, subduing to itself every thought of personal interest, and setting as the end—the greatness, not of one man, but of a whole nation.
但是这个学生还没有到回首自己整个人生并且进行冷静评判的年龄。 But the student had not yet reached the time of life when a man surveys the whole course of existence and judges it soberly.
迄今为止，他几乎仍旧无法摆脱新鲜和优雅事物的影响散发出的魔力，它们仿佛绿叶和青草一样，环绕在乡下孩子的周围。 Hitherto he had scarcely so much as shaken off the spell of the fresh and gracious influences that envelop a childhood in the country, like green leaves and grass.
他在巴黎鲁比肯河的岸边踟蹰。尽管野心让他内心刺痛，他依然坚持着原先的理想所带来的、一种根深蒂固的传统：想过贵族在城堡里享受的那种平静的生活。 He had hesitated on the brink of the Parisian Rubicon, and in spite of the prickings of ambition, he still clung to a lingering tradition of an old ideal—the peaceful life of the noble in his chateau.
但是昨天晚上，当他看到他的房间时，那些踟蹰都消失了。 But yesterday evening, at the sight of his rooms, those scruples had vanished.
他已经靠着出身在社交方面获得了优势，同时也学会了靠好运气在物质方面获得优势。从那一刻起，他不再是个乡下人，而是自然而然并且轻而易举地悄悄获得了一个地位，这个地位让他的前途看上去一片光明。 He had learned what it was to enjoy the material advantages of fortune, as he had already enjoyed the social advantages of birth; he ceased to be a provincial from that moment, and slipped naturally and easily into a position which opened up a prospect of a brilliant future.
因此，当在那个他自认为百分之百有权呆的漂亮卧室里等德尔菲娜的时候，他觉得自己已经和一年前回到巴黎的拉斯蒂涅大不一样了。他回顾原来的自己，自问以前的拉斯蒂涅和此刻的拉斯蒂涅是否有任何相同之处。 So, as he waited for Delphine, in the pretty boudoir, where he felt that he had a certain right to be, he felt himself so far away from the Rastignac who came back to Paris a year ago, that, turning some power of inner vision upon this latter, he asked himself whether that past self bore any resemblance to the Rastignac of that moment.
“夫人在她的房间里。”泰蕾兹进来告诉他。 “Madame is in her room,” Therese came to tell him.
这个女人的声音把他吓了一跳。 The woman’s voice made him start.
他看见德尔菲娜靠在壁炉旁的低背椅上，看上去神采奕奕、容光焕发。 He found Delphine lying back in her low chair by the fireside, looking fresh and bright.
她身处飘逸的、平纹细布织成的帏帐之中，让人想到了美丽的热带花丛簇拥着的果实。 The sight of her among the flowing draperies of muslin suggested some beautiful tropical flower, where the fruit is set amid the blossom.
“啊，”她说，激动得声音都颤抖了，“你来了。” “Well,” she said, with a tremor in her voice, “here you are.”
“猜猜我给你带了什么。”欧仁坐到她的旁边说。 “Guess what I bring for you,” said Eugene, sitting down beside her.
欧仁抬起她的手吻了一下。德纽沁根夫人一看到请帖，立刻喜出望外。她转向欧仁，用手臂搂住他的脖子，怀着虚荣心得到满足的狂喜把他拉过来，眼里涌满了泪水。 He took possession of her arm to kiss her hand. Mme. de Nucingen gave a joyful start as she saw the card.She turned to Eugene; there were tears in her eyes as she flung her arms about his neck, and drew him towards her in a frenzy of gratified vanity.
“你给了我幸福——你。（她悄悄地在他的耳边说着更亲密的话）但是，泰蕾兹在我的化妆室，我们还是谨慎一点好——你给我带来幸福——是的，当幸福是由你带给我的时候，我管它叫幸福——肯定不只是自尊心的满足。 “And I owe this happiness to you—to @thee@” (she whispered the more intimate word in his ear); “but Therese is in my dressing-room, let us be prudent.—This happiness—yes, for I may call it so, when it comes to me through YOU—is surely more than a triumph for self-love?
过去没人愿意介绍我进入那个圈子。 No one has been willing to introduce me into that set.
也许刚刚我看上去轻佻、渺小而浅薄，就像个巴黎女人。但是，我的朋友，请记住我打算为你放弃一切。如果我比以前更想踏进圣日耳曼郊区，那是因为我可以在那里遇到你。” Perhaps just now I may seem to you to be frivolous, petty, shallow, like a Parisienne, but remember, my friend, that I am ready to give up all for you; and that if I long more than ever for an entrance into the Faubourg Saint-Germain, it is because I shall meet you there.”
“德伯桑夫人在字条里似乎写得很明白，她不想德纽沁根男爵参加她的舞会，你不这样认为吗？”欧仁说。 “Mme. de Beauseant’s note seems to say very plainly that she does not expect to see the @Baron@ de Nucingen at her ball; don’t you think so?” said Eugene.
“嗯，是的，”男爵夫人把信还给他，说道， “Why, yes,” said the Baroness as she returned the letter.
“那些女人天生都很傲慢。 “Those women have a talent for insolence.
但是这没什么，我会去的。 But it is of no consequence, I shall go.
我姐姐一定在那里，一定穿得非常漂亮——欧仁，”她压低声音继续说，“她肯定会去澄清那些丑恶的猜疑。 My sister is sure to be there, and sure to be very beautifully dressed.—Eugene,” she went on, lowering her voice, “she will go to dispel ugly suspicions.
你不知道人们都说她些什么。 You do not know the things that people are saying about her.
就在今天早上，纽沁根还告诉我，他们曾在俱乐部里谈论过她。 Only this morning Nucingen came to tell me that they had been discussing her at the club.
我的天啊！女人的名誉和整个家族的荣誉是多么不堪一击啊！ Great heavens! on what does a woman’s character and the honor of a whole family depend!
可怜的姐姐受到侮辱，我觉得自己也几乎受到牵连，受到侮辱了。 I feel that I am nearly touched and wounded in my poor sister.
听人说，德特拉尔先生欠了十万法郎的债务，几乎所有的债务都到期了，人家威胁说要告他。 According to some people, M. de Trailles must have put his name to bills for a hundred thousand francs, nearly all of them are overdue, and proceedings are threatened.
面对这样的困境，我姐姐似乎把她的钻石卖给了一个犹太人——那些美丽的钻石是他丈夫的母亲，老德雷斯多夫人传下来的——你应该看见她戴过吧。 In this predicament, it seems that my sister sold her diamonds to a Jew—the beautiful diamonds that belonged to her husband’s mother, Mme. de Restaud the elder,—you have seen her wearing them.
事实上，过去的两天，人们谈论的都是这件事。 In fact, nothing else has been talked about for the last two days.
所以我敢肯定阿纳斯塔谢一定会穿着金丝织的晚装、戴着耀眼的钻石去参加德伯桑夫人的舞会，把所有人的眼光都吸引到她的身上。但是我是不会被比下去的。 So I can see that Anastasie is sure to come to Mme. de Beauseant’s ball in tissue of gold, and ablaze with diamonds, to draw all eyes upon her; and I will not be outshone.
她一辈子都想盖过我的风头，从来都没对我好过，而我却经常帮助她，在她没钱的时候就借钱给她——但是现在，我不管其他人了，今天我要痛痛快快地高兴一下。”那天凌晨一点，欧仁仍然和德纽沁根夫人在一起。 She has tried to eclipse me all her life, she has never been kind to me, and I have helped her so often, and always had money for her when she had none.—But never mind other people now, to-day I mean to be perfectly happy.”At one o’clock that morning Eugene was still with Mme. de Nucingen.
她和他告别，言语中充满了对未来幸福的期望。这时她伤感地说道：“我很害怕，很迷信。 In the midst of their lovers’ farewell, a farewell full of hope of bliss to come, she said in a troubled voice, “I am very fearful, superstitious.
随便你怎样定义我的预感，但是我害怕会遇到某个可怕的灾祸，我的幸福会为此付出代价。” Give what name you like to my presentiments, but I am afraid that my happiness will be paid for by some horrible catastrophe.”
“真是个孩子！”欧仁说。 “Child!” said Eugene.
“啊！难道今晚我们身份互换，我变成孩子了？”她笑着问道。 “Ah! have we changed places, and am I the child to-night?” she asked, laughingly.
欧仁回到“沃盖之家”，确信明天就能永远离开这里。他又回味起刚刚的幸福和甜蜜，一路上做了许多美梦，年轻人常做这样的美梦。 Eugene went back to the Maison Vauquer, never doubting but that he should leave it for good on the morrow; and on the way he fell to dreaming the bright dreams of youth, when the cup of happiness has left its sweetness on the lips.
“喂，怎么样？”高老头在拉斯蒂涅从他门前经过的时候问道。 “Well?” cried Goriot, as Rastignac passed by his door.
“嗯，很好。”欧仁说，“明天我会告诉你所有事情的。” “Yes,” said Eugene; “I will tell you everything to-morrow.”
“所有事情？你不会食言吧？”老人大声说。 “Everything, will you not?” cried the old man.
“去睡吧。 “Go to bed.
明天我们的幸福生活就要开始了。” To-morrow our happy life will begin.”
第二天，高老头和拉斯蒂涅准备好离开旅馆，只等搬运工来给他们搬行李了。但是接近中午的时候，新圣热讷维耶沃街上传来了车轮声，一辆马车停在了“沃盖之家”门前。 Next day, Goriot and Rastignac were ready to leave the lodging-house, and only awaited the good pleasure of a porter to move out of it; but towards noon there was a sound of wheels in the Rue Neuve-Sainte-Genevieve, and a carriage stopped before the door of the Maison Vauquer.
德纽沁根夫人下车问西尔维，她的父亲是不是还住在这房子里。得到肯定回答后，她轻轻地跑上楼去。 Mme. de Nucingen alighted, and asked if her father was still in the house, and, receiving an affirmative reply from Sylvie, ran lightly upstairs.
欧仁恰巧在家，可是他的邻居对此却全然不知。 It so happened that Eugene was at home all unknown to his neighbor.
早饭的时候，欧仁叫高老头负责替他搬行李，说他四点会在阿图瓦街和他碰面。不过拉斯蒂涅的名字在法学院的学员名单上排得很靠前，因此他很快就被点到名了。然后他立刻回到了新圣热讷维耶沃街。 At breakfast time he had asked Goriot to superintend the removal of his goods, saying that he would meet him in the Rue d’Artois at four o’clock; but Rastignac’s name had been called early on the list at the Ecole de Droit, and he had gone back at once to the Rue Nueve-Sainte-Genevieve.
没人看见他进来，高老头去找搬运工了，旅馆的女主人也出去了。 No one had seen him come in, for Goriot had gone to find a porter, and the mistress of the house was likewise out.
欧仁想自己付钱给沃盖夫人，因为如果他不付的话，高老头很可能会热情地替他付钱，而这会让他很过意不去。 Eugene had thought to pay her himself, for it struck him that if he left this, Goriot in his zeal would probably pay for him.
就这样，欧仁上自己的房间去看看有没有什么落下。他很庆幸自己有这样的先见之明，因为他在抽屉里找到了一张沃尔特兰签过名的空白支票。那天他还钱后就把支票粗心地扔到那里了。 As it was, Eugene went up to his room to see that nothing had been forgotten, and blessed his foresight when he saw the blank bill bearing Vautrin’s signature lying in the drawer where he had carelessly thrown it on the day when he had repaid the amount.
壁炉里没有火，所以他打算把它撕成小碎片。这时候，高老头的房间传来了说话声，说话的人是德尔菲娜！ There was no fire in the grate, so he was about to tear it into little pieces, when he heard a voice speaking in Goriot’s room, and the speaker was Delphine!
他停了下来，静静地站在那里听着，觉得她对自己不应该隐瞒一点秘密。但是听了开始的几句话后，这父女间的谈话非常奇怪、非常有趣，吸引他全神贯注地听了下去。 He made no more noise, and stood still to listen, thinking that she should have no secrets from him; but after the first few words, the conversation between the father and daughter was so strange and interesting that it absorbed all his attention.
“啊！谢天谢地，父亲，在我完全破产之前，您想到要他给我一笔钱。 “Ah! thank heaven that you thought of asking him to give an account of the money settled on me before I was utterly ruined, father.
这里说话安全吗？”她添了一句。 Is it safe to talk?” she added.
“嗯，很安全，这个房子里一个人也没有。”她的父亲用微弱的声音说道。 “Yes, there is no one in the house,” said her father faintly.
“您怎么了？”德纽沁根夫人问道。 “What is the matter with you?” asked Mme. de Nucingen.
“但愿上帝能够原谅你！孩子，你刚刚让我很吃惊，简直是给了我当头一棒！”老人说， “God forgive you! you have just dealt me a staggering blow, child!” said the old man.
“你不知道我有多爱你，否则你听到这样的消息，特别是希望犹存时，就不会突然冲进来找我了。 “You cannot know how much I love you, or you would not have burst in upon me like this, with such news, especially if all is not lost.
究竟发生了什么重要的事，你得上这里来告诉我？ Has something so important happened that you must come here about it?
过不了多长时间，我们就应该在阿图瓦街了。” In a few minutes we should have been in the Rue d’Artois.”
“唉！遇到灾祸，谁还顾得上想自己正在做什么呢。 “Eh! does one think what one is doing after a catastrophe?
我都六神无主了。 It has turned my head.
您的律师现在已经发现一些端倪了，而真相迟早都会被揭露出来。 Your attorney has found out the state of things now, but it was bound to come out sooner or later.
我们需要您长期积累的商业经验。我来找您，就像落水的人抓到了一根树枝。 We shall want your long business experience; and I come to you like a drowning man who catches at a branch.
当德维尔先生发现纽沁根百般刁难他的时候，便威胁要起诉他，还清楚地告诉他，很快就会从法院院长那里拿到批准令。 When M. Derville found that Nucingen was throwing all sorts of difficulties in his way, he threatened him with proceedings, and told him plainly that he would soon obtain an order from the President of the Tribunal.
所以今天早上纽沁根来我的房间问我是不是打算一下子毁掉我们两个人。 So Nucingen came to my room this morning, and asked if I meant to ruin us both.
我告诉他，我对这件事一无所知，我只知道我有一笔钱，应该由我自己掌管，一切事务都由我的律师全权处理。后来我又重复了一遍，我对这件事一无所知，什么都不能和他谈。 I told him that I knew nothing whatever about it, that I had a fortune, and ought to be put into possession of my fortune, and that my attorney was acting for me in the matter; I said again that I knew absolutely nothing about it, and could not possibly go into the subject with him.
您不是叫我这么说的吗？” Wasn’t that what you told me to tell him?”
“是啊，很对啊。”高老头回答。 “Yes, quite right,” answered Goriot.
“唉，可是，”德尔菲娜继续说，“他告诉了我生意的情形。 “Well, then,” Delphine continued, “he told me all about his affairs.
他刚刚把自己和我的所有资产都用来做了投机生意。生意才刚刚起步，大笔的钱都被套牢了。 He had just invested all his capital and mine in business speculations; they have only just been started, and very large sums of money are locked up.
如果我现在逼他还嫁妆，他就会被迫申请破产；如果我等上一年，他就能把钱投到房地产开发上去，他以他的名誉保证会给我两倍或者三倍的财产，到时候我就能自由支配我所有的财产了。 If I were to compel him to refund my dowry now, he would be forced to file his petition; but if I will wait a year, he undertakes, on his honor, to double or treble my fortune, by investing it in building land, and I shall be mistress at last of the whole of my property.
我亲爱的父亲，他讲的都是真话，他让我害怕极了！ He was speaking the truth, father dear; he frightened me!
他请求我原谅他的行为，他已经给了我自由，我可以喜欢干什么就干什么，但条件是我让他继续以我的名义打理我的生意。 He asked my pardon for his conduct; he has given me my liberty; I am free to act as I please on condition that I leave him to carry on my business in my name.
为了证明他的诚意，他许诺我可以随时叫德维尔先生去查账，这样我就能确定一切都被管理得妥妥当当了。 To prove his sincerity, he promised that M. Derville might inspect the accounts as often as I pleased, so that I might be assured that everything was being conducted properly.
简而言之，他绑起手脚把自己交给我管了。 In short, he put himself in my power, bound hand and foot.
他希望我这两年能够继续维持目前的家庭开支安排，还恳求我除了月钱外不要额外花钱。 He wishes the present arrangements as to the expenses of housekeeping to continue for two more years, and entreated me not to exceed my allowance.
他直白地告诉我，为了保住面子他可以做的只有这些了。他已经和剧院的舞女分手了。为了确保信誉、等待时机，他不得不暗中想尽一切办法省钱。 He showed me plainly that it was all that he could do to keep up appearances; he has broken with his opera dancer; he will be compelled to practice the most strict economy (in secret) if he is to bide his time with unshaken credit.
我骂了他，做了我能做的一切让他绝望，好知道更多的事情。 I scolded, I did all I could to drive him to desperation, so as to find out more.
他给我看了他的账目。最后，他完全崩溃了，哭了起来。 He showed me his ledgers—he broke down and cried at last.
我从来没有看见过一个男人沦落到这样的地步。 I never saw a man in such a state.
他完全失去理智了，说要自杀，大吼起来，最后弄得我觉得自己对不起他了。” He lost his head completely, talked of killing himself, and raved till I felt quite sorry for him.”
“你真的相信那些愚蠢的废话吗？”她的父亲大叫， “Do you really believe that silly rubbish?”...cried her father.
“他编造的这些话都是用来打发你的！ “It was all got up for your benefit!
我做生意的时候不得不和德国人打交道。他们诚实、坦率，这倒是千真万确。但是除了直率和坦白，他们也喜欢骗人、喜欢伪装，他们是最糟糕的无赖。 I have had to do with Germans in the way of business, honest and straightforward they are pretty sure to be, but when with their simplicity and frankness they are sharpers and humbugs as well, they are the worst rogues of all.
你的丈夫在利用你。 Your husband is taking advantage of you.
他一有压力就假装要自杀，他是打算假借你的名义来掌控局面，这比他自己出面更可靠。 As soon as pressure is brought to bear on him he shams dead; he means to be more the master under your name than in his own.
他会利用这一点来规避商业风险，保护自己。 He will take advantage of the position to secure himself against the risks of business.
他既精明又奸诈，真是个坏东西！ He is as sharp as he is treacherous; he is a bad lot!
不，不，在我离开我的女儿们进入拉雪兹公墓之前，我不会让你们身无分文的。 No, no; I am not going to leave my girls behind me without a penny when I go to Pere-Lachaise.
我还知道些生意经。 I know something about business still.
他说他把钱用在投机买卖上了，那很好，一定有东西证明这一点——支票、收据、某些文件。 He has sunk his money in speculation, he says; very well then, there is something to show for it—bills, receipts, papers of some sort.
让他拿出来和你算账。 Let him produce them, and come to an arrangement with you.
我们要选出他最有前途的投机买卖，接手过来自己做，自己承担风险，并把有价证券转入你的名下。它们会代表德尔菲娜·高里奥，德纽沁根男爵妻子的独立财产。 We will choose the most promising of his speculations, take them over at our own risk, and have the securities transferred into your name; they shall represent the separate estate of Delphine Goriot, wife of the Baron de Nucingen.
那个家伙真把我们当傻瓜了吗？ Does that fellow really take us for idiots?
他以为我知道你没有钱、没有饭吃后，还能够忍受两天吗？ Does he imagine that I could stand the idea of your being without fortune, without bread, for forty-eight hours?
我一天都不能忍——不，一个晚上都不能忍，两个小时都不能忍！ I would not stand it a day—no, not a night, not a couple of hours!
如果你真的落到那般地步，我一辈子都无法原谅我自己。 If there had been any foundation for the idea, I should never get over it.
什么！ What!
我四十年来辛苦工作，背面粉袋背得汗流浃背、腰酸背痛，还省吃俭用，所有的辛苦和负担都是为了你们，我亲爱的女儿们，为了你们少点辛苦、少点负担。现在，我的财产，我的整个人生都要烟消云散了！ I have worked hard for forty years, carried sacks on my back, and sweated and pinched and saved all my life for you, my darlings, for you who made the toil and every burden borne for you seem light; and now, my fortune, my whole life, is to vanish in smoke!
如果我相信他说的一个字的话，我就会狂怒地死去。 I should die raving mad if I believed a word of it.
以天上地下所有的神灵起誓，我们必须立刻弄清楚这一切。我们要仔细检查账目，把整个生意都查得一清二楚！ By all that’s holiest in heaven and earth, we will have this cleared up at once; go through the books, have the whole business looked thoroughly into!
只有查明你所有的财产都分文不少，我才会满意，否就就睡不着、休息不了、吃不下饭。 I will not sleep, nor rest, nor eat until I have satisfied myself that all your fortune is in existence.
你的钱就是你的，感谢上帝！ Your money is settled upon you, God be thanked!
幸好你的代理人德维尔律师是个诚实的人。 And, luckily, your attorney, Maitre Derville, is an honest man.
请上帝作证！你到老都会有一百万的贴己钱，每年都有五万法郎的收入。要不然我会把巴黎闹得满城风雨。我一定会这样做的！ Good Lord! you shall have your snug little million, your fifty thousand francs a year, as long as you live, or I will raise a racket in Paris, I will so!
如果法院不公正，我就向国民议会请愿。 If the Tribunals put upon us, I will appeal to the Chambers.
如果知道你很好，完全不用担心钱，即便我身体不好或遇到麻烦，我都会很安心了。 If I knew that you were well and comfortably off as far as money is concerned, that thought would keep me easy in spite of bad health and troubles.
钱？啊，它可是生命！ Money? why, it is life!
钱能做任何事情。 Money does everything.
那个阿尔萨斯大傻瓜会改变他的态度的！ That great dolt of an Alsatian shall sing to another tune!
听我说，德尔菲娜，别放弃，不要对那个傻瓜做一丁点的让步。他折磨着你，让你很悲惨。 Look here, Delphine, don’t give way, don’t make a concession of half a quarter of a farthing to that fathead, who has ground you down and made you miserable.
要是他不能没有你，咱们得好好揍他一顿，让他听话点。 If he can’t do without you, we will give him a good cudgeling, and keep him in order.
哦，天啊！我的脑袋着火了，里面好像有东西在燃烧。 Great heavens! my brain is on fire; it is as if there were something redhot inside my head.
我的德尔菲娜躺在草席上！ My Delphine lying on straw!
你！我的菲芬！ You! my Fifine!
哦，老天爷啊！ Good gracious!
我的手套在哪里？ Where are my gloves?
哎，我们快走吧。我打算亲眼看看每一样东西——账目、现金、信件、整个生意。 Come, let us go at once; I mean to see everything with my own eyes—books, cash, and correspondence, the whole business.
要是不确定你的财产很安全，我是不会安心的。” I shall have no peace until I know for certain that your fortune is secure.”
“哦，亲爱的父亲，您得小心处理这件事啊！ “Oh! father dear, be careful how you set about it!
如果您露出一丁点想借这件事出气的迹象，如果您公开与他为敌，我就完了。 If there is the least hint of vengeance in the business, if you show yourself openly hostile, it will be all over with me.
他知道他得对付谁。他会理所当然地认为如果您跟我讲了这个观点，我就会担心我的钱。但是我向您保证他不光现在死抓着我的钱，而且还打算一直抓着不放。 He knows whom he has to deal with; he thinks it quite natural that if you put the idea into my head, I should be uneasy about my money; but I swear to you that he has it in his own hands, and that he had meant to keep it.
他正是那种会带着所有钱逃跑、让我们陷入困境的人，这个混蛋！ He is just the man to abscond with all the money and leave us in the lurch, the scoundrel!
他非常清楚，我不会为了让他受到法律制裁而玷污自己拥有的名誉。 He knows quite well that I will not dishonor the name I bear by bringing him into a court of law.
他现在的处境很有利，同时也很不利。 His position is strong and weak at the same time.
如果我们逼得他绝望了，我就会变得一无所有。” If we drive him to despair, I am lost.”
“为什么？那家伙难道是个流氓吗？” “Why, then, the man is a rogue?”
“嗯，是的，父亲。”她扑到椅子上哭着说，“我本来不打算告诉您这些的，免得惹您伤心。”之后她流下了泪水，说：“我不想让您知道您把我嫁给了他这样的人。 “Well, yes, father,” she said, flinging herself into a chair, “I wanted to keep it from you to spare your feelings,” and she burst into tears; “I did not want you to know that you had married me to such a man as he is.
他私下里也是这种货色——身体、灵魂和良知——全都是彻彻底底的丑陋！ He is just the same in private life—body and soul and conscience—the same through and through—hideous!
我恨他，我鄙视他！ I hate him; I despise him!
是的，在卑鄙的纽沁根跟我说了那一切之后，我再也无法尊重他了。 Yes, after all that that despicable Nucingen has told me, I cannot respect him any longer.
他可以干出那种勾当，还可以毫无顾虑地跟我讲出来——因为我把他看得一清二楚，所以才很怕他。 A man capable of mixing himself up in such affairs, and of talking about them to me as he did, without the slightest scruple,—it is because I have read him through and through that I am afraid of him.
他，我的丈夫，坦白地提议给我自由。您知道那意味着什么吗？ He, my husband, frankly proposed to give me my liberty, and do you know what that means?
那意味着如果事情变得对他不利，我就得任他排布，做他的挡箭牌。” It means that if things turn out badly for him, I am to play into his hands, and be his stalking-horse.”
“但是，我们还有法律啊！ “But there is law to be had!
还有格雷夫广场等着那种女婿呢！”她的父亲大声说，“哼，如果没有刽子手的话，我就亲自把他斩了。” There is a Place de Greve for sons-in-law of that sort,” cried her father; “why, I would guillotine him myself if there was no headsman to do it.”
“不，父亲，法律是对付不了他的。 “No, father, the law cannot touch him.
您听着，这是他的原话，一点委婉的语气也没有——‘你自己选择吧，除了你没人会和我联手。要么失去所有的东西，你破产，一分钱也没有；要么你让我继续做这笔生意’。他说得还不明白吗？ Listen, this is what he says, stripped of all his circumlocutions—‘Take your choice, you and no one else can be my accomplice; either everything is lost, you are ruined and have not a farthing, or you will let me carry this business through myself.’Is that plain speaking?
他必须得要我的帮助。 He MUST have my assistance.
他确信他的妻子会公平地对待他，因为他知道我不会要他的钱，只想保住自己的钱。 He is assured that his wife will deal fairly by him; he knows that I shall leave his money to him and be content with my own.
这是个不可容忍、欺骗人心的合同，他以破产相要挟，迫使我同意。 It is an unholy and dishonest compact, and he holds out threats of ruin to compel me to consent to it.
他在收买我的良心，出价是让我随意和欧仁来往，只是保留原来的名分。 He is buying my conscience, and the price is liberty to be Eugene’s wife in all but name.
‘我允许你胡来，你也得让我犯罪，让那些可恶的家庭倾家荡产！’他说得还不够明白吗？ ‘I connive at your errors, and you allow me to commit crimes and ruin poor families!’Is that sufficiently explicit?
您知道他的投机生意是指什么吗？ Do you know what he means by speculations?
他以自己的名义买下土地，然后找些傀儡上那里盖房子。 He buys up land in his own name, then he finds men of straw to run up houses upon it.
这些人先和房子的承建人订立分期付款合同，然后把房子低价卖给我丈夫，最后宣告破产，赖掉欠承建人的款项。 These men make a bargain with a contractor to build the houses, paying them by bills at long dates; then in consideration of a small sum they leave my husband in possession of the houses, and finally slip through the fingers of the deluded contractors by going into bankruptcy.
纽沁根公司的名字被用来迷惑那些可怜的承建人。 The name of the firm of Nucingen has been used to dazzle the poor contractors.
那些我都知道。 I saw that.
我也注意到纽沁根把大笔的钱寄到了阿姆斯特丹、伦敦、那不勒斯和维也纳，这是为了在有必要的时候来证明公司已经支付了大笔的钱。 I noticed, too, that Nucingen had sent bills for large amounts to Amsterdam, London, Naples, and Vienna, in order to prove if necessary that large sums had been paid away by the firm.
我们怎样才能得到那些钱呢？” How could we get possession of those bills?”
欧仁听见地板上砰的一声，很沉重，高老头一定是跪在地上了。 Eugene heard a dull thud on the floor; Father Goriot must have fallen on his knees.
“上帝啊！我做了什么事冒犯了您？ “Great heavens! what have I done to you?
女儿竟然落到这个恶棍的手里，任他随意摆布！——哦！我的孩子，我的孩子！原谅我吧！”老人哭着喊道。 Bound my daughter to this scoundrel who does as he likes with her!—Oh! my child, my child! forgive me!” cried the old man.
“是的，如果我掉进绝望的深渊，也许是该责备您。”德尔菲娜说， “Yes, if I am in the depths of despair, perhaps you are to blame,” said Delphine.
“我们结婚的时候都没有多少判断力！ “We have so little sense when we marry!
对世界、生意、男人或生活我们知道些什么？ What do we know of the world, of business, or men, or life?
我们的父亲应该为我们着想！ Our fathers should think for us!
亲爱的父亲，我完全没有责怪您的意思，请原谅我刚刚说的话。 Father dear, I am not blaming you in the least, forgive me for what I said.
这全是我自己的错。 This is all my own fault.
不，不要哭，爸爸。”她说着亲吻了父亲。 Nay, do not cry, papa,” she said, kissing him.
“我亲爱的小德尔菲娜，你也不要哭了。 “Do not cry either, my little Delphine.
抬起头来，让我亲掉你的眼泪。 Look up and let me kiss away the tears.
好了！我要好好想想，解决你丈夫造成的一大堆麻烦。” There! I shall find my wits and unravel this skein of your husband’s winding.”
“不，还是让我自己解决吧，我应该能对付他。 “No, let me do that; I shall be able to manage him.
他一直都很喜欢我，对我也很好。我会利用我的影响让他把我的钱尽快以我的名义投资到不动产上。 He is fond of me, well and good; I shall use my influence to make him invest my money as soon as possible in landed property in my own name.
我很有可能会让他以我的名义买回纽沁根家族在阿尔萨斯的田地，这一直是他的小心愿。 Very likely I could get him to buy back Nucingen in Alsace in my name; that has always been a pet idea of his.
不过，您明天还是过来仔细看看账目，仔细查查业务吧。 Still, come to-morrow and go through the books, and look into the business.
德维尔先生对商业上的事情一无所知。 M. Derville knows little of mercantile matters.
不，还是不要明天了。 No, not to-morrow though.
我不想让自己心烦意乱。 I do not want to be upset.
后天德伯桑夫人要举行舞会，我得保持平静，好调养得精神饱满，展现出最好的状态，给我亲爱的欧仁挣面子！……来，我们看看他的房间！” Mme. de Beauseant’s ball will be the day after to-morrow, and I must keep quiet, so as to look my best and freshest, and do honor to my dear Eugene!...Come, let us see his room.”
但是，正当她说着的时候，一辆马车停在新圣热讷维耶沃街上，楼梯上传来了德雷斯多夫人的声音。 But as she spoke a carriage stopped in the Rue Nueve-Sainte-Genevieve, and the sound of Mme. de Restaud’s voice came from the staircase.
“我父亲在吗？”她问西尔维。 “Is my father in?” she asked of Sylvie.
这意外事件倒是恰到好处，欧仁幸运地以此为自己解了围，他本来是打算倒到床上装睡的。 This accident was luckily timed for Eugene, whose one idea had been to throw himself down on the bed and pretend to be asleep.
“哦，父亲，您听说阿纳斯塔谢的消息没有？”德尔菲娜听见姐姐说话的时候问， “Oh, father, have you heard about Anastasie?” said Delphine, when she heard her sister speak.
“她家里看上去似乎发生了一些不同寻常的事情。” “It looks as though some strange things had happened in that family.”
“什么事情？”高老头问， “What sort of things?” asked Goriot.
“这就像是我的死期。 “This is like to be the death of me.
真是祸不单行，可怜我的头会受不了的。” My poor head will not stand a double misfortune.”
“早上好，父亲！”伯爵夫人进门的时候说， “Good-morning, father,” said the Countess from the threshold.
“哦！德尔菲娜，你在这里啊？” “Oh! Delphine, are you here?”
德雷斯多夫人看见自己妹妹在这里似乎有点吃惊。 Mme. de Restaud seemed taken aback by her sister’s presence.
“早上好，纳西！”男爵夫人说， “Good-morning, Nasie,” said the Baroness.
“我在这里有什么奇怪的啊？ “What is there so extraordinary in my being here?
我每天都来看我们的父亲啊。” I see our father every day.”
“从什么时候开始的？” “Since when?”
“如果你自己来的话，你就会知道了。” “If you came yourself you would know.”
“别开玩笑了，德尔菲娜。”伯爵夫人不耐烦地说， “Don’t tease, Delphine,” said the Countess fretfully.
“我很可怜，我很迷茫。 “I am very miserable, I am lost.
哦！我可怜的父亲，这次真是没有希望了！” Oh! my poor father, it is hopeless this time!”
“怎么了，纳西？”高老头问道， “What is it, Nasie?” cried Goriot.
“孩子，告诉我们所有的一切吧！ “Tell us all about it, child!
她的脸色多白啊！ How white she is!
快点，做点什么，德尔菲娜，对她好些。如果可能的话，我会更加爱你的。” Quick, do something, Delphine; be kind to her, and I will love you even better, if that were possible.”
“可怜的纳西！”德纽沁根夫人说着把姐姐拉到椅子上坐下， “Poor Nasie!” said Mme. de Nucingen, drawing her sister to a chair.
“这世上只有我们两个人的爱能够永远原谅你的一切过失。 “We are the only two people in the world whose love is always sufficient to forgive you everything.
瞧见了吧，亲情才是最稳当的。” Family affection is the surest, you see.”
伯爵夫人听了这些话后振作了起来。 The Countess inhaled the salts and revived.
“这会杀了我的！”她们的父亲的说。 “This will kill me!” said their father.
“好了，”他拨着奄奄一息的炭火继续说，“你们俩都坐近些吧。 “There,” he went on, stirring the smoldering fire, “come nearer, both of you.
很冷的。 It is cold.
怎么回事，纳西？ What is it, Nasie?
快点告诉我。这都足以——”“好吧。我丈夫知道了一切。”伯爵夫人说， Be quick and tell me, this is enough to—”“Well, then, my husband knows everything,” said the Countess.
“想想看，父亲，您记得不久前马克西姆的那张票据吗？ “Just imagine it; do you remember, father, that bill of Maxime’s some time ago?
唉，那不是第一笔债。 Well, that was not the first.
之前我已经还过很多次了。 I had paid ever so many before that.
一月初，德特拉尔先生看上去愁眉苦脸的。他什么也没对我说。但是爱人的心思很容易看透——一个小细节就够了——而且你凭直觉就能感到发生了什么事情。 About the beginning of January M. de Trailles seemed very much troubled. He said nothing to me; but it is so easy to read the hearts of those you love, a mere trifle is enough; and then you feel things instinctively.
实际上，他比以往更温柔、更深情了，我也比以前更快乐了。 Indeed, he was more tender and affectionate than ever, and I was happier than I had ever been before.
可怜的马克西姆！他后来告诉我，他真的打算和我诀别，把自己的脑袋打开花！ Poor Maxime! in himself he was really saying good-bye to me, so he has told me since; he meant to blow his brains out!
最后，我很担心他，于是苦苦乞求和哀求。我在他面前跪了两个小时，恳求他，乞求他，他终于告诉我——他欠了十万法郎的债务。 At last I worried him so, and begged and implored so hard; for two hours I knelt at his knees and prayed and entreated, and at last he told me—that he owed a hundred thousand francs.
哦！爸爸！十万法郎！ Oh! papa! a hundred thousand francs!
我简直不敢想象！ I was beside myself!
我知道您没有那么多钱，我把您的钱都花光了——”“是的，”高里奥说，“我无法给你筹到那么多钱，除非去偷。 You had not the money, I knew, I had eaten up all that you had—” “No,” said Goriot; “I could not have got it for you unless I had stolen it.
但是为了你，我会去偷的，纳西！ But I would have done that for you, Nasie!
我是会去偷的。” I will do it yet.”
他的话从喉咙里出来好像呜咽一般，嘶哑的声音好比人临终之前痛苦的呻吟。当父爱无能为力的时候，看上去的确就像是垂死挣扎。 The words came from him like a sob, a hoarse sound like the death rattle of a dying man; it seemed indeed like the agony of death when the father’s love was powerless.
他停了一下，两姐妹都没吭声。 There was a pause, and neither of the sisters spoke.
如果有人听了这么痛苦的声音还无动于衷的话，那他一定是自私自利之人。这种声音就像扔下悬崖的鹅卵石，显出了高老头的痛苦之深。 It must have been selfishness indeed that could hear unmoved that cry of anguish that, like a pebble thrown over a precipice, revealed the depths of his despair.
“父亲，我卖掉了不属于我的东西筹到了一些钱。”伯爵夫人大哭起来。 “I found the money, father, by selling what was not mine to sell,” and the Countess burst into tears.
德尔菲娜被感动了，她把头靠在姐姐的肩膀上，也哭了起来。 Delphine was touched; she laid her head on her sister’s shoulder, and cried too.
“那么这一切都是真的了？”她说。 “Then it is all true,” she said.
阿纳斯塔谢低下了头，德纽沁根夫人抱着她，温柔地亲吻她，把姐姐搂在胸前。 Anastasie bowed her head, Mme. de Nucingen flung her arms about her, kissed her tenderly, and held her sister to her heart.
“我会一直爱你，不会指责你的，纳西。”她说。 “I shall always love you and never judge you, Nasie,” she said.
“我的天使们，”高老头有气无力地嘟囔道， “My angels,” murmured Goriot faintly.
“哦，为什么到了大难临头的时候才肯和好呢？” “Oh, why should it be trouble that draws you together?”
这种温暖、令人感动的关怀似乎给了伯爵夫人勇气。 This warm and palpitating affection seemed to give the Countess courage.
“为了救马克西姆的性命，”她说，“为了挽救我所有的幸福，我去找了你们认识的放债人，那个地狱之火锻造的、铁石心肠的人，任何事都不能感动他。我把德雷斯多先生引以为豪的所有家传钻石——他的和我自己的——都卖给了那个戈布塞克先生。 “To save Maxime’s life,” she said, “to save all my own happiness, I went to the money-lender you know of, a man of iron forged in hell-fire; nothing can melt him; I took all the family diamonds that M. de Restaud is so proud of—his and mine too—and sold them to that M. Gobseck.
把它们都卖了！你们明白吗？我救了马克西姆，但是我一无所有了。 Sold them.Do you understand?I saved Maxime, but I am lost.
雷斯多全知道了。” Restaud found it all out.”
“他怎么知道的？ “How?
谁告诉他的？ Who told him?
我要杀了他。”高老头大声说。 I will kill him,” cried Goriot.
“昨天他叫我去他的房间。我去了……‘阿纳斯塔谢，’他的声音不对——哦！这样的声音，够了，他的声音把一切都告诉我了，‘你的钻石都上哪里去了？’——‘在我房间里——’——‘不对，’他直视着我说，‘它们明明放在那边的五斗橱里——’他拿起手帕，给我看首饰盒。‘你知道它们从哪里来的吗？’他说。我跪到他的脚下……我哭了起来，问他想要我怎么死。” “Yesterday he sent to tell me to come to his room.I went…‘Anastasie,’ he said in a voice—Oh! such a voice; that was enough, it told me everything—‘where are your diamonds?’—‘In my room—’—‘No,’ he said, looking straight at me, ‘there they are on that chest of drawers—’ and he lifted his handkerchief and showed me the casket.‘Do you know where they came from?’ he said.I fell at his feet…I cried; I besought him to tell me the death he wished to see me die.”
“你说了那话！”高老头大叫， “You said that!” cried Goriot.
“上帝在上，只要我活着，谁欺负了你们任何一个人，他们就等着被火慢慢烤吧！ “By God in heaven, whoever lays a hand on either of you so long as I am alive may reckon on being roasted by slow fires!
是的，我要把他切成一块一块的，就像……” Yes, I will cut him in pieces like...”
高老头停了下来，话都到了嘴边又咽了回去。 Goriot stopped; the words died away in his throat.
“哎呀，他这可是要我做比死还难受的事啊。 “And then, dear, he asked something worse than death of me.
哦！但愿其他所有的女人都不会听到我听过的那些话啊！” Oh! heaven preserve all other women from hearing such words as I heard then!”
“我要杀了他。”高老头平静地说， “I will murder that man,” said Goriot quietly.
“要不是他只有一条命，他简直应该死两次——他接下来说了什么？”他看着阿纳斯塔谢又问道。 “But he has only one life, and he deserves to die twice.—And then, what next?” he added, looking at Anastasie.
“然后，”伯爵夫人继续说，“他停了下来看着我。 “Then,” the Countess resumed, “there was a pause, and he looked at me.
‘阿纳斯塔谢，’他说，‘我可以不追究这件事，和你继续住在一起，毕竟我们有孩子。 ‘Anastasie,’ he said, ‘I will bury this in silence; there shall be no separation; there are the children.
我不会杀了德特拉尔先生的。 I will not kill M. de Trailles.
如果决斗的话，我不一定能得手。要是通过别的方式除去他，我就会触犯法律。 I might miss him if we fought, and as for other ways of getting rid of him, I should come into collision with the law.
如果我在你的怀抱里杀掉他的话，就会让那些孩子蒙羞。 If I killed him in your arms, it would bring dishonor on @those@ children.
但是如果你不想看着孩子们死，不想看着他们的父亲死，不想看着我死，你首先必须遵守两个条件。 But if you do not want to see your children perish, nor their father nor me, you must first of all submit to two conditions.
回答我。 Answer me.
孩子中有没有我亲生的？’我回答，‘有。’——‘哪一个？’——‘埃内斯特，我们的长子。’——‘很好，’他说，‘现在发誓从这一刻开始服从我一件事。’我发了誓。 Have I a child of my own?’I answered, ‘Yes,’—‘Which?’—‘Ernest, our eldest boy.’—‘Very well,’ he said, ‘and now swear to obey me in this particular from this time forward.’ I swore.
‘我要求你把你的财产都转让给我。’”“千万别那样做！”高老头大声说， ‘You will make over your property to me when I require you to do so.’”“Do nothing of the kind!” cried Goriot.
“啊哈！德雷斯多先生，你不能让妻子快乐，她就自己寻找快乐，并在别的地方找到了，你还让她因为你自己的不称职而受罪？ “Aha! M. de Restaud, you could not make your wife happy; she has looked for happiness and found it elsewhere, and you make her suffer for your own ineptitude?
你就等着我去收拾你吧。 He will have to reckon with me.
别担心，纳西。 Make yourself easy, Nasie.
啊哈！他关心自己的继承人！ Aha! he cares about his heir!
很好，非常好。 Good, very good.
我会抓住那个孩子的。他不也是我外孙吗？ I will get hold of the boy; isn’t he my grandson?
我到底在想些什么啊！ What the blazes!
我定能去看看那小家伙！ I can surely go to see the brat!
我会把他偷偷藏在某个地方。我会照顾他的，你可以彻底放心。 I will stow him away somewhere; I will take care of him, you may be quite easy.
我会和雷斯多达成协议，这个魔鬼！ I will bring Restaud to terms, the monster!
我会对他说，‘我只跟你说一两句话！ I shall say to him, ‘A word or two with you!
如果你想要回儿子，就把我女儿的财产还给她，让她做自己喜欢的事。’”“父亲！” If you want your son back again, give my daughter her property, and leave her to do as she pleases.’”“Father!”
“是的。 “Yes.
纳西，我是你的父亲，一个真正的父亲！ I am your father, Nasie, a father indeed!
那个贵族流氓最好不要伤害我的女儿。 That rogue of a great lord had better not ill-treat my daughter.
天打雷劈！我的血管里流的到底是什么？ Tonnerre! What is it in my veins?
我身体里有老虎的血，我可以把那两个人撕成碎片！ There is the blood of a tiger in me; I could tear those two men to pieces!
哦！孩子们，孩子们！这就是你们过的生活啊！ Oh! children, children! so this is what your lives are!
哎呀，这简直是生不如死啊！……我死了的话，你们会变成什么样啊？ Why, it is death!...What will become of you when I shall be here no longer?
父亲应该和他们的孩子活得一样长久。 Fathers ought to live as long as their children.
啊！上帝啊！您把这世界弄得多糟啊！ Ah! Lord God in heaven! how ill Thy world is ordered!
如果他们的话不假，您自己也有个儿子，可是您却让我们在子女身上如此受罪。 Thou hast a Son, if what they tell us is true, and yet Thou leavest us to suffer so through our children.
我亲爱的女儿们，我亲爱的女儿们！ My darlings, my darlings!
想想看，你们只在遇到麻烦的时候才会来看我，所以我只能看到你们泪流满面的样子！ To think that trouble only should bring you to me, that I should only see you with tears on your faces!
啊！是的，是的，你们爱我，我知道你们是爱我的。 Ah! yes, yes, you love me, I see that you love me.
来找我倾诉你们的伤心事吧，我的心足够大，什么都容得下。 Come to me and pour out your griefs to me; my heart is large enough to hold them all.
哦！你们也许会把我的心撕成碎片，但是每一个碎片都会成为一个父亲的心。 Oh! you might rend my heart in pieces, and every fragment would make a father’s heart.
要是我能为你们承担所有的痛苦就好了！……啊！你们小时候、仍然和我住在一起的时候是多么开心啊……” If only I could bear all your sorrows for you!...Ah! you were so happy when you were little and still with me…”
“打那以后我们从来都没有开心过。”德尔菲娜说， “We have never been happy since,” said Delphine.
“我们过去在大谷仓的面粉袋上打滚的日子到哪里去了？” “Where are the old days when we slid down the sacks in the great granary?”
“父亲，事情还没完呢。”阿纳斯塔谢在高老头的耳旁说。 “That is not all, father,” said Anastasie in Goriot’s ear.
老人吓得发起抖来。 The old man gave a startled shudder.
“钻石只卖了十万法郎。 “The diamonds only sold for a hundred thousand francs.
马克西姆被逼得很紧。 Maxime is hard pressed.
我们还差一万两千法郎。 There are twelve thousand francs still to pay.
他已经承诺我将来会安定下来，放弃赌博。 He has given me his word that he will be steady and give up play in future.
除了他的爱，我在这个世上一无所有了。 His love is all that I have left in the world.
我已经为此付出了如此可怕的代价，要是我现在失去他，我会死的。 I have paid such a fearful price for it that I should die if I lose him now.
我为了他已经牺牲了财产、名誉、内心的平静和我的孩子。 I have sacrificed my fortune, my honor, my peace of mind, and my children for him.
哦！父亲，做点什么吧，那样马克西姆至少可以免于刑罚、体面地活在世上。他以后一定会打拼出一番事业的。 Oh! do something, so that at the least Maxime may be at large and live undisgraced in the world, where he will assuredly make a career for himself.
比我的幸福更重要的东西正面临着危险，孩子们会一无所有。如果他被送到圣佩拉吉监狱，他所有的前途就毁了。” Something more than my happiness is at stake; the children have nothing, and if he is sent to Sainte-Pelagie all his prospects will be ruined.”
“我没有这笔钱，纳西。 “I haven’t the money, Nasie.
我什么也没有——什么也没剩下了。 I have @nothing@—nothing left.
这真是世界末日啊。 This is the end of everything.
是的，这世界正在分崩离析，我肯定。 Yes, the world is crumbling into ruin, I am sure.
逃跑吧！ Fly!
自己救自己吧！ Save yourselves!
啊！——我还有银搭扣，半打银调羹和叉子，这些是我人生中第一次买的银制品。 Ah!—I have still my silver buckles left, and half-a-dozen silver spoons and forks, the first I ever had in my life.
但是，除了我那一千二百法郎的终身年金，我什么都没有了……” But I have nothing else except my life annuity, twelve hundred francs...”
“可您的长期公债去哪里了？” “Then what has become of your money in the funds?”
“我卖掉了，只留下一小笔生活费。 “I sold out, and only kept a trifle for my wants.
我需要一万两千法郎替德尔菲娜装修几个房间。” I wanted twelve thousand francs to furnish some rooms for Delphine.”
“在你家里的房间吗？”德雷斯多夫人看着妹妹问道。 “In your own house?” asked Mme. de Restaud, looking at her sister.
“房间在哪里有什么关系？”高老头问， “What does it matter where they were?” asked Goriot.
“反正钱现在是花了。” “The money is spent now.”
“我明白了，”伯爵夫人说， “I see how it is,” said the Countess.

可怜的德尔菲娜，一定要吸取我的教训啊！” Poor Delphine, take warning by me!”
“亲爱的，德拉斯蒂涅先生是不会毁了自己心爱的人的。” “M. de Rastignac is incapable of ruining the woman he loves, dear.”

我以为在危机关头你会对我好些，但是你从来没有真心爱过我。” I thought you would have been kinder to me in my troubles, but you never did love me.”
“不，不，纳西，她是爱你的。”高老头大叫，“她刚刚还这样说了。 “Yes, yes, she loves you, Nasie,” cried Goriot; “she was saying so only just now.
我们谈到你的时候，她强调你很美丽，而她自己只不过是好看而已！” We were talking about you, and she insisted that you were beautiful, and that she herself was only pretty!”
“好看！”伯爵夫人说， “Pretty!” said the Countess.
“她和大理石雕像一样冷酷无情。” “She is as hard as a marble statue.”
“我是那样的吗？”德尔菲娜红着脸大声说，“你是怎么对我的呢？ “And if I am?” cried Delphine, flushing up, “how have you treated me?
你不认我这个妹妹，还让其他所有人都不理睬我；你从来都不会放弃任何羞辱我的机会。 You would not recognize me; you closed the doors of every house against me; you have never let an opportunity of mortifying me slip by.
你每过来一次就要一千法郎，榨干了我们可怜的父亲。你看他现在都变成什么样子了，我是这样的吗？ And when did I come, as you were always doing, to drain our poor father, a thousand francs at a time, till he is left as you see him now?
这可都是你干的，姐姐！ That is all your doing, sister!
我自己可是尽可能多地来看望父亲。 I myself have seen my father as often as I could.
我可没把他撵出门外，等到需要钱的时候又来讨好他。 I have not turned him out of the house, and then come and fawned upon him when I wanted money.
我甚至不知道他为我花了一万两千法郎。 I did not so much as know that he had spent those twelve thousand francs on me.
你知道的，我很节俭。爸爸送我礼物从来都不是因为我来向他讨要的。” I am economical, as you know; and when papa has made me presents, it has never been because I came and begged for them.”
“你的境况比我好。 “You were better off than I.
你肚子里明白，德马尔塞先生有钱。 M. de Marsay was rich, as you have reason to know.
你总是和黄金一样不可靠。 You always were as slippery as gold.
再见！我没有妹妹，也没有——”“哦！别说了，别说了，纳西！”她的父亲大叫道。 Good-bye; I have neither sister nor—” “Oh! hush, hush, Nasie!” cried her father.
“除了你，没有人会重复人人都不再相信的话。 “Nobody else would repeat what everybody has ceased to believe.
你简直是个不正常的姐姐！”德尔菲娜大叫。 You are an unnatural sister!” cried Delphine.
“哦，孩子们，孩子们！别说了！别说了！要不我就死在你们的面前。” “Oh, children, children! hush! hush! or I will kill myself before your eyes.”
“好吧，纳西，我原谅你。”德纽沁根夫人说，“你很不开心。 “There, Nasie, I forgive you,” said Mme. de Nucingen; “you are very unhappy.
但我比你要和善。 But I am kinder than you are.
我准备竭尽全力帮助你的时候，你怎么能说出那样的话，我甚至都准备向我丈夫妥协了。要是为了我自己，我绝对——哦！这就是你的作风，你这九年来一直对我很残忍。” How could you say @that@ just when I was ready to do anything in the world to help you, even to be reconciled with my husband, which for my own sake I—Oh! it is just like you; you have behaved cruelly to me all through these nine years.”
“孩子们，孩子们，你们快亲吻对方和好吧！”父亲大声说， “Children, children, kiss each other!” cried the father.
“你们是我的天使，你们俩都是。” “You are angels, both of you.”
“不！ “No.
你松手。”伯爵夫人甩掉父亲放在她胳膊上的手，大声说， Let me alone,” cried the Countess shaking off the hand that her father had laid on her arm.
“她比我丈夫更残忍。 “She is more merciless than my husband.
不过有人也许还会认为她集所有美德于一身呢！” Any one might think she was a model of all the virtues herself!”
“我宁可让人认为我欠德马尔塞先生的钱，也不愿意承认德特拉尔先生花了我二十多万法郎。”德纽沁根夫人反驳道。 “I would rather have people think that I owed money to M. de Marsay than own that M. de Trailles had cost me more than two hundred thousand francs,” retorted Mme. de Nucingen.
“德尔菲娜！”伯爵夫人走向妹妹大声说， “@Delphine!@” cried the Countess, stepping towards her sister.

“德尔菲娜！你是一个——”高老头快速走到她们之间，抓住伯爵夫人的手，把自己的手盖到了她的嘴上。 “Delphine! you are a—”Father Goriot sprang between them, grasped the Countess’ hand, and laid his own over her mouth.
“老天啊，父亲！ “Good heavens, father!
您今天早上用手拿过什么了？”阿纳斯塔谢说。 What have you been handling this morning?” said Anastasie.
“啊！是的，是的，我不应该碰你。”可怜的父亲说着在裤子上擦了擦手，“我刚才一直在收拾东西，我不知道你要来看我。” “Ah! well, yes, I ought not to have touched you,” said the poor father, wiping his hands on his trousers, “but I have been packing up my things; I did not know that you were coming to see me.”
他很高兴把女儿的怒气转到了自己的身上。 He was glad that he had drawn down her wrath upon himself.
“唉！”他叹了叹气坐了下来，“孩子们，你们俩已经伤了我的心。 “Ah!” he sighed, as he sat down, “you children have broken my heart between you.
这简直是要我的命。 This is killing me.
我觉得我的脑袋里好像有团火在燃烧似的。 My head feels as if it were on fire.
你们要和和气气、相亲相爱！ Be good to each other and love each other!
这会要了我的命的！ This will be the death of me!
德尔菲娜！纳西！别这样，你们得理智些，你们俩都有错。 Delphine! Nasie! come, be sensible; you are both in the wrong.
别这样，德尔。”他含泪看着男爵夫人,又说道，“你看，她必须得要一万两千法郎。我们张罗一下看看能不能筹到。 Come, Dedel,” he added, looking through his tears at the Baroness, “she must have twelve thousand francs, you see; let us see if we can find them for her.
哦，我的女儿们，不要那样看着对方！”他跪到了德尔菲娜的旁边。 Oh, my girls, do not look at each other like that!”And he sank on his knees beside Delphine.
“请她原谅你——就当是为了让我高兴。”他在她的耳边说， “Ask her to forgive you—just to please me,” he said in her ear.
“她比你更可怜。 “She is more miserable than you are.
说啊，就现在，德尔。” Come now, Dedel.”
“可怜的纳西！”德尔菲娜被父亲脸上流露的、无比的悲伤神情给吓着了，说道，“我错了，吻我吧——”“啊！这就像是抚慰我心灵的妙药啊。”高老头大声说， “Poor Nasie!” said Delphine, alarmed at the wild extravagant grief in her father’s face, “I was in the wrong, kiss me—” “Ah! that is like balm to my heart,” cried Father Goriot.
“但我们怎么才能筹到一万两千法郎呢？ “But how are we to find twelve thousand francs?
也许我可以替别人服兵役——”“哦！亲爱的父亲！”她们一齐大叫着抱住他， I might offer myself as a substitute in the army—” “Oh! father dear!” they both cried, flinging their arms about him.
“不，不要！” “No, no!”
“愿上帝赐福给你这个高尚的想法。 “God reward you for the thought.
可是我们不值得您这样做，是吧，纳西？”德尔菲娜问。 We are not worth it, are we, Nasie?” asked Delphine.
“而且除此之外，亲爱的父亲，这样所挣到的钱也只是杯水车薪。”伯爵夫人说道。 “And besides, father dear, it would only be a drop in the bucket,” observed the Countess.
“但是这幅血肉之躯什么都不值吗？”老人绝望地大叫， “But is flesh and blood worth nothing?” cried the old man in his despair.
“纳西，为了救你，我愿意献出自己的身体和灵魂。 “I would give body and soul to save you, Nasie.
如果有人肯救你，我可以为他去杀人。 I would do a murder for the man who would rescue you.
我会像沃尔特兰一样去监狱，去——”他停了下来，仿佛被雷击中了一般，把两只手放到头上。 I would do, as Vautrin did, go to the hulks, go—” he stopped as if struck by a thunderbolt, and put both hands to his head.
“什么也没有了！”他抓着自己的头发大叫， “Nothing left!” he cried, tearing his hair.
“要是我知道偷钱的办法就好了。但是偷钱太难了，而且不能单独行动，抢银行又得花时间。 “If I only knew of a way to steal money, but it is so hard to do it, and then you can’t set to work by yourself, and it takes time to rob a bank.
