是的，我应该去死。除了死，我什么也做不了。 Yes, it is time I was dead; there is nothing left me to do but to die.
我在这世上一无是处！我不再是父亲了！ I am no good in the world; I am no longer a father!
不是了。 No.
她在绝境中来找我，而我是个不幸的人，我什么也给不了她。 She has come to me in her extremity, and, wretch that I am, I have nothing to give her.
啊！老混蛋，你把钱存了终身年金，难道你没有女儿吗？ Ah! you put your money into a life annuity, old scoundrel; and had you not daughters?
你根本不爱她们。 You did not love them.
死吧，像狗一样死在阴沟里吧！对，你就是狗！ Die, die in a ditch, like the dog that you are!
不，我连狗都不如，畜生都不会像我这样做！ Yes, I am worse than a dog; a beast would not have done as I have done!
哦！我的头……胀痛得似乎要爆炸了。” Oh! my head...It throbs as if it would burst.”
“爸爸！”两位年轻的女士立刻大叫，“求您了，一定要理智些！” “Papa!” cried both the young women at once, “do, pray, be reasonable!”
姐妹俩拦着他，不让他把脑袋往墙上撞。 And they clung to him to prevent him from dashing his head against the wall.
他哭了起来。 There was a sound of sobbing.
欧仁吓坏了，他拿起沃尔特兰签过名的支票，发现上面的印花足以支付更大的一笔钱，就改了改数目，写上高里奥的抬头，把它做成一张一万两千法郎的平常票据，然后去了邻居的房间。 Eugene, greatly alarmed, took the bill that bore Vautrin’s signature, saw that the stamp would suffice for a larger sum, altered the figures, made it into a regular bill for twelve thousand francs, payable to Goriot’s order, and went to his neighbor’s room.
“这里有钱，夫人。”他说着把这张纸交给她， “Here is the money, madame,” he said, handing the piece of paper to her.
“我刚才正在睡觉，你们的谈话吵醒了我。就这样，我想起自己还欠高里奥先生的钱。 “I was asleep; your conversation awoke me, and by this means I learned all that I owed to M. Goriot.
这张支票可以贴现，我到时会准时还钱的。” This bill can be discounted, and I shall meet it punctually at the due date.”
伯爵夫人哑口无言，一动不动地站在原地，她手里却攥着那张支票。 The Countess stood motionless and speechless, but she held the bill in her fingers.
“德尔菲娜，”她脸色惨白，因为恼怒、生气、愤怒而浑身颤抖，说，“我什么都能原谅你，上帝可以为我作证，我原谅你了。但是，我不能原谅这个！ “Delphine,” she said, with a white face, and her whole frame quivering with indignation, anger, and rage, “I forgave you everything; God is my witness that I forgave you, but I cannot forgive this!
这么说，这位绅士一直都在那里，你事先知道吧！ So this gentleman was there all the time, and you knew it!
你太卑鄙了，为了报复我，竟然不惜泄露我的秘密、我的生活、我孩子们的生活、我的耻辱、我的名誉！ Your petty spite has let you to wreak your vengeance on me by betraying my secrets, my life, my children’s lives, my shame, my honor!
好吧，我跟你从此一刀两断。 There, you are nothing to me any longer.
我恨你。 I hate you.
我会想尽一切办法来伤害你。 I will do all that I can to injure you.
我会……” I will...”
她气得都说不出话了，喉咙又干又热。 Anger paralyzed her; the words died in her dry parched throat.
“啊，他是我的儿子、我的孩子，是你的兄弟、你的救星啊！”高老头大叫， “Why, he is my son, my child; he is your brother, your preserver!” cried Goriot.
“快吻他的手，纳西！ “Kiss his hand, Nasie!
等一下，我先拥抱他吧。”他说着拼命把欧仁紧紧抱到胸前， Stay, I will embrace him myself,” he said, straining Eugene to his breast in a frenzied clasp.
“哦，我的孩子！ “Oh my boy!
我不仅仅要当你的父亲，我会比父亲更爱你的。如果我有上帝的力量，我会把世界都丢在你的脚下。 I will be more than a father to you; if I had God’s power, I would fling worlds at your feet.
纳西，你为什么不吻他？ Why don’t you kiss him, Nasie?
他不是凡人，而是天使，来自天堂的天使。” He is not a man, but an angel, a angel out of heaven.”
“父亲，别管她，她现在疯了。” “Never mind her, father; she is mad just now.”
“疯了！是吗？ “Mad! am I?
你又是什么东西呢？”德雷斯多夫人大叫。 And what are you?” cried Mme. de Restaud.
“孩子们，孩子们，你们要是继续这样，我就要死了。”老人大叫着，摇摇晃晃地倒在了床上，像中了子弹似的——“她们正在把我往死里逼啊。”他自言自语道。 “Children, children, I shall die if you go on like this,” cried the old man, and he staggered and fell on the bed as if a bullet had struck him.—“They are killing me between them,” he said to himself.
欧仁被剧烈的争吵弄得不知所措，他一动不动地愣在那里，被伯爵夫人盯着。 The Countess fixed her eyes on Eugene, who stood stock still; all his faculties were numbed by this violent scene.
“先生……”她说道，神情、声音和举止都显出疑惑和质询，既没在意父亲也没在意正在急急忙忙给父亲解开背心的德尔菲娜。 “Sir?...” she said, doubt and inquiry in her face, tone, and bearing; she took no notice now of her father nor of Delphine, who was hastily unfastening his waistcoat.
“夫人，”欧仁在她问问题之前就答道，“我会付钱的，而且会对此保密的。” “Madame,” said Eugene, answering the question before it was asked, “I will meet the bill, and keep silence about it.”
“纳西，你把父亲逼死了！”德尔菲娜指着躺在床上不省人事的高老头说道。 “You have killed our father, Nasie!” said Delphine, pointing to Goriot, who lay unconscious on the bed.
伯爵夫人逃走了。 The Countess fled.
“我完全原谅她。”老人张开眼睛说，“她的处境很可怕，比她有经验的人也承受不住。 “I freely forgive her,” said the old man, opening his eyes; “her position is horrible; it would turn an older head than hers.
德尔菲娜，你要安慰纳西，对她好些。你得答应你可怜的父亲，答应你快死的父亲。”他抽搐着紧紧握住德尔菲娜的手，说道。 Comfort Nasie, and be nice to her, Delphine; promise it to your poor father before he dies,” he asked, holding Delphine’s hand in a convulsive clasp.
“哦！父亲，你生了什么病啊？”她真的吓着了，哭着问道。 “Oh! what ails you, father?” she cried in real alarm.
“没事，没事，”高老头说，“会好起来的。 “Nothing, nothing,” said Goriot; “it will go off.
有什么东西压着我的额头，好重，有一点头痛…… There is something heavy pressing on my forehead, a little headache…
啊！可怜的纳西，她将来要过怎样的生活啊！” Ah! poor Nasie, what a life lies before her!”
正当他说话的时候，伯爵夫人回来了，她扑到父亲的面前跪下。 Just as he spoke, the Countess came back again and flung herself on her knees before him.
“原谅我吧！”她哭着说道。 “Forgive me!” she cried.
“过来，”她的父亲说，“你现在叫我越发难受了。” “Come,” said her father, “you are hurting me still more.”
“先生，”伯爵夫人转身对拉斯蒂涅说，“悲惨的遭遇让我昏了头，错怪了你。 “Monsieur,” the Countess said, turning to Rastignac, “misery made me unjust to you.
你会成为我的兄弟，是吗？” You will be a brother to me, will you not?”
她伸出了手。 And she held out her hand.
她说话的时候眼中含满了泪水。 Her eyes were full of tears as she spoke.
“纳西，”德尔菲娜抱着姐姐，哭着说道，“我的小纳西，我们忘记一切，原谅对方吧。” “Nasie,” cried Delphine, flinging her arms round her sister, “my little Nasie, let us forget and forgive.”
“不，不，”纳西大声说，“我绝不会忘记的！” “No, no,” cried Nasie; “I shall never forget!”
“亲爱的天使们，”高老头大叫，“挡在我眼前的黑色窗帘好像被拉起来了，你们的声音让我起死回生了。 “Dear angels,” cried Goriot, “it is as if a dark curtain over my eyes had been raised; your voices have called me back to life.
你们再亲吻对方一次吧。 Kiss each other once more.
纳西，现在那张支票会解救你的，不是吗？” Well, now, Nasie, that bill will save you, won’t it?”
“希望如此。 “I hope so.
喂，爸爸，你可不可以把你的名字写在上面？” I say, papa, will you write your name on it?”
“哦，对了！我好蠢啊，怎么把那给忘了！ “There! how stupid of me to forget that!
但是，纳西，我一直都感觉不舒服，所以你可千万别因此记恨我啊。 But I am not feeling at all well, Nasie, so you must not remember it against me.
你解决问题后记得马上给我捎个信。 Send and let me know as soon as you are out of your strait.
不，我会到你那里去的。 No, I will go to you.
不，我还是不去了，毕竟去了说不定会遇见你的丈夫，我会当场打死他的。 No, after all, I will not go; I might meet your husband, and I should kill him on the spot.
我是不会同意他把你的财产过户到他的名下的。 And as for signing away your property, I shall have a word to say about that.
快去救马克西姆吧，我的孩子，此后你得让他安定下来。” Quick, my child, and keep Maxime in order in future.”
欧仁不知所措，一句话也说不出。 Eugene was too bewildered to speak.
“可怜的阿纳斯塔谢，她的脾气总是这么暴躁。”德纽沁根夫人说，“但她的心地很善良。” “Poor Anastasie, she always had a violent temper,” said Mme. de Nucingen, “but she has a good heart.”
“她回来是为了得到背书。”欧仁在德尔菲娜的耳旁说道。 “She came back for the endorsement,” said Eugene in Delphine’s ear.
“你这样认为吗？” “Do you think so?”
“我也希望可以不这样想。 “I only wish I could think otherwise.
不要相信她。”他说着抬起头，好像正在向上帝倾诉自己不敢说的想法。 Do not trust her,” he answered, raising his eyes as if he confided to heaven the thoughts that he did not venture to express.
“是的。 “Yes.
她多少有些装腔作势，她总是这样。” She is always acting a part to some extent.”
“您现在觉得怎么样了，亲爱的高老头？”拉斯蒂涅问。 “How do you feel now, dear Father Goriot?” asked Rastignac.
“我就想睡觉。”他答道。 “I should like to go to sleep,” he replied.
欧仁帮他躺下，德尔菲娜坐在床边，握着他的手直到他睡着。 Eugene helped him to bed, and Delphine sat by the bedside, holding his hand until he fell asleep.
然后她走出了高老头的房间。 Then she went.
“今天晚上在意大利剧院等你。”她对欧仁说，“到时候你可以告诉我父亲的情况。 “This evening at the Italiens,” she said to Eugene, “and you can let me know how he is.
先生，明天你就要离开这个地方了。 To-morrow you will leave this place, monsieur.
我们一起去看看你的房间吧——哦！好可怕啊！”她在门口大叫， Let us go into your room.—Oh! how frightful!” she cried on the threshold.
“什么，你住的地方比我们父亲的房间还差啊。 “Why, you are even worse lodged than our father.
欧仁，你刚才太好心了。 Eugene, you have behaved well.
如果可以的话，我要更加爱你。可是，亲爱的孩子，如果你想有所成就，就不能像刚才那样把一万两千法郎扔出窗外。 I would love you more if that were possible; but, dear boy, if you are to succeed in life, you must not begin by flinging twelve thousand francs out of the windows like that.
德特拉尔伯爵是个十足的赌徒。 The Comte de Trailles is a confirmed gambler.
我姐姐对此假装看不见。 My sister shuts her eyes to it.
他会用老办法来挣那一万两千法郎，就像他以前如何赢来和输掉那一座座金山一样。” He would have made the twelve thousand francs in the same way that he wins and loses heaps of gold.”
他们听到隔壁房间传来了呻吟声，就回到了高老头的床边。他看上去睡着了，可是这对情人明明听见他说：“他们过得不开心啊！” A groan from the next room brought them back to Goriot’s bedside; to all appearances he was asleep, but the two lovers caught the words, “They are not happy!”
不管他是醒着还是睡着了，他说话的语气震撼了女儿的心灵。 Whether he was awake or sleeping, the tone in which they were spoken went to his daughter’s heart.
她悄悄走到父亲躺着的简陋的床边，亲吻了父亲的额头。 She stole up to the pallet-bed on which her father lay, and kissed his forehead.
他睁开了眼睛。 He opened his eyes.
“啊！德尔菲娜！”他说。 “Ah! Delphine!” he said.
“您现在感觉怎么样？”她问。 “How are you now?” she asked.
“非常舒服。 “Quite comfortable.
别担心我，我马上就起床了。 Do not worry about me; I shall get up presently.
不要和我呆在一起，孩子们。去吧，去吧，去快活吧。” Don’t stay with me, children; go, go and be happy.”
欧仁把德尔菲娜送回了家，但是他很担心高老头，就没有听从她叫他留在那里吃饭的建议。 Eugene went back with Delphine as far as her door; but he was not easy about Goriot, and would not stay to dinner, as she proposed.
他想回到“沃盖之家”。 He wanted to be back at the Maison Vauquer.
他进门的时候，高老头刚刚离开房间，正坐下准备吃饭。 Father Goriot had left his room, and was just sitting down to dinner as he came in.
比安卡肖恩已经选了个可以仔细观察老人的地方坐下。当年老的面条制造商拿起自己的那块面包嗅一嗅，好判断面粉的质量时，近距离观察他的医科学生看出这完全是个机械式的动作，便摇了摇头。 Bianchon had placed himself where he could watch the old man carefully; and when the old vermicelli maker took up his square of bread and smelled it to find out the quality of the flour, the medical student, studying him closely, saw that the action was purely mechanical, and shook his head.
“过来坐这里，科钦医院的牧师。”欧仁说。 “Just come and sit over here, hospitaler of Cochin,” said Eugene.
比安卡肖恩很乐意换位置，因为那样他就可以坐到老人的旁边了。 Bianchon went the more willingly because his change of place brought him next to the old lodger.
“他得了什么病？”拉斯蒂涅问。 “What is wrong with him?” asked Rastignac.
“如果我没看错的话，他快要死了！ “It is all up with him, or I am much mistaken!
他的身体定是发生了某些非常特别的变化。他看上去似乎有即将脑中风的危险。 Something very extraordinary must have taken place; he looks to me as if he were in imminent danger of serous apoplexy.
他下半边脸还够紧实，可是上半边脸却扭曲变形了。 The lower part of his face is composed enough, but the upper part is drawn and distorted.
他奇怪的眼神也表明血浆已经渗进脑子了。他的眼睛看上去似乎蒙上了一层薄薄的尘土，你注意到了没有？ Then there is that peculiar look about the eyes that indicates an effusion of serum in the brain; they look as though they were covered with a film of fine dust, do you notice?
明天早上我就可以知道得更清楚些。” I shall know more about it by to-morrow morning.”
“他还有救吗？” “Is there any cure for it?”
“没有。 “None.
要是能找到某种方法把反应限制在下肢，他也许还可以多活一段时间。但是，如果症状到明天晚上还不减轻，他就完了。可怜的老家伙！ It might be possible to stave death off for a time if a way could be found of setting up a reaction in the lower extremities; but if the symptoms do not abate by to-morrow evening, it will be all over with him, poor old fellow!
他怎么发病的，你知道吗？ Do you know what has happened to bring this on?
他肯定是受到剧烈的刺激，精神崩溃了。” There must have been some violent shock, and his mind has given way.”
“是的，有过这样的事情。”拉斯蒂涅说着就想起了两个女儿接二连三地打击父亲的心。 “Yes, there was,” said Rastignac, remembering how the two daughters had struck blow on blow at their father’s heart.
“但是无论如何德尔菲娜还是爱她的父亲的。”他自言自语道。 “But Delphine at any rate loves her father,” he said to himself.
那天晚上在剧院的时候，拉斯蒂涅说话很小心，以免给德纽沁根夫人带来不必要的惊慌。 That evening at the opera Rastignac chose his words carefully, lest he should give Mme. de Nucingen needless alarm.
“别担心他。”不过欧仁才刚开始说，她就说道，“我们的父亲真的很强壮，只不过是我们今天早上刺激到他了。 “Do not be anxious about him,” she said, however, as soon as Eugene began, “our father has really a strong constitution, but this morning we gave him a shock.
我们的全部财产危在旦夕，你看，这件事才很严重。 Our whole fortunes were in peril, so the thing was serious, you see.
如果你的爱无法让我对我忘却那些曾经认为无力承担的麻烦，我就活不下去了。 I could not live if your affection did not make me insensible to troubles that I should once have thought too hard to bear.
现在，我只担心一件事，只害怕一个痛苦——失去让我觉得生活很快乐的爱。 At this moment I have but one fear left, but one misery to dread—to lose the love that has made me feel glad to live.
和你的爱相比，其他所有东西对我而言都没有意义。我对其他所有东西都不在意，因为你就是我的整个世界。 Everything else is as nothing to me compared with our love; I care for nothing else, for you are all the world to me.
如果我喜欢富有，那也是为了你。 If I feel glad to be rich, it is for your sake.
说起来很惭愧，我把情人摆在父亲的前面。 To my shame be it said, I think of my lover before my father.
你会问为什么呢？ Do you ask why?
我无法告诉你，但是我的整个生命都在你身上。 I cannot tell you, but all my life is in you.
我的心是父亲给的，却是你让它学会了跳动。 My father gave me a heart, but you have taught it to beat.
也许整个世界都会指责我，但是只要我在你的眼中是无罪的，那又算得了什么。你没有权利指责我，因为不顾一切的爱逼迫我为你犯罪！ The whole world may condemn me; what does it matter if I stand acquitted in your eyes, for you have no right to think ill of me for the faults which a tyrannous love has forced me to commit for you!
你认为我是个丧尽天良的女儿吗？ Do you think me an unnatural daughter?
哦！不，没人能不爱我们那样的好爸爸。 Oh! no, no one could help loving such a dear kind father as ours.
但是，他给我们安排的婚姻如此凄惨，落得这般糟糕的后果；我如何能忘记这一点？ But how could I hide the inevitable consequences of our miserable marriages from him?
当年他为什么不阻止我们结婚？ Why did he allow us to marry when we did?
为我们着想，为我们预见将来不正是他的责任吗？ Was it not his duty to think for us and foresee for us?
现在我知道他和我们一样痛苦，可是我们又能做些什么呢？ To-day I know he suffers as much as we do, but how can it be helped?
至于安慰他，其实我们也安慰不了什么。 And as for comforting him, we could not comfort him in the least.
我们忍气吞声给他带来的痛苦，对他造成的伤害远比抱怨和指责多。 Our resignation would give him more pain and hurt him far more than complaints and upbraidings.
人这一生就是会有事事不顺心的时候。” There are times in life when everything turns to bitterness.”
她朴实、真诚的感情流露令欧仁很感动，他什么也没说。 Eugene was silent, the artless and sincere outpouring made an impression on him.
巴黎女人通常都很虚伪、极其虚荣、自私自利、不顾他人、轻佻而肤浅。但是，任何一个女人只要动了真心，都会为爱情牺牲自己的个人情感；她会上升到能够摆脱一切卑鄙本性的高度，变得高尚起来。 Parisian women are often false, intoxicated with vanity, selfish and self-absorbed, frivolous and shallow; yet of all women, when they love, they sacrifice their personal feelings to their passion; they rise but so much the higher for all the pettiness overcome in their nature, and become sublime.
得到特殊优待的爱情已经使她远离了亲情。欧仁被这个女人在评判亲情时所表现出的深邃洞察力和识别力震撼了。 Then Eugene was struck by the profound discernment and insight displayed by this woman in judging of natural affection, when a privileged affection had separated and set her at a distance apart.
德纽沁根夫人看他不声不响，生气地问：“你在想什么？” Mme. de Nucingen was piqued by the silence, “What are you thinking about?” she asked.
“我在想你刚刚说过的话。 “I am thinking about what you said just now.
迄今为止，我一直确信我在乎你远远比你在乎我要多。” Hitherto I have always felt sure that I cared far more for you than you did for me.”
她笑了笑，竭力掩饰自己所感到的快乐，以免他们的谈话逾越礼节的界限。 She smiled, and would not give way to the happiness she felt, lest their talk should exceed the conventional limits of propriety.
她的爱人年轻、真诚，说话的语调令她心神荡漾。她从来没有听过这样的话。要是再多说几句，她怕自己会克制不住。 She had never heard the vibrating tones of a sincere and youthful love; a few more words, and she feared for her self-control.
“欧仁，”她换了个话题说，“难道你不知道发生了什么事情吗？ “Eugene,” she said, changing the conversation, “I wonder whether you know what has been happening?
明天整个巴黎的人都要去德伯桑夫人家。 All Paris will go to Mme. de Beauseant’s to-morrow.
洛希斐特家和德阿尤达侯爵约好不走漏一丁点消息，但是明天国王就会签署他们的婚约。你可怜的表姐，那个子爵夫人对此还一无所知。 The Rochefides and the Marquis d’Ajuda have agreed to keep the matter a profound secret, but to-morrow the king will sign the marriage-contract, and your poor cousin the Vicomtesse knows nothing of it as yet.
她不能推迟自己的舞会，侯爵也不会到场。 She cannot put off her ball, and the Marquis will not be there.
人们都在猜到时候会发生什么事。” People are wondering what will happen?”
“整个世界都会嘲笑她的下贱和纵容。 “The world laughs at baseness and connives at it.
但是这会气死德伯桑夫人的。” But this will kill Mme. de Beauseant.”
“哦，不，”德尔菲娜笑着说，“你不了解那种女人。 “Oh, no,” said Delphine, smiling, “you do not know that kind of woman.
哎呀，整个巴黎的人都会去那里，所以我也应该去哦，我应该为你去。” Why, all Paris will be there, and so shall I; I ought to go there for your sake.”
“也许这只是这个圈子里流传的种种谣言之一罢了。” “Perhaps, after all, it is one of those absurd reports that people set in circulation here.”
“明天我们就能知道真相了。” “We shall know the truth to-morrow.”
欧仁没有回“沃盖之家”。 Eugene did not return to the Maison Vauquer.
他无法不先享受一下自己在阿图瓦街的新居。 He could not forego the pleasure of occupying his new rooms in the Rue d’Artois.
昨天晚上他在午夜过后被迫马上离开德尔菲娜，但是今天晚上是德尔菲娜自己主动和他呆到凌晨两点的。 Yesterday evening he had been obliged to leave Delphine soon after midnight, but that night it was Delphine who stayed with him until two o’clock in the morning.
他起得很晚，然后便一直等着德纽沁根夫人。她直到中午才来和他一起吃早饭。 He rose late, and waited for Mme. de Nucingen, who came about noon to breakfast with him.
年轻人都迫切地想抓住这些幸福、美妙的时刻，欧仁几乎已经忘记了高老头的存在了。 Youth snatches eagerly at these rosy moments of happiness, and Eugene had almost forgotten Goriot’s existence.
他对周围那些精美绝伦的物件渐渐熟悉起来。熟悉的过程对他而言本来就是一个长长的节日，而德纽沁根夫人的出现更是让新居光彩夺目。 The pretty things that surrounded him were growing familiar; this domestication in itself was one long festival for him, and Mme. de Nucingen was there to glorify it all by her presence.
四点钟的时候他们才想起高老头，才想起他是多么盼望在那里开始新生活。 It was four o’clock before they thought of Goriot, and of how he had looked forward to the new life in that house.
欧仁说老人应该立刻搬家，以免他病得太重而动不了。 Eugene said that the old man ought to be moved at once, lest he should grow too ill to move.
他离开德尔菲娜，匆匆赶回旅馆。 He left Delphine and hurried back to the lodging-house.
高老头和年轻的比安卡肖恩没有和其他人一起在餐厅。 Neither Father Goriot nor young Bianchon was in the dining-room with the others.
“啊哈！”欧仁进来的时候，画家说，“高老头终于要完了。 “Aha!” said the painter as Eugene came in, “Father Goriot has broken down at last.
比安卡肖恩在楼上陪他。 Bianchon is upstairs with him.
他的一个女儿——德雷斯多拉玛伯爵夫人——来看过他，后来他起床出去了，这让他自己的状况更糟了。 One of his daughters—the Comtesse de Restaurama—came to see the old gentleman, and he would get up and go out, and made himself worse.
社会将要失去一个最耀眼的装饰品了。” Society is about to lose one of its brightest ornaments.”
拉斯蒂涅迅速冲上楼梯。 Rastignac sprang to the staircase.
“嗨！欧仁先生！” “Hey! Monsieur Eugene!”
“欧仁先生，夫人叫您。”西尔维大叫。 “Monsieur Eugene, the mistress is calling you,” shouted Sylvie.
“是这样的，先生，”寡妇说， “It is this, sir,” said the widow.
“你和高里奥先生本应该在二月十五那天搬出去。 “You and M. Goriot should by rights have moved out on the 15th of February.
现在已经过了三天了，今天是十八号。你们确实得再预先支付一个月的房租。如果你答应也为高里奥付钱的话，我会非常高兴的。” That was three days ago; to-day is the 18th, I ought really to be paid a month in advance; but if you will engage to pay for both, I shall be quite satisfied.”
“你为什么不能相信他呢？” “Why can’t you trust him?”
“相信他？ “Trust him, indeed!
如果老绅士昏迷、死了，他的那些女儿们一分钱都不会给我，而他的东西值不了十法郎。 If the old gentleman went off his head and died, those daughters of his would not pay me a farthing, and his things won’t fetch ten francs.
今天早上他带着剩下的所有调羹和叉子出去了，我不明白为什么。 This morning he went out with all the spoons and forks he has left, I don’t know why.
他打扮得非常年轻——上帝，原谅我吧——但是我想他在脸颊上擦了胭脂，他看起来恢复青春了。” He had got himself up to look quite young, and—Lord, forgive me—but I thought he had rouge on his cheeks; he looked quite young again.”
“我会负责的。”欧仁说。他因为害怕而发抖，因为他预见了结局。 “I will be responsible,” said Eugene, shuddering with horror, for he foresaw the end.
他上楼去了高老头的房间。 He climbed the stairs and reached Father Goriot’s room.
老人倒在床上。 The old man was tossing on his bed.
比安卡肖恩坐在他旁边。 Bianchon was with him.
“晚上好，父亲。”欧仁说。 “Good-evening, father,” said Eugene.
老人玻璃珠子般的眼睛望着他，温柔地笑了笑，说：“她怎么样？” The old man turned his glassy eyes on him, smiled gently, and said: “How is @she@?”
“她很好。 “She is quite well.
但是您怎么样？” But how are you?”
“没事，这算不了什么。” “There is nothing much the matter.”
“别让他累着。”比安卡肖恩把欧仁拉到房间角落说。 “Don’t tire him,” said Bianchon, drawing Eugene into a corner of the room.
“怎么了？”拉斯蒂涅问。 “Well?” asked Rastignac.
“现在除了奇迹没什么能救他了。 “Nothing but a miracle can save him now.
脑淤血已经发作了。我刚刚给他用了芥子膏，幸好他还有感觉，芥子膏正在起作用。” Serous congestion has set in; I have put on mustard plasters, and luckily he can feel them, they are acting.”
“可以把他抬到别处去吗？” “Is it possible to move him?”
“绝对不行。 “Quite out of the question.
他必须呆在这里，并且尽可能保持安静——”“亲爱的比安卡肖恩，”欧仁说，“我们一起照顾他吧。” He must stay where he is, and be kept as quiet as possible—”“Dear Bianchon,” said Eugene, “we will nurse him between us.”
“我已经请医院的主任医师来过了。” “I have had the head physician round from my hospital to see him.”
“他怎么说的？” “And what did he say?”
“明天晚上才能给出结果。 “He will give no opinion till to-morrow evening.
他答应今天晚些时候再过来看一下他。 He promised to look in again at the end of the day.
真不幸，这个蠢蛋今天早上偏偏要去做蠢事，也不说去干什么。 Unluckily, the preposterous creature must needs go and do something foolish this morning; he will not say what it was.
他和驴子一样倔。 He is as obstinate as a mule.
我一跟他讲话，他就装没听见，躺在那里好像睡着了似的，不回答我的问题，或者一睁眼就开始哼哼。 As soon as I begin to talk to him he pretends not to hear, and lies as if he were asleep instead of answering, or if he opens his eyes he begins to groan.
今天早上不知什么时候，他走路上街了。没人知道他去了哪里，他把值钱的东西都带上了。 Some time this morning he went out on foot in the streets, nobody knows where he went, and he took everything that he had of any value with him.
他做了些该死的交易。按照他目前的体力来看，他根本撑不住做这么多交易。 He has been driving some confounded bargain, and it has been too much for his strength.
他的一个女儿来过这里。” One of his daughters has been here.”
“是伯爵夫人吗？”欧仁问， “Was it the Countess?” asked Eugene.
“是不是一个高高的黑头发女人，眼睛很大很亮，身体苗条，脚也很小？” “A tall, dark-haired woman, with large bright eyes, slender figure, and little feet?”
“是的。” “Yes.”
“让我和他单独呆一会。”拉斯蒂涅说， “Leave him to me for a bit,” said Rastignac.
“我会让他坦白的，他会告诉我一切的。” “I will make him confess; he will tell me all about it.”
“我正好趁这个时候去吃饭。 “And meanwhile I will get my dinner.
但是千万别刺激他，咱们还是有一线希望的。” But try not to excite him; there is still some hope left.”
“好的。” “All right.”
“明天她们会很开心的。”只剩他俩的时候，高老头说， “How they will enjoy themselves to-morrow,” said Father Goriot when they were alone.
“她们要去参加一个盛大的舞会。” “They are going to a grand ball.”
“爸爸，您今天早上干什么去了，累得晚上不得不躺在床上？” “What were you doing this morning, papa, to make yourself so poorly this evening that you have to stop in bed?”
“没干什么。” “Nothing.”
“阿纳斯塔谢来看过您吗？”拉斯蒂涅问。 “Did not Anastasie come to see you?” demanded Rastignac.
“是的，”高老头说。 “Yes,” said Father Goriot.
“哎！别瞒我。 “Well, then, don’t keep anything from me.
她还想找您要什么？” What more did she want of you?”
“哦，她非常可怜。”他用尽所有的力气答道， “Oh, she was very miserable,” he answered, gathering up all his strength to speak.
“事情是这样的，我的孩子。 “It was this way, my boy.
自钻石事件发生后，纳西自己一分钱也没有了。 Since that affair of the diamonds, Nasie has not had a penny of her own.
为了参加这个舞会，她订了一件金线绣的礼服来搭配珠宝。 For this ball she had ordered a golden gown like a setting for a jewel.
她的女裁缝一点良心也没有，不肯赊账，所以纳西的女仆垫了一千法郎定金。 Her mantuamaker, a woman without a conscience, would not give her credit, so Nasie’s waiting-woman advanced a thousand francs on account.
可怜的纳西！居然落到了这般田地！ Poor Nasie! reduced to such shifts!
一想到这些，我就心如刀绞！ It cut me to the heart to think of it!
但是女仆见雷斯多不相信纳西，担心自己拿不回钱，就和裁缝串通好，要等到付清钱后才肯送衣服来。 But when Nasie’s maid saw how things were between her master and mistress, she was afraid of losing her money, and came to an understanding with the dressmaker, and the woman refuses to send the ball-dress until the money is paid.
礼服做好了，舞会明天晚上也要开始了！ The gown is ready, and the ball is to-morrow night!
纳西绝望了。 Nasie was in despair.
她想借我的叉子和调羹去典当。 She wanted to borrow my forks and spoons to pawn them.
她丈夫非要她去参加舞会，还得戴着钻石，好让传遍整个巴黎的谣言不攻自破。 Her husband is determined that she shall go and wear the diamonds, so as to contradict the stories that are told all over Paris.
可她怎么能去对那个冷酷无情的混蛋说，‘我欠裁缝一千法郎，替我付钱吧！’她不能！我自己也知道。 How can she go to that heartless scoundrel and say, ‘I owe a thousand francs to my dressmaker; pay her for me!’She cannot.I saw that myself.
德尔菲娜也会去，而且会打扮得很华丽。阿纳斯塔谢不应该被妹妹的光彩掩盖住。 Delphine will be there too in a superb toilette, and Anastasie ought not to be outshone by her younger sister.
当时——她都哭成泪人了，可怜的女儿！ And then—she was drowned in tears, poor girl!
昨天拿不出一万两千法郎的时候，我觉得十分惭愧。我会豁出剩下的悲惨生命来弥补那个错误。 I felt so humbled yesterday when I had not the twelve thousand francs, that I would have given the rest of my miserable life to wipe out that wrong.
你看，以前我什么都能忍受，但是这一回没钱让我的心都碎了。 You see, I could have borne anything once, but latterly this want of money has broken my heart.
哦！我没有丝毫犹豫，稍微梳妆了一下便出去卖掉了调羹、叉子和钮扣，共卖了六百法郎。然后我又去了戈布塞克老爹家，把我一年的养老金利息以四百法郎的价格卖给了他。 Oh! I did not do it by halves; I titivated myself up a bit, and went out and sold my spoons and forks and buckles for six hundred francs; then I went to old Daddy Gobseck, and sold a year’s interest on my annuity for four hundred francs down.
哼！我可以吃干面包过活，就像年轻时一样。以前我那样做了，现在也行。 Pshaw! I can live on dry bread, as I did when I was a young man; if I have done it before, I can do it again.
我的纳西不管怎样都应该度过一个美妙的晚上。 My Nasie shall have one happy evening, at any rate.
她应该打扮得漂漂亮亮的。 She shall be smart.
一千法郎的钞票就在我枕头下。想到它在头下，我的心里就暖暖的，因为这些钱会让我可怜的纳西开心快乐。 The banknote for a thousand francs is under my pillow; it warms me to have it lying there under my head, for it is going to make my poor Nasie happy.
她可以把那个可恶的女仆维克图瓦赶出去了。 She can turn that bad girl Victoire out of the house.
区区一个仆人居然不相信自己的女主人，这样的事情简直没人听说过！ A servant that cannot trust her mistress, did any one ever hear the like!
我明天应该就会完全好了。 I shall be quite well to-morrow.
纳西十点钟会来。 Nasie is coming at ten o’clock.
我不能让她们知道我病了，要不她们就会呆在这里照顾我，而不会去参加舞会了。 They must not think that I am ill, or they will not go to the ball; they will stop and take care of me.
明天纳西会来拥抱我，好像我是她的孩子一样。她的吻会让我重新好起来的。 To-morrow Nasie will come and hold me in her arms as if I were one of her children; her kisses will make me well again.
毕竟我有可能会把这一千法郎用在看病上。可我宁愿把钱给我的小纳西，她可以治愈所有的疼痛。 After all, I might have spent the thousand francs on physic; I would far rather give them to my little Nasie, who can charm all the pain away.
无论如何，我可以给予身处苦难的她些许安慰，这可以弥补我买了终身年金的过失。 At any rate, I am some comfort to her in her misery; and that makes up for my unkindness in buying an annuity.
现在，她掉进了痛苦的深渊，可我却没有能力救她出来。 She is in the depths, and I cannot draw her out of them now.
哦！我要再去做买卖，我会去敖德萨买小麦，那里的小麦价格只有这里的四分之一。 Oh! I will go into business again, I will buy wheat in Odessa; out there, wheat fetches a quarter of the price it sells for here.
法律禁止进口谷物，可是制定法律的好心人并没有禁止进口小麦制品和用玉米做的食品啊。 There is a law against the importation of grain, but the good folk who made the law forgot to prohibit the introduction of wheat products and food stuffs made from corn.
嗨！嗨！…… Hey! hey!...
那是我今天早上突然想到的。 That struck me this morning.
淀粉买卖有很大的赚头。” There is a fine trade to be done in starch.”
欧仁看着老人的脸，觉得他的朋友有些晕头晕脑了。 Eugene, watching the old man’s face, thought that his friend was light-headed.
“好了，”他说，“别再说话了，您必须休息了——”就在这时比安卡肖恩上来了，欧仁就下去吃晚饭了。 “Come,” he said, “do not talk any more, you must rest—”Just then Bianchon came up, and Eugene went down to dinner.
那天晚上，两个学生轮流坐在他身边照看他。 The two students sat up with him that night, relieving each other in turn.
比安卡肖恩读自己带过来的医书；欧仁给母亲和妹妹们写信。 Bianchon brought up his medical books and studied; Eugene wrote letters home to his mother and sisters.
第二天早上，比安卡肖恩认为症状略有好转，但是需要有人来不断关注病人的状况。也只有这两个学生愿意这样做。这项繁重的任务是当时拘谨的文风所无法表达的。 Next morning Bianchon thought the symptoms more hopeful, but the patient’s condition demanded continual attention, which the two students alone were willing to give—a task impossible to describe in the squeamish phraseology of the epoch.
老人瘦骨嶙峋的身体上得放水蛭，除此之外，又要涂膏药，又要用热水烫脚，还有其他的种种细枝末节的治疗方法，这都需要两个年轻人不惜体力地倾情奉献。 Leeches must be applied to the wasted body, the poultices and hot foot-baths, and other details of the treatment required the physical strength and devotion of the two young men.
德雷斯多夫人没有过来，但是她派了一个信差来拿钱。 Mme. de Restaud did not come; but she sent a messenger for the money.
“我还以为她自己会来呢。不过也好，要是她来了，她就会担心我，那样多可惜啊。”这位父亲说道。他看上去倒很开心似的。 “I expected she would come herself; but it would have been a pity for her to come, she would have been anxious about me,” said the father, and to all appearances he was well content.
那天晚上七点钟的时候泰蕾兹送来了一封德尔菲娜的信。 At seven o’clock that evening Therese came with a letter from Delphine.
“你在干什么，亲爱的朋友？ “What are you doing, dear friend?
我们才刚刚相爱不久，你就已经忘了我吗？ I have been loved for a very little while, and I am neglected already?
我已经从你对我说的那些推心置腹的话中了解到了你的心灵——你太高尚了，因此会永远忠实。因为你知道，爱情和它所带来的一切无穷无尽的微妙情感变化从来都是不一样的。 In the confidences of heart and heart, I have learned to know your soul—you are too noble not to be faithful for ever, for you know that love with all its infinite subtle changes of feeling is never the same.
有一次我们在听《摩西在埃及》这出悲剧里的祈祷词时，你说，‘对有的人来说，这不过是在重复一个音符，而对其他人来说，这是无穷无尽的音乐。’别忘了今晚我等着你带我去参加德伯桑夫人的舞会。 Once you said, as we were listening to the Prayer in @Mose in Egitto@, ‘For some it is the monotony of a single note; for others, it is the infinite of sound.’Remember that I am expecting you this evening to take me to Mme. de Beauseant’s ball.
现在人人都知道今天早上国王签署了德阿尤达先生的婚约了，可怜的子爵夫人直到今天下午两点才得知这一消息。 Every one knows now that the King signed M. d’Ajuda’s marriage-contract this morning, and the poor Vicomtesse knew nothing of it until two o’clock this afternoon.
当然，全巴黎的人都会聚到她的家里，就像人群涌到格雷夫广场去看执行死刑一样。 All Paris will flock to her house, of course, just as a crowd fills the Place de Greve to see an execution.
人们会满怀好奇心去看她是否隐藏了自己的痛苦、是否愿意勇敢地死去。这简直太可怕了，不是吗？ It is horrible, is it not, to go out of curiosity to see if she will hide her anguish, and whether she will die courageously?
我的朋友，如果我以前去过她的家，这次就当然不会去了。可是，这次舞会以后，她当然不会再招待宾客了，那样我所有的努力都白费了。 I certainly should not go, my friend, if I had been at her house before; but, of course, she will not receive society any more after this, and all my efforts would be in vain.
我的处境非常特殊，而且，我去那里的部分原因也是为了你。 My position is a very unusual one, and besides, I am going there partly on your account.
我会等着你的。 I am waiting for you.
如果你在两个小时以内没有来到我的身边，我不知道自己能不能原谅你这样的背叛。” If you are not beside me in less than two hours, I do not know whether I could forgive such treason.”
拉斯蒂涅拿起笔写道：“我会一直等到医生过来看你父亲还能不能救活。 Rastignac took up a pen and wrote:“I am waiting till the doctor comes to know if there is any hope of your father’s life.
他病得很严重，快要死了。 He is lying dangerously ill.
我会来告诉你诊断结果，但恐怕会是死亡宣判。 I will come and bring you the news, but I am afraid it may be a sentence of death.
等我来了你再决定自己是否能去参加舞会——爱你天长地久。” When I come you can decide whether you can go to the ball.—Yours a thousand times.”
八点半的时候，医生来了。 At half-past eight the doctor arrived.
他认为情况并不乐观，但是认为高老头在短时间内不会有危险。 He did not take a very hopeful view of the case, but thought that there was no immediate danger.
他的情况可能会改善，也可能会旧病复发。现在还无法断定这个好人还能活多久，还能否保持清醒。 Improvements and relapses might be expected, and the good man’s life and reason hung in the balance.
“他还是快点死比较好。”医生离开的时候说。 “It would be better for him to die at once,” the doctor said as he took leave.
欧仁把高老头托付给比安卡肖恩照顾，自己带着这个不幸的消息去找德纽沁根夫人了。 Eugene left Goriot to Bianchon’s care, and went to carry the sad news to Mme. de Nucingen.
她的家庭观念还是很重的，这一定会毁掉她的娱乐计划的。 Family feeling lingered in her, and this must put an end for the present to her plans of amusement.
“你就当什么也没发生过，告诉她今晚好好玩。”高老头大声说。 “Tell her to enjoy her evening as if nothing had happened,” cried Goriot.
他已经躺在床在处于半昏迷状态，但是欧仁出去的时候他突然坐起来说了那番话。 He had been lying in a sort of stupor, but he suddenly sat upright as Eugene went out.
欧仁的心碎了一半，来到了德尔菲娜的家中。 Eugene, half heartbroken, entered Delphine’s.
她的头发已经梳好了，还穿着舞鞋，只需要穿上晚礼服就行了。但是，一位艺术家给自己的创作添上最后的点睛之笔时，最后的几笔往往比整个画作之前所耗费的时间更多。 Her hair had been dressed; she wore her dancing slippers; she had only to put on her ball-dress; but when the artist is giving the finishing stroke to his creation, the last touches require more time than the whole groundwork of the picture.
“哎呀，你还没有换衣服！”她大叫。 “Why, you are not dressed!” she cried.
“夫人，您的父亲——”“又是我父亲！”她打断他的话大声说， “Madame, your father—”“My father again!” she exclaimed, breaking in upon him.
“你不需要教我应该怎么样对待我的父亲。我都认识他多少年了。 “You need not teach me what is due to my father, I have known my father this long while.
不要再说了，欧仁。 Not a word, Eugene.
你先换好衣服了，我才听你要讲的话。 I will hear what you have to say when you are dressed.
我的马车就在外面，你快坐车回家换衣服，泰蕾兹已经为你准备好一切了。 My carriage is waiting, take it, go round to your rooms and dress, Therese has put out everything in readiness for you.
你尽快回来，我们在去德伯桑夫人家的途中再谈父亲的事。 Come back as soon as you can; we will talk about my father on the way to Mme. de Beauseant’s.
我们得早点出发。如果得在一排马车中排队等着进门，那么我们能在十一点到那里就算幸运了。” We must go early; if we have to wait our turn in a row of carriages, we shall be lucky if we get there by eleven o’clock.”
“夫人——”“快点！别说了！”她大叫着冲进化妆室去拿项链。 “Madame—”“Quick! not a word!” she cried, darting into her dressing-room for a necklace.
“走吧，欧仁先生，要不您会惹夫人生气的。”泰蕾兹说着推他走。欧仁被这个优雅的不孝女儿吓坏了，他没法反抗。 “Do go, Monsieur Eugene, or you will vex madame,” said Therese, hurrying him away; and Eugene was too horror-stricken by this elegant parricide to resist.
他去自己的家里换好衣服。整个过程中他都很伤心而沮丧，一直都在沉思。 He went to his rooms and dressed, sad, thoughtful, and dispirited.
那时候，巴黎对他来说就像个泥海，似乎不管谁一脚踩上那个黑泥潭，都必定会陷进去，一直陷到下巴。 The world of Paris was like an ocean of mud for him just then; and it seemed that whoever set foot in that black mire must needs sink into it up to the chin.
“她们的罪过都不算什么。”欧仁自言自语， “Their crimes are paltry,” said Eugene to himself.
“沃尔特兰犯的才是大罪。” “Vautrin was greater.”
他对社会的看法已经经历了三个重大的阶段——服从、挣扎和反抗；家庭、社会和沃尔特兰。他犹豫不决，不知道应该选哪条路。 He had seen society in its three great phases—Obedience, Struggle, and Revolt; the Family, the World, and Vautrin; and he hesitated in his choice.
服从很枯燥，反抗不可能，而挣扎又太危险。 Obedience was dull, Revolt impossible, Struggle hazardous.
他的思绪回到了家庭上。 His thoughts wandered back to the home circle.
他想到了和那些爱自己的人住在家乡的日子，想到了那时安静、平凡的生活和单纯、简单的幸福。 He thought of the quiet uneventful life, the pure happiness of the days spent among those who loved him there.
那些爱着和被爱着的人们在服从家庭生活的自然规律度中过自己的人生，并在服从中找到深邃而恒久的恬静，而不会被这般痛苦所困扰。 Those loving and beloved beings passed their lives in obedience to the natural laws of the hearth, and in that obedience found a deep and constant serenity, unvexed by torments such as these.
但是尽管他有这些高尚的念头，却不敢向德尔菲娜说明自己纯洁的心灵和信仰，也不敢以爱的名义要求她尽孝心。 Yet, for all his good impulses, he could not bring himself to make profession of the religion of pure souls to Delphine, nor to prescribe the duties of piety to her in the name of love.
他所受的教育已经开始结出果实，他已经爱得很自私了。 His education had begun to bear its fruits; he loved selfishly already.
除此以外，他凭着自己的聪颖已经看清了德尔菲娜的本性。他本能地预感到她可以踏过自己父亲的尸体去参加舞会。而对于他自己，他觉得自己既没有勇气去担当良师的角色，也没有勇气去激怒她，也没有胆量让她单独一人去参加舞会。 Besides, his tact had discovered to him the real nature of Delphine; he divined instinctively that she was capable of stepping over her father’s corpse to go to the ball; and within himself he felt that he had neither the strength of mind to play the part of mentor, nor the strength of character to vex her, nor the courage to leave her to go alone.
“要是让她认识到自己在这件事上做错了，她绝不会原谅我的。”他自言自语道。 “She would never forgive me for putting her in the wrong over it,” he said to himself.
然后他想到了医生的话，并试着相信高老头的病并不像他想得那样严重。最后他还为德尔菲娜的不孝行为找到了一大堆借口。 Then he turned the doctor’s dictum over in his mind; he tried to believe that Goriot was not so dangerously ill as he had imagined, and ended by collecting together a sufficient quantity of traitorous excuses for Delphine’s conduct.
她不知道父亲病得有多严重，就算她去看望高老头了，那个善良的老人也会叫她去参加舞会的。 She did not know how ill her father was; the kind old man himself would have made her go to the ball if she had gone to see him.
依据管理家庭关系的社会法则，这个或者那个人常常会受到谴责。但是这次的情况很特殊，人们各异的性格、利益的分歧和家庭生活中不计其数的复杂因素都会为这个表面上的罪过开脱。 So often it happens that this one or that stands condemned by the social laws that govern family relations; and yet there are peculiar circumstances in the case, differences of temperament, divergent interests, innumerable complications of family life that excuse the apparent offence.
欧仁不愿意看得太透彻，他准备好为了情人牺牲自己的良知了。 Eugene did not wish to see too clearly; he was ready to sacrifice his conscience to his mistress.
在过去的几天里，他的整个人生经历了一次改变。 Within the last few days his whole life had undergone a change.
女人进入了他的世界，把他的生活弄得一团糟。在她面前他的家庭观念渐渐变淡。德尔菲娜把他整个人都据为己用了。 Woman had entered into his world and thrown it into chaos, family claims dwindled away before her; she had appropriated all his being to her uses.
拉斯蒂涅和德尔菲娜在人生的危机时刻遇到了对方，他们的结合给彼此带来了最令人痛苦的幸福。 Rastignac and Delphine found each other at a crisis in their lives when their union gave them the most poignant bliss.
他们长久以来就被证实的激情，在欲望得到满足的情况下不仅没有被消灭，反而变得愈加强烈。 Their passion, so long proved, had only gained in strength by the gratified desire that often extinguishes passion.
这个女人是他的，欧仁在爱上她之后才认识到这一点。也许爱情只是对快乐所表示的感激。 This woman was his, and Eugene recognized that not until then had he loved her; perhaps love is only gratitude for pleasure.
不管这个女人是卑鄙还是高尚，他都会爱她，因为她和她的嫁妆一样都给他带来了快乐。德尔菲娜爱拉斯蒂涅就像丹达罗斯(注：“丹达罗斯”在希腊神话中因泄天机被罚站于湖中饱受痛苦)会爱上某个给他充饥解渴的天使一样。 This woman, vile or sublime, he adored for the pleasure she had brought as her dower; and Delphine loved Rastignac as Tantalus would have loved some angel who had satisfied his hunger and quenched the burning thirst in his parched throat.
“嗯，”他穿着晚礼服回来的时候，德纽沁根夫人说，“我父亲怎么样？” “Well,” said Mme. de Nucingen when he came back in evening dress, “how is my father?”
“病得非常严重。”他回答，“如果你想向我证明一下你对我的爱，我们正好可以在半路上进去看看他。” “Very dangerously ill,” he answered; “if you will grant me a proof of your affections, we will just go in to see him on the way.”
“很好。”她说， “Very well,” she said.
“好吧，但是舞会过后再去吧。 “Yes, but afterwards.
亲爱的欧仁，一定要乖乖的哦，别对我说教了。 Dear Eugene, do be nice, and don’t preach to me.
来吧。” Come.”
他们出发了。 They set out.
欧仁好一会儿都一声不吭。 Eugene said nothing for a while.
“你现在又怎么啦？”她问。 “What is it now?” she asked.
“我可以听见你父亲临终前喉咙里发出的痛苦的呻吟。”他几近愤怒地说道。 “I can hear the death-rattle in your father’s throat,” he said almost angrily.
接着年轻人义愤填膺地讲出了德雷斯多夫人的虚荣和残忍以及她父亲最后的自我牺牲——正是这些使得高老头挣扎在生死之间——还有他为了阿纳斯塔谢金线绣的晚礼服付出了多大的代价。 And with the hot indignation of youth, he told the story of Mme. de Restaud’s vanity and cruelty, of her father’s final act of self-sacrifice, that had brought about this struggle between life and death, of the price that had been paid for Anastasie’s golden embroideries.
德尔菲娜哭了起来。 Delphine cried.
“我看上去应该很可怕吧。”她想道。 “I shall look frightful,” she thought.
她擦干了眼泪。 She dried her tears.
“我会照顾父亲，我会一直呆在他床边的。”她大声说。 “I will nurse my father; I will not leave his bedside,” she said aloud.
“啊！这才是我心中的你。”拉斯蒂涅大声说。 “Ah! now you are as I would have you,” exclaimed Rastignac.
五百辆马车的灯照亮了德伯桑府的黑暗。 The lamps of five hundred carriages lit up the darkness about the Hotel de Beauseant.
灯火通明的大门两旁各站了一个穿着华丽制服的宪兵。 A gendarme in all the glory of his uniform stood on either side of the brightly lighted gateway.
那晚，上流社会的人都齐聚到那里，迫切而好奇地想看那个伟大的女士当场栽跟头。德纽沁根夫人和拉斯蒂涅出现的时候，一楼的房间都已经挤满了人。 The great world was flocking thither that night in its eager curiosity to see the great lady at the moment of her fall, and the rooms on the ground floor were already full to overflowing, when Mme. de Nucingen and Rastignac appeared.
自从路易十四把拉格朗小姐的情人从她身边赶走，整个皇宫的人都匆匆去拜访那位不幸的公主以来，还没有一件灾难性的风流韵事能在巴黎引起如此大的轰动。 Never since Louis XIV tore her lover away from La grand Mademoiselle, and the whole court hastened to visit that unfortunate princess, had a disastrous love affair made such a sensation in Paris.
但是堪比王室的勃艮第家的小女儿傲慢地从伤痛中恢复过来，直到最后一刻，其行为举止还像这个世界的女王一样——除了有助于她在爱情上取得胜利的虚荣，这个世界的虚荣对她而言总是毫无价值。 But the youngest daughter of the almost royal house of Burgundy had risen proudly above her pain, and moved till the last moment like a queen in this world—its vanities had always been valueless for her, save in so far as they contributed to the triumph of her passion.
每间客厅里都挤满了巴黎最美的女人，她们个个盛装艳服、笑容满面、容光焕发。 The salons were filled with the most beautiful women in Paris, resplendent in their toilettes, and radiant with smiles.
部长和大使们，这些宫廷中最显要、巴黎最富盛名的人物胸前戴满了十字勋章，腰间系着五光十色的缎带，集聚在子爵夫人的周围。 Ministers and ambassadors, the most distinguished men at court, men bedizened with decorations, stars, and ribbons, men who bore the most illustrious names in France, had gathered about the Vicomtesse.
管弦乐队奏出的音乐一浪接一浪，回荡在宅邸金碧辉煌的天花板下。现在，音乐让宅邸的女王倍感孤独和凄凉。 The music of the orchestra vibrated in wave after wave of sound from the golden ceiling of the palace, now made desolate for its queen.
德伯桑夫人站在第一间客厅的门口招待那些自称是她朋友的宾客。 Madame de Beauseant stood at the door of the first salon to receive the guests who were styled her friends.
她穿着白色的晚礼服，头上简简单单地盘着辫子，没有任何头饰。她的脸很平静，既没有高傲的表情，也没有悲痛的迹象，也没有假装的快乐。 She was dressed in white, and wore no ornament in the plaits of hair braided about her head; her face was calm; there was no sign there of pride, nor of pain, nor of joy that she did not feel.
没人能够读懂她的心，她站在那里就像座大理石雕成的尼俄伯(注：“尼俄伯”在希腊神话中十四个儿子因自夸而全被杀死, 她悲伤不已, 后化为石头)塑像。 No one could read her soul; she stood there like some Niobe carved in marble.
她对一些密友的笑容中暗含几分嘲讽意味，但是不管怎么仔细观察，都发现不了她有任何改变，也看不出她和过去被幸福光辉照耀时有什么不同。 For a few intimate friends there was a tinge of satire in her smile; but no scrutiny saw any change in her, nor had she looked otherwise in the days of the glory of her happiness.
她的态度叫那些最无情的宾客也佩服不已，一如年轻的罗马人对着某个含笑而死的角斗士拍手喝彩。 The most callous of her guests admired her as young Rome applauded some gladiator who could die smiling.
上流社会似乎特意浓妆艳服来最后一次觐见某个王后。 It seemed as if society had adorned itself for a last audience of one of its sovereigns.
“我还怕你不来了。”她对拉斯蒂涅说。 “I was afraid that you would not come,” she said to Rastignac.
“夫人，”他把她的话当成了责备，不安地说，“我应该是最后离开的人，那是我来这里的原因。” “Madame,” he said, in an unsteady voice, taking her speech as a reproach, “I shall be the last to go, that is why I am here.”
“很好。”她说着握起了他的手， “Good,” she said, and she took his hand.
“你也许是这里所有人中我唯一可以信任的人。 “You are perhaps the only one I can trust here among all these.
哦，我的朋友，你要是恋爱了，就得爱一个自己确信会爱一辈子的女人， Oh, my friend, when you love, love a woman whom you are sure that you can love always.
绝不要抛弃她。” Never forsake a woman.”
她挽起拉斯蒂涅的胳膊，朝桥牌室的沙发走去。 She took Rastignac’s arm, and went towards a sofa in the card-room.
“我想要你去一趟侯爵家。”她说， “I want you to go to the Marquis,” she said.
“我的男仆雅克会和你一起去，他手里有一封信，你帮我交给侯爵。 “Jacques, my footman, will go with you; he has a letter that you will take.
我想要侯爵把我写给他的信还给我。 I am asking the Marquis to give my letters back to me.
他会把所有的信都交出来的，我希望是这样。 He will give them all up, I like to think that.
你拿到了信，就带着去我的房间。 When you have my letters, go up to my room with them.
到时有人会通知我的。” Some one shall bring me word.”
她站起来迎接自己最亲密的朋友德朗热公爵夫人。她和其他的贵族一样也来了。 She rose to go to meet the Duchesse de Langeais, her most intimate friend, who had come like the rest of the world.
拉斯蒂涅出发了。 Rastignac went.
他上洛希斐特府求见德阿尤达侯爵，觉得他肯定会在那里度过今晚，事实也的确如此。 He asked for the Marquis d’Ajuda at the Hotel Rochefide, feeling certain that the latter would be spending his evening there, and so it proved.
侯爵和拉斯蒂涅一起回到了侯爵府邸，他在把一个匣子递给学生的时候说道：“这些信都在这里面了。” The Marquis went to his own house with Rastignac, and gave a casket to the student, saying as he did so, “They are all there.”
他似乎想对欧仁说点什么，问问舞会或者子爵夫人的情况。或许这时他都快承认自己非常绝望，已经知道结婚等于铸下大错；但是他眼中突然亮起了一道骄傲的光，他鼓起可叹的勇气把自己最高尚的感情隐藏在了心里。 He seemed as if he was about to say something to Eugene, to ask about the ball, or the Vicomtesse; perhaps he was on the brink of the confession that, even then, he was in despair, and knew that his marriage had been a fatal mistake; but a proud gleam shone in his eyes, and with deplorable courage he kept his noblest feelings a secret.
“亲爱的欧仁，千万不要向她提起我的名字。” “Do not even mention my name to her, my dear Eugene.”
他悲伤而真挚地抓起拉斯蒂涅的手，然后转过身去。 He grasped Rastignac’s hand sadly and affectionately, and turned away from him.
欧仁回到了伯桑府，仆人把他带到了子爵夫人的房间。 Eugene went back to the Hotel Beauseant, the servant took him to the Vicomtesse’s room.
房里流露出准备旅行的迹象。 There were signs there of preparations for a journey.
他坐在火堆旁，盯着雪松木匣子，陷入了悲伤的沉思。 He sat down by the fire, fixed his eyes on the cedar wood casket, and fell into deep mournful musings.
德伯桑夫人在这些意象中格外突出，就像《伊利亚特》中的女神。 Mme. de Beauseant loomed large in these imaginings, like a goddess in the @Iliad@.
“啊！我的朋友！……”子爵夫人穿过房间，把手放到了拉斯蒂涅的肩膀上。 “Ah! my friend!...” said the Vicomtesse; she crossed the room and laid her hand on Rastignac’s shoulder.
他看见表姐仰着头，眼中含满了泪水，举起一只手来拿匣子，另一只手的手指颤抖着。 He saw the tears in his cousin’s uplifted eyes, saw that one hand was raised to take the casket, and that the fingers of the other trembled.
突然她接过匣子放进火中，看着它燃烧起来。 Suddenly she took the casket, put it in the fire, and watched it burn.
“他们在跳舞，”她说， “They are dancing,” she said.
“他们来得都很早。但是死亡却还得等很长一段时间。 “They all came very early; but death will be long in coming.
嘘！朋友。”她看见拉斯蒂涅想要说话，就把一根手指放到了他的嘴唇上， Hush! my friend,” and she laid a finger on Rastignac’s lips, seeing that he was about to speak.
“我再也不会看见巴黎了。 “I shall never see Paris again.
我要离开这个社会。 I am taking my leave of the world.
今天早上五点我就应该出发了，我打算躲到诺曼底最偏远的地方去。 At five o’clock this morning I shall set out on my journey; I mean to bury myself in the remotest part of Normandy.
我没有多少时间准备。从下午三点开始，我就一直忙着签署文件，打理好各项事务。我没有一个人能派去……”她停住了。 I have had very little time to make my arrangements; since three o’clock this afternoon I have been busy signing documents, setting my affairs in order; there was no one whom I could send to...”She broke off.
“他一定会是……” “He was sure to be...”
她又停住了，她的悲伤超过了她所能承受的重量。 Again she broke off; the weight of her sorrow was more than she could bear.
在这种时候，一切都是极大的痛苦，有些话则完全说不出口。 In such moments as these everything is agony, and some words are impossible to utter.
“因此我指望你今晚最后帮我一次。”她说， “And so I counted upon you to do me this last piece of service this evening,” she said.
“我想送你一件代表友谊的纪念品。 “I should like to give you some pledge of friendship.
我会经常想起你的。 I shall often think of you.
在我看来，你善良、高尚、年轻、真诚。在这个世界，很少能找到这些品质了。 You have seemed to me to be kind and noble, fresh-hearted and true, in this world where such qualities are seldom found.
我希望你也能偶尔想起我。 I should like you to think sometimes of me.
等一下，”她四处看了看，说，“有了，这是我放手套的盒子。 Stay,” she said, glancing about her, “there is this box that has held my gloves.
每次去舞会或者剧院前打开它的时候，我就会觉得自己一定很漂亮，因为我是如此快乐。除了往里面放进美好的记忆，我从不碰它。这里面装着很多以前的我，一个如今不再存在的德伯桑夫人。 Every time I opened it before going to a ball or to the theatre, I used to feel that I must be beautiful, because I was so happy; and I never touched it except to lay some gracious memory in it: there is so much of my old self in it, of a Madame de Beauseant who now lives no longer.
你要吗？ Will you take it?
我会差人把它送到你住的阿图瓦街——德纽沁根夫人今晚看上去非常迷人。 I will leave directions that it is to be sent to you in the Rue d’Artois.—Mme. de Nucingen looked very charming this evening.
欧仁，你一定要好好爱她。 Eugene, you must love her.
也许今后我们再也不会见到对方了，我的朋友。但是请相信，你对我这么好，我会为你祈祷的——现在，我们一起下楼吧。 Perhaps we may never see each other again, my friend; but be sure of this, that I shall pray for you who have been kind to me.—Now, let us go downstairs.
不能让人们以为我在哭。 People shall not think that I am weeping.
我前面还有很长的日子要过。不管去哪里，我都会一个人，那样就不会有人追问我哭的原因了。 I have all time and eternity before me, and where I am going I shall be alone, and no one will ask me the reason of my tears.
让我再看这房子最后一眼吧。“ One last look round first.”
她站了一会儿。 She stood for a moment.
然后她用双手捂住了双眼，片刻之后便擦掉眼泪，用冷水洗了洗脸，接着挽起了学生的胳膊。 Then she covered her eyes with her hands for an instant, dashed away the tears, bathed her face with cold water, and took the student’s arm.
“我们走吧！”她说。 “Let us go!” she said.
她用如此高贵的坚强承受着痛苦。这让欧仁震惊得无以复加。 This suffering, endured with such noble fortitude, shook Eugene with a more violent emotion than he had felt before.
他们回到了舞厅。德伯桑夫人挽着欧仁的胳膊在每个房间绕了一圈——这是一位优雅的女士最后的优美和典雅。 They went back to the ballroom, and Mme. de Beauseant went through the rooms on Eugene’s arm—the last delicately gracious act of a gracious woman.
过了一会儿，他看见了两姐妹：德雷斯多夫人和德纽沁根夫人。 In another moment he saw the sisters, Mme. de Restaud and Mme. de Nucingen.
伯爵夫人戴着华丽的钻石，艳光四射。每一块钻石都一定像火一样在灼烧她。她再也不能戴它们了。 The Countess shone in all the glory of her magnificent diamonds; every stone must have scorched like fire, she was never to wear them again.
尽管爱得深切而且心存傲气，她觉得很难直视丈夫的眼睛。 Strong as love and pride might be in her, she found it difficult to meet her husband’s eyes.
看到她拉斯蒂涅的伤感并没有减轻。透过那些钻石的光芒，他似乎看见了高老头躺的简陋平板床。 The sight of her was scarcely calculated to lighten Rastignac’s sad thoughts; through the blaze of those diamonds he seemed to see the wretched pallet-bed on which Father Goriot was lying.
子爵夫人误读了他的伤感，就把手从他的胳膊抽了回来。 The Vicomtesse misread his melancholy; she withdrew her hand from his arm.
“去吧，”她说，“我不应该剥夺你的快乐。” “Come,” she said, “I must not deprive you of a pleasure.”
欧仁很快被德尔菲娜邀了去。 Eugene was soon claimed by Delphine.
她对自己给他人留下的印象感到很高兴，迫切地想把自己在这个新社会得到的敬意献于爱人的脚下。她希望自此以后生活在这个社会。 She was delighted by the impression that she had made, and eager to lay at her lover’s feet the homage she had received in this new world in which she hoped to live and move henceforth.
“你觉得纳西怎么样？”她问他。 “What do you think of Nasie?” she asked him.
“她对任何事都不关心，甚至连自己父亲的生死也毫不在意。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “She has discounted everything, even her own father’s death,” said Rastignac.
早上四点的时候，房间里开始空了起来。 Towards four o’clock in the morning the rooms began to empty.
片刻之后，音乐停止了，偌大的舞厅里只剩下德朗热公爵夫人和拉斯蒂涅。 A little later the music ceased, and the Duchesse de Langeais and Rastignac were left in the great ballroom.
子爵夫人以为学生一个人在那里，最后也回到了那里。 The Vicomtesse, who thought to find the student there alone, came back there at last.
德伯桑先生要去睡觉，于是和她道别。德伯桑先生离开时再一次说道：“亲爱的，你这个年纪就隐居，太可惜了！ She had taken leave of M. de Beauseant, who had gone off to bed, saying again as he went, “It is a great pity, my dear, to shut yourself up at your age!
请和我们呆在一起吧。” Pray stay among us.”
德伯桑夫人看见公爵夫人后，不由自主地大叫起来。 Mme. de Beauseant saw the Duchesse, and, in spite of herself, an exclamation broke from her.
“我知道怎么回事了，克拉拉。”德朗热夫人说， “I saw how it was, Clara,” said Mme. de Langeais.
“你准备离开我们，再不回来了。 “You are going from among us, and you will never come back.
但是你得先听我说一番话，直到我们理解了对方才能离开。” But you must not go until you have heard me, until we have understood each other.”
她挽起朋友的胳膊，一起去了隔壁的房间。 She took her friend’s arm, and they went together into the next room.
在那里，公爵夫人满眼泪光地看着她。她紧紧地拥抱着自己的朋友，亲吻着她的脸颊。 There the Duchess looked at her with tears in her eyes; she held her friend in close embrace and kissed her cheek.
“亲爱的，我不能一言不发地让你离开，我无法承受这么沉重的悔恨。 “I could not let you go without a word, dearest; the remorse would have been too hard to bear.
你可以相信我，就像相信你自己一样。 You can count upon me as surely as upon yourself.
今晚你表现得很伟大。我觉得自己有资格和你做朋友，也打算证明自己有这个资格。 You have shown yourself great this evening; I feel that I am worthy of our friendship, and I mean to prove myself worthy of it.
我并非一直都很和善，有时候也会犯错。亲爱的，原谅我吧。我多希望自己没有说过任何可能会伤害你的话啊，我会收回那些话。 I have not always been kind; I was in the wrong; forgive me, dearest; I wish I could unsay anything that may have hurt you; I take back those words.
共同的悲伤让我们又在一起了，我不知道我们俩谁更可怜。 One common sorrow has brought us together again, for I do not know which of us is the more miserable.
德蒙特里沃先生今天不在这里，你明白那意味着什么吗？——克拉拉，今晚见到你的那些人绝不会忘记你的。 M. de Montriveau was not here to-night; do you understand what that means?—None of those who saw you to-night, Clara, will ever forget you.
我打算做最后的努力。 I mean to make one last effort.
如果失败了，我就会进修道院。 If I fail, I shall go into a convent.
克拉拉，你要去哪里？” Clara, where are you going?”
“去诺曼底的库尔塞勒。 “Into Normandy, to Courcelles.
我会在那里爱着、祈祷着，直到上帝将我从这个世界带走的那天为止——德拉斯蒂涅先生！”子爵夫人想起年轻人正在那里等着，便用颤抖的声音叫道。 I shall love and pray there until the day when God shall take me from this world.—M. de Rastignac!” called the Vicomtesse, in a tremulous voice, remembering that the young man was waiting there.
学生跪下亲吻表姐的手。 The student knelt to kiss his cousin’s hand.
“再见，安托瓦妮特！”德伯桑夫人说， “Good-bye, Antoinette!” said Mme. de Beauseant.
“但愿你会幸福。”她转向这个学生。 “May you be happy.”—She turned to the student.
“你很年轻，”她说，“仍然有很多信念。 “You are young,” she said; “you have some beliefs still left.
我就像某些将死的人一样，在离开这个世界的时候发现自己周围的那些人中还有真挚和虔诚，这样我已经很幸运了。” I have been privileged, like some dying people, to find sincere and reverent feeling in those about me as I take my leave of this world.”
那天早上拉斯蒂涅回去的时候都快五点了。 It was nearly five o’clock that morning when Rastignac came away.
他把德伯桑夫人送上了远行马车。德伯桑夫人和他做最后道别的时候，一边说话，眼泪一边唰唰直掉。社会地位高的人并不像某些煽动者想让人民相信的那样，伟大到了能够超越人类情感规律，或者到了能超脱于痛苦之外生活的程度。 He had put Mme. de Beauseant into her traveling carriage, and received her last farewells, spoken amid fast-falling tears; for no greatness is so great that it can rise above the laws of human affection, or live beyond the jurisdiction of pain, as certain demagogues would have the people believe.
欧仁冒着严寒和黑暗走回了“沃盖之家”。 Eugene returned on foot to the Maison Vauquer through the cold and darkness.
他快要毕业了。 His education was nearly complete.
“可怜的高老头没有希望了。”拉斯蒂涅进屋的时，比安卡肖恩说。 “There is no hope for poor Father Goriot,” said Bianchon, as Rastignac came into the room.
欧仁盯着熟睡的老人看了一会儿，然后转向自己的朋友。 Eugene looked for a while at the sleeping man, then he turned to his friend.
“亲爱的伙计，你已经为自己选择了一个合适的职业，并且从中得到了满足，坚持自己的路吧。我陷入了地狱，必须呆在那里。相信你听到的关于这个世界的一切言论吧，所有的一切都太糟糕了。没有一个朱文诺尔（注：“朱文诺尔”是古罗马讽刺作家）能写尽隐藏在珠宝和黄金下面的丑恶。” “Dear fellow, you are content with the modest career you have marked out for yourself; keep to it.I am in hell, and I must stay there.Believe everything that you hear said of the world, nothing is too impossibly bad.No Juvenal could paint the horrors hidden away under the covering of gems and gold.”
第六章 Chapter 6
下午两点，比安卡肖恩来叫醒了拉斯蒂涅，乞求他照顾高老头。随着时间的流逝，高老头的病情越来越严重了。 At two o’clock in the afternoon Bianchon came to wake Rastignac, and begged him to take charge of Goriot, who had grown worse as the day wore on.
这个医科学生必须去出诊。 The medical student was obliged to go out.
“可怜的老头，他活不过两天了，或许几个小时后就会死去。”他说，“但不管怎样，我们都要全力以赴给他治病。这是个非常棘手的病例，我们需要钱。当然，我们两个可以看护他。但是，就我而言，我可是一分钱都没有的。我掏遍了他的口袋，翻遍了他的抽屉——结果什么也没找到。在他意识清醒的时候我问过他，他告诉我他一分钱都没有。你有多少钱呢？” “Poor old man, he has not two days to live, maybe not many hours,” he said; “but we must do our utmost, all the same, to fight the disease.It will be a very troublesome case, and we shall want money.We can nurse him between us, of course, but, for my own part, I have not a penny.I have turned out his pockets, and rummaged through his drawers—result, nix.I asked him about it while his mind was clear, and he told me he had not a farthing of his own.What have you?”
“我还剩二十法郎，”拉斯蒂涅说，“但是我要把它们押在轮盘赌桌上，我肯定会赢钱的。” “I have twenty francs left,” said Rastignac; “but I will take them to the roulette table, I shall be sure to win.”
“那要是你输了呢？” “And if you lose?”
“那我就去找他的女儿和女婿们，问他们要钱。” “Then I shall go to his sons-in-law and his daughters and ask them for money.”
“那要是他们拒绝了呢？”比安卡肖恩反问道， “And suppose they refuse?” Bianchon retorted.
“当下最紧急的还不是钱，我们必须给他敷上芥子膏，脚和大腿都要敷，而且膏药越热越好。 “The most pressing thing just now is not really money; we must put mustard poultices, as hot as they can be made, on his feet and legs.
要是他喊出来了，那么他还有些许希望。 If he calls out, there is still some hope for him.
你知道怎么着手处理这件事，还有，克里斯托夫会帮助你的。 You know how to set about doing it, and besides, Christophe will help you.
我要去药房走一趟，说服他们赊给我们一些需要的药品。 I am going round to the dispensary to persuade them to let us have the things we want on credit.
可惜我们不能把他送进医院。可怜的老头，他要是在医院的话，情况会好一些。 It is a pity that we could not move him to the hospital; poor fellow, he would be better there.
好吧，快点，我把他交给你照顾了。在我回来之前，你必须看着他。” Well, come along, I leave you in charge; you must stay with him till I come back.”
两个年轻人回到了老人躺着的房间里。 The two young men went back to the room where the old man was lying.
欧仁看到高老头的脸变得如此扭曲、脸色发青、没有一点生气，感到非常吃惊。 Eugene was startled at the change in Goriot’s face, so livid, distorted, and feeble.
“您怎么样，老爹？”他在简陋的床边弯下身，问道。 “How are you, papa?” he said, bending over the pallet-bed.
高老头呆滞的目光转向了欧仁，仔细地看着他，却没有认出他是谁。 Goriot turned his dull eyes upon Eugene, looked at him attentively, and did not recognize him.
这个学生再也忍受不住了，眼睛里充满了泪水。 It was more than the student could bear; the tears came into his eyes.
“比安卡肖恩，我们要不要在窗户上挂上窗帘？” “Bianchon, ought we to have the curtains put up in the windows?”
“不用，温度和阳光现在都不能对他产生影响了。 “No, the temperature and the light do not affect him now.
他能感觉到冷或热是好事，但无论如何我们都要生个火用来煎药，或者加热其他东西。 It would be a good thing for him if he felt heat or cold; but we must have a fire in any case to make tisanes and heat the other things.
我会送一些木棒过来，能一直坚持到我们有柴火用的时候。 I will send round a few sticks; they will last till we can have in some firewood.
昨天一天一夜，我已经把你和高老头剩下的树皮柴火全烧完了，可怜的老头。 I burned all the bark fuel you had left, as well as his, poor man, yesterday and during the night.
这个地方太潮湿了，墙上都渗出水滴来了，我很难让房间干燥起来。 The place is so damp that the water stood in drops on the walls; I could hardly get the room dry.
克里斯托夫进来扫了地。但这个地方就像马棚一样。我不得不烧了些杜松木。这里的味道太难闻了。” Christophe came in and swept the floor, but the place is like a stable; I had to burn juniper, the smell was something horrible.”
“我的上帝！”拉斯蒂涅说道， “Mon Dieu!” said Rastignac.
“想想他的女儿们。” “To think of those daughters of his.”
“等一会儿，要是他什么时候要喝水的话，给他喝这个。”这个医科学生指着一只大白罐说， “One moment, if he asks for something to drink, give him this,” said the house student, pointing to a large white jar.
“要是他开始呻吟，腹部发热，摸起来很硬的话，你知道该怎么办，找克里斯托夫帮你。 “If he begins to groan, and the belly feels hot and hard to the touch, you know what to do; get Christophe to help you.
要是他变得非常兴奋，开始说很多话，甚至开始胡言乱语的话，不要惊慌。 If he should happen to grow much excited, and begin to talk a good deal and even to ramble in his talk, do not be alarmed.
这也许不是坏现象。 It would not be a bad symptom.
但是叫克里斯托夫去一趟科钦医院。 But send Christophe to the Hospice Cochin.
我们的医生、我的同学或者是我会来做一次艾灸。 Our doctor, my chum, or I will come and apply moxas.
今天早上你睡觉的时候，我们做了次大型会诊。 We had a great consultation this morning while you were asleep.
来了一位外科医生，就是加尔的一个学生，还有我们的外科住院医师和主宫医院的主任内科医师。 A surgeon, a pupil of Gall’s came, and our house surgeon, and the head physician from the Hotel-Dieu.
那些先生们都认为这些症状非常少见，对此都很感兴趣。我们必须密切关注这个病例，因为这会有助于解释几个令人费解却非常重要的科学难题。 Those gentlemen considered that the symptoms were very unusual and interesting; the case must be carefully watched, for it throws a light on several obscure and rather important scientific problems.
其中的一位权威专家说，要是大脑某处的血浆压力再大一点，就会在某种方面上影响到他的心智。 One of the authorities says that if there is more pressure of serum on one or other portion of the brain, it should affect his mental capacities in such and such directions.
所以要是他开口讲话了，仔细留意他脑子里有什么样的想法。是有关记忆的，有关洞察力的，还是有关推理的器官在发挥作用；占据他思想的是情感还是实际问题；他是在预测未来，还是叙述过去。事实上，你得准备准确地报告他的病情。 So if he should talk, notice very carefully what kind of ideas his mind seems to run on; whether memory, or penetration, or the reasoning faculties are exercised; whether sentiments or practical questions fill his thoughts; whether he makes forecasts or dwells on the past; in fact; you must be prepared to give an accurate report of him.
溢出的血液很有可能扩散到整个大脑。这样他就会虚弱地死去，就像他现在躺在这里一样。 It is quite likely that the extravasation fills the whole brain, in which case he will die in the imbecile state in which he is lying now.
对于这种神秘的神经系统疾病，你没法下任何论断。 You cannot tell anything about these mysterious nervous diseases.
假如在这里病发，”比安卡肖恩碰了碰后脑勺说，“就会发生很奇怪的事。有时大脑会部分恢复，暂时还死不了。 Suppose the crash came here,” said Bianchon, touching the back of the head, “very strange things have been known to happen; the brain sometimes partially recovers, and death is delayed.
或者淤塞的血浆会一起从某处涌出，至于具体的位置就只有尸检能确定了。 Or the congested matter may pass out of the brain altogether through channels which can only be determined by a post-mortem examination.
绝症病人收容所里有一个老头，是一个痴呆病人。在他的病例中，血液朝着脊髓方向溢出。他承受着极大的痛苦，但却依旧活着。” There is an old man at the Hospital for Incurables, an imbecile patient, in his case the effusion has followed the direction of the spinal cord; he suffers horrid agonies, but he lives.”
“她们玩得开心吗？” “Did they enjoy themselves?”
这是高老头在说话。 It was Father Goriot who spoke.
他认出了欧仁。 He had recognized Eugene.
“哦！他只想着他的女儿们。”比安卡肖恩说， “Oh! he thinks of nothing but his daughters,” said Bianchon.
“他昨晚对我说了几十次，‘她们现在在跳舞了！她有她的裙子了。’他叫着她们的名字。他把我弄哭了，真见鬼，用他那样的声音和语调叫着‘德尔菲娜！ “Scores of times last night he said to me, ‘They are dancing now!She has her dress.’ He called them by their names.He made me cry, the devil take it, calling with that tone in his voice, for ‘Delphine!
我的小德尔菲娜！还有纳西！’的确，”这医科学生说，“这足以让任何人掉眼泪了。” My little Delphine! and Nasie!’ Upon my word,” said the medical student, “it was enough to make any one burst out crying.”
“德尔菲娜，”这老头说，“她就在那里，不是吗？ “Delphine,” said the old man, “she is there, isn’t she?
我知道她就在那里。”他说着就用眼睛搜寻着门口。 I knew she was there,” and his eyes sought the door.
“现在我要下去叫西尔维准备好膏药。”比安卡肖恩说， “I am going down now to tell Sylvie to get the poultices ready,” said Bianchon.
“应该立即上药。” “They ought to go on at once.”
拉斯蒂涅一个人留下陪着老人。 Rastignac was left alone with the old man.
他在床脚坐下，盯着眼前这张脸，看到这张脸发生了如此可怕的变化，他感到非常震惊。 He sat at the foot of the bed, and gazed at the face before him, so horribly changed that it was shocking to see.
“高贵的灵魂不能在这个社会久留。”他说，“德伯桑夫人选择逃离，而他躺在这里等死。 “Noble natures cannot dwell in this world,” he said; “Mme. de Beauseant has fled from it, and there he lies dying.
在这肤浅、卑鄙、轻浮的所谓社会之中，哪里还有高贵思想和情感的一席之地呢？” What place indeed is there in the shallow petty frivolous thing called society for noble thoughts and feelings?”
昨天舞会的画面在他的记忆中浮现，与他面前这位临终之人形成了奇怪的对比。 Pictures of yesterday’s ball rose up in his memory, in strange contrast to the deathbed before him.
比安卡肖恩突然出现了。 Bianchon suddenly appeared.
“我说，欧仁，我刚才见了我们医院的主治医生，然后就一路跑了回来。 “I say, Eugene, I have just seen our head surgeon at the hospital, and I ran all the way back here.
要是这老头显示出任何理智的迹象，要是他开始说话，就用芥子膏从脖子一直覆盖到脊椎底部，再叫人通知我们。” If the old man shows any signs of reason, if he begins to talk, cover him with a mustard poultice from the neck to the base of the spine, and send round for us.”
“亲爱的比安卡肖恩。”欧仁喊道。 “Dear Bianchon,” exclaimed Eugene.
“哦！从科学角度说，这是一个有趣的病例。”这个医科学生带着新入教者般的狂热说道。 “Oh! it is an interesting case from a scientific point of view,” said the medical student, with all the enthusiasm of a neophyte.
“那么！”欧仁说， “So!” said Eugene.
“真的只有我一个人是为了他本人而照顾他的吗？” “Am I really the only one who cares for the poor old man for his own sake?”
“如果你今天早上见到我，你就不会这样说了。”比安卡肖恩回答说，没有因为这句话而生气。 “You would not have said so if you had seen me this morning,” returned Bianchon, who did not take offence at this speech.
“很多有经验的医生们眼里从来只有疾病，但是，我亲爱的伙伴，我眼里还是有病人的。” “Doctors who have seen a good deal of practice never see anything but the disease, but, my dear fellow, I can see the patient still.”
他走了。 He went.
欧仁独自留下照顾老人。他担心病情很快就会恶化，而事实果然如此。 Eugene was left alone with the old man, and with an apprehension of a crisis that set in, in fact, before very long.
“啊！亲爱的孩子，是你吗？”高老头说，他认出了欧仁。 “Ah! dear boy, is that you?” said Father Goriot, recognizing Eugene.
“您感觉好点了吗？”这个法律系学生握住了他的手，问道。 “Do you feel better?” asked the law student, taking his hand.
“是的。 “Yes.
刚才感觉我的头就好像被钳子紧紧夹住一样，不过现在那把钳子又松开了。 My head felt as if it were being screwed up in a vise, but now it is set free again.
你看见我的女儿们了吗？ Did you see my girls?
她们马上就会来这里的。她们一旦知道我生病了，就会立刻赶过来。在裘森尼街的时候，她们曾经那么关心我！ They will be here directly; as soon as they know that I am ill they will hurry here at once; they used to take such care of me in the Rue de la Jussienne!
我的老天！要是这间屋子衬得起她们就好了！ Great Heavens! if only my room was fit for them to come into!
有个年轻人在这里呆过，他烧光了我所有的树皮柴火。” There has been a young man here, who has burned up all my bark fuel.”
“我能听见克里斯托夫上楼的声音。”欧仁回答说， “I can hear Christophe coming upstairs,” Eugene answered.
“他拿上来一些木柴，都是那个年轻人送来给您的。” “He is bringing up some firewood that that young man has sent you.”
“很好，但是我怎么能负担得起这些木柴呢。 “Good, but how am I to pay for the wood.
我身上一分钱都不剩了，亲爱的孩子。 I have not a penny left, dear boy.
我已经付出了我的一切，一切。 I have given everything, everything.
我现在就是一个乞丐。 I am a pauper now.
嗯，至少那件金线礼服很华丽，不是吗？ Well, at least the golden gown was grand, was it not?
（啊！好痛啊！）谢谢，克里斯托夫！ (Ah! what pain this is!)Thanks, Christophe!
上帝会报答你的，我的孩子。我现在一无所有了。” God will reward you, my boy; I have nothing left now.”
欧仁走向克里斯托夫，在他耳边低声说：“给你们添麻烦了，我会给你报酬，也会给西尔维的。” Eugene went over to Christophe and whispered in the man’s ear, “I will pay you well, and Sylvie too, for your trouble.”
“我女儿们跟你说她们要过来，不是吗，克里斯托夫？ “My daughters told you that they were coming, didn’t they, Christophe?
你再去找她们一次，我给你五法郎。 Go again to them, and I will give you five francs.
告诉她们我感觉很不好，在我临死之前，我想再见到她们，亲吻她们。 Tell them that I am not feeling well, that I should like to kiss them both and see them once again before I die.
告诉她们这些，但是别太吓着她们了。” Tell them that, but don’t alarm them more than you can help.”
拉斯蒂涅示意克里斯托夫离开，他便走了。 Rastignac signed to Christophe to go, and the man went.
“她们不久之后就会过来的。”老人继续说， “They will come before long,” the old man went on.
“我太了解她们了。 “I know them so well.
我那有着仁慈心肠的德尔菲娜！ My tender-hearted Delphine!
倘若我要死了，她会感到非常伤心的！ If I am going to die, she will feel it so much!
纳西也会的。 And so will Nasie.
我不想死。要是我死了她们会痛哭的。而且，亲爱的欧仁，要是我死了，就再也见不到她们了。 I do not want to die; they will cry if I die; and if I die, dear Eugene, I shall not see them any more.
我即将去的地方非常沉闷。 It will be very dreary there where I am going.
对于一个父亲来说，没有孩子在的地方就是地狱。自从她们结婚以来，我就已经初尝了这种滋味。 For a father it is hell to be without your children; I have served my apprenticeship already since they married.
我的天堂就在裘森尼街。 My heaven was in the Rue de la Jussienne.
欧仁，你觉得要是我上了天堂，我的灵魂还能回到人间，靠近她们吗？ Eugene, do you think that if I go to heaven I can come back to earth, and be near them in spirit?
我曾听说过这样的事情。 I have heard some such things said.
这是真的吗？ It is true?
这时，我好像能看到她们；她们和我们三人过去一起住在裘森尼街的时候一模一样。 It is as if I could see them at this moment as they used to be when we all lived in the Rue de la Jussienne.
她们过去常常在早晨下楼。 They used to come downstairs of a morning.
‘早上好，爸爸！’她们过去总是这么说，然后我就会把她们抱上我的膝盖，和她们一起玩各种各样的小游戏；她们总有哄人的可爱小把戏。 ‘Good-morning, papa!’ they used to say, and I would take them on my knees; we had all sorts of little games of play together, and they had such pretty coaxing ways.
我们每天早上都一起吃早餐，她们也和我一起吃晚餐——事实上，我那时就是一个父亲。 We always had breakfast together, too, every morning, and they had dinner with me—in fact, I was a father then.
我享受孩子带来的乐趣。 I enjoyed my children.
只要她们住在裘森尼街，就不为自己着想；她们对这个社会一无所知，她们全心全意地爱我。 They did not think for themselves so long as they lived in the Rue de la Jussienne; they knew nothing of the world; they loved me with all their hearts.
我的上帝！为什么她们不能停留在小女孩的时代呢？ Mon Dieu! why could they not always be little girls?
（哦！我的头，我的脑袋疼痛得难以忍受！）哦！啊！原谅我，孩子们，这种疼痛太可怕了。这应该叫做‘煎熬’吧，因为你们早就让我习惯所谓的‘疼痛’了。 (Oh! my head this racking pain in my head!)Ah! ah! forgive me, children, this pain is fearful; it must be agony indeed, for you have used me to endure pain.
我的上帝！要是我能抓住她们的手，就根本不会感觉到痛苦——你认为她们已经在路上了吗？ Mon Dieu! if only I held their hands in mine, I should not feel it at all.—Do you think that they are on the way?
克里斯托夫这么笨，我应该自己去。 Christophe is so stupid; I ought to have gone myself.
他会见到她们的。 He will see them.
但是你昨天去了舞会，告诉我她们看起来怎么样。 But you went to the ball yesterday; just tell me how they looked.
她们不知道我生病了，不是吗？否则她们就不会去跳舞了，可怜的小家伙们。 They did not know that I was ill, did they, or they would not have been dancing, poor little things?
哦！我再也不会生病了。 Oh! I must not be ill any longer.
她们现在非常需要我的帮助，她们的财产岌岌可危。 They stand too much in need of me; their fortunes are in danger.
而且她们又嫁了那种丈夫！ And such husbands as they are bound to!
我必须好起来！ I must get well!
（哦！怎么那么疼！怎么那么疼！……啊！啊！）——你知道，我必须好起来。因为她们必须要有钱，而我知道怎么赚到钱。 (Oh! what pain this is! what pain this is!...ah! ah!)—I must get well, you see; for they @must@ have money, and I know how to set about making some.
我要去敖德萨，在那里生产淀粉。 I will go to Odessa and manufacture starch there.
我有经验，能赚几百万呢。 I am an old hand, I will make millions.
（哦！剧痛又来了！）”高老头沉默了一会儿，似乎需要集中全部力量来忍受痛苦。 (Oh! this is agony!)”Goriot was silent for a moment; it seemed to require his whole strength to endure the pain.
“要是她们在这里，我就不会抱怨了。”他说， “If they were here, I should not complain,” he said.
“所以现在我为什么要抱怨呢？” “So why should I complain now?”
他似乎已经精疲力尽了，就昏睡起来；他静静地躺了很长时间。 He seemed to grow drowsy with exhaustion, and lay quietly for a long time.
克里斯托夫回来了。拉斯蒂涅觉得高老头已经睡着了，就让他大声说出刚才的遭遇。 Christophe came back; and Rastignac, thinking that Goriot was asleep, allowed the man to give his story aloud.
“一开始，先生，我去了伯爵夫人那里，”他说，“但是她和她的丈夫都很忙，我没法跟她说上话。 “First of all, sir, I went to Madame la Comtesse,” he said; “but she and her husband were so busy that I couldn’t get to speak to her.
当我坚持要见她时，德雷斯多先生一个人出来见我，然后说道，‘高里奥先生快死了，是不是？ When I insisted that I must see her, M. de Restaud came out to me himself, and went on like this:‘M. Goriot is dying, is he?
很好，这是他能做的最好事情了。 Very well, it is the best thing he can do.
我想让德雷斯多夫人处理一些重要的生意，等完成这些事，她就能去了。’我想，那位先生看起来非常生气。 I want Mme. de Restaud to transact some important business, when it is all finished she can go.’ The gentleman looked angry, I thought.
我刚要走的时候，德雷斯多夫人从一扇我没注意到的门走进入了前厅，然后说，‘克里斯托夫，告诉我父亲，我丈夫想让我和他商量一些事情，我不能离开这里，因为我的孩子们命悬一线。这件事情一处理完毕，我就过去。’至于男爵夫人，就是另外一回事了！ I was just going away when Mme. de Restaud came out into an ante-chamber through a door that I did not notice, and said, ‘Christophe, tell my father that my husband wants me to discuss some matters with him, and I cannot leave the house, the life or death of my children is at stake; but as soon as it is over, I will come.’As for Madame la Baronne, that is another story!
我和她也说不上话，我甚至没有见到她。 I could not speak to her either, and I did not even see her.
她的侍女说：‘啊，没错，但是夫人早上四点四十五分才从一个舞会回来。她现在在睡觉呢。要是我在正午之前叫醒她，她会发脾气的。 Her waiting-woman said, ‘Ah yes, but madame only came back from a ball at a quarter to five this morning; she is asleep now, and if I wake her before mid-day she will be cross.
她一按铃，我就去告诉她，她的父亲已病入膏肓了。 As soon as she rings, I will go and tell her that her father is worse.
还有足够的时间来告诉她一个坏消息呢！’我又是哀求又是乞求，但是，哼！没有一点用。 It will be time enough then to tell her bad news!’I begged and I prayed, but, there!It was no good.
然后我要求见男爵先生，但是他出去了。” Then I asked for M. le Baron, but he was out.”
“想想他的两个女儿，一个都不会来！”拉斯蒂涅喊道， “To think that neither of his daughters should come!” exclaimed Rastignac.
“我要写信给她们俩。” “I will write to them both.”
“一个都不会来！”老人从床上坐起来，大声说道， “Neither of them!” cried the old man, sitting upright in bed.
“她们很忙，她们在睡觉，她们不会来了！ “They are busy, they are asleep, they will not come!
我就知道她们不会来。 I knew that they would not.
直到你垂死之时，才知道你的孩子们……哦！我的朋友，不要结婚，不要生孩子！ Not until you are dying do you know your children…Oh! my friend, do not marry; do not have children!
你给她们生命，她们却将你置于死地。 You give them life; they give you your deathblow.
你把她们带到这个世界上，她们却把你从这世上赶出去。 You bring them into the world, and they send you out of it.
不，她们不会来了。 No, they will not come.
我十年前就知道了。 I have known that these ten years.
有时候我会这样跟自己说，但却不敢相信。” Sometimes I have told myself so, but I did not dare to believe it.”
眼泪在他红通通的眼眶里聚集，但没有流出来。 The tears gathered and stood without overflowing the red sockets.
“啊！要是我还是那么有钱，要是我存下了我的财产，要是我没有全给了她们，她们现在会陪着我，会讨好我，她们的亲吻会落满我的脸颊！ “Ah! if I were rich still, if I had kept my money, if I had not given all to them, they would be with me now; they would fawn on me and cover my cheeks with their kisses!
我若住在大宅子里，我若有富丽堂皇的房间、成群的仆人，房间里还有壁炉，她们和她们丈夫、孩子都会泪流满面地围绕在我的周围。 I should be living in a great mansion; I should have grand apartments and servants and a fire in my room; and @they@ would be about me all in tears, and their husbands and their children.
我原本能拥有那一切的，但现在——我一无所有。 I should have had all that; now—I have nothing.
钱能带给你任何东西，甚至是你的女儿。 Money brings everything to you; even your daughters.
我的钱。 My money.
哦！我的钱在哪里？ Oh! where is my money?
要是我能留下一大笔钱，她们就会照顾我、护理我，我就能听到她们的声音，看到她们的面庞。 If I had plenty of money to leave behind me, they would nurse me and tend me; I should hear their voices, I should see their faces.
哦，上帝！谁知道呢？ Ah, God! who knows?
她们两个都是铁石心肠。 They both of them have hearts of stone.
我太爱她们了，但是她们不见得爱我。 I loved them too much; it was not likely that they should love me.
一位父亲就应该永远富有。他应该把孩子们牢牢地掌握在手中，就像驾驭不羁的马一样。 A father ought always to be rich; he ought to keep his children well in hand, like unruly horses.
我曾向她们下跪。 I have gone down on my knees to them.
不幸的人！这一至高无上的举动为过去十年划上了圆满的句号。 Wretches! this is the crowning act that brings the last ten years to a proper close.
你不知道她们一结婚就向我提出了多少无理的要求。 If you but knew how much they made of me just after they were married.
（哦！这真是残酷的折磨！）我刚刚分给她们每人八十万法郎。之后，她们不得不对我客客气气，她们的丈夫也很客气。 (Oh! this is cruel torture!)I had just given them each eight hundred thousand francs; they were bound to be civil to me after that, and their husbands too were civil.
我过去常常去她们的住处，她们口口声声喊着‘我的好父亲’、‘我亲爱的父亲’。 I used to go to their houses: it was ‘My kind father’ here, ‘My dear father’ there.
她们的餐桌总有我的位子。 There was always a place for me at their tables.
我曾经时不时和她们的丈夫一起用餐，他们对我也很尊敬。 I used to dine with their husbands now and then, and they were very respectful to me.
他们认为我还有一点价值。 I was still worth something, they thought.
他们怎么知道的呢？ How should they know?
我一点都没说自己的事。 I had not said anything about my affairs.
对一位给了每个女儿八十万法郎的先生客气一点，还是很值得的。他们那时把我照顾得无微不至——但都是为了我的钱。 It is worth while to be civil to a man who has given his daughters eight hundred thousand francs apiece; and they showed me every attention then—but it was all for my money.
达官贵人并不伟大。 Grand people are not great.
这是我亲身得到的教训！ I found that out by experience!
我乘她们的马车和她们一起去剧院，我可以在她们的晚会里随意逗留。 I went to the theatre with them in their carriage; I might stay as long as I cared to stay at their evening parties.
实际上，她们把我当作她们的父亲，她们也公开承认是我的女儿。 In fact, they acknowledged me their father; publicly they owned that they were my daughters.
但是你知道我一直是一个精明的人，没什么能瞒得过我。 But I was always a shrewd one, you see, and nothing was lost upon me.
所有事都直指一点，刺穿了我的心。 Everything went straight to the mark and pierced my heart.
我很清楚地看到，所有的事都是伪装和虚饰，但对于这些事情，我却毫无办法。 I saw quite well that it was all sham and pretence, but there is no help for such things as these.
我在她们家饭桌上还没有在这里楼下自在呢。 I felt less at my ease at their dinner-table than I did downstairs here.
我没说自己的任何事情。 I had nothing to say for myself.
于是这些地位显赫的人就会在我女婿的耳边问,‘那位先生是谁啊？’——‘那是我背着钱袋的岳父，他非常有钱’——‘哎呀，他真有钱呢！’他们会这样说，然后因为我的钱而以尊敬的目光看着我。 So these grand folks would ask in my son-in-law’s ear, ‘Who may that gentleman be?’—‘The father-in-law with the money bags; he is very rich.’—‘The devil, he is!’ they would say, and look again at me with the respect due to my money.
嗯，即便我有时候妨碍了他们，我也慷慨地为我的错误付账。 Well, if I was in the way sometimes, I paid dearly for my mistakes.
而且，有谁是完美的呢？ And besides, who is perfect?
（我的头好疼！）亲爱的欧仁先生，我现在正忍受着折磨，这种痛苦可能会让一个人死去；但这远不及我第一次说了蠢话之后，阿纳斯塔谢让我感觉和承受的痛苦。 (My head is one sore!)Dear Monsieur Eugene, I am suffering so now, that a man might die of the pain; but it is nothing to be compared with the pain I endured when Anastasie made me feel, for the first time, that I had said something stupid.
她看着我的眼神让我觉得我所有的血管都胀开了。 She looked at me, and that glance of hers opened all my veins.
我过去想知道一切，想成为有学问的人；但是我彻底明白了一件事——我知道我在这世上不受欢迎。 I used to want to know everything, to be learned; and one thing I did learn thoroughly—I knew that I was not wanted here on earth.
“第二天我去德尔菲娜那里寻求安慰，但是我在那里却又犯下了愚蠢的错误，让她生了我的气。 “The next day I went to Delphine for comfort, and what should I do there but make some stupid blunder that made her angry with me.
我就像一个失去理性的人一样。 I was like one driven out of his senses.
之后的一个星期，我不知道要做什么，我不敢去看她们，害怕她们会责备我。 For a week I did not know what to do; I did not dare to go to see them for fear they should reproach me.
她们俩就这样把我赶出了家门。 And that was how they both turned me out of the house.
“哦！上帝啊！ “Oh God!
您了解我所承受的所有不幸和痛苦；您数算过这些岁月在我身上留下的伤痕，这些伤痕让我变老，改变了我的容貌，催白了我的头发，耗尽了我的生命。为什么现在还让我承受这样的痛苦呢？ Thou knowest all the misery and anguish that I have endured; Thou hast counted all the wounds that have been dealt to me in these years that have aged and changed me and whitened my hair and drained my life; why dost Thou make me to suffer so to-day?
难道我还没有赎完因为太爱她们而犯下的罪孽吗？ Have I not more than expiated the sin of loving them too much?
她们自己已经成了复仇的工具，她们因为我爱她们这一罪行而折磨我。 They themselves have been the instruments of vengeance; they have tortured me for my sin of affection.
“啊！做父亲的是再明白不过了。我那么爱她们，我回到她们的身边，就像赌徒回到赌桌上一样。 “Ah, well! fathers know no better; I loved them so; I went back to them as a gambler goes to the gaming table.
你瞧，这种爱就是我的弱点，她们是我的女主人——在这世上，她们就是我的一切。 This love was my vice, you see, my mistress—they were everything in the world to me.
她们总是想要这个想要那个，衣服、首饰或是其他东西。之前她们的女仆常常告诉我她们想要的东西，于是，为了换取她们对我的欢迎，我就会送给她们那些东西。 They were always wanting something or other, dresses and ornaments, and what not; their maids used to tell me what they wanted, and I used to give them the things for the sake of the welcome that they bought for me.
但同时，只要我在公开场合的言行举止不符合她们的训导，她们就会立马开始说我。 But, at the same time, they used to give me little lectures on my behavior in society; they began about it at once.
后来，她们还因为我而感到羞耻。 Then they began to feel ashamed of me.
这就是让你的孩子接受良好教育的后果。 That is what comes of having your children well brought up.
我那个年纪不能回到学校上学。 I could not go to school again at my time of life.
（这疼痛太可怕了！ (This pain is fearful!
我的上帝啊！医生呢！医生！ Mon Dieu!These doctors! these doctors!
要是他们能打开我的脑袋，我还能好受些！）哦，我的女儿，我的女儿！ If they would open my head, it would give me some relief!)Oh, my daughters, my daughters!
阿纳斯塔谢！德尔菲娜！ Anastasie! Delphine!
要是我能见见她们，那该多好啊！ If I could only see them!
让警察抓她们来见我！ Send for the police, and make them come to me!
正义在我这边，整个世界都在我这边，我自然有这个权利，法律也会支持我的。 Justice is on my side, the whole world is on my side, I have natural rights, and the law with me.
我抗议！ I protest!
要是父亲的权利被踩在脚底下，这个国家就会走向毁灭。 The country will go to ruin if a father’s rights are trampled under foot.
这是显而易见的。 That is easy to see.
整个世界都依赖着父爱，父爱是社会的基础。当孩子们不再爱他们的父亲时，这个世界就会分崩离析。 The whole world turns on fatherly love; fatherly love is the foundation of society; it will crumble into ruin when children do not love their fathers.
哦！要是我能见到她们，听到她们的声音就好了。不管她们说什么，只要我能听到她们的声音，我的痛苦就会减轻一点。 Oh! if I could only see them, and hear them, no matter what they said; if I could simply hear their voices, it would soothe the pain.
德尔菲娜！ Delphine!
最爱的德尔菲娜。 Delphine most of all.
但是在她们来的时候，告诉她们别用之前那种冷漠的眼神看着我。 But tell them when they come not to look so coldly at me as they do.
哦！我的朋友，我的好欧仁先生，你不知道当她们目光中所有的金光突然变成沉闷的铅灰色时，我是什么心情。 Oh! my friend, my good Monsieur Eugene, you do not know that it is when all the golden light in a glance suddenly turns to a leaden gray.
当她们看我的目光失去光彩时，我仿佛在过一个漫长的冬季。 It has been one long winter here since the light in their eyes shone no more for me.
我默默吞下的只有失望。 I have had nothing but disappointments to devour.
失望变成了我每天吞食的面包，我在羞耻和侮辱中艰难度日。 Disappointment has been my daily bread; I have lived on humiliation and insults.
我吞下了她们给我的所有侮辱，就为了她们能给我偷偷摸摸的短暂快乐，因为我如此爱她们！ I have swallowed down all the affronts for which they sold me my poor stealthy little moments of joy; for I love them so!
想想吧！ Think of it!
一个父亲把自己藏起来，就为了看他的孩子们一眼！ A father hiding himself to get a glimpse of his children!
我把我整个生命都给了她们，现在她们却不肯给我一个小时！ I have given all my life to them, and to-day they will not give me one hour!
我多么渴望见到她们啊，我的心在身体里燃烧，但是她们还是不肯来为我减轻一点痛苦。我现在就快死了，我感觉这就是死亡。 I am hungering and thirsting for them, my heart is burning in me, but they will not come to bring relief in the agony, for I am dying now, I feel that this is death.
她们不知道践踏父亲的尸体意味着什么吗？ Do they not know what it means to trample on a father’s corpse?
不管我们愿意与否，天堂里的上帝会为我们当父亲的报仇的。 There is a God in heaven who avenges us fathers whether we will or no.
“哦！她们一定会来的！ “Oh! they will come!
来看看我吧，亲爱的孩子们，再给我一个亲吻。这最后的一个吻，就是给你们父亲的临终圣餐，他会在天堂向上帝为你们祈祷的。 Come to me, darlings, and give me one more kiss; one last kiss, the Viaticum for your father, who will pray God for you in heaven.
我会告诉他，你们对父亲很好，我会向上帝解释你们的动机。 I will tell Him that you have been good children to your father, and plead your cause with God!
毕竟，这不是她们的错。 After all, it is not their fault.
我跟你说，她们是无辜的，我的朋友。 I tell you they are innocent, my friend.
告诉每一个人，这不是她们的错，没有人需要为了我而感到哀伤。 Tell every one that it is not their fault, and no one need be distressed on my account.
这都是我的错，我教会了她们践踏我。 It is all my own fault, I taught them to trample upon me.
我喜欢被她们践踏。 I loved to have it so.
这件事除了我和其他任何人都无关，人类的正义和上帝的正义都与此无关。 It is no one’s affair but mine; man’s justice and God’s justice have nothing to do in it.
要是上帝因为她们曾对我做的任何事而责难她们，那么上帝就不公平了。 God would be unjust if He condemned them for anything they may have done to me.
我在她们面前表现得不够得体，我非常愚蠢，理应收回我的权利。 I did not behave to them properly; I was stupid enough to resign my rights.
为了她们，我愿意卑微地死去。 I would have humbled myself in the dust for them.
你还能盼望什么呢？ What could you expect?
最美丽的心灵和最高贵的灵魂在这样的溺爱之下都会被宠坏。 The most beautiful nature, the noblest soul, would have been spoiled by such indulgence.
我是一个卑鄙的人，我接受了公正的惩罚。 I am a wretch, I am justly punished.
我，只有我，应该为她们所有的罪孽承担责任，我把她们宠坏了。 I, and I only, am to blame for all their sins; I spoiled them.
今天她们渴望享乐正像她们以前渴望糖果一样。 To-day they are as eager for pleasure as they used to be for sugar-plums.
在她们小的时候，我放纵她们，满足她们所有的想法。 When they were little girls I indulged them in every whim.
她们在十五岁的时候就有了自己的马车。 They had a carriage of their own when they were fifteen.
她们从没有被拒绝过。 They have never been crossed.
有罪的是我，不是她们——但我是因为爱而犯下罪孽的。 I am guilty, and not they—but I sinned through love.
要是能听到她们的声音，我的心就会敞开。 My heart would open at the sound of their voices.
