我能听见她们，她们来了。 I can hear them; they are coming.
是的！是的！她们来了。 Yes! yes! they are coming.
法律规定，在父亲临死之时，她们应该出现在父亲的床边；法律站在我这边。 The law demands that they should be present at their father’s deathbed; the law is on my side.
她们只要花一点租马车的钱。 It would only cost them the hire of a cab.
我会付这个钱的。 I would pay that.
写信给她们，告诉她们我有几百万留给她们！ Write to them, tell them that I have millions to leave to them!
以我的名义写，是的。 On my word of honor, yes.
我会去敖德萨生产意大利面食。 I am going to manufacture Italian paste foods at Odessa.
我了解这笔生意。 I understand the trade.
这笔生意能赚几百万呢。 There are millions to be made in it.
还没有人能想出这种计划呢。 Nobody has thought of the scheme as yet.
你看，这方法将避免小麦和面粉在运输中经常出现的浪费或变质的问题。 You see, there will be no waste, no damage in transit, as there always is with wheat and flour.
嗨！嗨！还有淀粉，做淀粉生意能赚上几百万呢！ Hey! hey! and starch too; there are millions to be made in the starch trade!
我没有说谎话。 You will not be telling a lie.
几百万，告诉她们。即便她们来，真的只是因为她们觊觎那些钱，我也甘心被她们欺骗。不管怎样我都要见到她们。 Millions, tell them; and even if they really come because they covet the money, I would rather let them deceive me; and I shall see them in any case.
我想要我的孩子！ I want my children!
我给了她们生命，她们是我的，我的！”说着他坐了起来。 I gave them life; they are mine, mine!” and he sat upright.
他长着稀疏白发的头也随之抬了起来，这在欧仁看来好像是一种威胁，他的每一句话都带着恐吓的意味。 The head thus raised, with its scanty white hair, seemed to Eugene like a threat; every line that could still speak spoke of menace.
“嘿，嘿，亲爱的老爹，”欧仁说，“再躺下去吧，我会立即写信给她们的。 “There, there, dear father,” said Eugene, “lie down again; I will write to them at once.
要是她们再不过来，等比安卡肖恩一回来，我就去找她们。” As soon as Bianchon comes back I will go for them myself, if they do not come before.”
“要是她们不过来呢？”老人哭着重复道， “If they do not come?” repeated the old man, sobbing.
“哎，我不久就会死了；我会因为一时的愤怒而死的，就因为愤怒！ “Why, I shall be dead before then; I shall die in a fit of rage, of rage!
我已经开始生气了。 Anger is getting the better of me.
在这一分钟里我能看清我的一辈子。 I can see my whole life at this minute.
我被欺骗了！ I have been cheated!
她们不爱我——她们一生中从来就没有爱过我！ They do not love me—they have never loved me all their lives!
我全明白了。 It is all clear to me.
她们没来，也不会来了。 They have not come, and they will not come.
她们来得越晚，能够带给我的快乐就越少。 The longer they put off their coming, the less they are likely to give me this joy.
我了解她们。 I know them.
她们从未关心我的失望、我的悲伤、我的渴望；她们从来没有试图了解我的生活。她们不会在我临死之时出现了，她们甚至不知道我暗地里对她们所投入的感情。 They have never cared to guess my disappointments, my sorrows, my wants; they never cared to know my life; they will have no presentiment of my death; they do not even know the secret of my tenderness for them.
是的，我都看清楚了。 Yes, I see it all now.
我曾经不断地敞开心扉，这让她们觉得我为她们做的一切都是理所应当的。 I have laid my heart open so often, that they take everything I do for them as a matter of course.
她们可以让我把自己的眼珠子挖出来，我还会出价鼓励她们这样做。 They might have asked me for the very eyes out of my head and I would have bidden them to pluck them out.
她们认为所有的父亲都像她们的父亲一样。 They think that all fathers are like theirs.
你应该一直让人感觉到你的价值。 You should always make your value felt.
她们自己的孩子会为我报仇的。 Their own children will avenge me.
嗯，为了她们自己，她们也应当来看我！ Why, for their own sakes they should come to me!
去告诉她们，她们会在自己临终的病榻上遭到报应的。 Make them understand that they are laying up retribution for their own deathbeds.
所有的罪行都包含在这一桩……去找她们，就告诉她们，要是她们还是远远避开我的话，就等于犯了弑父罪！ All crimes are summed up in this one…Go to them; just tell them that if they stay away it will be parricide!
即使不加上这一条，对她们的控诉书上已经列了足够多的罪名了。 There is enough laid to their charge already without adding that to the list.
像我一样大声哭喊，‘纳西！德尔菲娜！这里！来你父亲这里，对你们那么好的父亲就要死了！’没有回音，没人会来！ Cry aloud as I do now, ‘Nasie! Delphine! here!Come to your father; the father who has been so kind to you is lying ill!’—Not a sound; no one comes!
之后我就会像一条狗一样死去吗？ Then am I do die like a dog?
这就是我得到的奖赏——最后我被遗弃了。 This is to be my reward—I am forsaken at the last.
她们都是邪恶、无情的女人，我诅咒她们，我憎恶她们。 They are wicked, heartless women; curses on them, I loathe them.
我会在晚上从我的坟墓里爬出来诅咒她们，我的朋友，我终究还是做错了吗？ I shall rise at night from my grave to curse them again; for, after all, my friends, have I done wrong?
她们对我很不好，嗯？ They are behaving very badly to me, eh?...
我在说些什么啊？ What am I saying?
你刚才不是告诉我，德尔菲娜在房间里了吗？ Did you not tell me just now that Delphine is in the room?
她比她的姐姐更善良…… She is more tender-hearted than her sister…
欧仁，你是我的儿子，你知道的。 Eugene, you are my son, you know.
你要爱她，像父亲一样对她！ You will love her; be a father to her!
她的姐姐很不开心。 Her sister is very unhappy.
而且还有她们的财产啊！ And there are their fortunes!
哦，上帝！ Ah, God!
我要死了，这种痛苦远在我的承受范围之外。 I am dying, this anguish is almost more than I can bear!
割掉我的头吧，只要把我的心留给我就可以了。” Cut off my head; leave me nothing but my heart.”
“克里斯托夫！”欧仁被老人呻吟、哭喊的样子吓着了，他大声叫道，“去找比安卡肖恩先生，还有给我叫一辆马车来——我去找她们过来，亲爱的老爹，我会把她们带来见您的。” “Christophe!” shouted Eugene, alarmed by the way in which the old man moaned, and by his cries, “go for M. Bianchon, and send a cab here for me.—I am going to fetch them, dear father; I will bring them back to you.”
“让她们来！ “Make them come!
押也要把她们押过来！ Compel them to come!
出动护卫队，或者军队，运用任何方法、一切方法，总之就要她们来！” Call out the Guard, the military, anything and everything, but make them come!”
他看着欧仁，眼睛里闪烁着最后一丝智慧的光芒， He looked at Eugene, and a last gleam of intelligence shone in his eyes.
“去找政府机关，去找检察官，让他们把她们带过来，她们应该来！” “Go to the authorities, to the Public Prosecutor, let them bring them here; come they shall!”
“但是您已经诅咒她们了。” “But you have cursed them.”
“谁说的！”老人带着一脸呆滞而惊讶的表情说道， “Who said that!” said the old man in dull amazement.
“你非常清楚，我爱她们，非常喜欢她们！ “You know quite well that I love them, I adore them!
要是我能见到她们，病很快就会好了…… I shall be quite well again if I can see them…
去找她们，我的好邻居，我的好孩子，你真善良。我希望能报答你的善良，但是现在除了我这个将死之人的祝福之外，我也没什么能给你了。 Go for them, my good neighbor, my dear boy, you are kind-hearted; I wish I could repay you for your kindness, but I have nothing to give you now, save the blessing of a dying man.
啊！要是我能见到德尔菲娜，我会告诉她，让她偿还我欠你的债。 Ah! if I could only see Delphine, to tell her to pay my debt to you.
要是另外一个不能来，不管怎样也要把德尔菲娜带来。 If the other cannot come, bring Delphine to me at any rate.
告诉她，她若不来，你就不再爱她。 Tell her that unless she comes, you will not love her any more.
她那么爱你，她会立刻过来看我的。 She is so fond of you that she will come to me then.
给我点喝的东西！ Give me something to drink!
我的肚子里好像有火在烧似的。 There is a fire in my bowels.
在我的额头上压点东西吧！ Press something against my forehead!
要是我的女儿们能把她们的手放在这里，我想我会好受一点……我的上帝！要是我死了，谁还能帮她们拿回她们的钱呢？我要在敖德萨做面条，为了她们我要去敖德萨。” If my daughters would lay their hands there, I think I should get better…Mon Dieu! who will recover their money for them when I am gone?...I will manufacture vermicelli out in Odessa; I will go to Odessa for their sakes.”
“这是喝的。”欧仁说道。他用左胳膊撑着这个垂死之人，同时右胳膊拿着一杯汤药送到高老头嘴边。 “Here is something to drink,” said Eugene, supporting the dying man on his left arm, while he held a cup of tisane to Goriot’s lips.
“你肯定很爱自己的父亲和母亲！”老人说着双手抓住了这个学生的手。 “How you must love your own father and mother!” said the old man, and grasped the student’s hand in both of his.
高老头那双无力的手不停地颤抖着。 It was a feeble, trembling grasp.
“我就要死了，我死前是看不到我的女儿们了，你明白吗？ “I am going to die; I shall die without seeing my daughters; do you understand?
总是很渴却永远喝不到水，这就是我生命中最后的十年……我没有女儿，我的女婿们杀死了她们。 To be always thirsting, and never to drink; that has been my life for the last ten years…I have no daughters, my sons-in-law killed them.
不，自从她们结婚起，她们对我来说就已经死了。 No, since their marriages they have been dead to me.
父亲们应该请求国民议会通过一项禁止结婚的法律。 Fathers should petition the Chambers to pass a law against marriage.
要是你爱你的女儿们，就别让她们结婚。 If you love your daughters, do not let them marry.
女婿就是流氓，他毒害了一个女孩的思想，还玷污了她的所有天性。 A son-in-law is a rascal who poisons a girl’s mind and contaminates her whole nature.
不要有结婚这回事！ Let us have no more marriages!
婚姻抢走了我们的女儿。当我们被遗弃在病床上时，她们却不来看我们了。 It robs us of our daughters; we are left alone upon our deathbeds, and they are not with us then.
他们应该为了垂死的父亲们通过一项法律。 They ought to pass a law for dying fathers.
这真的太糟糕了！ This is awful!
我要报仇啊！ It cries for vengeance!
她们不能来，因为我的女婿们不让她们来！ They cannot come, because my sons-in-law forbid them!...
杀了他们！雷斯多和那阿尔萨斯人，把他们俩都杀了！ Kill them!...Restaud and the Alsatian, kill them both!
他们俩谋杀了我！不还我的女儿，就要他们的命！啊！太晚了，我就要死了，她们还是不在这里！没有她们陪伴就这样死去！ They have murdered me between them!...Death or my daughters!...Ah! it is too late, I am dying, and they are not here!...Dying without them!...
纳西！菲芬！ Nasie! Fifine!
你们为什么不来看我呢？ Why do you not come to me?
你们的爸爸就要——”“亲爱的高老头，冷静一下。 Your papa is going—”“Dear Father Goriot, calm yourself.
嘿，嘿，静静地躺着，休息一下。不要担心你自己，不要多想。” There, there, lie quietly and rest; don’t worry yourself, don’t think.”
“我不会见到她们了。哦！又疼了！” “I shall not see them.Oh! the agony of it!”
“你会见到她们的。” “You @shall@ see them.”
“真的吗？”老人喊道，他的神情依旧恍惚。 “Really?” cried the old man, still wandering.
“哦！我会见到她们的，我会见到她们并且听到她们的声音的。 “Oh! shall I see them; I shall see them and hear their voices.
我会快乐地死去。 I shall die happy.
啊！毕竟我也不想活了，我不能继续忍受这种痛苦了，疼痛越来越剧烈了。 Ah! well, after all, I do not wish to live; I cannot stand this much longer; this pain that grows worse and worse.
但是，哦！见到她们，触摸一下她们的衣服——啊！只是触摸一下她们的衣服，这个要求一点都不过分。还有，去感受一些属于她们的东西。 But, oh! to see them, to touch their dresses—ah! nothing but their dresses, that is very little; still, to feel something that belongs to them.
让我用手指摸一下她们的头发……她们的头发……” Let me touch their hair with my fingers...their hair...”
他的头落在枕头上，好像被什么突然而沉重地击倒了一般，但是他的双手还在棉被上无力地摸索，就好像在找寻他女儿们的头发。 His head fell back on the pillow, as if a sudden heavy blow had struck him down, but his hands groped feebly over the quilt, as if to find his daughters’ hair.
“我祝福她们……”他努力说着，“我祝福她们……”他的声音渐渐变弱。 “My blessing on them...” he said, making an effort, “my blessing...”His voice died away.
就在这时，比安卡肖恩走进了屋子。 Just at that moment Bianchon came into the room.
“我见到了克里斯托夫，”他说，“他给你叫车去了。” “I met Christophe,” he said; “he is gone for your cab.”
然后他看着病人，用手掀起高老头闭着的眼皮瞧了瞧。 Then he looked at the patient, and raised the closed eyelids with his fingers.
两个学生看到下面的眼睛变得非常暗淡且没有光泽。 The two students saw how dead and lusterless the eyes beneath had grown.
“他熬不过这一关了，我肯定。”比安卡肖恩说。 “He will not get over this, I am sure,” said Bianchon.
他把了把老人的脉搏，将一只手放在他的心脏上， He felt the old man’s pulse, and laid a hand over his heart.
“机器还在运转，但情况更糟糕了；就他这样的情况，死了比活着好。” “The machinery works still; more is the pity, in his state it would be better for him to die.”
“啊！说实话，的确是！” “Ah! my word, it would!”
“你怎么了？你脸色苍白，像死人一样。” “What is the matter with you?You are as pale as death.”
“亲爱的伙计，我刚才听到了他的呻吟和呼喊，那声音……一定有上帝！ “Dear fellow, the moans and cries that I have just heard…There is a God!
啊！是的，是的，一定有上帝；他为我们创造了一个更美好的世界，否则我们这个世界会是一个噩梦。 Ah! yes, yes, there is a God, and He has made a better world for us, or this world of ours would be a nightmare.
我本来会像一个小孩一样大哭，但这太悲惨了，我的心都碎了。” I could have cried like a child; but this is too tragical, and I am sick at heart.”
“你知道，我们需要很多东西，但是钱从哪里来呢？” “We want a lot of things, you know; and where is the money to come from?”
拉斯蒂涅拿出了他的表。 Rastignac took out his watch.
“给你，快点把这个当了。 “There, be quick and pawn it.
我不想在去埃尔德街的路上停顿。没时间浪费了，而且我必须等到克里斯托夫回来才能走。 I do not want to stop on the way to the Rue du Helder; there is not a moment to lose, I am afraid, and I must wait here till Christophe comes back.
我一分钱都没有，但我再回来的时候，我必须要给马车夫付车钱。” I have not a farthing; I shall have to pay the cabman when I get home again.”
拉斯蒂涅冲下楼梯，驱车前往埃尔德街。 Rastignac rushed down the stairs, and drove off to the Rue du Helder.
他刚才经历的可怕场景刺激了他的想象力，他变得极度愤慨。 The awful scene through which he had just passed quickened his imagination, and he grew fiercely indignant.
他到了德雷斯多夫人的房子，仆人却告诉他女主人不能见任何人。 He reached Mme. de Restaud’s house only to be told by the servant that his mistress could see no one.
“但是我从她父亲那里带来一个消息，他就要死了。”拉斯蒂涅告诉那个人。 “But I have brought a message from her father, who is dying,” Rastignac told the man.
“伯爵给我们下了最严厉的命令，先生——”“倘若这是德雷斯多先生下的命令，那么告诉他，他的岳父生命垂危，我就在这里，我要立刻和他说话。” “The Count has given us the strictest orders, sir—”“If it is M. de Restaud who has given the orders, tell him that his father-in-law is dying, and that I am here, and must speak with him at once.”
这个人出去了。 The man went out.
欧仁等了很长时间。 Eugene waited for a long while.
“也许这时她的父亲就要死了。”他想。 “Perhaps her father is dying at this moment,” he thought.
那人后来回来了；欧仁跟着他进了一个小客厅。 Then the man came back, and Eugene followed him to the little drawing-room.
德雷斯多先生站在没有生火的壁炉前面，也没有让客人坐下。 M. de Restaud was standing before the fireless grate, and did not ask his visitor to seat himself.
“伯爵先生，”拉斯蒂涅说，“您的岳父高里奥先生此时生命垂危，躺在拉丁区的一个肮脏小屋子里。 “Monsieur le Comte,” said Rastignac, “M. Goriot, your father-in-law, is lying at the point of death in a squalid den in the Latin Quarter.
他没有一分钱来支付烧柴火的费用,他随时都会死去，但却不停地喊着他女儿——”“我对高里奥先生没有感情，先生，您可能也意识到了。”伯爵冷漠地回答说, He has not a penny to pay for firewood; he is expected to die at any moment, and keeps calling for his daughter—”“I feel very little affection for M. Goriot, sir, as you probably are aware,” the Count answered coolly.
“他的本性在与德雷斯多夫人的接触中已经变坏了。他是不幸的始作俑者，那些不幸让我的生活充满了苦难，也扰乱了我心绪的宁静。 “His character has been compromised in connection with Mme. de Restaud; he is the author of the misfortunes that have embittered my life and troubled my peace of mind.
不论他是生是死，我都完全不会在意。 It is a matter of perfect indifference to me if he lives or dies.
现在你知道我对他的感觉了。 Now you know my feelings with regard to him.
公众舆论也许会谴责我，但是我从不关心公众舆论。 Public opinion may blame me, but I care nothing for public opinion.
现在，除了愚蠢和喋喋不休之人对我的评头论足，我还有其他更重要的事情要考虑。 Just now I have other and much more important matters to think about than the things that fools and chatterers may say about me.
至于德雷斯多夫人，她不能离开这间房子，她现在不适宜离开。 As for Mme. de Restaud, she cannot leave the house; she is in no condition to do so.
而且，我也不允许她离开。 And, besides, I shall not allow her to leave it.
告诉她的父亲，她只要一尽到对她丈夫和孩子的责任，就可以去看他了。 Tell her father that as soon as she has done her duty by her husband and child she shall go to see him.
要是她对父亲还有一点爱的话，她可以自由地去看他。如果她选择那样的话，几秒钟之内就可以去看他，这完全取决于她——”“伯爵先生，对于您的行为，我本无权作出任何评价；您可以对您夫人做任何您想做的事，但是我能否指望您遵守对我的承诺呢？ If she has any love for her father, she can be free to go to him, if she chooses, in a few seconds; it lies entirely with her—” “Monsieur le Comte, it is no business of mine to criticise your conduct; you can do as you please with your wife, but may I count upon your keeping your word with me?
好吧，答应我要告诉她，她的父亲活不过二十四小时了；他已经不指望看到她了，他躺在病床上的时候，已经诅咒过她了——这就是我的全部要求。” Well, then, promise me to tell her that her father has not twenty-four hours to live; that he looks in vain for her, and has cursed her already as he lies on his deathbed,—that is all I ask.”
“你可以自己告诉她。”伯爵回答道，他感受到了在欧仁声音中颤抖的愤恨。 “You can tell her yourself,” the Count answered, impressed by the thrill of indignation in Eugene’s voice.
伯爵把欧仁带到了他夫人经常呆的房间里。 The Count led the way to the room where his wife usually sat.
她泪流满面地把身子深深蜷在一张扶手椅里，就像她已厌倦了生活而渴望死亡一样。 She was drowned in tears, and lay crouching in the depths of an armchair, as if she were tired of life and longed to die.
看见她让人觉得非常可怜。 It was piteous to see her.
在她斗胆看拉斯蒂涅之前，她瞥了一眼她的丈夫，那眼神明显带有可怜的恐惧感，这显示了她在身体和灵魂上彻底的屈服。她似乎被精神上和身体上的残暴统治完全摧毁了。 Before venturing to look at Rastignac, she glanced at her husband in evident and abject terror that spoke of complete prostration of body and mind; she seemed crushed by a tyranny both mental and physical.
伯爵将头转向她，她把这一动作理解为伯爵允许她开口说话。 The Count jerked his head towards her; she construed this as a permission to speak.
“您说的话我都听到了，先生。告诉我父亲，要是他了解事情的全部，他会原谅我的……我从没想过世上竟有像这样的折磨，这绝非我所能忍受的，先生！——但只要我活着，就不会屈服。”她说着转向了她的丈夫， “I heard all that you said, monsieur.Tell my father that if he knew all he would forgive me…I did not think there was such torture in the world as this; it is more than I can endure, monsieur!—But I will not give way as long as I live,” she said, turning to her husband.
“我是一位母亲——告诉我父亲，不管看上去怎么样，我从来没有得罪过他！”她绝望地大声哭诉。 “I am a mother.—Tell my father that I have never sinned against him in spite of appearances!” she cried aloud in her despair.
欧仁向这对夫妇鞠了一躬；他猜测着这一幕的含义，认为伯爵夫人的生活肯定出现了严重的危机。 Eugene bowed to the husband and wife; he guessed the meaning of the scene, and that this was a terrible crisis in the Countess’ life.
德雷斯多先生的举止告诉他，他的使命毫无结果。他知道阿纳斯塔谢不再拥有行动自由了。 M. de Restaud’s manner had told him that his errand was a fruitless one; he saw that Anastasie had no longer any liberty of action.
他迷惘而不知所措地离开了，然后就匆忙赶去了德纽沁根夫人家。 He came away mazed and bewildered, and hurried to Mme. de Nucingen.
德尔菲娜躺在床上。 Delphine was in bed.
“可怜的欧仁，我生病了。”她说， “Poor dear Eugene, I am ill,” she said.
“我舞会之后就患上了感冒，我害怕会染上肺炎。 “I caught cold after the ball, and I am afraid of pneumonia.
我在等医生来。” I am waiting for the doctor to come.”
“就算你在死亡的门槛上，”欧仁打断了她，“也得抬你去见你的父亲。 “If you were at death’s door,” Eugene broke in, “you must be carried somehow to your father.
他在呼唤你。 He is calling for you.
要是你能听到一丁点那些呼唤，你就不会再感到自己有病了。” If you could hear the faintest of those cries, you would not feel ill any longer.”
“欧仁，我敢说我父亲的病没有你说的那么严重，但是我不能忍受做任何你不赞成的事，所以我会遵照你的意愿做的。 “Eugene, I dare say my father is not quite so ill as you say; but I cannot bear to do anything that you do not approve, so I will do just as you wish.
至于他，我知道要是我出去见他，然后带回一场危险的病，他会悲伤而死的。嗯，我一看完医生就会去那里——啊！”她喊道，“你没有戴你的表，为什么呢？” As for HIM, he would die of grief I know if I went out to see him and brought on a dangerous illness.Well, I will go as soon as I have seen the doctor.—Ah!” she cried out, “you are not wearing your watch, how is that?”
欧仁脸红了。 Eugene reddened.
“欧仁，欧仁！要是你已经把它卖了，或丢了……哦！这就是你的错了！” “Eugene, Eugene! if you have sold it already or lost it…Oh! it would be very wrong of you!”
这个学生将身体侧向德尔菲娜，在她耳边说：“你想知道吗？ The student bent over Delphine and said in her ear, “Do you want to know?
很好，那么，你应当知道。 Very well, then, you shall know.
你的父亲没有钱来买今天晚上要盖在他身上的裹尸布了。 Your father has nothing left to pay for the shroud that they will lay him in this evening.
你的表我已经当了，因为我也没有钱。” Your watch has been pawned, for I had nothing either.”
德尔菲娜从床上弹了起来，冲向她的桌子，拿出她的钱包。 Delphine sprang out of bed, ran to her desk, and took out her purse.
她把钱包给了欧仁，然后按了铃，喊道：“我就去，我马上就去，欧仁。 She gave it to Eugene, and rang the bell, crying:“I will go, I will go at once, Eugene.
出去吧，我要换衣服。 Leave me, I will dress.
啊，我竟然是一个没良心的女儿！ Why, I should be an unnatural daughter!
回去吧，我会在你之前赶到那里的—— Go back; I will be there before you.—
泰蕾兹，”她对女仆说，“马上叫德纽沁根先生上楼来，我有话要说。” Therese,” she called to the waiting-woman, “ask M. de Nucingen to come upstairs at once and speak to me.”
当欧仁到了新圣热讷维耶沃街的时候，他几乎高兴起来了。他很高兴能够给这个垂死之人带来这一消息：他的一个女儿要来了。 Eugene was almost happy when he reached the Rue Nueve-Sainte-Genevieve; he was so glad to bring the news to the dying man that one of his daughters was coming.
他在德尔菲娜德的钱包里乱摸一通，想拿钱出来尽快打发这辆马车，但是他发现这位年轻、美丽、富有的上流社会女人的私人钱包里只有七十法郎。 He fumbled in Delphine’s purse for money, so as to dismiss the cab at once; and discovered that the young, beautiful, and wealthy woman of fashion had only seventy francs in her private purse.
他爬上楼梯，发现比安卡肖恩正支撑着高老头，而从医院来的外科住院医师在内科医师的指导下，正在病人的背上做艾灸，这是科学上的最后一搏，不过也是徒劳。 He climbed the stairs and found Bianchon supporting Goriot, while the house surgeon from the hospital was applying moxas to the patient’s back—under the direction of the physician, it was the last expedient of science, and it was tried in vain.
“你能感觉到针刺吗？”内科医师问。 “Can you feel them?” asked the physician.
但是高老头瞥见了拉斯蒂涅，回答说：“她们正在赶来，是不是？” But Goriot had caught sight of Rastignac, and answered, “They are coming, are they not?”
“还是有希望，”外科医师说，“他还能说话。” “There is hope yet,” said the surgeon; “he can speak.”
“是的。”欧仁说，“德尔菲娜要来了。” “Yes,” said Eugene, “Delphine is coming.”
“哦，这不算什么！”比安卡肖恩说，“他总是在说他的女儿们。 “Oh! that is nothing!” said Bianchon; “he has been talking about his daughters all the time.
他呼唤她们，就像一个钉在行刑柱上的人呼唤水一样，他们说——”“我们还是放弃吧。”内科医师对外科医师说道， He calls for them as a man impaled calls for water, they say—”“We may as well give up,” said the physician, addressing the surgeon.
“现在我们已经做不了什么了，这个病例是没希望了。” “Nothing more can be done now; the case is hopeless.”
比安卡肖恩和外科住院医师把这个垂死之人平摊在他那张令人作呕的床上。 Bianchon and the house surgeon stretched the dying man out again on his loathsome bed.
“床单总得换吧。”内科医师补充道， “But the sheets ought to be changed,” added the physician.
“即便是没了希望，他终究也是个人。 “Even if there is no hope left, something is due to human nature.
我一会儿就回来，比安卡肖恩。”他对这个医科学生说着， I shall come back again, Bianchon,” he said, turning to the medical student.
“要是他再喊疼的话，在他的横膈膜上抹点鸦片酊。” “If he complains again, rub some laudanum over the diaphragm.”
内科医师走了，外科住院医师也跟着他走了。 He went, and the house surgeon went with him.
“过来，欧仁，振作起精神来，我的伙计。”他们一单独留下的时候，比安卡肖恩就说，“我们必须开始换他的床单，给他穿上干净的衬衣。 “Come, Eugene, pluck up heart, my boy,” said Bianchon, as soon as they were alone; “we must set about changing his sheets, and put him into a clean shirt.
去告诉西尔维拿床单来，并叫她过来帮我们铺床。” Go and tell Sylvie to bring some sheets and come and help us to make the bed.”
欧仁下了楼，看见沃盖太太正在摆餐具，西尔维也在帮忙。 Eugene went downstairs, and found Mme. Vauquer engaged in setting the table; Sylvie was helping her.
欧仁还没开口，这个寡妇就走向欧仁，脸上带着尖酸的哂笑。这种笑让她看起来像个谨小慎微的店主，既不想在钱上有损失，也不想得罪房客。 Eugene had scarcely opened his mouth before the widow walked up to him with the acidulous sweet smile of a cautious shopkeeper who is anxious neither to lose money nor to offend a customer.
“我亲爱的欧仁先生，”他刚一说话，她就说道，“您和我都很明白高老头一分钱也没留下来。 “My dear Monsieur Eugene,” she said, when he had spoken, “you know quite as well as I do that Father Goriot has not a brass farthing left.
要是您把干净的亚麻床单都用在一个快闭眼的人身上，您就不太可能再见到您的床单了，因为总有一条床单是要用来裹他尸体的。 If you give out clean linen for a man who is just going to turn up his eyes, you are not likely to see your sheets again, for one is sure to be wanted to wrap him in.
现在，您欠我一百四十四法郎，加上两条共四十法郎的床单，还有一些零碎的东西，再算上西尔维要给您的蜡烛，全部加起来至少要二百法郎，这不是我这个穷寡妇能承受的损失啊。 Now, you owe me a hundred and forty-four francs as it is, add forty francs for the pair of sheets, and then there are several little things, besides the candle that Sylvie will give you; altogether it will all mount up to at least two hundred francs, which is more than a poor widow like me can afford to lose.
主啊！现在，欧仁先生，您要公平看待这事啊。 Lord! now, Monsieur Eugene, look at it fairly.
自从坏运气转到我头上，我这五天来已经损失够多了。 I have lost quite enough in these five days since this run of ill-luck set in for me.
就像你们说的那样，我宁愿花十个克朗让这位老先生搬出去。 I would rather than ten crowns that the old gentlemen had moved out as you said.
这会让其他房客对旅馆有抵触情绪的。 It sets the other lodgers against the house.
若我送他去救济院，也不会花很多钱。 It would not take much to make me send him to the workhouse.
总而言之，您要站到我的角度考虑考虑。 In short, just put yourself in my place.
我不得不首先考虑我的产业，因为我还要谋生呢。” I have to think of my establishment first, for I have my own living to make.”
欧仁急忙走上高老头的房间。 Eugene hurried up to Goriot’s room.
“比安卡肖恩，”他喊道，“手表换来的钱呢？” “Bianchon,” he cried, “the money for the watch?”
“就在桌子上，还剩下三百六十多法郎。 “There it is on the table, or the three hundred and sixty odd francs that are left of it.
在他们让我拿东西之前，我付清了之前所有的旧账。 I paid up all the old scores out of it before they let me have the things.
当票就在钱下面。” The pawn ticket lies there under the money.”
拉斯蒂涅又赶忙下了楼。 Rastignac hurried downstairs.
“这里，太太，”他以厌恶的口吻说，“我们来结账。高里奥先生不会在你的旅馆里住很久了，我也不会——”“是的，他就要蹬腿归西了，可怜的老先生。”她一边说话，一边调侃着，假装忧郁地数着钱。 “Here, madame” he said in disgust, “let us square accounts.M. Goriot will not stay much longer in your house, nor shall I—” “Yes, he will go out feet foremost, poor old gentleman,” she said, counting the francs with a half-facetious, half-lugubrious expression.
“我们快点结束吧。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “Let us get this over,” said Rastignac.
“西尔维，拿出床单，上楼给这位先生帮忙去。” “Sylvie, look out some sheets, and go upstairs to help the gentlemen.”
“您不会忘了西尔维的。”沃盖太太在欧仁的耳边说，“她已经熬了两夜没睡觉了。” “You won’t forget Sylvie,” said Mme. Vauquer in Eugene’s ear; “she has been sitting up these two nights.”
欧仁刚一转身，这位老妇人就匆忙跑向她的女仆。 As soon as Eugene’s back was turned, the old woman hurried after her handmaid.
“拿那种两边缝到中间的旧床单，7号。 “Take the sheets that have had the sides turned into the middle, number 7.
主啊！这些对于一具尸体来说已经够好了。”她在西尔维的耳边说。 Lord! they are plenty good enough for a corpse,” she said in Sylvie’s ear.
此时，欧仁正在上楼梯，没有听到这个节俭的老妇人的话。 Eugene, by this time, was part of the way upstairs, and did not overhear the elderly economist.
“快点，”比安卡肖恩说，“我们要给他换衬衣。扶他坐起来。” “Quick,” said Bianchon, “let us change his shirt.Hold him upright.”
欧仁走到床头，扶起这个将死之人；比安卡肖恩则脱下他的衬衣。之后，高老头动了一下，好像想要抓住胸口上的什么东西。他发出了一声低沉而模糊的呻吟，好像某个忍受着致命痛苦却不会说话的动物。 Eugene went to the head of the bed and supported the dying man, while Bianchon drew off his shirt; and then Goriot made a movement as if he tried to clutch something to his breast, uttering a low inarticulate moaning the while, like some dumb animal in mortal pain.
“啊！对了！”比安卡肖恩叫道， “Ah! yes!” cried Bianchon.
“他想要那个小金盒和那个用头发编的链子。我们刚才做艾灸时把它们摘下来了。 “It is the little locket and the chain made of hair that he wants; we took it off a while ago when we put the blisters on him.
可怜的家伙！他必须再得到它。 Poor fellow! he must have it again.
就在壁炉架上。” There it lies on the chimney-piece.”
欧仁走去壁炉架，看见了一束褪色金发扎成的链子——毫无疑问是高里奥夫人的头发。 Eugene went to the chimney-piece and found the little plait of faded golden hair—Mme. Goriot’s hair, no doubt.
他看着小圆盒上的名字，一边是阿纳斯塔谢，另一边是德尔菲娜。 He read the name on the little round locket, ANASTASIE on the one side, DELPHINE on the other.
这是他心灵的象征，他一直将父亲这一角色挂在胸前。 It was the symbol of his own heart that the father always wore on his breast.
金盒里的卷发那么纤细、柔软，很明显是从两个孩子的头上取下来的。 The curls of hair inside the locket were so fine and soft that is was plain they had been taken from two childish heads.
当老人再次摸到这个小金盒的时候，他满足地深深叹了一口气，胸脯也随之起伏，但声音却像呻吟一样。 When the old man felt the locket once more, his chest heaved with a long deep sigh of satisfaction, like a groan.
这是一幅可怕的景象，因为他们似乎能看清人体神经的最后颤动，这是感觉和某个神秘点的最后一次交流——我们的同情来自那个神秘点，也去往那个神秘点。 It was something terrible to see, for it seemed as if the last quiver of the nerves were laid bare to their eyes, the last communication of sense to the mysterious point within whence our sympathies come and whither they go.
神志不清的快乐使这张扭曲的脸上有了光彩。 A delirious joy lighted up the distorted face.
厚重而强烈的情感力量超越了思想的力量，这给这两个学生留下了如此深刻的印象，他们的泪水落在了这个垂死之人的脸上。高老头感到了这些热泪，发出了欢快的尖叫： The terrific and vivid force of the feeling that had survived the power of thought made such an impression on the students, that the dying man felt their hot tears falling on him, and gave a shrill cry of delight.
“纳西！菲芬！” “Nasie! Fifine!”
“他的生命还没有停止。”比安卡肖恩说。 “There is life in him yet,” said Bianchon.
“他继续活着还为了什么呢？”西尔维说。 “What does he go on living for?” said Sylvie.
“为了受罪。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “To suffer,” answered Rastignac.
比安卡肖恩示意他的朋友效仿他的动作。他跪了下来，将手臂放在病人身下，拉斯蒂涅则在另一头做着相同的动作。这样做好准备的西尔维就可以从下面抽出床单，然后拿一条刚带来的床单换上。 Bianchon made a sign to his friend to follow his example, knelt down and pressed his arms under the sick man, and Rastignac on the other side did the same, so that Sylvie, standing in readiness, might draw the sheet from beneath and replace it with the one that she had brought.
毫无疑问，刚才的眼泪使高老头产生了错觉。他使尽了最后一点力气，伸出双手，摸索着两个学生的头。当他的手指颤抖着碰到他们的头发时，他们听到了微弱的声音：“啊！我的天使们！” Those tears, no doubt, had misled Goriot; for he gathered up all his remaining strength in a last effort, stretched out his hands, groped for the students’ heads, and as his fingers caught convulsively at their hair, they heard a faint whisper: “Ah! my angels!”
随着这几声含糊不清的嘟囔，这几个用灵魂说出的话语一起离开他嘴唇的还有他的灵魂。 Two words, two inarticulate murmurs, shaped into words by the soul which fled forth with them as they left his lips.
“可怜的家伙！”西尔维喊道。她被这样的呼喊感动了。在最无奈、最无心的谎言下，这种伟大父爱的流露最后一次被提升到了一个崇高的地位。 “Poor dear!” cried Sylvie, melted by that exclamation; the expression of the great love raised for the last time to a sublime height by that most ghastly and involuntary of lies.
高老头最后一次呼吸一定是愉快的叹息，在那次叹息中，他的一生走到了尽头。即便是在生命的最后，他也被欺骗了。 The father’s last breath must have been a sigh of joy, and in that sigh his whole life was summed up; he was cheated even at the last.
他们恭恭敬敬地把高老头放在了他肮脏的床上。 They laid Father Goriot upon his wretched bed with reverent hands.
从那以后，他脸上再也没有表情了，而只有他体内过去一直在进行的生死挣扎所留下的痛苦痕迹。因为人体内能够区分快乐和痛苦的大脑意识已经灭亡了，而整副躯壳的毁灭只是个时间问题了。 Thenceforward there was no expression on his face, only the painful traces of the struggle between life and death that was going on in the machine; for that kind of cerebral consciousness that distinguishes between pleasure and pain in a human being was extinguished; it was only a question of time—and the mechanism itself would be destroyed.
“他会这样子躺上几个小时，最后平静地死去。我们也不会知道他什么时候走，他的喉咙里也不会再发出声音了。 “He will lie like this for several hours, and die so quietly at last, that we shall not know when he goes; there will be no rattle in the throat.
大脑肯定完全充血了。” The brain must be completely suffused.”
就在他说话的时候，楼梯那里传来了脚步声，一位年轻女士气喘吁吁地匆忙赶了上来。 As he spoke there was a footstep on the staircase, and a young woman hastened up, panting for breath.
“她来得太晚了。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “She has come too late,” said Rastignac.
但是站在门外的不是德尔菲娜，是她的女仆泰蕾兹。 But it was not Delphine; it was Therese, her waiting-woman, who stood in the doorway.
“欧仁先生，”她说，“可怜的夫人想为她父亲要一点钱，和先生大吵了一架。 “Monsieur Eugene,” she said, “monsieur and madame have had a terrible scene about some money that Madame poor thing wanted for her father.
她晕过去了，医生也赶到了，她必须放点血，但她嘴里总是大喊：‘我的父亲就要死了，我要见我的爸爸！’听到她那样喊，简直让人心都碎了——”“就这样吧，泰蕾兹。 She fainted, and the doctor came, and she had to be bled, calling out all the while, ‘My father is dying; I want to see papa!’ It was heartbreaking to hear her—” “That will do, Therese.
要是她现在来，也是无济于事了。 If she came now, it would be trouble thrown away.
高里奥先生已经认不出任何人了。” M. Goriot cannot recognize any one now.”
“哦，亲爱的先生，他病得这么严重吗？”泰蕾兹说。 “Poor, dear gentleman, is he as bad at that?” said Therese.
“你们现在不需要我了，我得去看看我的晚饭，已经四点半了。”西尔维说。 “You don’t want me now, I must go and look after my dinner; it is half-past four,” remarked Sylvie.
下一刻，她差点与站在外面楼梯平台上的德雷斯多夫人撞了个满怀。 The next instant she all but collided with Mme. de Restaud on the landing outside.
伯爵夫人的突然出现令人觉得既难受，又震惊。 There was something awful and appalling in the sudden apparition of the Countess.
她借着唯一一支蜡烛的微弱火光，看见了那张临死之人躺着的床。当她看到她父亲那张无精打采而又几乎没有生命迹象的脸时，她的眼泪涌了出来。 She saw the bed of death by the dim light of the single candle, and her tears flowed at the sight of her father’s passive features, from which the life had almost ebbed.
比安卡肖恩识趣地离开了房间。 Bianchon with thoughtful tact left the room.
“我不能及时脱身。”她对拉斯蒂涅说。 “I could not escape soon enough,” she said to Rastignac.
这个学生悲伤地鞠了一躬以示回应。 The student bowed sadly in reply.
德雷斯多夫人拿起了她父亲的手，亲吻了一下。 Mme. de Restaud took her father’s hand and kissed it.
“原谅我，父亲！您过去说过，我的声音能将您从坟墓中叫回来。啊！就回来一会儿，保佑您已悔悟的女儿吧。 “Forgive me, father!You used to say that my voice would call you back from the grave; ah! come back for one moment to bless your penitent daughter.
您听见我说话了吗？ Do you hear me?
哦！这太可怕了！ Oh! this is fearful!
从此之后，这世上没有人会再祝福我了，每个人都恨我，这世上只有您爱我。 No one on earth will ever bless me henceforth; every one hates me; no one loves me but you in all the world.
我自己的孩子会恨我。 My own children will hate me.
把我带走吧，父亲，我会爱您，照顾您。 Take me with you, father; I will love you, I will take care of you.
他听不到我说话……我要发疯了……”她跪了下来，死死地盯着她面前这个不成人样的人。 He does not hear me…I am mad…”She fell on her knees, and gazed wildly at the human wreck before her.
“我的苦杯满溢。”她将目光转向欧仁，说道， “My cup of misery is full,” she said, turning her eyes upon Eugene.
“德特拉尔已经逃走了，他欠下了一大笔债。我也发现了他一直在欺骗我。 “M. de Trailles has fled, leaving enormous debts behind him, and I have found out that he was deceiving me.
我的丈夫永远也不会原谅我的，我的财产也已经在他的手上了。 My husband will never forgive me, and I have left my fortune in his hands.
我所有的幻想都破灭了。 I have lost all my illusions.
唉！ Alas!
我抛弃了一颗爱我的心（她说话之时就指着她的父亲），这是为了谁呢？ I have forsaken the one heart that loved me (she pointed to her father as she spoke), and for whom?
我曾认为他的善意一文不值，还轻视他对我的关爱。我一次又一次让他承受痛苦，我是一个忘恩负义的混蛋啊！” I have held his kindness cheap, and slighted his affection; many and many a time I have given him pain, ungrateful wretch that I am!”
“他了解。”拉斯蒂涅说。 “He knew it,” said Rastignac.
就在那时，高老头的眼皮睁开了，这只是肌肉的收缩，但是伯爵夫人忽然恢复的希望就像那双垂死的眼睛那样可怕。 Just then Goriot’s eyelids unclosed; it was only a muscular contraction, but the Countess’ sudden start of reviving hope was no less dreadful than the dying eyes.
“他有可能听到我说话吗？”伯爵夫人喊道。 “Is it possible that he can hear me?” cried the Countess.
“没可能。”她自己又回答道，之后就坐在了床边。 “No,” she answered herself, and sat down beside the bed.
因为德雷斯多夫人似乎想和父亲坐一会儿，于是欧仁就下楼吃了点东西。 As Mme. de Restaud seemed to wish to sit by her father, Eugene went down to take a little food.
房客们都已经坐在那里了。 The boarders were already assembled.
“嗯，”当他加入他们的时候，那个画家说，“看来楼上要上演一出死亡的戏码了。” “Well,” remarked the painter, as he joined them, “it seems that there is to be a death-drama upstairs.”
“夏尔，我认为你可以找一些不那么痛苦的事开玩笑。”欧仁说。 “Charles, I think you might find something less painful to joke about,” said Eugene.
“那么我们就不能在这里笑了？”画家反问道， “So we may not laugh here?” returned the painter.
“有什么不好吗？ “What harm does it do?
比安卡肖恩说那老头已经完全没有知觉了。” Bianchon said that the old man was quite insensible.”
“嗯，那么，”博物馆员工说，“他死时也会和活着一样。” “Well, then,” said the @employee@ from the Museum, “he will die as he has lived.”
“我的父亲死了！”伯爵夫人尖声叫道。 “My father is dead!” shrieked the Countess.
西尔维、拉斯蒂涅和比安卡肖恩随着这声可怕的尖叫迎了上去。德雷斯多夫人已经晕过去了。 The terrible cry brought Sylvie, Rastignac, and Bianchon; Mme. de Restaud had fainted away.
当她苏醒过来时，他们抬着她下了楼，将她抬进在门外等候的出租马车上。 When she recovered they carried her downstairs, and put her into the cab that stood waiting at the door.
欧仁送泰蕾兹和她出去，吩咐女仆把伯爵夫人送到德纽沁根夫人家去。 Eugene sent Therese with her, and bade the maid take the Countess to Mme. de Nucingen.
比安卡肖恩下楼走向他们。 Bianchon came down to them.
“是的，他死了。”他说。 “Yes, he is dead,” he said.
“来吧，坐下吃晚饭吧，先生们。”沃盖太太说，“不然汤就要凉了。” “Come, sit down to dinner, gentlemen,” said Mme. Vauquer, “or the soup will be cold.”
两个学生一起坐了下来。 The two students sat down together.
“下面要做什么呢？”欧仁问比安卡肖恩。 “What is the next thing to be done?” Eugene asked of Bianchon.
“我已经把他的双眼合上了，四肢也摆好了。”比安卡肖恩说， “I have closed his eyes and composed his limbs,” said Bianchon.
“一旦有了在市长办公室正式登记的证书以后，我们就把他缝进裹尸布里，把他在葬在某个地方吧。 “When the certificate has been officially registered at the Mayor’s office, we will sew him in his winding sheet and bury him somewhere.
我觉得我们还能做什么呢？” What do you think we ought to do?”
“他再也不能这样闻他的面包了。”画家边说，边模仿者老人的小把戏。 “He will not smell at his bread like this any more,” said the painter, mimicking the old man’s little trick.
“哦，该死的！”助教大声说，“别再说高老头了，我们换点别的话题说吧。 “Oh, hang it all!” cried the tutor, “let Father Goriot drop, and let us have something else for a change.
他都成为我们每日必谈的话题了，而且我们这一个多小时以来都在说他的事。 He is a standing dish, and we have had him with every sauce this hour or more.
巴黎这样的好城市的一点好处就是，任何人在这里出生、生存和死亡都不会吸引任何注意力。 It is one of the privileges of the good city of Paris that anybody may be born, or live, or die there without attracting any attention whatsoever.
让我们享受这种文明带来的好处吧。 Let us profit by the advantages of civilization.
每天都有五六十人死亡。要是你有心关注这些，你随时都可以坐下来，为巴黎所有死者的祭祀哀号。 There are fifty or sixty deaths every day; if you have a mind to do it, you can sit down at any time and wail over whole hecatombs of dead in Paris.
高老头已经死了，不是吗？ Father Goriot has gone off the hooks, has he?
对他而言，死远比活着好。 So much the better for him.
要是你对他的记忆还有一点崇敬之情，就留在你的心里，让我们其他人恢复宁静吧。” If you venerate his memory, keep it to yourselves, and let the rest of us feed in peace.”
“哦，的确。”这寡妇说道，“对他而言，他死了反而更好。 “Oh, to be sure,” said the widow, “it is all the better for him that he is dead.
他活着的时候似乎已经有够多麻烦了，可怜的人啊。” It looks as though he had had trouble enough, poor soul, while he was alive.”
这就是他葬礼上的所有致词了，而在欧仁的眼中他是父爱的化身。 And this was all the funeral oration delivered over him who had been for Eugene the type and embodiment of Fatherhood.
十五位房客又开始像平常那样谈话了。 The fifteen lodgers began to talk as usual.
当比安卡肖恩和欧仁吃饱时，其他人刀叉的碰撞声、喧闹的说话声以及脸上的表情都显示了他们不同程度的欲望、贪婪和冷漠。他们身上的每一点都让两个学生厌恶得发抖。 When Bianchon and Eugene had satisfied their hunger, the rattle of spoons and forks, the boisterous conversation, the expressions on the faces that bespoke various degrees of want of feeling, gluttony, or indifference, everything about them made them shiver with loathing.
他们去找了一个神父，为这已逝之人守夜。 They went out to find a priest to watch that night with the dead.
他们有必要用仅剩的一点钱来尽他们最后一点责任。 It was necessary to measure their last pious cares by the scanty sum of money that remained.
那晚九点之前，尸体停放在那个凄凉的房间里，放在里面床架上那光秃秃的麻布上。床架两边各点了一支蜡烛，神父就守在床尾。 Before nine o’clock that evening the body was laid out on the bare sacking of the bedstead in the desolate room; a lighted candle stood on either side, and the priest watched at the foot.
拉斯蒂涅向神父询问了有关葬礼的费用，然后就写信给德纽沁根男爵和德雷斯多伯爵，请两位先生委托他们的律师支付他们岳父下葬的费用。 Rastignac made inquiries of this latter as to the expenses of the funeral, and wrote to the Baron de Nucingen and the Comte de Restaud, entreating both gentlemen to authorize their man of business to defray the charges of laying their father-in-law in the grave.
他让克里斯托夫去送信，之后便上了床。他太累了，很快就睡着了。 He sent Christophe with the letters; then he went to bed, tired out, and slept.
第二天，比安卡肖恩和拉斯蒂涅不得不亲自带着证书去注册员那里登记。十二点的时候，正式手续就办好了。 Next day Bianchon and Rastignac were obliged to take the certificate to the registrar themselves, and by twelve o’clock the formalities were completed.
两个小时过去了，伯爵和男爵那里都没有回音。没人来代表他们，拉斯蒂涅不得不付钱给神父。 Two hours went by, no word came from the Count nor from the Baron; nobody appeared to act for them, and Rastignac had already been obliged to pay the priest.
西尔维要了十法郎，作为给老人缝裹尸布好让他下葬的报酬。欧仁和比安卡肖恩计算了之后，发现要是老人的家庭不出钱的话，他们的钱是不足以支付葬礼费用的。 Sylvie asked ten francs for sewing the old man in his winding-sheet and making him ready for the grave, and Eugene and Bianchon calculated that they had scarcely sufficient to pay for the funeral, if nothing was forthcoming from the dead man’s family.
所以这个医科学生把他放进了穷酸的棺材里，那是比安卡肖恩所在医院派发的，所以他能以更便宜的价格买到。 So it was the medical student who laid him in a pauper’s coffin, dispatched from Bianchon’s hospital, whence he obtained it at a cheaper rate.
“我们跟那些混蛋们开个玩笑吧。”他说， “Let us play those wretches a trick,” said he.
“去公墓，在拉雪兹买个五年的墓地，然后安排教堂和承办者举行一个三等葬礼。 “Go to the cemetery, buy a grave for five years at Pere-Lachaise, and arrange with the Church and the undertaker to have a third-class funeral.
要是女儿们和她们的丈夫拒绝偿还你钱的话，你就在石碑上刻上——‘高里奥先生，德雷斯多伯爵夫人和德纽沁根男爵夫人的父亲，两个大学生出钱埋葬’。”欧仁首先亲自去了德纽沁根夫妇家，又去了德雷斯多夫妇家。两次尝试无果之后，他接受了他朋友的部分建议。 If the daughters and their husbands decline to repay you, you can carve this on the headstone—‘HERE LIES M. GORIOT, FATHER OF THE COMTESSE DE RESTAUD AND THE BARONNE DE NUCINGEN, INTERRED AT THE EXPENSE OF TWO STUDENTS.’”Eugene took part of his friend’s advice, but only after he had gone in person first to M. and Mme. de Nucingen, and then to M. and Mme. de Restaud—a fruitless errand.
在他们两家，他都止步于门口，没有进屋。 He went no further than the doorstep in either house.
仆人们收到了严格的命令，不接待任何人。 The servants had received strict orders to admit no one.
“先生和夫人谢绝见客。 “Monsieur and Madame can see no visitors.
他们刚刚失去父亲，正处在失去亲人的极度悲痛之中。” They have just lost their father, and are in deep grief over their loss.”
欧仁在巴黎的经历告诉他，反复提这件事也无济于事。 Eugene’s Parisian experience told him that it was idle to press the point.
当他看到不可能接近德尔菲娜时，一种奇怪的东西揪住了他的心。 Something clutched strangely at his heart when he saw that it was impossible to reach Delphine.
“卖一些你的首饰吧，”他在门房里匆忙写着，“那么你父亲就可以体面地躺在他最后的安息之地了。” “Sell some of your ornaments,” he wrote hastily in the porter’s room, “so that your father may be decently laid in his last resting-place.”
他封好了字条，乞求看门人将其交给泰蕾兹，让她转交给她的女主人。但是那人将字条交给了德纽沁根男爵，而他把字条扔进了火炉里。 He sealed the note, and begged the porter to give it to Therese for her mistress; but the man took it to the Baron de Nucingen, who flung the note into the fire.
欧仁完成了他的使命之后，大约三点的时候回到了旅馆。 Eugene, having finished his errands, returned to the lodging-house about three o’clock.
即使是他也不由自主地掉了眼泪。 In spite of himself, the tears came into his eyes.
棺材上盖着一块寒酸的黑布，棺材搭在两张椅子上，放在门前的人行道上。 The coffin, in its scanty covering of black cloth, was standing there on the pavement before the gate, on two chairs.
一条枯萎了的牛膝草枝正浸泡在镀银铜碗中的圣水里。街上没有一个人，没有一个过路人驻足为棺材洒点圣水，甚至没有人想起在便门上挂上一匹黑帷帐。 A withered sprig of hyssop was soaking in the holy water bowl of silver-plated copper; there was not a soul in the street, not a passer-by had stopped to sprinkle the coffin; there was not even an attempt at a black drapery over the wicket.
躺在那里的是一个穷光蛋，没有人会假装悼念他。他既没有朋友也没有亲戚——没有人跟随他去墓地。 It was a pauper who lay there; no one made a pretence of mourning for him; he had neither friends nor kindred—there was no one to follow him to the grave.
比安卡肖恩不得不留在医院，这是他的职责所在，但是他给欧仁留下了几行字来告诉他的朋友关于下葬的安排。 Bianchon’s duties compelled him to be at the hospital, but he had left a few lines for Eugene, telling his friend about the arrangements he had made for the burial service.
这个医科学生的字条告诉拉斯蒂涅，他们支付不起一场弥撒，但是对于死者的普通服务要便宜一点，而且也足够了，所以他叫克里斯托夫去给承办人带话了。 The house student’s note told Rastignac that a mass was beyond their means, that the ordinary office for the dead was cheaper, and must suffice, and that he had sent word to the undertaker by Christophe.
欧仁还没读完比安卡肖恩的潦草字迹，就抬眼看到沃盖太太手里拿着那个金质的小圆盒，那里面放着高老头两个女儿的头发。 Eugene had scarcely finished reading Bianchon’s scrawl, when he looked up and saw the little circular gold locket that contained the hair of Goriot’s two daughters in Mme. Vauquer’s hands.
“你怎么敢拿走这个呢？”他问道。 “How dared you take it?” he asked.
“我的上帝啊！那么这个东西要和他一起下葬吗？”西尔维反驳道， “Good Lord! is that to be buried along with him?” retorted Sylvie.
“这是金的。” “It is gold.”
“当然要一起下葬了！”欧仁愤怒地回答道，“不管怎样，他应该带着一件可以代表他女儿们的东西下葬。” “Of course it shall!” Eugene answered indignantly; “he shall at any rate take one thing that may represent his daughters into the grave with him.”
当灵车到达时，欧仁将棺材再一次抬进屋子里。他打开棺材盖子，虔诚地将那个纪念物放在老人的胸前——它能让人回忆起德尔菲娜和阿纳斯塔谢还是天真小女孩时的日子，她们那时还没有开始像他在痛苦中抱怨的那样“为自己着想”。 When the hearse came, Eugene had the coffin carried into the house again, unscrewed the lid, and reverently laid on the old man’s breast the token that recalled the days when Delphine and Anastasie were innocent little maidens, before they began “to think for themselves,” as he had moaned out in his agony.
参加这场葬礼的只有拉斯蒂涅、克里斯托夫和两个承办人。 Rastignac and Christophe and the two undertaker’s men were the only followers of the funeral.
圣艾蒂安·杜蒙教堂到新圣热讷维耶沃街的距离不是很远。 The Church of Saint-Etienne du Mont was only a little distance from the Rue Nueve-Sainte-Genevieve.
当棺材被放在一间低矮、黑暗的小礼拜堂时，这个法律系学生环顾四周，寻找高老头两个女儿和她们丈夫的踪迹，却是徒劳。 When the coffin had been deposited in a low, dark, little chapel, the law student looked round in vain for Goriot’s two daughters or their husbands.
克里斯托夫是唯一一个和他一起悼念的人，不过克里斯托夫似乎只是认为，对于一个曾经给自己很多小费的人，他有责任参加他的葬礼。 Christophe was his only fellow-mourner; Christophe, who appeared to think it was his duty to attend the funeral of the man who had put him in the way of such handsome tips.
就在他们在礼拜堂里等候两位神父、唱诗班领唱和教区执事时，拉斯蒂涅抓住了克里斯托夫的手。 As they waited there in the chapel for the two priests, the chorister, and the beadle, Rastignac grasped Christophe’s hand.
他那时说不出一个字来。 He could not utter a word just then.
“是的，欧仁先生，”克里斯托夫说，“他是一位善良可敬的人，从不对其他人大声说话，从来没有伤害过任何人，也没给任何人惹过麻烦。” “Yes, Monsieur Eugene,” said Christophe, “he was a good and worthy man, who never said one word louder than another; he never did any one any harm, and gave nobody any trouble.”
两位神父、唱诗班领唱和教区执事来了。在那个时代，宗教已经不做没有回报的祷告了，所以他们说了七十法郎所付得起的话，做了七十法郎所付得起的事。 The two priests, the chorister, and the beadle came, and said and did as much as could be expected for seventy francs in an age when religion cannot afford to say prayers for nothing.
教友们唱了一段圣歌，分别是《葬礼应答圣咏》和《深沉的哀痛》。 The ecclesiastics chanted a psalm, the @Libera nos@and the @De profundis@.
整个仪式持续了大约二十分钟。 The whole service lasted about twenty minutes.
因为只有一辆送殡马车，所以神父和唱诗班领唱同意和欧仁和克里斯托夫一起乘坐。 There was but one mourning coach, which the priest and chorister agreed to share with Eugene and Christophe.
“没有其他人跟着我们了。”神父说，“所以我们最好走快一点，好节省时间，已经五点半了。” “There is no one else to follow us,” remarked the priest, “so we may as well go quickly, and so save time; it is half-past five.”
但就在棺材被抬上灵车的时候，两辆分别有德雷斯多伯爵和德纽沁根男爵徽章的空马车来了，跟随着队伍前往拉雪兹神父公墓。 But just as the coffin was put in the hearse, two empty carriages, with the armorial bearings of the Comte de Restaud and the Baron de Nucingen, arrived and followed in the procession to Pere-Lachaise.
六点钟时，高老头的灵柩被放入了墓穴之中，这时他两个女儿的仆人们也站在周围。 At six o’clock Goriot’s coffin was lowered into the grave, his daughters’ servants standing round the while.
教友们诵读了两个大学生能付得起的一段简短祷告词，之后神父和他的跟班们便立刻消失了。 The ecclesiastic recited the short prayer that the students could afford to pay for, and then both priest and lackeys disappeared at once.
两个挖墓人在棺材上扔了几铲土之后，就停下来问拉斯蒂涅要钱。 The two grave diggers flung in several spadefuls of earth, and then stopped and asked Rastignac for their fee.
欧仁在自己的口袋里没有摸到钱，于是不得不向克里斯托夫借了五法郎。 Eugene felt in vain in his pocket, and was obliged to borrow five francs of Christophe.
这件事，尽管本身微不足道，却给拉斯蒂涅带来了沉重而悲痛的一击。 This thing, so trifling in itself, gave Rastignac a terrible pang of distress.
渐渐降临的薄暮和减退的微光腐蚀了他的神经。他注视着墓穴，神圣的情感和单纯的哀伤使他留下了眼泪。 It was growing dusk, the damp twilight fretted his nerves; he gazed down into the grave and the tears he shed were drawn from him by the sacred emotion, a single-hearted sorrow.
当眼泪滴在泥土之上，它们的光芒直射天堂。 When such tears fall on earth, their radiance reaches heaven.
随着在高老头墓前留下的泪，欧仁·拉斯蒂涅的青年时代也结束了。 And with that tear that fell on Father Goriot’s grave, Eugene Rastignac’s youth ended.
他交叉双臂，仰望乌云密布的天空。克里斯托夫看了他一眼便转身走了——拉斯蒂涅独自留了下来。 He folded his arms and gazed at the clouded sky; and Christophe, after a glance at him, turned and went—Rastignac was left alone.
他向前走了几步，走到了公墓的最高处，眺望着巴黎和蜿蜒的塞纳河。在河的两侧，灯火逐渐亮了起来。 He went a few paces further, to the highest point of the cemetery, and looked out over Paris and the windings of the Seine; the lamps were beginning to shine on either side of the river.
他急切地望着位于旺多姆广场圆柱和荣军院穹顶之间的地方，那里是他曾经希望进入的世界，是一个光芒四射的地方。 His eyes turned almost eagerly to the space between the column of the Place Vendome and the cupola of the Invalides; there lay the shining world that he had wished to reach.
他俯瞰着那个喧闹的蜂房，似乎提前尝到其中蜂蜜的味道，然后他夸张地说：“从此之后，我们之间会有一场战争。” He glanced over that humming hive, seeming to draw a foretaste of its honey, and said magniloquently:“Henceforth there is war between us.”
之后，为了向这个社会发出挑战，拉斯蒂涅去了德纽沁根夫人家，和她共进晚餐。 And by way of throwing down the glove to Society, Rastignac went to dine with Mme. de Nucingen.
